Title: Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023
Date: 2024-11-11
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2023/56

## Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023

B e it enacted  by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the advice
and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this present
Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Companies etc

#### The registrar of companies

##### The registrar’s objectives

1

1.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

1.2

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (2), at the appropriate
place insert—

section  1081A  (registrar’s objectives to promote integrity of registers
etc),

.

1.3

After section 1081 insert—

########### Registrar’s objectives to promote integrity of registers etc

1.3.1081A

1.3.1081A.1

The registrar must, in performing the registrar’s functions, seek to promote
the following objectives.

Objective 1 Objective 1 is to ensure that any person who is required to
deliver a document to the registrar does so (and that the requirements for
proper delivery are complied with). Objective 2 Objective 2 is to ensure that
information contained in the register is accurate and that the register
contains everything it ought to contain. Objective 3 Objective 3 is to ensure
that records kept by the registrar do not create a false or misleading
impression to members of the public. Objective 4 Objective 4 is to prevent
companies and others from— carrying out unlawful activities, or facilitating
the carrying out by others of unlawful activities.

1.3.1081A.2

In Objective 2 the reference to “ the register ” includes any records kept by
the registrar under any enactment.

#### Company formation

##### Statement as to lawful purposes

2

In section 9 of the Companies Act 2006 (registration documents), in subsection
(2)—

2.a

omit the “and” at the end of paragraph (c);

2.b

at the end of paragraph (d) insert

, and

2.b.e

that the subscribers wish to form the company for lawful purposes.

##### Information about subscribers

3

3.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

3.2

In section 9 (registration documents)—

3.2.a

after subsection (3) insert—

3.2.a.3A

The application must contain—

3.2.a.3A.a

a statement of the required information about each of the subscribers to the
memorandum of association (see section  9A ),

3.2.a.3A.b

a statement that none of the subscribers to the memorandum of association is
disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see section
159A(2)),

3.2.a.3A.c

if any of them would be so disqualified but for the permission of a court to
act, a statement to that effect, in respect of each of them, specifying—

3.2.a.3A.c.i

the subscriber’s name,

3.2.a.3A.c.ii

the court by which permission was given, and

3.2.a.3A.c.iii

the date on which permission was given, and

3.2.a.3A.d

if any of them would be disqualified under the directors disqualification
legislation by virtue of section 11A of the Company Directors Disqualification
Act 1986 or Article 15A of the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern
Ireland) Order 2002 (designated persons under sanctions legislation) but for
the authority of a licence of the kind mentioned in that section or Article, a
statement to that effect, in respect of each of them, specifying—

3.2.a.3A.d.i

the subscriber’s name, and

3.2.a.3A.d.ii

the date on which it was issued and by whom it was issued.

;

3.2.b

after subsection (6) insert—

3.2.b.7

In subsection  (3A)(c)  “ permission of a court to act ” means permission of a
court under a provision mentioned in column 2 of the table in section 159A(2).

3.3

After section 9 insert—

########### Required information about the subscribers

3.3.9A

3.3.9A.1

The required information about a subscriber who is an individual is—

3.3.9A.1.a

name;

3.3.9A.1.b

a service address.

3.3.9A.2

The required information about a subscriber that is a body corporate, or a
firm that is a legal person under the law by which it is governed, is—

3.3.9A.2.a

corporate or firm name;

3.3.9A.2.b

a service address.

3.3.9A.3

In subsection  (1)  “ name ” means the individual’s forename and surname.

3.3.9A.4

Where a subscriber is a peer or an individual usually known by a title, that
title may be stated in the application for the registration of the company
instead of the subscriber’s forename and surname.

3.3.9A.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

3.3.9A.5.a

amend this section so as to change the required information about a
subscriber;

3.3.9A.5.b

repeal subsection  (4) .

3.3.9A.6

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

3.4

In section 10 (statement of capital and initial shareholdings), omit
subsection (3).

3.5

In section 11 (statement of guarantee), omit subsection (2).

##### Proposed officers: identity verification

4

4.1

Section 12 of the Companies Act 2006 (statement of proposed officers) is
amended as follows.

4.2

After subsection (2) insert—

4.2.2A

The statement must, in the case of each individual named as a director,
confirm that the individual’s identity is verified (see section 1110A).

4.3

The provision that may be made under section 220 (1)  in connection with the
coming into force of this section includes—

4.3.a

provision requiring a company incorporated in pursuance of an application
delivered before the coming into force of this section to deliver to the
registrar, at the same time as a confirmation statement, a statement, in
respect of any individual who became a director of the company on its
incorporation, confirming that the individual’s identity is verified (within
the meaning of section 1110A of the Companies Act 2006), and

4.3.b

provision for section 853A(1)(b)(i) of the Companies Act 2006 (as substituted
by section 59 of this Act) to have effect as if it included a reference to any
duty imposed by virtue of paragraph  (a) .

4.4

In subsection  (3) —

“ confirmation statement ” has the meaning given by section 853A of the
Companies Act 2006; “ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Companies
Acts (see section 1060 of the Companies Act 2006).

##### Proposed officers: disqualification

5

5.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows

5.2

In section 12 (statement of proposed officers), at the end insert—

5.2.4

The statement must also include a statement by the subscribers to the
memorandum of association that no one named as a director is—

5.2.4.a

disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see section
159A(2)), or

5.2.4.b

otherwise ineligible by virtue of any enactment for appointment as a director.

5.2.5

Where any of the persons named as directors would be disqualified under the
directors disqualification legislation but for the permission of a court to
act, the statement must also include a statement to that effect, in respect of
each of them, specifying—

5.2.5.a

the person’s name,

5.2.5.b

the court by which permission was given, and

5.2.5.c

the date on which permission was given.

5.2.6

In subsection  (5)  “ permission of a court to act ” means permission of a
court under a provision mentioned in column 2 of the table in section 159A(2).

5.2.7

Where any of the persons named as directors would be disqualified under the
directors disqualification legislation by virtue of section 11A of the Company
Directors Disqualification Act 1986 or Article 15A of the Company Directors
Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 (designated persons under
sanctions legislation) but for the authority of a licence of the kind
mentioned in that section or Article, the statement must also include a
statement to that effect, in respect of each of them, specifying—

5.2.7.a

the person’s name, and

5.2.7.b

the date on which the licence was issued and by whom it was issued.

5.3

In section 16 (effect of registration), in subsection (6), at the end insert
“unless ineligible for appointment to that office by virtue of any enactment”
.

##### Persons with initial significant control: disqualification

6

6.1

Section 12A of the Companies Act 2006 (statement of initial significant
control) is amended as follows.

6.2

After subsection (1) insert—

6.2.1A

If there is anyone who will be a registrable person, or a registrable relevant
legal entity, in relation to the company on incorporation, the statement must
also include—

6.2.1A.a

a statement that none of them is disqualified under the directors
disqualification legislation (see section 159A(2)),

6.2.1A.b

if any of them would be so disqualified but for the permission of a court to
act, a statement to that effect, in respect of each of them, specifying—

6.2.1A.b.i

the person’s name,

6.2.1A.b.ii

the court by which permission was given,

6.2.1A.b.iii

the date on which permission was given, and

6.2.1A.c

if any of them would be so disqualified by virtue of section 11A of the
Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986 or Article 15A of the Company
Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 (designated persons
under sanctions legislation) but for the authority of a licence of the kind
mentioned in that section or Article, a statement to that effect, in respect
of each of them, specifying—

6.2.1A.c.i

the person’s name, and

6.2.1A.c.ii

the date on which the licence was issued and by whom it was issued.

6.3

For subsection (4) substitute—

6.3.4

In this section—

“ permission of a court to act ” means permission of a court under a provision
mentioned in column 2 of the table in section 159A(2); “ registrable person ”
has the meaning given by section 790C (see also section 790J); “ registrable
relevant legal entity ” has the meaning given by section 790C (see also
section 790J); “ required particulars ” has the meaning given by section 790K.

##### Persons with initial significant control: identity verification

7

After section 12A of the Companies Act 2006 insert—

######### Option to provide ID verification information about PSCs

7.12B

7.12B.1

This section applies if an application for the registration of a company
contains a statement of initial significant control that identifies a person
who will be a registrable person, or a registrable relevant legal entity, in
relation to the company on its incorporation.

7.12B.2

In relation to any person who will be a registrable person, the statement may
include a statement that the person’s identity is verified (see section
1110A).

7.12B.3

In relation to any person who will be a registrable relevant legal entity, the
statement may include a statement that—

7.12B.3.a

specifies the name of one of its relevant officers (within the meaning given
by section  790LO (6) ) who is an individual and whose identity is verified,
and

7.12B.3.b

confirms that the individual’s identity is verified.

7.12B.4

If a statement under subsection  (3)  is included in relation to a person who
will be a registrable relevant legal entity, the application for registration
of the company must be accompanied by a statement by the individual confirming
that the individual is a relevant officer of that entity.

7.12B.5

To find out what happens if the option in subsection  (2)  or  (3)  is not
exercised, see sections  790LM  and  790LO .

7.12B.6

In this section—

“ registrable person ” has the meaning given by section 790C, except that it
does not include a person mentioned in section 790C(12)(a) to (d) (see also
section 790J); “ registrable relevant legal entity ” has the meaning given by
section 790C (see also section 790J).

#### Company names

##### Names for criminal purposes

8

8.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

8.2

After section 53 insert—

########### Names for criminal purposes

8.2.53A

A company must not be registered under this Act by a name if, in the opinion
of the Secretary of State, the registration of the company by that name is
intended to facilitate—

8.2.53A.a

the commission of an offence involving dishonesty or deception, or

8.2.53A.b

the carrying out of conduct that, if carried out in any part of the United
Kingdom, would amount to such an offence.

8.3

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph (a) insert—

8.3.aa

section  53A  (names for criminal purposes);

.

##### Names suggesting connection with foreign governments etc

9

9.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

9.2

After section 56 insert—

########### Names suggesting connection with foreign governments etc

9.2.56A

A company must not be registered under this Act by a name that, in the opinion
of the Secretary of State, would be likely to give the false impression that
the company is connected with—

9.2.56A.a

a foreign government or an agency or authority of a foreign government, or

9.2.56A.b

an international organisation whose members include two or more countries or
territories (or their governments).

9.3

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph (b) insert—

9.3.bza

section  56A  (names suggesting connection with foreign governments etc);

.

##### Names containing computer code

10

10.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

10.2

After section 57 insert—

########### Computer code

############ Names containing computer code

10.2.57A

A company must not be registered under this Act by a name that, in the opinion
of the Secretary of State, consists of or includes computer code.

10.3

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph (ba) insert—

10.3.bb

section  57A  (names containing computer code);

.

##### Prohibition on re-registering name following direction

11

11.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

11.2

After section  57A  (inserted by section 10 of this Act) insert—

########### Prohibitions where a company has been required to change a name

############ Prohibition on re-registering name following direction

11.2.57B

11.2.57B.1

Where a company’s name has at any time been changed following a direction
under section 67, 75, 76, 76A or  76B , or an order under section 73, the
company must not subsequently be registered under this Act by the original
name or a name that is similar to it.

11.2.57B.2

But subsection  (1)  does not prevent the registration of the company by any
name approved by the Secretary of State.

11.2.57B.3

In subsection  (1) —

11.2.57B.3.a

the reference to the name of a company being changed following a direction
under a particular section includes a case where a new name is determined for
the company under section  76D  because of its failure to comply with the
direction;

11.2.57B.3.b

the reference to the name of a company being changed following an order under
section 73 includes a case where a new name is determined for the company
under section 73(4) because of its failure to comply with an order.

11.3

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph  (bb)  (inserted by section 10 of this Act) insert—

11.3.bc

section  57B  (restriction on re-registering name following direction).

##### Prohibition on using name that another company has been directed to change

12

12.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

12.2

After section  57B  (inserted by section 11 of this Act) insert—

########### Name that another company has been directed to change

12.2.57C

12.2.57C.1

Where a company has at any time been directed under section 67, 75, 76, 76A or
76B , or ordered under section 73, to change its name, no other company may be
registered under this Act by that name or a name that is similar if—

12.2.57C.1.a

that company is an existing company and there is a person who has, or has had,
a relevant relationship with both companies, or

12.2.57C.1.b

an application has been made for the registration of that company and, if it
is registered, there will on its incorporation be a person who has, or has
had, a relevant relationship with both companies.

12.2.57C.2

But subsection  (1)  does not prevent the registration of the company by any
name approved by the Secretary of State.

12.2.57C.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  it is irrelevant whether the person has,
or has had, a relevant relationship with both companies at the same time.

12.2.57C.4

For the purposes of this section a person has a “relevant relationship” with a
company if the person is—

12.2.57C.4.a

an officer, or

12.2.57C.4.b

a member or former member.

12.2.57C.5

In subsection  (1) —

12.2.57C.5.a

the reference to the name of a company being changed following a direction
under a particular section includes a case where a new name is determined for
the company under section  76D  because of its failure to comply with the
direction;

12.2.57C.5.b

the reference to the name of a company being changed following an order under
section 73 includes a case where a new name is determined for the company
under section 73(4) because of its failure to comply with an order.

12.3

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph  (bc)  (inserted by section 11 of this Act) insert—

12.3.bd

section  57C  (names that another company has been directed to change);

.

##### Directions to change name: period for compliance

13

13.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows

13.2

In section 64 (power to direct change of name in case of company ceasing to be
entitled to exemption), after subsection (2) insert—

13.2.2A

The period must be a period of at least 28 days beginning with the date of the
direction.

13.2.2B

The Secretary of State may by further direction in writing extend the period.

Any such direction must be given before the end of the period for the time
being specified.

13.3

In section 68 (direction to change name in case of similarity to existing
name: supplementary provisions), after subsection (2) insert—

13.3.2A

The period must be a period of at least 28 days beginning with the date of the
direction.

13.4

In section 75 (provision of misleading information etc), after subsection (2)
insert—

13.4.2A

The period must be at least 28 days beginning with the date of the direction.

13.5

In section 76 (misleading indication of activities)—

13.5.a

for subsections (2) and (3) substitute—

13.5.a.2

The direction must be in writing and must specify the period within which the
company is to change its name.

13.5.a.3

The period must be a period of at least 28 days beginning with the date of the
direction.

13.5.a.3A

The Secretary of State may by further direction in writing extend the period.

Any such direction must be given before the end of the period for the time
being specified.

;

13.5.b

for subsection (4) substitute—

13.5.b.4

A company may apply to the court to set aside a direction under subsection
(1).

13.5.b.4A

Any application under subsection  (4)  must be made within the period of three
weeks beginning with the date of the direction.

13.5.c

after subsection (5) insert—

13.5.c.5A

If a company applies to the court under subsection (4) to set aside a
direction, it is not required to comply with the direction while the
proceedings are ongoing.

;

13.5.d

in subsection (6), for “this section” substitute  “subsection (1)” .

##### Requirements to change name: removal of old name from public inspection

14

14.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

14.2

In section 64 (company ceasing to be entitled to exemption in relation to use
of “limited” etc), after subsection (6) insert—

14.2.6A

Where a direction is given under subsection (1), the registrar may omit from
the material on the register that is available for public inspection any
mention of the name to which the direction relates.

14.3

In section 67 (power to direct change of name in case of similarity to
existing name), after subsection (1) insert—

14.3.1A

Where a direction is given under subsection (1), the registrar may omit from
the material on the register that is available for public inspection any
mention of the name to which the direction relates (so far as it relates to
the company to which the direction is given).

14.4

In section 73 (order requiring name to be changed), after subsection (6)
insert—

14.4.7

Where an order is made under subsection (1), the registrar may omit from the
material on the register that is available for public inspection any mention
of the name to which the order relates.

14.5

In section 75 (provision of misleading information), after subsection (4)
insert—

14.5.4A

Where a direction is given under subsection (1), the registrar may omit from
the material on the register that is available for public inspection any
mention of the name to which the direction relates.

14.6

In section 76 (misleading indication of activities), after subsection (5A)
(inserted by section 13 of this Act) insert—

14.6.5B

Where a direction is given under subsection (1), the registrar may omit from
the material on the register that is available for public inspection any
mention of the name to which the direction relates.

##### Objections to company’s registered name

15

15.1

Section 69 of the Companies Act 2006 (objection to company’s registered name)
is amended as follows.

15.2

In subsection (1)(b)—

15.2.a

after “in the United Kingdom” insert  “or elsewhere” ;

15.2.b

after “mislead” insert  “members of the public in the United Kingdom or
elsewhere” .

15.3

In subsection (3), for the second sentence substitute  “Any of the following
may be joined as respondents—

15.3.a

any member or person who was a member at the time at which the name was
registered;

15.3.b

any director or person who was a director at the time at which the name was
registered.”

15.4

In subsection (4), omit paragraph (b) (and the “or” at the end of that
paragraph).

15.5

In subsection (5), omit “, (b)”.

##### Misleading indication of activities

16

In section 76 of the Companies Act 2006 (misleading indication of activities),
in subsection (1), for “be likely to cause harm to the public” substitute
“pose a risk of harm to the public in the United Kingdom or elsewhere” .

##### Direction to change name used for criminal purposes

17

17.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

17.2

Before section 75 insert—

Provision of misleading information

.

17.3

Before section 76 insert—

Misleading indication of activities and names used for criminal purposes

.

17.4

After section 76 insert—

########### Power to direct change of name used for criminal purposes

17.4.76A

17.4.76A.1

The Secretary of State may direct a company to change its name if it appears
to the Secretary of State that the name has been used, or is intended to be
used, by the company to facilitate—

17.4.76A.1.a

the commission of an offence involving dishonesty or deception, or

17.4.76A.1.b

the carrying out of conduct that, if carried out in any part of the United
Kingdom, would amount to such an offence.

17.4.76A.2

The direction must be in writing and must specify the period within which the
company is to change its name.

17.4.76A.3

The period must be a period of at least 28 days beginning with the date of the
direction.

17.4.76A.4

The Secretary of State may by further direction in writing extend the period.

Any such direction must be given before the end of the period for the time
being specified.

17.4.76A.5

A company may apply to the court to set aside a direction under subsection
(1) .

17.4.76A.6

Any application under subsection  (5)  must be made within the period of three
weeks beginning with the date of the direction.

17.4.76A.7

On an application under subsection  (5)  the court may set the direction aside
or confirm it.

17.4.76A.8

If on an application under subsection  (5)  the direction is confirmed, the
court must specify the period within which the direction is to be complied
with.

17.4.76A.9

Where a direction is given under subsection  (1) , the registrar may omit from
the material on the register that is available for public inspection any
mention of the name to which the direction relates.

17.4.76A.10

If a company applies to the court under subsection  (5)  to set aside a
direction, the company is not required to comply with the direction while the
proceedings are ongoing.

17.4.76A.11

If a company fails to comply with a direction under subsection  (1) , an
offence is committed by—

17.4.76A.11.a

the company, and

17.4.76A.11.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

For this purpose a shadow director is treated as an officer of the company.

17.4.76A.12

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale and, for
continued contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-tenth of level
3 on the standard scale.

17.5

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph (f) insert—

17.5.g

section  76A  (power to direct change of name used for criminal purposes);

.

##### Direction to change name wrongly registered

18

18.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

18.2

After section  76A  (inserted by section 17 of this Act) insert—

########### Direction to change name wrongly registered

############ Direction to change name wrongly registered

18.2.76B

18.2.76B.1

The Secretary of State may direct a company to change its name if—

18.2.76B.1.a

it appears to the Secretary of State that the company’s registration by that
name was in contravention of any requirement imposed by this Part, or

18.2.76B.1.b

the Secretary of State did not, at the time at which the name was registered,
form the opinion mentioned in section 53,  56A  or  57A , but had proper
grounds for doing so.

18.2.76B.2

The direction must be in writing and must specify the period within which the
company is to change its name.

18.2.76B.3

The period must be a period of at least 28 days beginning with the date of the
direction.

18.2.76B.4

The Secretary of State may by further direction in writing extend the period.

Any such direction must be given before the end of the period for the time
being specified.

18.2.76B.5

A company may apply to the court to set aside a direction under subsection
(1) .

18.2.76B.6

Any application under subsection  (5)  must be made within the period of three
weeks beginning with the date of the direction.

18.2.76B.7

On an application under subsection  (5)  the court may set the direction aside
or confirm it.

18.2.76B.8

If on an application under subsection  (5)  the direction is confirmed, the
court must specify the period within which the direction is to be complied
with.

18.2.76B.9

Where a direction is given under subsection  (1) , the registrar may omit from
the material on the register that is available for public inspection any
mention of the name to which the direction relates.

18.2.76B.10

If a company applies to the court under subsection  (5)  to set aside a
direction, the company is not required to comply with the direction while the
proceedings are ongoing.

18.2.76B.11

If a company fails to comply with a direction under subsection  (1) , an
offence is committed by—

18.2.76B.11.a

the company, and

18.2.76B.11.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

For this purpose a shadow director is treated as an officer of the company.

18.2.76B.12

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale and, for
continued contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-tenth of level
3 on the standard scale.

18.3

In section 1047 (registered name of overseas company), in subsection (4),
after paragraph (g) (inserted by section 17 of this Act) insert—

18.3.h

section  76B  (direction to change name wrongly registered);

.

##### Registrar’s power to change names containing computer code

19

19.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows

19.2

In the heading of Chapter 4 of Part 5, after “Secretary of State” insert  “and
the registrar” .

19.3

After section  76B  (inserted by section 18 of this Act) insert—

########### Registrar’s powers to change names

############ Registrar’s power to change name containing computer code

19.3.76C

19.3.76C.1

Where, in the opinion of the registrar, a company’s registered name consists
of or includes computer code, the registrar may—

19.3.76C.1.a

determine a new name for the company, and

19.3.76C.1.b

remove from the register any reference to the company’s old name.

19.3.76C.2

If the registrar determines a new name for a company under this section, the
registrar must—

19.3.76C.2.a

give the company notice of the determination, and

19.3.76C.2.b

place a note of the determination in the register.

19.3.76C.3

Where a company is given a direction under section  76B  to change its name—

19.3.76C.3.a

that does not affect the registrar’s power to act under subsection  (1) , but

19.3.76C.3.b

if the registrar does so, the direction lapses.

19.4

In section 1081 (annotation of the register), in subsection (6), after
“subsection (2)” insert  “or of any other enactment” .

##### Registrar’s power to change company’s name for breach of direction

20

After section  76C  of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by section 19 of this
Act) insert—

######### Registrar’s power to change name for failure to comply with direction

20.76D

20.76D.1

Where a company fails to comply with a direction to change its name, the
registrar may determine a new name for the company.

20.76D.2

The reference in subsection  (1)  to a direction to change a company’s name is
to a direction under section 64, 67, 75, 76,  76A  or  76B .

20.76D.3

If the registrar determines a new name for a company under this section, the
registrar must—

20.76D.3.a

give the company notice of the determination, and

20.76D.3.b

place a note of the determination in the register.

##### Company names: exceptions based on national security etc

22

After section  76D  of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by section 20 of this
Act) insert—

######### Exceptions

########## Exceptions based on national security etc

22.76E

22.76E.1

Nothing in this Part prevents the registration of a company under this Act by
a name if the Secretary of State is satisfied that the registration of the
company by that name is necessary—

22.76E.1.a

in the interests of national security, or

22.76E.1.b

for the purposes of preventing or detecting serious crime.

22.76E.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(b) —

22.76E.2.a

“ crime ” means conduct which—

22.76E.2.a.i

constitutes a criminal offence, or

22.76E.2.a.ii

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute a criminal offence, and

22.76E.2.b

crime is “serious” if—

22.76E.2.b.i

the offence which is or would be constituted by the conduct is an offence for
which the maximum sentence (in any part of the United Kingdom) is imprisonment
for 3 years or more, or

22.76E.2.b.ii

the conduct involves the use of violence, results in substantial financial
gain or is conduct by a large number of persons in pursuit of a common
purpose.

#### Business names

##### Use of name suggesting connection with foreign governments etc

23

In the Companies Act 2006, after section 1196 insert—

######### Names suggesting connection with foreign governments etc

23.1196A

23.1196A.1

A person must not carry on business in the United Kingdom under a name that
would be likely to give the false impression that the business is connected
with—

23.1196A.1.a

a foreign government or an agency or authority of a foreign government, or

23.1196A.1.b

an international organisation whose members include two or more countries or
territories (or their governments).

23.1196A.2

A person who contravenes this section commits an offence.

23.1196A.3

Where an offence under this section is committed by a body corporate, an
offence is also committed by every officer of the body who is in default.

23.1196A.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale and, for
continued contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-tenth of level
3 on the standard scale.

##### Use of name giving misleading indication of activities

24

In section 1198 of the Companies Act 2006 (misleading indication of
activities), in subsection (1), for “be likely to cause harm to the public”
substitute  “pose a risk of harm to the public in the United Kingdom or
elsewhere” .

##### Use of name that a company has been required to change

25

25.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

25.2

In section 1192 (application of this Chapter), at the beginning of subsection
(1) insert  “Subject to any express provision to the contrary,” .

25.3

After section 1198 insert—

########### Restrictions where a company has been required to change a name

############ Name that a company has been required to change

25.3.1198A

25.3.1198A.1

Where a relevant direction has been given to a company to change its name, or
it has been ordered under section 73 to change its name, the company must not
carry on business in the United Kingdom under the name that it was directed or
ordered to change, except as mentioned in subsection  (2) .

25.3.1198A.2

Subsection  (1)  does not prevent the use by a company of a name if—

25.3.1198A.2.a

the period for complying with the direction or order has not yet expired,

25.3.1198A.2.b

the company complied with the direction or order and has since become
registered with the name again following approval given under section  57B ,
or

25.3.1198A.2.c

the direction was given, or the order was made, before section 25 of the
Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023 came fully into force.

25.3.1198A.3

If a company uses a name in contravention of this section an offence is
committed by—

25.3.1198A.3.a

the company, and

25.3.1198A.3.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

25.3.1198A.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale and, for
continued contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-tenth of level
3 on the standard scale.

25.3.1198A.5

In this section—

“ company ” includes an overseas company; “ relevant direction ” means a
direction under section 67, 75, 76,  76A  or  76B , other than a direction
under section  76B (1)(b)  given on the basis that, at the time at which a
company’s name was registered, the Secretary of State had proper grounds for
forming the opinion mentioned in section  57A .

##### Use of name that another company has been required to change

26

After section 1198A of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by section 25 of this
Act) insert—

######### Name that another company has been required to change

26.1198B

26.1198B.1

Where a relevant direction has been given to a company to change its name, or
it has been ordered under section 73 to change its name, another company must
not carry on business in the United Kingdom under the name that the first
company was directed or ordered to change if there is a person who has, or has
had, a relevant relationship with both companies.

26.1198B.2

Subsection  (1)  does not prevent the use by a company of a name if—

26.1198B.2.a

it is registered under this Act by that name,

26.1198B.2.b

the period for complying with the direction or order has not yet expired, or

26.1198B.2.c

the direction was given, or the order was made, before section 26 of the
Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023 came fully into force.

26.1198B.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  it is irrelevant whether the person has,
or has had, a relevant relationship with both companies at the same time.

26.1198B.4

For the purposes of this section a person has a “relevant relationship” with a
company if the person is—

26.1198B.4.a

an officer, or

26.1198B.4.b

a member or former member.

26.1198B.5

If a company uses a name in contravention of this section an offence is
committed by—

26.1198B.5.a

the company, and

26.1198B.5.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

26.1198B.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale and, for
continued contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-tenth of level
3 on the standard scale.

26.1198B.7

In this section—

“ company ” includes an overseas company; “ relevant direction ” means a
direction under section 67, 75,  76A  or  76B , other than a direction under
section  76B (1)(b)  given on the basis that, at the time at which a company’s
name was registered, the Secretary of State had proper grounds for forming the
opinion mentioned in section  57A .

##### Use of names: exceptions based on national security etc

######### Exceptions based on national security etc

27.1199A.1

The Secretary of State may, by written notice given to a person, provide that
a prohibition imposed by this Chapter does not apply in relation to the
carrying on of a business by that person under a name specified in the notice,
if satisfied that to do so is necessary—

27.1199A.1.a

in the interests of national security, or

27.1199A.1.b

for the purposes of preventing or detecting serious crime.

27.1199A.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(b) —

27.1199A.2.a

“ crime ” means conduct which—

27.1199A.2.a.i

constitutes a criminal offence, or

27.1199A.2.a.ii

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute a criminal offence, and

27.1199A.2.b

crime is “serious” if—

27.1199A.2.b.i

the offence which is or would be constituted by the conduct is an offence for

27.1199A.2.b.ii

#### Registered offices

##### Registered office: appropriate address

28

28.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

28.2

In section 9 (registration documents), in subsection (5)(a), at the end insert
“, which must be an appropriate address within the meaning given by section
86 (2) ” .

28.3

For section 86 substitute—

########### Duty to ensure registered office at appropriate address

28.3.86

28.3.86.1

A company must ensure that its registered office is at all times at an
appropriate address.

28.3.86.2

An address is an “appropriate address” if, in the ordinary course of events—

28.3.86.2.a

a document addressed to the company, and delivered there by hand or by post,
would be expected to come to the attention of a person acting on behalf of the
company, and

28.3.86.2.b

the delivery of documents there is capable of being recorded by the obtaining
of an acknowledgement of delivery.

28.3.86.3

If a company fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with this section an
offence is committed by—

28.3.86.3.a

the company, and

28.3.86.3.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

28.3.86.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

28.3.86.4.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

28.3.86.4.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

28.3.86.5

Subsection  (1)  does not apply in relation to a company during any period for
which the address of its registered office is a default address nominated by
virtue of section 1097A(3)(h).

28.4

In section 87 (change of address of registered office), after subsection (1)
insert—

28.4.1A

The notice must include a statement that the new address is an appropriate
address within the meaning given by section  86 (2) .

28.5

In section 853B (duties to notify a relevant event), omit paragraph (a).

28.6

After section 853C insert—

########### Duty to notify a change in registered office

28.6.853CA

28.6.853CA.1

This section applies where—

28.6.853CA.1.a

a company makes a confirmation statement,

28.6.853CA.1.b

the company’s registered office is not at an appropriate address within the
meaning given by section  86 (2) , and

28.6.853CA.1.c

the company has not given a notice under section 87 (change of registered
office) that is awaiting registration by the registrar.

28.6.853CA.2

The company must deliver a notice under section 87 at the same time as it
delivers the confirmation statement.

##### Registered email addresses etc

29

29.1

29.2.aa

a statement of the intended registered email address of the company, which

(2) ;

.

insert  “, registered email address” .

In the heading to Part 6 (a company’s registered office), after “registered
office” insert  “and email address” .

29.5

After section 88 insert—

########### Registered email address

############ Duty to maintain a registered email address

29.5.88A

29.5.88A.1

A company must ensure that its registered email address is at all times an
appropriate email address.

29.5.88A.2

An email address is an “appropriate email address” if, in the ordinary course
of events, emails sent to it by the registrar would be expected to come to the
attention of a person acting on behalf of the company.

29.5.88A.3

If a company fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with this section an
offence is committed by—

29.5.88A.3.a

the company, and

29.5.88A.3.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

29.5.88A.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

29.5.88A.4.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

29.5.88A.4.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

############ Change of registered email address

29.5.88B

29.5.88B.1

A company may change its registered email address by giving notice to the
registrar.

29.5.88B.2

The notice must include a statement that the new address is an appropriate
email address within the meaning given by section  88A (2) .

29.5.88B.3

The change takes effect upon the notice being registered by the registrar.

29.6

After section  853CA  (inserted by section 28 of this Act) insert—

########### Duty to notify a change in registered email address

29.6.853CB

29.6.853CB.1

This section applies where—

29.6.853CB.1.a

a company makes a confirmation statement,

29.6.853CB.1.b

the company’s registered email address is not an appropriate email address
within the meaning given by section  88A (2) , and

29.6.853CB.1.c

the company has not given a notice under section  88B  (change of registered
email address) that is awaiting registration by the registrar.

29.6.853CB.2

The company must deliver a notice under section  88B  at the same time as it
delivers the confirmation statement.

29.7

In section 1087 (material not available for public inspection), in subsection
(1), before paragraph (a) insert—

29.7.za

an email address delivered to the registrar under—

29.7.za.i

section 9(5) (aa)  or  88B  (initial registered email address and change of
address);

29.7.za.ii

section 30 of the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023
(company’s registered email address: transitional provision);

.

29.8

In section 1115 (supplementary provisions relating to electronic
communications), omit subsection (1).

29.9

In Schedule 4 (documents and information sent or supplied to a company)—

29.9.a

after Part 2 insert—

############# Communications in electronic form from the registrar or the Secretary of State

29.9.a.4A

29.9.a.4A.1

A document or information is validly sent or supplied to a company by the
registrar or the Secretary of State if it is sent or supplied in electronic
form in accordance with sub-paragraph  (2)  or  (3) .

29.9.a.4A.2

Where the document or information is sent or supplied by electronic means it
may only be sent—

29.9.a.4A.2.a

in the case of a company registered under this Act, to the company’s
registered email address;

29.9.a.4A.2.b

in the case of any company, to an address specified by the company for that
purpose (generally or specifically).

29.9.a.4A.3

Where the document or information is sent or supplied in electronic form by
hand or by post, it must be sent or supplied to an address to which it could
be validly sent if it were in hard copy form.

;

29.9.b

in the heading of Part 3, at the end insert  “in other cases” ;

29.9.c

in paragraph 5, after “company” insert  “by a person other than the registrar
or the Secretary of State” .

##### Registered email addresses: transitional provision

30

30.1

This section applies in relation to a company registered under the Companies
Act 2006 in pursuance of an application for registration delivered to the
registrar before section 29 (2)  comes fully into force.

30.2

On the first occasion on which the company delivers a confirmation statement
with a confirmation date that is after the day on which section 29 (2)  comes
fully into force—

30.2.a

it must, at the same time, deliver to the registrar a statement specifying its
registered email address for the purposes of section  88A  of that Act
(inserted by section 29 of this Act);

30.2.b

section  853CB  of that Act (inserted by section 29 of this Act) does not
apply.

30.3

Section 853A(1) (b)(ii)  of the Companies Act 2006 (as substituted by section
59 of this Act) has effect as if it included a reference to the duty imposed
by subsection  (2)  (and section 853L of that Act applies accordingly).

30.4

Section  88A  of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by section 29 of this Act)
does not apply in relation to the company until it has delivered the
confirmation statement mentioned in subsection  (2)  or, if it does not
deliver the statement on time, the latest time by which it was required to do
so.

30.5

In this section—

“ confirmation statement ” has the meaning given by section 853A of the
Companies Act 2006; “ the registrar ” has the meaning given by section 1060(3)
of the Companies Act 2006.

##### Power to impose director disqualification sanctions

35

35.1

impose director disqualification sanctions (see section  3A );

.

########### Director disqualification sanctions

35.3.3A

35.3.3A.1

For the purposes of section 1(5) (aa)  regulations “impose director
disqualification sanctions” if they provide for designated persons (see
section 9) to be persons subject to director disqualification sanctions for
the purposes of—

35.3.3A.1.a

section 11A of the Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986, and

35.3.3A.1.b

Article 15A of the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order
2002.

35.3.3A.2

As to the effect of such provision, see—

35.3.3A.2.a

section 11A of the Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986, and

35.3.3A.2.b

Article 15A of the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order
2002.

35.5

35.5.3A

Where regulations provide for designated persons to be persons subject to
director disqualification sanctions for the purposes of section 11A of the
Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986 and Article 15A of the Company
Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002, the regulations may—

35.5.3A.a

create exceptions from subsection (1) of that section or paragraph (1) of that
Article;

35.5.3A.b

confer power on an appropriate Minister to issue a licence to authorise a
designated person to do anything that would otherwise be prohibited by
subsection (1) of that section or paragraph (1) of that Article.

35.5.3B

Regulations may, as respects any licences provided for under subsection  (3A)
, make any provision mentioned (in relation to licences) in subsection (3).

##### Disqualification of persons designated under sanctions legislation: GB

36

36.1

The Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986 is amended as follows.

36.2

After section 11 insert—

########### Designated persons under sanctions legislation

36.2.11A

36.2.11A.1

It is an offence for a person who is subject to director disqualification
sanctions to act as a director of a company or directly or indirectly to take
part in or be concerned in the promotion, formation or management of a company
(but see subsection  (2) ).

36.2.11A.2

Subsection  (1)  does not apply—

36.2.11A.2.a

to the extent that an exception from subsection (1) has been created by virtue
of section 15(3A) of the Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018, or

36.2.11A.2.b

to anything done under the authority of a licence issued by virtue of section
15(3A) of that Act.

36.2.11A.3

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that they did not know and could not reasonably have been expected to
know that they were subject to director disqualification sanctions at the time
at which they engaged in that conduct.

36.2.11A.4

In this section “ person who is subject to director disqualification sanctions
” means a person who under regulations under section 1 of the Sanctions and
Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 is a person subject to director
disqualification sanctions for the purposes of this section and Article 15A of
the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 (see
section 3A of the Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018).

36.3

In section 13 (criminal penalties), after “section 11” insert  “or  11A ” .

36.4

In section 14 (offences by body corporate), for subsection (1) substitute—

36.4.1

Where—

36.4.1.a

a body corporate is—

36.4.1.a.i

guilty of an offence of acting in contravention of a disqualification order or
disqualification undertaking or in contravention of section 12A or 12B, or

36.4.1.a.ii

guilty of an offence under section 11A, and

36.4.1.b

it is proved that the offence occurred with the consent or connivance of, or
was attributable to any neglect on the part of any director, manager,
secretary or other similar officer of the body corporate, or any person who
was purporting to act in any such capacity,

the person, as well as the body corporate, is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

36.5

In section 15 (personal liability for company’s debts where person acts while
disqualified)—

36.5.a

in subsection (1)(a), after “section 11” insert  “,  11A ” ;

36.5.b

omit the “or” at the end of subsection (1)(a);

36.5.c

after subsection (1)(b) insert

, or

36.5.c.c

as a person who is involved in the management of the company, they act or are
willing to act on instructions where—

36.5.c.c.i

the instructions are given by a person whom they know at that time to be
subject to director disqualification sanctions (within the meaning of section
11A),

36.5.c.c.ii

the giving of the instructions does not fall within any exception from section
11A(1) created by virtue of section 15(3A) of the Sanctions and Anti-Money
Laundering Act 2018, and

36.5.c.c.iii

the instructions are not authorised,

(but see subsection (3A)).

;

36.5.d

in subsection (3)(b), after “(b)” insert  “or (c)” ;

36.5.e

after subsection (3) insert—

36.5.e.3A

But—

36.5.e.3A.a

a person who is subject to director disqualification sanctions (within the
meaning of section 11A) is not personally responsible under subsection (1)(a)
for any relevant debts of the company incurred at a time when the person did
not know and could not reasonably have been expected to know that they were
subject to director disqualification sanctions;

36.5.e.3A.b

a person is not personally responsible under subsection (1)(c) for any
relevant debts of the company incurred at a time when the person reasonably
believed that the instructions were authorised.

;

36.5.f

after subsection (5) insert—

36.5.f.6

Subsection  (7)  applies where a person (“ P ”) at any time—

36.5.f.6.a

was involved in the management of a company, and

36.5.f.6.b

acted on instructions where—

36.5.f.6.b.i

the instructions were given by a person (“ D ”) whom P knew at that time to be
subject to director disqualification sanctions (within the meaning of section
11A),

36.5.f.6.b.ii

the giving of the instructions did not fall within any exception from section
11A(1) created by virtue of section 15(3A) of the Sanctions and Anti-Money
Laundering Act 2018, and

36.5.f.6.b.iii

the instructions were not authorised,

unless P reasonably believed at that time that the instructions were
authorised.

36.5.f.7

For the purposes of this section P is presumed, unless the contrary is shown,
to have been willing at any time thereafter to act on any instructions given
by D.

36.5.f.8

For the purposes of this section instructions are “authorised” if they are
given under the authority of a licence issued by virtue of section 15(3A) of
the Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018.

36.6

In section 18 (register of disqualification orders and undertakings), in
subsection (2A), after paragraph (c) insert—

36.6.d

persons who are subject to director disqualification sanctions within the
meaning of section 11A;

36.6.e

any licences issued by virtue of section 15(3A) of the Sanctions and Anti-
Money Laundering Act 2018.

36.7

In section 21 (interaction with Insolvency Act), in subsection (4), after
“section 11” insert  “,  11A ” .

#### Directors

##### Disqualified directors

40

40.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

40.2

After section 159 insert—

########### Disqualified person not to be appointed as director

40.2.159A

40.2.159A.1

A person may not be appointed a director of a company if the person is
disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see subsection
(2) ).

40.2.159A.2

In the table—

40.2.159A.2.a

Part 1 defines “ disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation
” for the purposes of provisions of this Act so far as relating to—

40.2.159A.2.a.i

a company registered in England and Wales or Scotland, or

40.2.159A.2.a.ii

the delivery of a document to the registrar of companies for England and Wales
or Scotland or a statement contained in such a document;

40.2.159A.2.b

Part 2 defines “ disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation
” for the purposes of provisions of this Act so far as relating to—

40.2.159A.2.b.i

a company registered in Northern Ireland, or

40.2.159A.2.b.ii

the delivery of a document to the registrar of companies for Northern Ireland
or a statement contained in such a document.

For those purposes a person (P) is disqualified under the directors
disqualification legislation if: Except in the application of the provision in
relation to P acting in a capacity, or doing anything, for which P has the
permission of a court or the authority of a licence, or in respect of which an
exception applies, by virtue of: Part 1: England and Wales and Scotland P is
subject to a disqualification order or undertaking under the Company Directors
Disqualification Act 1986. Section 1(1), 1A(1) or 9B(4) of the 1986 Act. Any
of the circumstances mentioned in section 11 of the Company Directors
Disqualification Act 1986 (bankruptcy etc) apply to P. Section 11 of the 1986
Act. P is subject to director disqualification sanctions within the meaning of
section 11A of the Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986. Section 15(3A)
of the Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 (exceptions and licences).
Section 12 of the Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986 (disabilities on
revocation of administration order against an individual) applies to P.
Section 12 of the 1986 Act. P is subject to a disqualification order or
undertaking mentioned in section 12A or 12B of the Company Directors
Disqualification Act 1986 (recognition of Northern Ireland disqualification
orders and undertakings). Section 12A or 12B of the 1986 Act. P is
disqualified as mentioned in section 1184(2)(a) or (b) or is subject to a
disqualification undertaking under section 1184(3). Section 1184(5). Part 2:
Northern Ireland P is subject to a disqualification order or undertaking under
the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 (
S.I.2002/3150 (N.I. 4) ). Article 3(1), 4(1) or 13B(4) of the 2002 Order. Any
of the circumstances mentioned in Article 15 of the Company Directors
Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 (bankruptcy etc) apply to P.
Article 15 of the 2002 Order. P is subject to director disqualification
sanctions within the meaning of Article 15A of the Company Directors
Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002. Section 15(3A) of the
Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 (exceptions and licences).
Article 16 of the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order
2002 (disabilities on revocation of administration order against an
individual) applies to P. Article 16 of the 2002 Order. P is subject to a
disqualification order or undertaking mentioned in Article 17 of the Company
Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 (recognition of GB
disqualification orders and undertakings). Article 17 of the 2002 Order. P is
disqualified as mentioned in section 1184(2)(a) or (b) or is subject to a
disqualification undertaking under section 1184(3). Section 1184(5).

40.2.159A.3

An appointment made in contravention of this section is void.

40.2.159A.4

Nothing in this section affects any liability of a person under any provision
of the Companies Acts or any other enactment if the person—

40.2.159A.4.a

purports to act as director, or

40.2.159A.4.b

acts as shadow director,

although the person could not, by virtue of this section, be validly appointed
as a director.

40.3

After section 169 insert—

########### Removal from office of disqualified directors

40.3.169A

40.3.169A.1

A person who has been appointed as a director of a company ceases to hold
office by virtue of that appointment if the person becomes disqualified under
the directors disqualification legislation (see section  159A (2) ).

40.3.169A.2

Nothing in this section affects any liability of a person under any provision
of the Companies Acts or any other enactment, if, having ceased to hold office
by virtue of subsection  (1) , the person—

40.3.169A.2.a

purports to act as director, or

40.3.169A.2.b

acts as shadow director.

40.3.169A.3

In relation to a person appointed as a director of a company before the time
when this section comes into force, the reference in subsection  (1)  to a
person who becomes disqualified includes a reference to a person who, at that
time, is already disqualified.

40.4

In Schedule 8 (index of defined expressions), at the appropriate place insert—

disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation section  159A
(2)

.

##### Prohibition on director acting unless ID verified

43

After section  167L  of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by Schedule 2 to this
Act) insert—

######### Directors: duties relating to ID verification and notification

########## Prohibition on director acting unless ID verified

43.167M

43.167M.1

An individual must not act as a director of a company unless the individual’s
identity is verified (see section 1110A).

43.167M.2

A company must ensure that an individual does not act as a director unless the
individual’s identity is verified (see section 1110A).

43.167M.3

A person who contravenes subsection  (1)  commits an offence.

43.167M.4

If a company contravenes subsection  (2)  an offence is committed by—

43.167M.4.a

the company, and

43.167M.4.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

For this purpose a shadow director is treated as an officer of the company.

43.167M.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

43.167M.5.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

43.167M.5.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

43.167M.6

The only consequences of contravening subsections  (1)  and  (2)  are the
offences provided for by this section (so that, for example, a contravention
does not in any way affect the validity of an individual’s acts as a
director).

##### Prohibition on acting unless directorship notified

44

After section  167M  of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by section 43 of this
Act) insert—

######### Prohibition on acting unless directorship notified

44.167N

44.167N.1

This section applies where—

44.167N.1.a

a person has become a director of a company otherwise than on its
incorporation, and

44.167N.1.b

notice under section  167G  of the person having done so has not been given
within the period mentioned in subsection  (6)  of that section.

44.167N.2

The person may not act as a director of the company until notice is given
under section  167G .

44.167N.3

A person who contravenes subsection  (2)  commits an offence.

44.167N.4

Where the offence is committed by a firm, every officer of the firm who is in
default also commits the offence.

44.167N.5

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that they reasonably believed that notice had been given under section
167G .

44.167N.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

44.167N.6.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

44.167N.6.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

44.167N.7

The only consequence of a contravention of subsection  (2)  is the offence
provided for by this section (so that, for example, a contravention does not
in any way affect the validity of a person’s acts as a director).

##### Registrar’s power to change a director’s service address

45

For section 246 of the Companies Act 2006 substitute—

######### Putting the address on the public record

45.246

45.246.1

If the registrar decides in accordance with section 245 that a director‘s
usual residential address is to be put on the public record, the registrar
must proceed as if each relevant company had given notice under section 167H—

45.246.1.a

stating a change in the director’s service address, and

45.246.1.b

stating the director’s usual residential address as their new service address.

45.246.2

The registrar must give notice of having done so—

45.246.2.a

to the director, and

45.246.2.b

to every relevant company.

45.246.3

The notice must state the date of the registrar’s decision to put the
director’s usual residential address on the public record.

45.246.4

Where a director’s usual residential address has been put on the public record
by the registrar under this section, for the period of five years beginning
with the date of the registrar’s decision no service address may be registered
for the director other than their usual residential address (but see
subsection (5)).

45.246.5

Subsection (4)—

45.246.5.a

does not limit the service address that may be registered for the director
under regulations under section  1097B  (rectification of register), and

45.246.5.b

ceases to apply in relation to the director if a new service address is
registered for the director under those regulations.

45.246.6

In this section “ relevant company ” means each company given notice under
section 245(2)(b).

the required information (see sections  113A  and  113B ), and

46.4.a.2.b

the date on which the person was registered as a member.

46.4.a.2A

Where a person ceases to be a member there must be entered in the register the
date at which the person’s membership ceased.

;

46.4.b

in subsection (3), omit “, with the names and addresses of the members,”;

46.4.c

in subsection (5), after “show a single” insert  “service” ;

46.4.d

in subsection (6), omit “, with the names and addresses of the members,”;

46.4.e

after subsection (6) insert—

46.4.e.6A

Where any of the information required to be entered in a company’s register of
members changes and, at the time of the change, it is a non-traded company—

46.4.e.6A.a

the fact that the information has changed does not relieve the company from
the obligation to include the old information in the register if it has not
already done so,

46.4.e.6A.b

the old information must be retained in the register until its removal is
authorised by section 121 or by court order under section 125, and

46.4.e.6A.c

a note must be included in the register recording the date on which the
information changed and the date on which the change was entered in the
register.

46.4.e.6B

Where any of the information required to be entered in a company’s register of
members changes and, at the time of the change, it is a traded company, the
company is not required to include or retain the old information in the
register.

46.4.e.6C

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

46.4.e.6C.a

amend subsection (6A) so as to provide for it to apply in relation to traded
companies, and

46.4.e.6C.b

repeal subsection  (6B)  in consequence.

46.4.e.6D

Regulations under subsection  (6C)  are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

;

46.4.f

in subsection (7), after “If” insert  “, without reasonable excuse,” ;

46.4.g

after subsection (8) insert—

46.4.g.9

In this section—

“ non-traded company ” means a company that is not a traded company; “
relevant market ” has the meaning given by section 853E(6); “ traded company ”
means a company any of whose shares are admitted to trading on a relevant
market or on any other market which is outside the United Kingdom.

46.5

After section 113 insert—

########### Required information about members: individuals

46.5.113A

46.5.113A.1

The required information about a member who is an individual is—

46.5.113A.1.a

name;

46.5.113A.1.b

a service address.

46.5.113A.2

In this section “ name ” means forename and surname.

46.5.113A.3

Where a member is a peer or an individual usually known by a title—

46.5.113A.3.a

any requirement imposed by section  113D  or  113E , or by a notice under
section  113F , to provide their name may be satisfied by providing their
title instead;

46.5.113A.3.b

the title may be entered in the register of members instead of their forename
and surname (and references in any enactment to the name of a person entered
in a company’s register of members are to be construed accordingly).

########### Required information about members: corporate members and firms

46.5.113B

The required information about a member that is a body corporate, or a firm
that is a legal person under the law by which it is governed, is—

46.5.113B.a

corporate or firm name;

46.5.113B.b

a service address.

########### Power to amend the required information

46.5.113C

46.5.113C.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

46.5.113C.1.a

make provision changing the required information about a member for the
purposes of this Chapter;

46.5.113C.1.b

repeal section  113A (3) .

46.5.113C.2

The provision that may be made in regulations under subsection  (1)(a)
includes provision amending this Chapter.

46.5.113C.3

The consequential provision that may be made in regulations under subsection
(1)(a)  by virtue of section 1292(1) also includes provision amending section
50 of the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023.

46.5.113C.4

Regulations under subsection  (1)  are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

########### Duty on new members to notify required information

46.5.113D

46.5.113D.1

A person who becomes a member of a company must provide the company with the
required information about the member (see sections  113A  and  113B ).

46.5.113D.2

Subsection (1) does not apply if or to the extent that—

46.5.113D.2.a

the person has already provided the information to the company, or

46.5.113D.2.b

the person becomes a member of the company on its incorporation and the
information is contained in the application for the registration of the
company.

46.5.113D.3

A person must comply with this section within the period of two months
beginning with the date on which the person became a member.

########### Duty on member to notify changes to required information

46.5.113E

46.5.113E.1

A person who is a member of a company must give notice to the company of any
change in the required information about the member (see sections  113A  and
113B ).

46.5.113E.2

The notice must specify the date on which the change occurred.

46.5.113E.3

A person must comply with this section within the period of two months
beginning with the date on which the change occurred.

########### Power for company to require information from members

46.5.113F

46.5.113F.1

A company may, for the purposes of ensuring that its register of members
includes the information that it is required to include, require a member or
former member of the company to provide any of the required information about
the member or former member (see sections  113A  and  113B ).

46.5.113F.2

The notice must require the recipient to comply with it within the period of
one month beginning with the date on which the notice is given.

########### Failure to comply with section 

46.5.113G

46.5.113G.1

A person who, without reasonable excuse, fails to comply with section  113D
or  113E  commits an offence.

46.5.113G.2

A person who, without reasonable excuse, fails to comply with a notice under
section  113F  commits an offence.

46.5.113G.3

Where an offence under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  is committed by a firm, the
offence is also committed by every officer of the firm who is in default.

46.5.113G.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

46.5.113G.4.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

46.5.113G.4.b

on summary conviction—

46.5.113G.4.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

46.5.113G.4.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued contravention, a
daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory maximum;

46.5.113G.4.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued
contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory
maximum.

########### Basic false statement offences in connection with sections 

46.5.113H

46.5.113H.1

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with section  113D  or
113E  and without reasonable excuse, the person makes a statement that is
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

46.5.113H.2

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with a notice under
section  113F  and without reasonable excuse, the person makes a statement
that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

46.5.113H.3

Where an offence under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  is committed by a firm, the
offence is also committed by every officer of the firm who is in default.

46.5.113H.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

46.5.113H.4.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

46.5.113H.4.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

46.5.113H.4.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

########### Aggravated false statement offences in connection with sections 

46.5.113I

46.5.113I.1

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with section  113D  or
113E , the person makes a statement that the person knows to be misleading,
false or deceptive in a material particular.

46.5.113I.2

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with a notice under
section  113F , the person makes a statement that the person knows to be
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

46.5.113I.3

Where an offence under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  is committed by a firm, the
offence is also committed by every officer of the firm who is in default.

46.5.113I.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

46.5.113I.4.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

46.5.113I.4.b

on summary conviction—

46.5.113I.4.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

46.5.113I.4.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued contravention, a
daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory maximum;

46.5.113I.4.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued
contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory
maximum.

48.6

After section 120 of the Companies Act 2006 insert—

########### Power to make regulations protecting material

48.6.120A

48.6.120A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

48.6.120A.1.a

require a company to refrain from using, or refrain from disclosing,
individual membership information except in circumstances specified in the
regulations;

48.6.120A.1.b

confer power on the registrar, on application, to make an order requiring a
company to refrain from using, or refrain from disclosing, individual
membership information except in circumstances specified in the regulations.

48.6.120A.2

“ Individual membership information ” means information that—

48.6.120A.2.a

relates to an individual who is a member or former member of the company, and

48.6.120A.2.b

is required to be entered in the company’s register of members or index of
members’ names.

48.6.120A.3

Regulations under subsection  (1)(b)  may make provision as to—

48.6.120A.3.a

who may make an application;

48.6.120A.3.b

the grounds on which an application may be made;

48.6.120A.3.c

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application;

48.6.120A.3.d

how an application is to be determined;

48.6.120A.3.e

the notice to be given of an application and its outcome;

48.6.120A.3.f

the duration of and procedures for revoking the restrictions on use and
disclosure.

48.6.120A.4

Provision under subsection  (3)  may in particular—

48.6.120A.4.a

confer a discretion on the registrar;

48.6.120A.4.b

provide for a question to be referred to a person other than the registrar for
the purposes of determining the application or revoking the restrictions.

48.6.120A.5

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

48.6.120A.6

Nothing in this section or in regulations made under it affects the use or
disclosure of information about a person in any other capacity (for example,
the use or disclosure of information about a person in that person’s capacity
as an officer of the company).

########### Offence of failing to comply with regulations under section 

48.6.120B

48.6.120B.1

If a company contravenes a restriction on the use or disclosure of information
imposed by virtue of regulations under section  120A , an offence is committed
by—

48.6.120B.1.a

the company, and

48.6.120B.1.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

48.6.120B.2

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

48.6.120B.2.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

48.6.120B.2.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

##### Register of members: removal of option to use central register

49

49.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

49.2

Omit the following (which allow companies to keep information on the central
register instead of entering it in their local register of members)—

49.2.a

section 112A;

49.2.b

Chapter 2A of Part 8.

49.3

After section 128 insert—

########### Transitional provision where information kept on central register

49.3.128ZA

49.3.128ZA.1

Where an election is made under section 128B (option to keep information on
central register) at any time before the repeal of that section by the
Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023—

49.3.128ZA.1.a

the company must enter in its register of members all of the information that
it would have had to enter in that register if the election had never been
made (but see subsection  (2) ), and

49.3.128ZA.1.b

the duty imposed by paragraph (a) is to be treated as having been imposed by
the provision which would have required the information to be entered on the
register if the election had never been made.

49.3.128ZA.2

Where, by virtue of section 128E(3)(a), (b) or (c), information delivered to
the registrar while the election was in force did not include a date that, but
for the election, the company would have had to enter in its register of
members (a “relevant date”), the relevant date is to be treated as being the
date recorded by the registrar under section 1081(1A).

49.4

Schedule 1 contains consequential amendments.

##### Membership information: one-off statement

50

50.1

This section applies in relation to a traded company, or a non-traded company,
registered under the Companies Act 2006 before the appointed day.

50.2

On the first occasion on which the company delivers a confirmation statement
with a confirmation date that is after the appointed day it must, at the same
time, deliver to the registrar the relevant membership information.

50.3

For this purpose “ the relevant membership information ” means—

50.3.a

in relation to a traded company—

50.3.a.i

the name and address (as they appear in the company’s register of members) of
each person who, at the end of the confirmation date, held at least 5% of the
issued shares of any class of the company, and

50.3.a.ii

the number of shares of each class held by each such person at that time;

50.3.b

in relation to a non-traded company—

50.3.b.i

the name (as it appears in the company’s register of members) of every person
who was a member of the company at the end of the confirmation date, and

50.3.b.ii

the number of shares of each class held at the end of the confirmation date by
each person who was a member of the company at that time.

50.4

Section 853A(1)(b)(ii) of the Companies Act 2006 (as substituted by section 59
of this Act) has effect as if it included a reference to the duty imposed by
subsection  (2)  (and section 853L of that Act applies accordingly).

50.5

In this section—

“ confirmation statement ” has the meaning given by section 853A(1)(b) of the
Companies Act 2006; “ non-traded company ” has the meaning given by section
853F(2) of that Act; “ the appointed day ” means such day as the Secretary of
State may by regulations appoint for the purposes of this section; “ traded
company ” has the meaning given by section 853G(2) and (3) of that Act.

50.6

Other expressions used in this section have the same meaning as in Part 24 of
the Companies Act 2006.
