##### Protection of date of birth information

52

52.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

52.2

In section 1087 (material not available for public inspection), for paragraph
(da) substitute—

52.2.da

relevant date of birth information that section  1087A  provides is not to be
made available for public inspection;

.

52.3

For sections 1087A and 1087B substitute—

########### Protection of date of birth information

52.3.1087A

52.3.1087A.1

The registrar must not make available for public inspection—

52.3.1087A.1.a

so much of any document delivered to the registrar as is required to contain
relevant date of birth information;

52.3.1087A.1.b

any record of the information contained in part of a document that is
unavailable because of paragraph  (a) .

52.3.1087A.2

This section has limited application in relation to documents delivered before
it comes fully into force: see section  1087B .

52.3.1087A.3

“ Relevant date of birth information ” means—

52.3.1087A.3.a

information as to the day of the month (but not the month or year) on which a
director (or proposed director) was born;

52.3.1087A.3.b

information as to the day of the month (but not the month or year) on which a
registrable person in relation to the company was born.

52.3.1087A.4

Information about a director (or proposed director) or registrable person does
not cease to be relevant date of birth information when they cease to be a
director (or proposed director) or registrable person.

52.3.1087A.5

Subsection  (1)(b)  does not affect the availability for public inspection of
the same information contained in material derived from a part of a document
that was not required to contain the information.

52.3.1087A.6

In this section “ registrable person ”, in relation to a company, has the
meaning given by section 790C(4).

########### Protection of date of birth information in old documents

52.3.1087B

52.3.1087B.1

This section limits the extent to which section  1087A  applies in relation to
documents delivered to the registrar before that section comes fully into
force (“old documents”).

52.3.1087B.2

Section  1087A  does not apply in relation to any old documents registered
before 10 October 2015.

52.3.1087B.3

Section  1087A  does not apply in relation to any old document that is—

52.3.1087B.3.a

a statement of a company’s proposed officers delivered under section 9 in
circumstances where the subscribers gave notice of election under section 167A
(election to keep information on central register) in respect of the company’s
register of directors when the statement was delivered;

52.3.1087B.3.b

a document delivered by the company under section 167D (duty to notify
registrar of changes while election in force);

52.3.1087B.3.c

a statement of initial significant control delivered under section 9 in
circumstances where the subscribers gave notice of election under section 790X
in respect of the company when the statement was delivered;

52.3.1087B.3.d

a document containing a statement or updated statement delivered by the
company under section 790X(6)(b) or (7) (statement accompanying notice of
election made after incorporation);

52.3.1087B.3.e

a document delivered by the company under section 790ZA (duty to notify
registrar of changes while election in force).

52.3.1087B.4

Section  1087A  does not apply in relation to any old document if—

52.3.1087B.4.a

the document is—

52.3.1087B.4.a.i

a statement of proposed officers delivered under section 9, or

52.3.1087B.4.a.ii

notice given under section 167 of a person having become a director of the
company,

52.3.1087B.4.b

after the delivery of the document an election was made under section 167A in
respect of the company’s register of directors, and

52.3.1087B.4.c

the relevant date of birth information relates to a person who was a director
of the company when that election took effect.

52.3.1087B.5

References in subsections  (3)(a)  to  (e)  and  (4)(a)  to  (c)  to a
provision of this Act are to the provision as it had effect at the time at
which the document was delivered (the provisions in question were repealed by
the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023).

########### Disclosure of date of birth information

52.3.1087C

52.3.1087C.1

The registrar must not disclose relevant date of birth information except—

52.3.1087C.1.a

in accordance with subsection (2) or (3), or

52.3.1087C.1.b

as permitted by section  1110F  (general powers of disclosure by the
registrar).

52.3.1087C.2

The registrar may disclose relevant date of birth information if the
information is made available for public inspection.

52.3.1087C.3

The registrar may disclose relevant date of birth information to a credit
reference agency (as defined by section 243(7)).

52.3.1087C.4

Subsections (3) to (8) of section 243 (permitted disclosure of address
information by the registrar) apply for the purposes of subsection (3) as for
the purposes of that section (reading references there to protected
information as references to relevant date of birth information).

52.3.1087C.5

In this section “ relevant date of birth information ” has the meaning given
by section  1087A (3) .

#### Accounts and reports

##### Filing obligations of micro-entities

53

Before section 444 of the Companies Act 2006 (but after the italic heading
before that section) insert—

######### Filing obligations of micro-entities

53.443A

53.443A.1

The directors of a company that qualifies as a micro-entity in relation to a
financial year, or that would do so but for being or having been a member of
an ineligible group—

53.443A.1.a

must deliver to the registrar a copy of the company’s annual accounts, and

53.443A.1.b

may also deliver to the registrar a copy of the directors’ report.

53.443A.2

The directors must also deliver to the registrar a copy of the auditor’s
report on those accounts (and any directors’ report).

This does not apply if the company is exempt from audit and the directors have
taken advantage of that exemption.

53.443A.3

The copies of the balance sheet and any directors’ report delivered to the
registrar under this section must state the name of the person who signed it
on behalf of the board.

53.443A.4

The copy of the auditor’s report delivered to the registrar under this section
must—

53.443A.4.a

state the name of the auditor and (where the auditor is a firm) the name of
the person who signed it as senior statutory auditor, or

53.443A.4.b

if the conditions in section 506 (circumstances in which names may be omitted)
are met, state that a resolution has been passed and notified to the Secretary
of State in accordance with that section.

53.443A.5

If more than one person is appointed as auditor, the reference in subsection
(4)(a)  to the name of the auditor is to be read as a reference to the names
of all the auditors.

##### Filing obligations of small companies other than micro-entities

54

For section 444 of the Companies Act 2006 substitute—

######### Filing obligations of small companies other than micro-entities

54.444

54.444.1

The directors of a company that is subject to the small companies regime in
relation to a financial year, or that would be so subject but for being or
having been a member of an ineligible group, must deliver to the registrar a
copy of—

54.444.1.a

the company’s annual accounts, and

54.444.1.b

the directors’ report.

54.444.2

The directors must also deliver to the registrar a copy of the auditor’s
report on those accounts (and on the directors’ report).

This does not apply if the company is exempt from audit and the directors have
taken advantage of that exemption.

54.444.3

The copies of the balance sheet and directors’ report delivered to the
registrar under this section must state the name of the person who signed it
on behalf of the board.

54.444.4

The copy of the auditor’s report delivered to the registrar under this section
must—

54.444.4.a

state the name of the auditor and (where the auditor is a firm) the name of
the person who signed it as senior statutory auditor, or

54.444.4.b

if the conditions in section 506 (circumstances in which names may be omitted)
are met, state that a resolution has been passed and notified to the Secretary
of State in accordance with that section.

54.444.5

If more than one person is appointed as auditor, the reference in subsection
(4)(a)  to the name of the auditor is to be read as a reference to the names
of all the auditors.

54.444.6

This section does not apply to companies within section 443A (filing
obligations of companies that qualify as micro-entities).

56.2.468A.1.a

56.2.468A.1.b

56.2.468A.2

56.2.468A.2.a

who may make an application;

56.2.468A.2.b

56.2.468A.2.c

#### Identity verification

##### Identity verification of persons with significant control

64

64.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

64.2

In section 790J (power to make exemptions), in subsection (2)(e), after “
790LH ” (inserted by Schedule 2 to this Act) insert  “and  790LM  to  790LS ”
.

64.3

After section  790LL  (inserted by Schedule 2 to this Act) insert—

########### Identity verification obligations for persons with significant control

############ Initial identity verification: registrable persons

64.3.790LM

64.3.790LM.1

This section applies in the following cases.

Case 1 is where— a company is incorporated in pursuance of an application for
registration containing a statement under section 12A(1)(a) naming a person as
someone who will, on the company’s incorporation, become a registrable person
(“the registrable person”), the application does not include a statement under
section  12B (2)  in respect of the registrable person or it appears to the
registrar that the statement is false, and the company has not given a notice
under section  790LG (1)  in respect of the person. Case 2 is where— the
registrar is notified under section  790LF  that a person has become a
registrable person in relation to a company (“the registrable person”), and
the notice does not include a statement under section  790LB (1)  or it
appears to the registrar that the statement is false.

64.3.790LM.2

The registrar must direct the registrable person to deliver to the registrar,
within the period of 14 days beginning with the date of the direction, a
statement confirming that the person’s identity is verified (see section
1110A).

64.3.790LM.3

The registrar may by further direction extend that period by up to 14 days at
a time.

64.3.790LM.4

A direction under this section must be in writing.

64.3.790LM.5

A direction given to a person under this section lapses if notice is later
given under section  790LG (1)  in respect of that person.

64.3.790LM.6

In this section “ registrable person ” does not include a person mentioned in
section 790C(12)(a) to (d).

############ Initial identity verification for registrable persons: transitional cases

64.3.790LN

64.3.790LN.1

A person must deliver to the registrar the statement required by this section
if the person—

64.3.790LN.1.a

is a registrable person in relation to a company at any time during the
appointed day, and

64.3.790LN.1.b

either—

64.3.790LN.1.b.i

became a registrable person on the incorporation of the company in pursuance
of an application for registration delivered before section  12B (2)  came
fully into force, or

64.3.790LN.1.b.ii

became a registrable person, otherwise than on the incorporation of the
company, before the day on which section  790LB (1)  came fully into force.

64.3.790LN.2

The statement required by this section is a statement confirming that person’s
identity is verified (see section 1110A).

64.3.790LN.3

A statement required by this section must be delivered within the period of 14
days beginning with the appointed day.

64.3.790LN.4

But the registrar may by direction in writing extend that period by up to 14
days at a time.

64.3.790LN.5

In this section—

“ the appointed day ” means such day as the Secretary of State may by
regulations appoint for the purposes of this section; “ registrable person ”
does not include a person mentioned in section 790C(12)(a) to (d).

64.3.790LN.6

The appointed day must not be before sections  12B (2)  and  790LB (1)  have
been brought fully into force.

############ Initial identity verification: registrable relevant legal entities

64.3.790LO

64.3.790LO.1

This section applies in the following cases.

Case 1 is where— a company is incorporated in pursuance of an application for
registration containing a statement under section 12A(1)(a) naming a person as
a person who will, on the company’s incorporation become a registrable
relevant legal entity (“the entity”), the application does not include a
statement under section  12B (3)  in respect of the entity, or is not
accompanied by a statement under section  12B (4)  by the person whose name is
specified in the statement under section  12B (3) , or it appears to the
registrar that either statement is false, and the company has not given a
notice under section  790LG (1)  in respect of the entity. Case 2 is where—
the registrar is notified under section 790LA that a person has become a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company (“the entity”), and
the notice does not include a statement under section  790LB (2) , or it is
not accompanied by a statement under section  790LB (3) , or it appears to the
registrar that either statement is false.

64.3.790LO.2

The registrar must direct the entity to deliver to the registrar, within the
period of 28 days beginning with the date of the direction—

64.3.790LO.2.a

a statement by the entity that—

64.3.790LO.2.a.i

specifies the name of one of its relevant officers who is an individual and
whose identity is verified, and

64.3.790LO.2.a.ii

confirms that the individual’s identity is verified, and

64.3.790LO.2.b

a statement by the individual confirming that the individual is a relevant
officer of the entity.

64.3.790LO.3

The registrar may by further direction extend that period by up to 28 days at
a time.

64.3.790LO.4

A direction under this section must be in writing.

64.3.790LO.5

A direction given to an entity under this section lapses if notice is later
given under section  790LG (1)  in respect of that entity.

64.3.790LO.6

In subsection  (2)  “relevant officer”—

64.3.790LO.6.a

in relation to a company, means a director;

64.3.790LO.6.b

in relation to a legal entity the affairs of which are managed by its members,
means one of those members;

64.3.790LO.6.c

in relation to any other legal entity, means an officer of the entity whose
functions correspond to that of a director of a company.

############ Initial identity verification in respect of registrable relevant legal entities: transitional cases

64.3.790LP

64.3.790LP.1

A person must deliver to the registrar the statements required by this section
if the person—

64.3.790LP.1.a

is a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company at any time
during the appointed day, and

64.3.790LP.1.b

either—

64.3.790LP.1.b.i

became a registrable relevant legal entity on the incorporation of the company
in pursuance of an application for registration delivered before section  12B
(3)  and  (4)  came fully into force, or

64.3.790LP.1.b.ii

became a registrable relevant legal entity, otherwise than on the
incorporation of the company, before section  790LB (2)  and  (3)  came fully
into force.

64.3.790LP.2

The statements are—

64.3.790LP.2.a

a statement by the entity that—

64.3.790LP.2.a.i

specifies the name of one of its relevant officers who is an individual and
whose identity is verified, and

64.3.790LP.2.a.ii

confirms that the individual’s identity is verified, and

64.3.790LP.2.b

a statement by the individual confirming that the individual is a relevant
officer of the entity.

64.3.790LP.3

The statements required by this section must be delivered within the period of
28 days beginning with the appointed day.

64.3.790LP.4

But the registrar may by direction in writing extend that period by up to 28
days at a time.

64.3.790LP.5

In this section—

“ the appointed day ” means such day as the Secretary of State may by
regulations appoint for the purposes of this section; “ relevant officer ” has
the meaning given by section  790LO (6) .

64.3.790LP.6

The appointed day must not be before sections  12B (3)  and  (4)  and  790LB
(2)  and  (3)  have been brought fully into force.

############ Registrable persons: duty to maintain verified identity status

64.3.790LQ

64.3.790LQ.1

A registrable person in relation to a company must ensure that, throughout the
relevant period, they maintain the status of a person whose identity is
verified (see section 1110A).

64.3.790LQ.2

In this section “ the relevant period ” means the period—

64.3.790LQ.2.a

beginning with—

64.3.790LQ.2.a.i

the incorporation of the company, in a case where the person became a
registrable person on its incorporation and the application for registration
of the company included a statement under section  12B (2)  in respect of the
person,

64.3.790LQ.2.a.ii

the delivery to the registrar of a statement in respect of the person under
section  790LB (1) , in a case where the person became a registrable person
after the incorporation of the company and such a statement was delivered to
the registrar,

64.3.790LQ.2.a.iii

the expiry of the period for complying with the direction under section  790LM
, in a case where a direction under that section is given to the person, and

64.3.790LQ.2.a.iv

the expiry of the period for complying with section  790LN , in a case where
that section applies to the person, and

64.3.790LQ.2.b

ending on the giving of a notice to the registrar under section  790LF  that
the person has ceased to be a registrable person in relation to the company.

64.3.790LQ.3

In this section “ registrable person ” does not include a person mentioned in
section 790C(12)(a) to (d).

############ Registrable relevant legal entities: duty to maintain registered officer whose identity is verified

64.3.790LR

64.3.790LR.1

A registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company must ensure that,
throughout the relevant period, its registered officer—

64.3.790LR.1.a

is a relevant officer of the entity, and

64.3.790LR.1.b

is an individual whose identity is verified (see section 1110A).

64.3.790LR.2

In this section “ registered officer ”, in relation to a registrable relevant
legal entity, means—

64.3.790LR.2.a

the person whose name is specified in—

64.3.790LR.2.a.i

a statement delivered to the registrar in respect of the entity under section
12B (3)  or  790LB (2) ,

64.3.790LR.2.a.ii

a statement delivered to the registrar by the entity in pursuance of a
direction under section  790LO (2) , or

64.3.790LR.2.a.iii

a statement delivered to the registrar under section  790LP (2) ,

unless the entity has changed its registered officer under section  790LS , or

64.3.790LR.2.b

if the entity has changed its registered officer under section  790LS , the
person specified in the latest notice under that section.

64.3.790LR.3

In this section “ the relevant period ” means the period—

64.3.790LR.3.a

beginning with—

64.3.790LR.3.a.i

the incorporation of the company, in a case where the entity became a relevant
registrable legal entity on the incorporation of the company and the
application for registration of the company included a statement under section
12B (3)  in respect of the entity,

64.3.790LR.3.a.ii

the delivery to the registrar of a statement in respect of the registrable
relevant legal entity under section  790LB (2) , in a case where the entity
became a relevant registrable legal entity after the incorporation of the
company and such a statement was delivered to the registrar,

64.3.790LR.3.a.iii

the expiry of the period for complying with the direction  790LO , in a case
where the entity is given a direction under that section, and

64.3.790LR.3.a.iv

the expiry of the period for complying with section  790LP , where that
section applies to the entity, and

64.3.790LR.3.b

ending with the giving of a notice to the registrar under section  790LF  that
the entity has ceased to be a relevant registrable legal entity in relation to
the company,

but see subsection  (4) .

64.3.790LR.4

If the registered officer of a registrable relevant legal entity ceases to be
a relevant officer of that entity, “ the relevant period ” does not include
the period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the person so ceases.

64.3.790LR.5

In this section “ relevant officer ” has the meaning given by section  790LO
(6) .

############ Registrable relevant legal entities: change of registered relevant officer

64.3.790LS

64.3.790LS.1

A registrable relevant legal entity may change its registered officer for the
purposes of section  790LR  by giving notice to the registrar.

64.3.790LS.2

The notice must include a statement by the entity that the new registered
officer—

64.3.790LS.2.a

is a relevant officer of the entity, and

64.3.790LS.2.b

is an individual whose identity is verified (see section 1110A).

64.3.790LS.3

The notice must be accompanied by a statement by the individual who is the new
registered officer confirming that the individual is a relevant officer of the
registrable relevant legal entity.

64.3.790LS.4

In this section “ relevant officer ” has the meaning given by section  790LO
(6) .

############ Offence of failing to comply with sections 

64.3.790LT

64.3.790LT.1

It is an offence for a person to fail, without reasonable excuse, to comply
with—

64.3.790LT.1.a

any of the following sections—

section  790LN ; section  790LP ; section  790LQ ; section  790LR ;

64.3.790LT.1.b

a direction under section  790LM  or  790LO .

64.3.790LT.2

Where an offence under this section is committed by a registrable relevant
legal entity, every officer of the entity who is in default also commits the
offence.

64.3.790LT.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

64.3.790LT.3.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

64.3.790LT.3.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

##### Procedure etc for verifying identity

65

65.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

65.2

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (3), at the appropriate
place insert—

sections  1110A  and  1110B  (identity verification),

.

65.3

In section 1087 (material not available for public inspection), in subsection
(1), after paragraph (gb) (inserted by section 66 of this Act) insert—

65.3.gc

any document delivered to the registrar under regulations under section  1110B
;

.

65.4

After section 1110 insert—

########### Identity verification

############ Meaning of “identity is verified”

65.4.1110A

65.4.1110A.1

For the purposes of this Act an individual’s “identity is verified” if—

65.4.1110A.1.a

the individual’s identity has been verified by the registrar in accordance
with regulations under section  1110B , or

65.4.1110A.1.b

a verification statement in respect of the individual has been delivered to
the registrar,

and the individual has not, since then, ceased to be an individual whose
identity is verified by virtue of regulations under subsection  (6) .

65.4.1110A.2

A verification statement is a statement by an authorised corporate service
provider confirming that it has verified an individual’s identity in
accordance with regulations under section  1110B .

65.4.1110A.3

A verification statement must also specify the authorised corporate service
provider’s supervisory authority or authorities for the purposes of the Money
Laundering Regulations.

65.4.1110A.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
contents of verification statements (including provision amending this
section).

65.4.1110A.5

Where a person is required or authorised by any other provision to deliver a
statement to the registrar that an individual’s identity is verified, that
statement may be delivered at the same time as the verification statement by
virtue of which the individual becomes someone whose identity is verified
under subsection  (1)(b) .

65.4.1110A.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for circumstances in which
someone ceases to be an individual whose identity is verified.

65.4.1110A.7

The provision that can be made under subsection  (6)  includes—

65.4.1110A.7.a

provision to confer a discretion on the registrar;

65.4.1110A.7.b

provision that someone ceases to be an individual whose identity is verified
unless, within a specified period of time—

65.4.1110A.7.b.i

their identity is reverified by the registrar in accordance with regulations
under section  1110B , or

65.4.1110A.7.b.ii

an authorised corporate service provider delivers to the registrar a
statement: (A) confirming that it has reverified the individual’s identity in
accordance with regulations under section  1110B , (B) specifying the
authorised corporate service provider’s supervisory authority or authorities
for the purposes of the Money Laundering Regulations, and (C) containing
anything else required by the regulations.

65.4.1110A.8

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

65.4.1110A.9

In this section—

“ Money Laundering Regulations ” means the Money Laundering, Terrorist
Financing and Transfer of Funds (Information on the Payer) Regulations 2017 (
S.I. 2017/692 ); “ supervisory authority ” means an authority that is a
supervisory authority under the Money Laundering Regulations (see regulation 7
of those Regulations).

############ Verification requirements

65.4.1110B

65.4.1110B.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for and in connection
with verification or reverification of an individual’s identity for the
purposes of this Act by the registrar or by an authorised corporate service
provider.

65.4.1110B.2

The regulations may, in particular, make provision about—

65.4.1110B.2.a

the procedure for verifying or reverifying an individual’s identity, including
the evidence required;

65.4.1110B.2.b

the records that a person who is or has been an authorised corporate service
provider is required to keep in connection with the verification or
reverification of an individual’s identity.

65.4.1110B.3

The regulations may create offences in relation to failures to comply with
requirements imposed by virtue of subsection  (2)(b) .

65.4.1110B.4

The regulations must provide for any such offence to be punishable—

65.4.1110B.4.a

on conviction on indictment, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

65.4.1110B.4.b

on summary conviction—

65.4.1110B.4.b.i

in England and Wales, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

65.4.1110B.4.b.ii

in Scotland, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued contravention, a
daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory maximum;

65.4.1110B.4.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, by imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued
contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory
maximum.

65.4.1110B.5

The provision that can be made in regulations under this section includes
provision conferring a discretion on the registrar, including provision
conferring power to impose requirements by registrar’s rules.

65.4.1110B.6

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

65.5

In Schedule 8 (index of defined expressions), at the appropriate place insert—

identity is verified section  1110A

.

##### Authorisation of corporate service providers

66

66.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

66.2

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (3), at the appropriate
place insert—

sections  1098A  to  1098H  (authorised corporate service providers),

.

66.3

In section 1087 (material not available for public inspection), in subsection
(1), after paragraph (ga) insert—

66.3.gb

any application or other document delivered to the registrar under section
1098B ,  1098D  or  1098E  or regulations under section  1098G  (authorised
corporate service providers);

.

66.4

After section 1098 insert—

########### Authorised corporate service providers

############ Meaning of “authorised corporate service provider”

66.4.1098A

In this Act “ authorised corporate service provider ” means a person—

66.4.1098A.a

whose application to the registrar to become an authorised corporate service
provider for the purposes of this Act has been granted (see section  1098B ),

66.4.1098A.b

who has not since ceased to be an authorised corporate service provider by
virtue of section  1098F , and

66.4.1098A.c

whose status as an authorised corporate service provider is not for the time
being suspended by virtue of section  1098F .

############ Application to become authorised corporate service provider

66.4.1098B

66.4.1098B.1

A person may apply to the registrar to become an authorised corporate service
provider for the purposes of this Act if—

66.4.1098B.1.a

the person is a relevant person as defined by regulation 8(1) of the Money
Laundering Regulations,

66.4.1098B.1.b

in the case of an individual, their identity is verified (see section  1110A
), and

66.4.1098B.1.c

the person meets any other requirements imposed by regulations made by the
Secretary of State for the purposes of this paragraph.

66.4.1098B.2

An application under this section must contain—

66.4.1098B.2.a

the name of the applicant’s supervisory authority or authorities for the
purposes of the Money Laundering Regulations,

66.4.1098B.2.b

the required information about the applicant (see section  1098C ), and

66.4.1098B.2.c

in the case of an application by an individual, a statement that the
individual’s identity is verified (see section 1110A).

(See also section  1098D , which imposes restrictions on who may deliver an
application under this section on behalf of a firm.)

66.4.1098B.3

Where an application is made under this section, the registrar must check with
the supervisory authority, or at least one of the supervisory authorities,
specified in the application, to find out whether the applicant is known to
and supervised by that authority.

66.4.1098B.4

Having carried out that check, the registrar must grant the application if—

66.4.1098B.4.a

the supervisory authority, or at least one of the supervisory authorities,
specified in the application has confirmed that the applicant is known to and
supervised by that authority,

66.4.1098B.4.b

where the applicant is an individual, the registrar is satisfied that their
identity is verified (see section  1110A ),

66.4.1098B.4.c

any other conditions that may be specified by regulations made by the
Secretary of State for the purposes of this paragraph are met, and

66.4.1098B.4.d

the registrar is not required by subsection  (5)  to refuse the application.

66.4.1098B.5

The registrar must refuse the application if it appears to the registrar that
the applicant is not a fit and proper person to carry out the functions of an
authorised corporate service provider.

66.4.1098B.6

The provision that can be made in regulations under subsection  (4)(c)
includes provision conferring a discretion on the registrar.

66.4.1098B.7

Regulations under subsection  (1)(c)  or  (4)(c)  are subject to affirmative
resolution procedure.

66.4.1098B.8

For the purposes of this section—

“ Money Laundering Regulations ” means the Money Laundering, Terrorist
Financing and Transfer of Funds (Information on the Payer) Regulations 2017 (
S.I. 2017/692 ); “supervised”: a person is supervised by a supervisory
authority if regulation 7(1) of the Money Laundering Regulations provides that
it is a supervisory authority for that person; “ supervisory authority ” means
an authority that is a supervisory authority under the Money Laundering
Regulations (see regulation 7 of those Regulations).

############ The required information about an applicant

66.4.1098C

66.4.1098C.1

The “required information” about the applicant, in the case of a firm that is
applying to become an authorised corporate service provider, means—

66.4.1098C.1.a

firm name,

66.4.1098C.1.b

principal office,

66.4.1098C.1.c

a service address,

66.4.1098C.1.d

an email address,

66.4.1098C.1.e

the legal form of the firm and the law by which it is governed, and

66.4.1098C.1.f

if applicable, the register in which it is entered (including details of the
state) and its registration number in that register.

66.4.1098C.2

The “required information” about the applicant, in the case of an individual
who is applying to become an authorised corporate service provider, means—

66.4.1098C.2.a

name, nationality and date of birth,

66.4.1098C.2.b

a service address,

66.4.1098C.2.c

an email address, and

66.4.1098C.2.d

the part of the United Kingdom in which the person is usually resident or, if
the person is usually resident in a country or state outside the United
Kingdom, that country or state.

66.4.1098C.3

In subsection  (2)(a)  “ name ” means forename and surname.

66.4.1098C.4

Where the applicant is a peer or an individual usually known by a title, the
requirement for the application to contain their name may be satisfied by
providing that title instead of the individual’s forename and surname.

66.4.1098C.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

66.4.1098C.5.a

amend this section so as to change the required information about the
applicant in the case of a firm or individual applying to become an authorised
corporate service provider;

66.4.1098C.5.b

repeal subsection  (4) .

66.4.1098C.6

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

############ Delivery of applications under section 

66.4.1098D

An application under section  1098B  by a firm mentioned in the first column
of the table—

66.4.1098D.a

must be delivered to the registrar on its behalf by a relevant officer
mentioned in the second column who is an individual (see also section
1067A(2)), and

66.4.1098D.b

must be accompanied by a statement by the individual confirming their status
as a relevant officer of the firm.

Firm Relevant officer company director body corporate other than a company
where the body’s affairs are managed by its members, a member of the body; in
any other case, any officer of the body whose functions correspond to that of
a director of a company. partnership in relation to a limited partnership, a
general partner as defined by section 3 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907;
in relation to any other partnership, a member of the partnership
unincorporated body other than a partnership where the body’s affairs are
managed by its members, a member of the body; in any other case, a member of
the governing body.

############ Updating duties of authorised corporate service providers

66.4.1098E

66.4.1098E.1

A person who is an authorised corporate service provider must notify the
registrar of any change in its supervisory authority or authorities for the
purposes of the Money Laundering Regulations within the period of 14 days
beginning with the date on which the change occurs.

66.4.1098E.2

Where the change is the result of an agreement under regulation 7(2) of the
Money Laundering Regulations, for the purposes of this section the change is
not to be treated as having occurred until the authority that has agreed to
act notifies the person or publishes the agreement under regulation 7(3).

66.4.1098E.3

A person who, without reasonable excuse, fails to comply with this section
commits an offence.

66.4.1098E.4

Where the offence is committed by a firm, every officer of the firm who is in
default also commits the offence.

66.4.1098E.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

66.4.1098E.5.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

66.4.1098E.5.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

66.4.1098E.6

In this section “Money Laundering Regulations” and “supervisory authority”
have the meanings given by section  1098B (8) .

############ Ceasing to be an authorised corporate service provider

66.4.1098F

66.4.1098F.1

A person ceases to be an authorised corporate service provider if the person
ceases to be a relevant person as defined by regulation 8(1) of the Money
Laundering Regulations.

66.4.1098F.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

66.4.1098F.2.a

provide for other circumstances in which a person ceases to be an authorised
corporate service provider, whether automatically or as a result of a decision
taken by the registrar;

66.4.1098F.2.b

provide for circumstances in which the registrar may suspend a person’s status
as an authorised corporate service provider pending a decision by the
registrar under regulations made by virtue of paragraph  (a) .

66.4.1098F.3

The provision that can be made under subsection  (2)  includes provision as
to—

66.4.1098F.3.a

procedure;

66.4.1098F.3.b

the period of a suspension;

66.4.1098F.3.c

the revocation of a suspension.

66.4.1098F.4

The provision that can be made in regulations under subsection  (2)  includes
provision conferring a discretion on the registrar.

66.4.1098F.5

Regulations under subsection  (2)  are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

66.4.1098F.6

In this section “ Money Laundering Regulations ” has the meaning given by
section  1098B (8) .

############ Power to impose duties to provide information

66.4.1098G

66.4.1098G.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations require a person who is or has been
an authorised corporate service provider to provide information to the
registrar in accordance with the regulations (including information for the
purpose of monitoring compliance with the requirements of this Act).

66.4.1098G.2

The provision that may be made by regulations under subsection  (1)  includes
provision requiring information to be provided on request, on the occurrence
of an event or at regular intervals.

66.4.1098G.3

The circumstances that may be specified under section  1098F (2)  include
failure to comply with a requirement under subsection  (1) .

66.4.1098G.4

Regulations under this section may create offences in relation to failures to
comply with requirements imposed by the regulations.

66.4.1098G.5

The regulations must provide for any such offence to be punishable on summary
conviction—

66.4.1098G.5.a

in England and Wales with a fine;

66.4.1098G.5.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, with a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

66.4.1098G.6

The provision that can be made in regulations under this section includes
provision conferring a discretion on the registrar.

66.4.1098G.7

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

############ Power to enable authorisation of foreign corporate service providers

66.4.1098H

66.4.1098H.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for the purposes of
enabling a person who is subject to a relevant regulatory regime under the law
of a territory outside the United Kingdom to become an authorised corporate
service provider, even if the person is not a relevant person as defined by
regulation 8(1) of the Money Laundering Regulations.

66.4.1098H.2

In subsection  (1)  “ relevant regulatory regime ” means a regulatory regime
that, in the opinion of the Secretary of State, has similar objectives to the
regulatory regime under the Money Laundering Regulations for relevant persons
and is likely to be no less effective in achieving those objectives.

66.4.1098H.3

Regulations under this section—

66.4.1098H.3.a

may amend any of sections  1098B  to  1098G  or insert new sections into this
Act;

66.4.1098H.3.b

may make consequential amendments or repeals in other provisions of this Act.

66.4.1098H.4

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

66.4.1098H.5

In this section “ Money Laundering Regulations ” has the meaning given by
section  1098B (8) .

66.5

In Schedule 8 (index of defined expressions), at the appropriate place insert—

authorised corporate service provider section  1098A

.

##### Exemption from identity verification: national security grounds

67

67.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

67.2

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (4), at the appropriate
place insert—

section  1110C  (identity verification: exemption on national security
grounds),

.

67.3

After section 1110B (inserted by section 65 of this Act) insert—

########### Identity verification: exemption on national security grounds etc

67.3.1110C

67.3.1110C.1

The Secretary of State may, by written notice given to a person, provide for
one or more of the effects listed in subsection  (2)  to apply in relation to
the person, if satisfied that to do so is necessary—

67.3.1110C.1.a

in the interests of national security, or

67.3.1110C.1.b

for the purposes of preventing or detecting serious crime.

67.3.1110C.2

The effects for which the notice may provide are that—

67.3.1110C.2.a

where a statement of proposed officers names the person as a director, section
12 (2A)  does not require a statement under that subsection to be made in
relation to the person;

67.3.1110C.2.b

section  167G (3)(c)  does not apply in relation to a notice of the person
having become a director;

67.3.1110C.2.c

section  167M (1)  does not apply in relation to the person and section
167M(2) does not impose any obligation on a company in relation to the person;

67.3.1110C.2.d

section  167N (1)  does not apply in relation to the person;

67.3.1110C.2.e

section 1067A does not apply in relation to the delivery of documents to the
registrar by the person on their own behalf or on behalf of another;

67.3.1110C.2.f

section 1098B(2)(c) does not apply in relation to the person.

67.3.1110C.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(b) —

67.3.1110C.3.a

“ crime ” means conduct which—

67.3.1110C.3.a.i

constitutes a criminal offence, or

67.3.1110C.3.a.ii

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute a criminal offence, and

67.3.1110C.3.b

crime is “serious” if—

67.3.1110C.3.b.i

the offence which is or would be constituted by the conduct is an offence for
which the maximum sentence (in any part of the United Kingdom) is imprisonment
for 3 years or more, or

67.3.1110C.3.b.ii

the conduct involves the use of violence, results in substantial financial
gain or is conduct by a large number of persons in pursuit of a common
purpose.

#### Striking off and restoration to the register

##### Registrar’s power to strike off company registered on false basis

70

70.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

70.2

After section 1002 insert—

########### Registrar’s power to strike off company registered on false basis

############ Power to strike off company registered on false basis

70.2.1002A

70.2.1002A.1

The registrar may strike a company’s name off the register if the registrar
has reasonable cause to believe that—

70.2.1002A.1.a

any information contained in the application for the registration of the
company, or in any application for restoration of the company to the register,
is misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular, or

70.2.1002A.1.b

any statement made to the registrar in connection with such an application is
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

70.2.1002A.2

In subsection  (1)  the reference to an application includes any documents
delivered to the registrar in connection with the application.

70.2.1002A.3

The registrar may not exercise the power in subsection  (1)  unless—

70.2.1002A.3.a

the registrar has published a notice in the Gazette that, at the end of the
period of 28 days beginning with the date of the notice, the name of the
company mentioned in the notice will, unless cause is shown to the contrary,
be struck off the register and the company will be dissolved, and

70.2.1002A.3.b

the period mentioned in paragraph  (a)  has expired.

70.2.1002A.4

If the registrar exercises the power in subsection  (1) , the registrar must
publish a notice in the Gazette of the company’s name having been struck off
the register.

70.2.1002A.5

On the publication of the notice in the Gazette the company is dissolved.

70.2.1002A.6

However—

70.2.1002A.6.a

the liability (if any) of every director, managing officer or member of the
company continues and may be enforced as if the company had not been
dissolved, and

70.2.1002A.6.b

nothing in this section affects the power of the court to wind up a company
the name of which has been struck off the register.

70.3

In section 1024 (application for administrative restoration to the register),
in subsection (1), for the words from “section” to the end substitute

—

70.3.a

section 1000 or 1001 (power of registrar to strike off defunct company), or

70.3.b

section 1002A (power of registrar to strike off company registered on false
basis).

70.4

In section 1025 (requirements for administrative restoration), for subsection
(2) substitute—

70.4.2

The first condition is that—

70.4.2.a

in the case of a company struck off the register under section 1000 or 1001,
the company was carrying on business or in operation at the time of its
striking off;

70.4.2.b

in the case of a company struck off the register under section 1002A, at the
time of its striking off, the registrar did not have reasonable cause to
believe the matter set out in section 1002A(1)(a) or (b).

70.5

In section 1028A (administrative restoration of company with share warrants),
in subsection (1), for “or 1001” substitute  “, 1001 or 1002A” .

70.6

In section 1029 (application to court for restoration to the register), in
subsection (1)(c)—

70.6.a

omit the “or” at the end of sub-paragraph (i);

70.6.b

after that sub-paragraph insert—

70.6.b.ia

under section 1002A (power of registrar to strike off company registered on
false basis), or

.

70.7

In section 1030 (timing for application to court for restoration to the
register), in subsection (5)(a), after “company)” insert  “or section 1002A
(power of registrar to strike off company registered on false basis)” .

;

##### Requirements for administrative restoration

71

In section 1025 of the Companies Act 2006 (requirements for administrative
restoration), for subsection (5) substitute—

71.5

The third condition is that the applicant has delivered to the registrar such
documents relating to the company as are necessary to ensure that if the
company is restored to the register the records kept by the registrar relating
to the company will be up to date.

71.5A

The fourth condition is—

71.5A.a

that any outstanding penalties under section 453 or corresponding earlier
provisions (civil penalty for failure to deliver accounts) in relation to the
company have been paid, and

71.5A.b

that each relevant person has paid any outstanding fines or financial
penalties imposed on them in respect of an offence under the Companies Acts
relating to the company.

71.5B

In subsection  (5A)(b)  “ relevant person ” means—

71.5B.a

the applicant,

71.5B.b

any person who—

71.5B.b.i

was a director of the company immediately before it was dissolved or struck
off, and

71.5B.b.ii

if the company is restored to the register, will be a director immediately
after its restoration, or

71.5B.c

any person who is a relevant officer of a firm where the firm is—

71.5B.c.i

a person mentioned in paragraph (a) or (b), or

71.5B.c.ii

a person falling within this paragraph.

71.5C

In subsection  (5B)(c)  “relevant officer”—

71.5C.a

in relation to a company, means a director;

71.5C.b

in relation to a firm the affairs of which are managed by its members, means
one of those members;

71.5C.c

in relation to any other firm, means an officer of the firm whose functions
correspond to that of a director of a company.

#### Who may deliver documents

##### Delivery of documents: identity verification etc

72

72.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

72.2

In section 9 (registration documents), omit subsection (3).

72.3

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (2), for “1068” substitute
“ 1067A ” .

72.4

After section 1067 insert—

########### Who may deliver documents to the registrar

############ Delivery of documents: identity verification requirements etc

72.4.1067A

72.4.1067A.1

An individual may not deliver a document to the registrar on their own behalf
unless—

72.4.1067A.1.a

their identity is verified (see section 1110A), and

72.4.1067A.1.b

the document is accompanied by a statement to that effect.

72.4.1067A.2

An individual (A) may not deliver a document to the registrar on behalf of
another person (B) who is of a description specified in column 1 of the
following table unless—

72.4.1067A.2.a

the individual is of a description specified in the corresponding entry in
column 2, and

72.4.1067A.2.b

the document is accompanied by the statement specified in the corresponding
entry in column 3.

1 2 3 Description of person on whose behalf document delivered (B) Description
of individual who may deliver document on B’s behalf (A) Accompanying
statement 1 Firm Individual who is an officer or employee of the firm and
whose identity is verified (see section 1110A). Statement by A— that A is an
officer or employee of the firm, that A is delivering the document on the
firm’s behalf, and that A’s identity is verified. 2 Firm Individual who is an
officer or employee of a corporate officer of the firm and whose identity is
verified. Statement by A— that A is an officer or employee of a corporate
officer of the firm, that A is delivering the document on the firm’s behalf,
and that A’s identity is verified. 3 Firm Individual who is an authorised
corporate service provider (see section 1098A). Statement by A— that A is an
authorised corporate service provider, and that A is delivering the document
on the firm’s behalf. 4 Firm Individual who is an officer or employee of an
authorised corporate service provider. Statement by A— that A is an officer or
employee of an authorised corporate service provider, and that A is delivering
the document on the firm’s behalf. 5 Individual Individual whose identity is
verified. Statement by A— that A is delivering the document on B’s behalf, and
that A’s identity is verified. 6 Individual Individual who is an authorised
corporate service provider. Statement by A— that A is an authorised corporate
service provider, and that A is delivering the document on B’s behalf. 7
Individual Individual who is an officer or employee of an authorised corporate
service provider. Statement by A— that A is an officer or employee of an
authorised corporate service provider, and that A is delivering the document
on B’s behalf.

72.4.1067A.3

In relation to a corporate officer that has only corporate officers, the
reference in row 2 of the table to an individual who is one of its officers is
to—

72.4.1067A.3.a

an individual who is an officer of one of those corporate officers, or

72.4.1067A.3.b

if the officers of those corporate officers are all corporate officers, an
individual who is an officer of any of the corporate officers’ corporate
officers,

and so on until there is at least one individual who is an officer.

72.4.1067A.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

72.4.1067A.4.a

create exceptions to subsections  (1)  or  (2)  (which may be framed by
reference to the person by whom or on whose behalf a document is delivered or
by reference to descriptions of document or in any other way);

72.4.1067A.4.b

amend this section for the purpose of changing the effect of the table in
subsection  (2) .

72.4.1067A.5

Regulations under subsection  (4)(a) —

72.4.1067A.5.a

may require any document delivered to the registrar in reliance on an
exception to be accompanied by a statement;

72.4.1067A.5.b

may amend this section.

72.4.1067A.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring a statement
delivered to the registrar under subsection  (2)  to be accompanied by
additional statements or additional information in connection with the
subject-matter of the statement.

72.4.1067A.7

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

72.4.1067A.8

In this section “ corporate officer ” means an officer that is not an
individual.

##### Disqualification from delivering documents

73

After section  1067A  of the Companies Act 2006 (inserted by section 72 of
this Act) insert—

######### Disqualification from delivering documents

73.1067B

73.1067B.1

An individual who is a disqualified person may not deliver documents to the
registrar on their own behalf or on behalf of another.

73.1067B.2

An individual may not deliver a document to the registrar on behalf of a
disqualified person unless—

73.1067B.2.a

the individual is an authorised corporate service provider (see section  1098A
), or

73.1067B.2.b

the individual is an officer or employee of an authorised corporate service
provider.

73.1067B.3

A document delivered to the registrar must be accompanied by the following two
statements made by the individual delivering it.

73.1067B.4

The first is a statement that the individual is not a disqualified person.

73.1067B.5

The second is—

73.1067B.5.a

a statement that the individual is delivering the document on their own
behalf,

73.1067B.5.b

a statement that the individual is delivering the document on behalf of
another person who is not a disqualified person, or

73.1067B.5.c

a statement that the individual is delivering the document on behalf of a
disqualified person.

73.1067B.6

For the purpose of this section “ disqualified person ” means a person who is
disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see section
159A (2) ).

73.1067B.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section for the purposes
of changing who may deliver a document to the registrar on behalf of a
disqualified person.

73.1067B.8

Regulations under subsection  (7)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Registrar’s rules requiring documents to be delivered together

78

78.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

78.2

After section 1068 insert—

########### Registrar’s rules requiring documents to be delivered together

78.2.1068A

78.2.1068A.1

Registrar’s rules may provide for circumstances where—

78.2.1068A.1.a

a person who is required to deliver two or more documents to the registrar
must deliver them together;

78.2.1068A.1.b

a person who wishes to deliver two or more documents authorised to be
delivered to the registrar is required to deliver them together (so that, for
example, if one document is delivered on its own, the others cannot be
delivered on a later occasion);

78.2.1068A.1.c

a person who wishes to deliver one or more documents authorised to be
delivered to the registrar is required to deliver them together with one or
more documents that the person is required to deliver to the registrar (so
that, for example, if a document that is required to be delivered has been
delivered on its own, the documents that are authorised to be delivered cannot
be delivered on a later occasion).

78.2.1068A.2

Provision may not be made under subsection  (1)(a)  that would have the effect
of requiring any document to be delivered earlier than it would otherwise be
required to be delivered.

#### Promoting the integrity of the register

##### Power to reject documents for inconsistencies

79

After section 1073 of the Companies Act 2006 insert—

######### Power to reject documents for discrepancies

79.1073A

79.1073A.1

The registrar may refuse to accept (and register) a document if—

79.1073A.1.a

it appears to the registrar to be inconsistent with other information that is
held by or available to the registrar, and

79.1073A.1.b

in light of the inconsistency, the registrar has reasonable grounds to doubt
whether it complies with any requirement as to its contents.

79.1073A.2

A document is refused by giving notice of the refusal to the person by whom
the document was delivered to the registrar.

79.1073A.3

A document that is refused by the registrar is treated for the purposes of any
provision authorising or requiring its delivery as not having been delivered.

##### Power to require additional information

83

83.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended in accordance with subsections  (2)  to  (4)
.

83.2

After section 1092 insert—

########### Additional information

############ Power to require information

83.2.1092A

83.2.1092A.1

The registrar may by notice in writing require a person to provide information
to the registrar for the purposes of enabling the registrar to determine—

83.2.1092A.1.a

whether a person has complied with any obligation imposed by an enactment to
deliver a document to the registrar,

83.2.1092A.1.b

whether any information contained in a document received by the registrar
falls within section 1080(1)(a).

83.2.1092A.2

A requirement under this section may specify—

83.2.1092A.2.a

the form and manner in which the information is to be provided;

83.2.1092A.2.b

the period within which it is to be provided.

83.2.1092A.3

The registrar may by notice in writing extend a period specified in a
requirement under this section.

############ Offence relating to provision of information

83.2.1092B

83.2.1092B.1

A person who, without reasonable excuse, fails to comply with a requirement
under section  1092A  commits an offence.

83.2.1092B.2

Where an offence under this section is committed by a firm, an offence is also
committed by every officer of the firm who is in default.

83.2.1092B.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

83.2.1092B.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

83.2.1092B.3.b

on summary conviction—

83.2.1092B.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

83.2.1092B.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued contravention, a
daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory maximum;

83.2.1092B.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both), and, for continued
contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory
maximum.

############ Privilege against self-incrimination

83.2.1092C

83.2.1092C.1

A statement made by a person in response to a requirement under section  1092A
may not be used against the person in criminal proceedings in which the person
is charged with an offence to which this subsection applies.

83.2.1092C.2

Subsection  (1)  applies to any offence other than—

83.2.1092C.2.a

an offence under one of the following provisions (which concern false
statements etc)—

83.2.1092C.2.a.i

section 1112 or 1112A;

83.2.1092C.2.a.ii

section 5 of the Perjury Act 1911;

83.2.1092C.2.a.iii

section 44(2) of the Criminal Law (Consolidation) (Scotland) Act 1995;

83.2.1092C.2.a.iv

Article 10 of the Perjury (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1714 (N.I.
19) );

83.2.1092C.2.a.v

section 32 or 32A of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act
2022;

83.2.1092C.2.a.vi

section 34 or 35 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907;

83.2.1092C.2.b

any offence, not within paragraph  (a) , an element of which is the delivery
to the registrar of a document, or the making of a statement to the registrar,
that is misleading, false or deceptive.

83.3

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (2), at the appropriate
place insert—

sections  1092A  to  1092C  (powers to require further information),

.

83.4

In section 1087 (material not available for public inspection), in subsection

##### Administrative removal of material from the register

85

85.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

85.2

For section 1094 substitute—

########### Removal of material from the register

85.2.1094

85.2.1094.1

The registrar may remove from the register anything that appears to the
registrar to be—

85.2.1094.1.a

a document, or material derived from a document, accepted under section 1073
(power to accept documents not meeting requirements for proper delivery), or

85.2.1094.1.b

unnecessary material as defined by section 1074.

85.2.1094.2

The power to remove material from the register under this section may be
exercised—

85.2.1094.2.a

on the registrar’s own motion, or

85.2.1094.2.b

on an application made in accordance with regulations under section  1094A (2)
.

85.2.1094.3

The registrar may exercise the power to remove from the register anything the
registration of which had legal consequences only if satisfied that the
interest of the company, or (if different) the applicant, in removing the
material outweighs any interest of other persons in the material continuing to
appear on the register.

85.2.1094.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that the registrar’s power
to remove material from the register under this section following an
application is limited to material of a description specified in the
regulations.

85.2.1094.5

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative resolution
procedure.

########### Further provision about removal of material from the register

85.2.1094A

85.2.1094A.1

The Secretary of State must by regulations make provision for notice to be
given in accordance with the regulations where material is removed from the
register under section  1094  otherwise than on an application.

85.2.1094A.2

The Secretary of State must by regulations make provision in connection with
the making and determination of applications for the removal of material from
the register under section  1094 .

85.2.1094A.3

The provision that may be made under subsection  (2)  includes provision as
to—

85.2.1094A.3.a

who may make an application,

85.2.1094A.3.b

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application,

85.2.1094A.3.c

the notice to be given of an application and of its outcome,

85.2.1094A.3.d

a period in which objections to an application may be made, and

85.2.1094A.3.e

how an application is to be determined, including provision as to evidence
that may be relied upon by the registrar for the purposes of satisfying the
test in section  1094 (1) .

85.2.1094A.4

The provision that may be made by virtue of subsection  (3)(e)  includes
provision as to circumstances in which—

85.2.1094A.4.a

evidence is to be treated by the registrar as conclusive proof that the test
in section  1094 (1)  is met, and

85.2.1094A.4.b

the power of removal must be exercised.

85.2.1094A.5

Regulations under this section may in particular confer a discretion on the
registrar.

85.2.1094A.6

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative resolution
procedure.

########### Power of court to make consequential orders following removal

85.2.1094B

85.2.1094B.1

Where the registrar removes anything from the register otherwise than in
pursuance of a court order, the court may, on an application by a person with
sufficient interest, make such consequential orders as the court thinks fit as
to the legal effects of the inclusion of the material on the register or its
removal.

85.2.1094B.2

In this section the reference to the registrar removing material from the
register includes the registrar determining that anything purported to be
delivered to the registrar under any enactment was not in fact delivered under
an enactment and therefore does not form part of the register.

85.3

In section 1073 (power to accept documents not meeting requirements for proper
delivery), in subsection (6)(a), for “section 1094(4)” substitute
“regulations under section  1094A (1) ” .

85.4.f

1094  (removal of material from the register);

.

85.5

Omit section 1095 (rectification of register on application to registrar).

85.6

Omit section 1095A (rectification of register to resolve a discrepancy).

##### Power to require businesses to report discrepancies

87

87.1

87.3

After section 1110C (inserted by section 67 of this Act) insert—

########### Discrepancy reporting

############ Power to require businesses to report discrepancies

87.3.1110D

87.3.1110D.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations impose requirements on a person who
is carrying on business in the United Kingdom (a “relevant person”)—

87.3.1110D.1.a

to obtain specified information about a customer (or prospective customer)—

87.3.1110D.1.a.i

before entering into a business relationship with them, or

87.3.1110D.1.a.ii

during a business relationship with them,

87.3.1110D.1.b

to identify discrepancies between information so obtained and information made
publicly available by the registrar, and

87.3.1110D.1.c

to report any discrepancies to the registrar.

87.3.1110D.2

The regulations may require the relevant person, when reporting discrepancies,
to provide such other information as may be required by the regulations
(including information about the relevant person).

87.3.1110D.3

The regulations may provide for reports or other information delivered to the
registrar under the regulations to be withheld from public inspection.

87.3.1110D.4

The regulations may create offences in relation to failures to comply with
requirements imposed by the regulations.

87.3.1110D.5

The regulations may not provide for an offence created by the regulations to
be punishable with imprisonment for a period exceeding—

87.3.1110D.5.a

in the case of conviction on indictment, 2 years;

87.3.1110D.5.b

in the case of summary conviction, 3 months.

87.3.1110D.6

In this section “ customer ”, in relation to a person carrying out estate
agency work, includes a purchaser (as well as a seller).

87.3.1110D.7

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

For section 1088 substitute—

########### Power to make regulations protecting material

91.4.1088

91.4.1088.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring the
registrar, on application—

91.4.1088.1.a

not to make available for public inspection any information on the register
relating to an individual;

91.4.1088.1.b

91.4.1088.1.c

not to make available for public inspection any address on the register that
is not information to which paragraph  (a)  applies;

91.4.1088.1.d

to refrain from disclosing any such address except in specified circumstances.

91.4.1088.2

registrar—

91.4.1088.2.a

not to make available for public inspection any information on the register
relating to an individual;

91.4.1088.2.b

to refrain from disclosing information on the register relating to an

91.4.1088.4

91.4.1088.6

91.4.1088.7.b

91.4.1088.8

from disclosing information under section  1110F  (general powers of
disclosure by the registrar).

91.4.1088.9

registrar.

91.4.1088.10

procedure.

#### Registrar's functions and fees

##### Analysis of information for the purposes of crime prevention or detection

92

After section 1062 of the Companies Act 2006 insert—

######### Analysis of information for the purposes of crime prevention or detection

92.1062A

of preventing or detecting crime.

92.1062A.2

See also section  1110F  (which, among other things, allows the registrar to
disclose information to other public authorities).

#### Information sharing and use

##### Disclosure of information

94

94.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

94.2

In section 243 (permitted disclosure by registrar), for subsection (6)
substitute—

94.2.6

Regulations under subsection (4) may in particular confer a discretion on the
registrar.

94.2.6A

Provision under subsection (5)(d) may in particular provide for a question to
be referred to a person other than the registrar for the purposes of
determining the application.

94.3

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (2), at the appropriate
place insert—

sections  1110E  to  1110G  (disclosure of information),

.

94.4

After section 1110D (inserted by section 87 of this Act) insert—

########### Disclosure of information

############ Disclosure to the registrar

94.4.1110E

Any person may disclose information to the registrar for the purposes of the
exercise of any of the registrar’s functions.

############ Disclosure by the registrar

94.4.1110F

94.4.1110F.1

The registrar may disclose information—

94.4.1110F.1.a

to any person for purposes connected with the exercise of any of the
registrar’s functions;

94.4.1110F.1.b

to a public authority for purposes connected with the exercise of any of that
public authority’s functions;

94.4.1110F.1.c

to a person of a description, and for a purpose, specified in regulations made
by the Secretary of State for the purposes of this paragraph.

94.4.1110F.2

Regulations under subsection  (1)(c)  are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

94.4.1110F.3

In this section “ public authority ” includes any person or body having
functions of a public nature.

############ Disclosure: supplementary

94.4.1110G

94.4.1110G.1

Except as provided by subsection  (2) , the disclosure of information under
section  1110E  or  1110F  does not breach—

94.4.1110G.1.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

94.4.1110G.1.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

94.4.1110G.2

Sections  1110E  and  1110F  do not authorise a disclosure of information if
the disclosure would contravene the data protection legislation (but in
determining whether a disclosure would do so, take into account the powers
conferred by those sections).

94.4.1110G.3

HMRC information may not be disclosed by the registrar under section  1110F
without authorisation from HMRC.

94.4.1110G.4

If the registrar discloses HMRC information under section  1110F , the
information must not be disclosed by the recipient, or by any person obtaining
the information directly or indirectly from them, without authorisation from
HMRC.

94.4.1110G.5

It is an offence for a person to disclose, in contravention of subsection  (3)
or  (4) , any revenue and customs information relating to a person whose
identity—

94.4.1110G.5.a

is specified in the disclosure, or

94.4.1110G.5.b

can be deduced from it.

94.4.1110G.6

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (5)  to
prove that the person reasonably believed—

94.4.1110G.6.a

that the disclosure was lawful, or

94.4.1110G.6.b

that the information had already lawfully been made available to the public.

94.4.1110G.7

Subsections (4) to (7) of section 19 of the Commissioners for Revenue and
Customs Act 2005 apply to an offence under subsection  (5)  as they apply to
an offence under that section.

94.4.1110G.8

In this section—

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act); “ HMRC ” means the
Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs; “ HMRC information ”
means information disclosed to the registrar under section  1110E  by HMRC or
a person acting on behalf of HMRC; “ revenue and customs information relating
to a person ” has the meaning given by section 19(2) of the Commissioners for
Revenue and Customs Act 2005.

94.5

In section 1114 (application of provisions about documents and delivery), in
subsection (1)(b), at the end insert  “(but do not include the provision of
any information by virtue of section  1110E  or any other enactment
authorising the disclosure of information to the registrar)” .

94.6

Schedule 3 contains consequential amendments.

95.3

95.3.a

the company, and

95.3.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

95.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

95.4.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

95.4.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

##### Use or disclosure of PSC information by companies

96

96.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

96.2

For section 790ZG substitute—

########### Power to make regulations protecting material

96.2.790ZG

96.2.790ZG.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

96.2.790ZG.1.a

require a company to refrain from using, or refrain from disclosing, relevant
PSC particulars except in circumstances specified in the regulations;

96.2.790ZG.1.b

confer power on the registrar, on application, to make an order requiring a
company to refrain from using, or refrain from disclosing, relevant PSC
particulars except in circumstances specified in the regulations.

96.2.790ZG.2

“ Relevant PSC particulars ” means such particulars of a person with
significant control over the company as may be prescribed.

96.2.790ZG.3

The reference in subsection  (2)  to a person with significant control over
the company—

96.2.790ZG.3.a

includes a person who used to be such a person, but

96.2.790ZG.3.b

does not include any person in relation to which this Part has effect by
virtue of section 790C(12) as if the person were an individual.

96.2.790ZG.4

96.2.790ZG.4.a

who may make an application;

96.2.790ZG.4.b

96.2.790ZG.4.c

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application;

96.2.790ZG.4.d

how an application is to be determined;

96.2.790ZG.4.e

the notice to be given of an application and its outcome;

96.2.790ZG.4.f

disclosure.

96.2.790ZG.5

Provision under subsection  (4)  may in particular—

96.2.790ZG.5.a

confer a discretion on the registrar;

96.2.790ZG.5.b

provide for a question to be referred to a person other than the registrar for
the purposes of determining the application or revoking the restrictions.

96.2.790ZG.6

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

96.2.790ZG.7

Nothing in this section or in regulations made under it affects the use or
disclosure of particulars of a person in any other capacity (for example, the
use or disclosure of particulars of a person in that person‘s capacity as a
member or director of the company).

96.2.790ZH.2.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

96.2.790ZH.2.b

######### Identity verification of directors

security grounds), with or without modifications.
