#### General offences and enforcement

##### General false statement offences

102

102.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

102.2

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (3), for the entry
relating to sections 1112 and 1113 substitute—

sections  1112 ,  1112A  and 1113 (enforcement).

102.3

For section 1112 substitute—

########### False statements: basic offence

102.3.1112

102.3.1112.1

It is an offence for a person, without reasonable excuse, to—

102.3.1112.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for any purpose of the
Companies Acts, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a
material particular, or

102.3.1112.1.b

make to the registrar, for any purpose of the Companies Acts, a statement that
is misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

102.3.1112.2

Where the offence is committed by a firm, every officer of the firm who is in
default also commits the offence.

102.3.1112.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

102.3.1112.3.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

102.3.1112.3.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

102.3.1112.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

########### False statements: aggravated offence

102.3.1112A

102.3.1112A.1

It is an offence for a person knowingly to—

102.3.1112A.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for any purpose of the
Companies Acts, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a
material particular, or

102.3.1112A.1.b

make to the registrar, for any purpose of the Companies Acts, a statement that
is misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

102.3.1112A.2

Where the offence is committed by a firm, every officer of the firm who is in
default also commits the offence.

102.3.1112A.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

102.3.1112A.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

102.3.1112A.3.b

on summary conviction—

102.3.1112A.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

102.3.1112A.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

102.3.1112A.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

102.4

In section 1126 (consents required for certain prosecutions)—

102.4.a

in subsection (1), for the entry relating to section 1112 substitute—

section  1112  or  1112A  of this Act (false statement offences);

;

102.4.b

in subsections (2)(a)(iv) and (3)(a)(iv), after “1112” insert  “or  1112A ” .

##### False statement offences: national security etc defence

103

103.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

103.2

In section 1059A (scheme of Part 35), in subsection (2), at the appropriate
place insert—

section  1112B  (false statement offences: national security etc defence).

103.3

After section  1112A  (inserted by section 102 of this Act) insert—

########### False statements offences: national security etc defence

103.3.1112B

103.3.1112B.1

A person to whom a certificate is issued by the Secretary of State for the
purposes of this section is not liable for the commission of any offence
relating to the delivery to the registrar, or the making of a statement, that
is misleading, false or deceptive.

103.3.1112B.2

The Secretary of State may issue a certificate to a person for the purposes of
this section only if satisfied that it is necessary for the person to engage
in conduct amounting to such an offence—

103.3.1112B.2.a

in the interests of national security, or

103.3.1112B.2.b

for the purposes of preventing or detecting serious crime.

103.3.1112B.3

A certificate under this section may be revoked by the Secretary of State at
any time.

103.3.1112B.4

For the purposes of subsection  (2)(b) —

103.3.1112B.4.a

“ crime ” means conduct which—

103.3.1112B.4.a.i

constitutes a criminal offence, or

103.3.1112B.4.a.ii

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute a criminal offence, and

103.3.1112B.4.b

crime is “serious” if—

103.3.1112B.4.b.i

the offence which is or would be constituted by the conduct is an offence for
which the maximum sentence (in any part of the United Kingdom) is imprisonment
for 3 years or more, or

103.3.1112B.4.b.ii

the conduct involves the use of violence, results in substantial financial
gain or is conduct by a large number of persons in pursuit of a common
purpose.

##### Financial penalties

104

104.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

104.2

In the heading to Part 36 (Offences under the Companies Acts), at the end
insert  “and financial penalties” .

104.3

After section 1132 insert—

########### Financial penalties

############ Power to make provision for financial penalties

104.3.1132A

104.3.1132A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision conferring power on
the registrar to impose a financial penalty on a person if satisfied, beyond
reasonable doubt, that the person has engaged in conduct amounting to a
relevant offence under this Act.

104.3.1132A.2

“ Relevant offence under this Act ” means any offence under this Act other
than an offence under a provision contained in—

104.3.1132A.2.a

Part 12 (company secretaries);

104.3.1132A.2.b

Part 13 (resolutions and meetings);

104.3.1132A.2.c

Part 16 (audit).

104.3.1132A.3

The regulations may include provision—

104.3.1132A.3.a

about the procedure to be followed in imposing penalties;

104.3.1132A.3.b

about the amount of penalties;

104.3.1132A.3.c

for the imposition of interest or additional penalties for late payment;

104.3.1132A.3.d

conferring rights of appeal against penalties;

104.3.1132A.3.e

about the enforcement of penalties.

104.3.1132A.4

Provision made under subsection  (3)(b)  must ensure that the maximum
financial penalty that may be imposed does not exceed £10,000.

104.3.1132A.5

The regulations must provide that—

104.3.1132A.5.a

no financial penalty may be imposed under the regulations on a person in
respect of conduct amounting to an offence if—

104.3.1132A.5.a.i

proceedings have been brought against the person for that offence in respect
of that conduct and the proceedings are ongoing, or

104.3.1132A.5.a.ii

the person has been convicted of that offence in respect of that conduct, and

104.3.1132A.5.b

no proceedings may be brought against a person in respect of conduct amounting
to an offence if the person has been given a financial penalty under the
regulations in respect of that conduct.

104.3.1132A.6

Amounts recovered by the registrar under the regulations are to be paid into
the Consolidated Fund.

104.3.1132A.7

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

104.3.1132A.8

In this section “ conduct ” means an act or omission.

registrar.

105.7

For subsection (6) substitute—

105.7.6

The regulations must confer a right on a company to appeal to the court
against any decision to change the address of its registered office under the
regulations.

105.7.6A

If the regulations enable a person to apply for a company’s registered office
to be changed, they must also confer a right on the applicant to appeal to the
court against a refusal of the application.

##### Rectification of register: service addresses

106

106.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

106.2

After section 1097A insert—

########### Rectification of register: service addresses

106.2.1097B

106.2.1097B.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising or
requiring the registrar to change a registered service address of a relevant
person if satisfied that the address does not meet the requirements of section
1141(1) and (2).

106.2.1097B.2

In this section—

“ registered service address ”, in relation to a relevant person, means the
address for the time being shown in the register as the person’s current
service address; “ relevant person ” means— a director of a company that is
not an overseas company, a secretary or one of the joint secretaries of a
company that is not an overseas company, or a registrable person or
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company (within the
meanings given by section 790C).

106.2.1097B.3

The regulations may authorise or require the address to be changed on the
registrar’s own motion or on an application by another person.

106.2.1097B.4

The regulations must provide for the change in the address to be effected by
the registrar proceeding as if the company had given notice under section
167H, 279H or 790LD of the change.

106.2.1097B.5

The regulations may make provision as to—

106.2.1097B.5.a

who may make an application,

106.2.1097B.5.b

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application,

106.2.1097B.5.c

the registrar requiring the company or an applicant to provide information for
the purposes of determining anything under the regulations,

106.2.1097B.5.d

the notice to be given of an application or that the registrar is considering
the exercise of powers under the regulations,

106.2.1097B.5.e

the notice to be given of any decision under the regulations,

106.2.1097B.5.f

the period in which objections to an application may be made,

106.2.1097B.5.g

how the registrar is to determine whether a registered service address meets
the requirements of section 1141(1) and (2), including in particular the
evidence, or descriptions of evidence, which the registrar may without further
enquiry rely on to be satisfied that the address meets those requirements,

106.2.1097B.5.h

the referral by the registrar of any question for determination by the court,

106.2.1097B.5.i

the registrar requiring the company to provide an address to be registered as
the relevant person’s service address,

106.2.1097B.5.j

the nomination by the registrar of an address (a “default address”) to be
registered as the relevant person’s service address (which need not meet the
requirements of section 1141(1) and (2)),

106.2.1097B.5.k

the period for which the default address is permitted to be the relevant
person’s registered service address, and

106.2.1097B.5.l

when the change of address takes effect and the consequences of registration
of the change (including provision similar or corresponding to section
1140(5)).

106.2.1097B.6

The provision made by virtue of subsection  (5)(k)  may in particular include
provision creating summary offences punishable with a fine not exceeding level
3 on the standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine
not exceeding one-tenth of level 3 on the standard scale.

106.2.1097B.7

The regulations must confer a right on the company to appeal to the court
against any decision to change the relevant person’s registered service
address under the regulations.

106.2.1097B.8

If the regulations enable a person to apply for a registered service address
to be changed, they must also confer a right on the applicant to appeal to the
court against a refusal of the application.

106.2.1097B.9

On an appeal, the court must direct the registrar to register such address as
the relevant person’s registered service address as the court considers
appropriate in all the circumstances of the case.

106.2.1097B.10

The regulations may make further provision about an appeal and in particular—

106.2.1097B.10.a

provision about the time within which an appeal must be brought and the
grounds on which an appeal may be brought;

106.2.1097B.10.b

further provision about directions by virtue of subsection  (9) .

106.2.1097B.11

The regulations may include such provision applying (including applying with
modifications), amending or repealing an enactment contained in this Act as
the Secretary of State considers necessary or expedient in consequence of any
provision made by the regulations.

106.2.1097B.12

Regulations under this section may in particular confer a discretion on the
registrar.

106.2.1097B.13

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

106.3

In section 1087 (material not available for public inspection), in subsection
(1)(ga)—

106.3.a

after “1097A” insert  “,  1097B ” ;

106.3.b

for “company registered office” substitute  “registered office, service
address” .

##### Rectification of register: principal office addresses

107

107.1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

107.2

After section  1097B  (inserted by section 106) insert—

########### Rectification of register: principal office addresses

107.2.1097C

107.2.1097C.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising or
requiring the registrar to change the address registered as the principal
office of a relevant person if satisfied that the address is not in fact their
principal office.

107.2.1097C.2

In this section—

“ address registered as the principal office ”, in relation to a relevant
person, means the address for the time being shown in the register as the
address of the person’s current principal office; “ relevant person ” means— a
director of a company that is not an overseas company, a secretary or one of
the joint secretaries of a company that is not an overseas company, a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company (within the meaning
given by section 790C), or a registrable person in relation to a company
(within the meaning given by section 790C) who falls within section 790C(12).

107.2.1097C.3

The regulations may authorise or require the address to be changed on the
registrar’s own motion or on an application by another person.

107.2.1097C.4

The regulations must provide for the change in the address to be effected by
the registrar proceeding as if the company had given notice under section
167H, 279H or 790LD of the change.

107.2.1097C.5

The regulations may make provision as to—

107.2.1097C.5.a

who may make an application,

107.2.1097C.5.b

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application,

107.2.1097C.5.c

the registrar requiring the company or an applicant to provide information for
the purposes of determining anything under the regulations,

107.2.1097C.5.d

the notice to be given of an application or that the registrar is considering
the exercise of powers under the regulations,

107.2.1097C.5.e

the notice to be given of any decision under the regulations,

107.2.1097C.5.f

the period in which objections to an application may be made,

107.2.1097C.5.g

how the registrar is to determine whether an address registered as the
principal office of a relevant person is in fact the person’s principal
office, including in particular the evidence, or descriptions of evidence,
which the registrar may without further enquiry rely on to be satisfied that
the address meets those requirements,

107.2.1097C.5.h

the referral by the registrar of any question for determination by the court,

107.2.1097C.5.i

the registrar requiring the company to provide an address to be registered as
the principal office of the relevant person,

107.2.1097C.5.j

the nomination by the registrar of an address (a “default address”) to be
registered as the principal office of the relevant person (which need not be
the relevant person’s actual principal office),

107.2.1097C.5.k

the period for which the default address is permitted to be the address
registered as the principal office of the relevant person, and

107.2.1097C.5.l

when the change of address takes effect and the consequences of registration
of the change.

107.2.1097C.6

The provision made by virtue of subsection  (5)(k)  may in particular include
provision creating summary offences punishable with a fine not exceeding level
3 on the standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine
not exceeding one-tenth of level 3 on the standard scale.

107.2.1097C.7

The regulations must confer a right on the company to appeal to the court
against any decision to change the address registered as the principal office
of the relevant person under the regulations.

107.2.1097C.8

If the regulations enable a person to apply for the address registered as the
principal office of a relevant person to be changed, the regulations must also
confer a right on the applicant to appeal to the court against a refusal of
the application.

107.2.1097C.9

On an appeal, the court must direct the registrar to register such address as
the principal office of the relevant person as the court considers appropriate
in all the circumstances of the case.

107.2.1097C.10

The regulations may make further provision about an appeal and in particular—

107.2.1097C.10.a

provision about the time within which an appeal must be brought and the
grounds on which an appeal may be brought;

107.2.1097C.10.b

further provision about directions by virtue of subsection  (9) .

107.2.1097C.11

The regulations may include such provision applying (including applying with
modifications), amending or repealing an enactment contained in this Act as
the Secretary of State considers necessary or expedient in consequence of any
provision made by the regulations.

107.2.1097C.12

Regulations under this section may in particular confer a discretion on the
registrar.

107.2.1097C.13

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

##### Meaning of “limited partnership”

###### Meaning of “limited partnership”

(2)  and  (3) .

“ limited partnership ” means a firm that is registered as a limited
partnership under this Act (for the only circumstances in which a firm can
cease to be registered as a limited partnership under this Act while remaining
a firm see section 26 (voluntary deregistration));

.

##### Required information about limited partnerships

###### Required information about partners

110

110.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

110.2

In section 3 (interpretation of terms)—

110.2.a

the existing text becomes subsection (1);

110.2.b

in that subsection, at the appropriate places insert—

“ body corporate ” has the same meaning as in the Companies Acts (see section
1173 of the Companies Act 2006);”;

;

“managing officer”— in relation to a company, means a director or shadow
director; in relation to a legal entity the affairs of which are managed by
some or all of its members, means one of those members; in relation to any
other legal entity, means an officer of the entity whose functions correspond
to that of a director of a company;”;

;

“ legal entity ” means a body corporate or other entity that (in each case) is
a legal person under the law by which it is governed;

;

“ service address ” has the same meaning as in the Companies Acts (see section
1141(1) and (2) of the Companies Act 2006).

;

110.2.c

after that subsection insert—

110.2.c.2

For the purposes of the definition of “managing officer” in subsection (1), “
director ” and “ shadow director ” have the same meanings as in the Companies
Acts (see sections 250 and 251 of the Companies Act 2006).

110.2.c.3

In this section “ the Companies Acts ” has the meaning given by section 2(1)
of the Companies Act 2006.

110.3

In section 4 (definition and constitution of limited partnership), in
subsection (4), for “body corporate” substitute  “legal entity” .

110.4

In section 8A (application for registration)—

110.4.a

in subsection (1)(c), after “each” insert  “proposed” ;

110.4.b

in subsections (2)(b) and (c), for “name of each” substitute  “required
information about each proposed” ;

110.4.c

in subsection (2)(d), after “each” insert  “proposed” ;

110.4.d

in subsections (3)(a) and (b), for “name of each” substitute  “required
information about each proposed” ;

110.4.e

after subsection (3) insert—

110.4.e.3A

For the required information about a proposed general partner or a proposed
limited partner see Part 2 of the Schedule.

110.5

Schedule 4 inserts a Schedule into the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 setting
out the required information about partners.

###### Required information about partners: transitional provision

111

111.1

This section applies in relation to a limited partnership that was registered
under the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 in pursuance of an application for
registration delivered to the registrar before section 110 (4)  came fully
into force.

111.2

The general partners in the limited partnership must, within the transitional
period, deliver a statement to the registrar specifying the required
information (within the meaning of the Schedule to that Act (inserted by
Schedule 4 to this Act)) about each person who—

111.2.a

is a partner in the limited partnership, and

111.2.b

became a partner on the registration of the limited partnership.

111.3

If a change in the required information about such a partner occurs before
whichever is earlier of—

111.3.a

the end of the transitional period, and

111.3.b

the delivery of the statement mentioned in subsection  (2) ,

the general partners in the limited partnership are not required by the
provisions mentioned in subsection  (4)  to give notice to the registrar of
the change, unless it is a change to the partner’s name.

111.4

The provisions are—

111.4.a

section 8S(1) of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 122 of
this Act), and

111.4.b

so far as it relates to section 8S(1) of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
section 10D(2)(a) of that Act (inserted by section 126 of this Act).

111.5

In this section—

“ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Limited Partnerships Act 1907
(see section 15 of that Act); “ transitional period ” means the period of 6
months beginning when section 110 (4)  came fully into force.

111.6

Failure by the general partners in a limited partnership to comply with
subsection  (2)  is, in the absence of any evidence to the contrary, to be
treated by the registrar as reasonable cause to believe that the limited
partnership has been dissolved for the purposes of section 19 of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 (registrar’s power to confirm dissolution of limited
partnership) (inserted by section 141 of this Act).

111.7

Where the registrar proposes to rely on a failure by the general partners in
the limited partnership to comply with subsection  (2)  as grounds for
exercising the power in section 19 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
subsections (2) to (4) of that section (publication of warning notice) do not
apply.

##### Registered offices

###### A limited partnership’s registered office

113

113.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

113.2

In section 3 (interpretation of terms)—

113.2.a

in subsection (1) (created by section 110 of this Act), at the appropriate
place insert—

“ authorised corporate service provider ” has the same meaning as in the
Companies Act 2006 (see section 1098A of that Act);

;

113.2.b

after subsection (3) (inserted by section 110 of this Act) insert—

113.2.b.4

Section 1125 of the Companies Act 2006 (meaning of “ daily default fine ”)
applies for the purpose of any provision made by this Act as it applies for
the purposes of provisions of the Companies Acts.

113.3

In section 8A (application for registration)—

113.3.a

in subsection (1), after paragraph (a) insert—

113.3.a.aa

specify the intended address of the limited partnership’s registered office,
which must be an appropriate address within the meaning given by section  8E
(2) ,

113.3.a.ab

specify which of the addresses mentioned in section  8E (2)(c)  the intended
address is,

;

113.3.b

after subsection (1) insert—

113.3.b.1A

An application for registration of a limited partnership which specifies that
the intended address of its registered office is an address mentioned in
section  8E (2) (c)(iv)  must be accompanied by a statement by the authorised
corporate service provider confirming that the address is the authorised
corporate service provider’s address.

113.4

After section 8D insert—

############ A limited partnership’s registered office

############# Duty to ensure registered office at appropriate address

113.4.8E

113.4.8E.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must ensure that its registered
office is at all times at an appropriate address.

113.4.8E.2

An address is an “appropriate address” if—

113.4.8E.2.a

in the ordinary course of events—

113.4.8E.2.a.i

a document addressed to the limited partnership, and delivered there by hand
or by post, would be expected to come to the attention of a person acting on
behalf of the limited partnership, and

113.4.8E.2.a.ii

the delivery of documents there is capable of being recorded by the obtaining
of an acknowledgement of delivery,

113.4.8E.2.b

it is in the part of the United Kingdom in which the limited partnership is
registered, and

113.4.8E.2.c

it is at least one of the following—

113.4.8E.2.c.i

the address of the principal place of business of the limited partnership;

113.4.8E.2.c.ii

the usual residential address of a general partner who is an individual;

113.4.8E.2.c.iii

the address of the registered or principal office of a general partner that is
a legal entity;

113.4.8E.2.c.iv

an address of an authorised corporate service provider that is acting for the
limited partnership.

113.4.8E.3

If the general partners fail to comply with this section an offence is
committed by each general partner who is in default.

113.4.8E.4

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

113.4.8E.5

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity also commits the offence if—

113.4.8E.5.a

the managing officer is an individual who is in default, or

113.4.8E.5.b

the managing officer is a legal entity that is in default and one of its
managing officers is in default.

113.4.8E.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

113.4.8E.6.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

113.4.8E.6.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

113.4.8E.7

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

113.4.8E.8

Subsection  (1)  does not apply in relation to a limited partnership during
any period for which the address of its registered office is an address
nominated by the registrar by virtue of regulations made under section  8G .

############# Change of address of registered office by general partners

113.4.8F

113.4.8F.1

The address of a limited partnership’s registered office can be changed by the
general partners giving notice to the registrar.

113.4.8F.2

The notice must include a statement—

113.4.8F.2.a

that the new address is an appropriate address within the meaning given by
section  8E (2) , and

113.4.8F.2.b

specifying which of the addresses in section  8E (2)(c)  the address is.

113.4.8F.3

If the statement under subsection  (2)(b)  specifies that the address is an
address mentioned in section  8E (2) (c)(iv) , the notice must be accompanied
by a statement by the authorised corporate service provider confirming that
the address is the authorised corporate service provider’s address.

113.4.8F.4

The change takes effect upon the notice being registered by the registrar, but
until the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the date on which it is
registered a person may validly serve any document on the limited partnership
at the address previously registered.

############# Regulations about change of address of registered office by registrar

113.4.8G

113.4.8G.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising or
requiring the registrar to change the address of a limited partnership’s
registered office if satisfied that it is not an appropriate address within
the meaning given by section  8E (2) .

113.4.8G.2

The regulations may authorise or require the address to be changed on the
registrar’s own motion or on an application by another person.

113.4.8G.3

The regulations—

113.4.8G.3.a

may include provision corresponding or similar to any provision that may be
included in regulations under section 1097A of the Companies Act 2006;

113.4.8G.3.b

must include—

113.4.8G.3.b.i

provision about appeals corresponding to the provision that must be included
in regulations under section 1097A by virtue of subsections  (6)  and  (6A)
of that section;

113.4.8G.3.b.ii

provision corresponding to subsection (7) of that section.

113.4.8G.4

The provision that may be made by virtue of subsection  (3)(a)  that is
corresponding or similar to provision that may be made by virtue of section
1097A (4A)(b)  and  (4B)  of the Companies Act 2006 (strike off and
restoration) includes provision applying or writing out, with or without
modifications, any provision made by section 19 (power to confirm dissolution)
or section 20 (administrative revival).

113.4.8G.5

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

###### A limited partnership’s registered office: transitional provision

114

114.1

This section applies in relation to a limited partnership registered under the
Limited Partnerships Act 1907 in pursuance of an application for registration
delivered to the registrar before section 113 (3)  came fully into force.

114.2

The general partners must, within the transitional period, deliver to the
registrar a statement specifying—

114.2.a

the address of its registered office (which must be an appropriate address
within the meaning given by section  8E (2)  of that Act (inserted by section
113 (4)  of this Act)), and

114.2.b

which of the addresses in section  8E (2)(c)  of that Act the address is.

114.3

If the statement under subsection  (2)(b)  specifies that the address is an
address mentioned in section  8E (2) (c) (iv)  of the Limited Partnerships Act
1907, the notice must be accompanied by a statement by the authorised
corporate service provider confirming that the address is the authorised
corporate service provider’s address.

114.4

The provisions mentioned in subsection  (5)  do not apply in respect of the
limited partnership until—

114.4.a

the end of the transitional period, or

114.4.b

if earlier, the delivery of the statement mentioned in subsection  (2) .

114.5

Those provisions are—

114.5.a

section  8E  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 113 (4)
of this Act);

114.5.b

section  10D (2)(b)  of that Act (inserted by section 126 of this Act).

114.6

In this section—

“ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Limited Partnerships Act 1907
(see section 15 of that Act); “ transitional period ” means the period of 6
months beginning when section 113 (3)  came fully into force.

114.7

Failure by the general partners in the limited partnership to comply with
subsection  (2)  is, in the absence of any evidence to the contrary, to be
treated by the registrar as reasonable cause to believe that the limited
partnership has been dissolved for the purposes of section 19 of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 (registrar’s power to confirm dissolution of limited
partnership) (inserted by section 141 of this Act).

114.8

Where the registrar proposes to rely on a failure by the general partners in
the limited partnership to comply with subsection  (2)  as grounds for
exercising the power in section 19 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
subsections (2) to (4) of that section (publication of warning notice) do not
apply.

##### Registered email addresses

###### A limited partnership’s registered email address

116

116.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

116.2

116.2.ac

specify the intended registered email address of the limited partnership,

8H (2) ,

.

116.3

After section  8G  (inserted by section 113 of this Act) insert—

############ A limited partnership‘s registered email address

############# Duty to maintain a registered email address

116.3.8H

116.3.8H.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must ensure that its registered
email address is at all times an appropriate email address.

116.3.8H.2

An email address is an “appropriate email address” if, in the ordinary course
of events, emails sent to it by the registrar would be expected to come to the
attention of a person acting on behalf of the limited partnership.

116.3.8H.3

If the general partners fail to comply with this section an offence is
committed by each general partner who is in default.

116.3.8H.4

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

116.3.8H.5

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity also commits the offence if—

116.3.8H.5.a

the managing officer is an individual who is in default, or

116.3.8H.5.b

the managing officer is a legal entity that is in default and one of its
managing officers is in default.

116.3.8H.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

116.3.8H.6.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

116.3.8H.6.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

116.3.8H.7

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

############# Change of registered email address

116.3.8I

116.3.8I.1

A limited partnership’s registered email address can be changed by the general
partners giving notice to the registrar.

116.3.8I.2

The notice must include a statement that the new address is an appropriate
email address within the meaning given by section  8H (2) .

116.3.8I.3

The change takes effect upon the notice being registered by the registrar.

###### A limited partnership’s registered email address: transitional provision

117

117.1

This section applies in relation to a limited partnership registered under the
Limited Partnerships Act 1907 in pursuance of an application for registration
delivered to the registrar before section 116 (2)  came fully into force.

117.2

The general partners must, within the transitional period, deliver to the
registrar a statement specifying its registered email address (which must be
an appropriate email address within the meaning given by section  8H (2)  of
that Act (inserted by section 116 (3)  of this Act)).

117.3

The provisions mentioned in subsection  (4)  do not apply in respect of the
limited partnership until—

117.3.a

the end of the transitional period, or

117.3.b

if earlier, the delivery of the statement mentioned in subsection  (2) .

117.4

Those provisions are—

117.4.a

section  8H  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 116 (3)
of this Act);

117.4.b

section  10D (2)(c)  of that Act (inserted by section 126 of this Act).

117.5

In this section—

“ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Limited Partnerships Act 1907
(see section 15 of that Act); “ transitional period ” means the period of 6
months beginning when section 116 (2)  came fully into force.

117.6

Failure by the general partners in a limited partnership to comply with
subsection  (2)  is, in the absence of any evidence to the contrary, to be
treated by the registrar as reasonable cause to believe that the limited
partnership has been dissolved for the purposes of section  19  of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 (registrar’s power to confirm dissolution of limited
partnership) (inserted by section 141 of this Act).

117.7

Where the registrar proposes to rely on a failure by the general partners in
the limited partnership to comply with subsection  (2)  as grounds for
exercising the power in section  19  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
subsections  (2)  to  (4)  of that section (publication of warning notice) do
not apply.

##### The general partners

###### Restrictions on general partners

118

118.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

118.2

In section 8A (application for registration)—

118.2.a

after subsection  (1A)  (inserted by section 113 of this Act) insert—

118.2.a.1B

The application must also contain a statement that none of the proposed
general partners is disqualified under the directors disqualification
legislation (see subsection (8)).

;

118.2.b

in subsection (8), at the appropriate place insert—

“disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation”— in relation
to a statement about a person delivered to the registrar for England and Wales
or Scotland, means that the person falls within any of the entries in the
first column of Part 1 of the table in section 159A of the Companies Act 2006;
in relation to a statement about a person delivered to the registrar for
Northern Ireland, means that the person falls within any of the entries in the
first column of Part 2 of that table;

118.3

After section  8I  (inserted by section 116 of this Act) insert—

############ Duty to remove disqualified general partners

############# Duty to remove disqualified general partners

118.3.8J

118.3.8J.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must take any steps that are
necessary to ensure that any general partner in the limited partnership who is
disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see subsection
(3) ) ceases to be a general partner.

118.3.8J.2

Examples of the types of steps that the general partners might need to take
include—

118.3.8J.2.a

enforcing any express or implied agreement between the partners;

118.3.8J.2.b

giving any notice, making any application or otherwise acting to dissolve the
limited partnership.

118.3.8J.3

A general partner in a limited partnership is “disqualified under the
directors disqualification legislation” if—

118.3.8J.3.a

where the limited partnership is registered in England and Wales or Scotland,
the general partner falls within any of the entries in the first column of
Part 1 of the table in section 159A of the Companies Act 2006;

118.3.8J.3.b

where the limited partnership is registered in Northern Ireland, the general
partner falls within any of the entries in the first column of Part 2 of that
table.

118.3.8J.4

Subsection  (1)  applies irrespective of whether the general partner concerned
became disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation before or
after this section comes into force.

118.3.8J.5

If the general partners fail to comply with this section an offence is
committed by each general partner who is in default.

118.3.8J.6

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

118.3.8J.7

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity also commits the offence if—

118.3.8J.7.a

the managing officer is an individual who is in default, or

118.3.8J.7.b

the managing officer is a legal entity that is in default and one of its
managing officers is in default.

118.3.8J.8

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

118.3.8J.8.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

118.3.8J.8.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

118.3.8J.9

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

###### Officers of general partners

119

119.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

119.2

In section 3 (interpretation of terms), in subsection (1) (created by section
110 of this Act), at the appropriate place insert—

“ corporate managing officer ” means a managing officer that is a legal
entity;

.

119.3

In section 8A (application for registration), after subsection  (1B)
(inserted by section 118 of this Act) insert—

119.3.1C

The application must be accompanied by a statement by each proposed general
partner that is a legal entity (if any) specifying the name of its proposed
registered officer, who must be an individual—

119.3.1C.a

who is one of the general partner’s managing officers,

119.3.1C.b

who is not disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see
subsection (8)), and

119.3.1C.c

whose identity is verified (within the meaning of section 1110A of the
Companies Act 2006).

119.3.1D

The application must also be accompanied by one of the following statements by
each proposed general partner that is a legal entity (if any)—

119.3.1D.a

a statement that the general partner does not have any corporate managing
officers, or

119.3.1D.b

if the general partner has one or more corporate managing officers, a
statement specifying, for each corporate managing officer, the name of the
proposed named contact for the corporate managing officer.

119.3.1E

The proposed named contact for a corporate managing officer must be an
individual who is a managing officer of the corporate managing officer.

119.3.1F

A statement under subsection  (1C)  must—

119.3.1F.a

contain the required information about the proposed registered officer (see
Part 3 of the Schedule), and

119.3.1F.b

be accompanied by a statement by the individual who is the proposed registered
officer confirming that the individual—

119.3.1F.b.i

is one of the general partner’s managing officers,

119.3.1F.b.ii

is not disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see
subsection (8)), and

119.3.1F.b.iii

is an individual whose identity is verified (within the meaning of section
1110A of the Companies Act 2006).

119.3.1G

A statement under subsection  (1D)(b)  must—

119.3.1G.a

contain the required information about each proposed named contact specified
in the statement (see Part  4  of the Schedule), and

119.3.1G.b

be accompanied by a statement by each proposed named contact confirming that
the proposed named contact is a managing officer of the corporate managing
officer concerned.

119.4

After section  8J  (inserted by section 118 of this Act) insert—

############ Officers of general partners

############# Duty to maintain registered officer and named contacts

119.4.8K

119.4.8K.1

A general partner that is a legal entity must at all times ensure that its
registered officer is an individual—

119.4.8K.1.a

who is one of its managing officers,

119.4.8K.1.b

who is not disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see
subsection  (2) ), and

119.4.8K.1.c

whose identity is verified (within the meaning of section 1110A of the
Companies Act 2006).

119.4.8K.2

The registered officer of a general partner in a limited partnership is
“disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation” if—

119.4.8K.2.a

where the limited partnership is registered in England and Wales or Scotland,
the registered officer falls within any of the entries in the first column of
Part 1 of the table in section 159A of the Companies Act 2006;

119.4.8K.2.b

where the limited partnership is registered in Northern Ireland, the
registered officer falls within any of the entries in the first column of Part
2 of that table.

119.4.8K.3

A general partner that is a legal entity and that has one or more corporate
managing officers must at all times ensure that the named contact for each
corporate managing officer is an individual who is a managing officer of the
corporate managing officer.

119.4.8K.4

In this section “ registered officer ”, in relation to a general partner that
is a legal entity, means—

119.4.8K.4.a

the individual whose name is specified by the general partner in—

119.4.8K.4.a.i

a statement delivered to the registrar under section 8A (1C)  or 8R(4), or

119.4.8K.4.a.ii

a statement delivered to the registrar under section 120 (2)(a)  or 124 (2)(a)
of the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023 (transitional
cases),

unless the general partner has changed its registered officer under section
8L (1) , or

119.4.8K.4.b

if the general partner has changed its registered officer under section  8L
(1) , the individual specified in the latest notice under that provision.

119.4.8K.5

In this section “ named contact ”, in relation to the corporate managing
officer of a general partner, means—

119.4.8K.5.a

the individual whose name is specified by the general partner for that
corporate managing officer in—

119.4.8K.5.a.i

a statement delivered to the registrar under section 8A (1D)(b) , 8R(5)(b) or
8N (3) , or

119.4.8K.5.a.ii

a statement delivered to the registrar under section 120 (2)(b)(ii)  or 124
(2)(b)(ii)  of the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023
(transitional cases),

unless the general partner has changed the named contact for that corporate
managing officer under section  8L (2) , or

119.4.8K.5.b

if the general partner has changed the named contact for that corporate
managing officer under section  8L (2) , the individual specified in the
latest notice under that provision.

119.4.8K.6

If a general partner’s registered officer ceases to fall within the
description mentioned in subsection  (1)(a)  or  (b) , the general partner
does not fail to comply with subsection  (1)  by reason of that fact during
the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the registered officer
so ceases.

119.4.8K.7

If the named contact for a general partner’s corporate managing officer ceases
to be a managing officer of the corporate managing officer, the general
partner does not fail to comply with subsection  (3)  by reason of that fact
during the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the named contact
so ceases.

############# Change of registered officers and named contacts by general partner

119.4.8L

119.4.8L.1

A general partner may change its registered officer for the purposes of
section  8K (1)  by giving notice to the registrar containing the required
information about the new registered officer (see Part 3 of the Schedule).

119.4.8L.2

A general partner may change the named contact for a corporate managing
officer of the general partner for the purposes of section  8K (3)  by giving
notice to the registrar containing the required information about the new
named contact (see Part  4  of the Schedule).

119.4.8L.3

A notice under subsection  (1)  must—

119.4.8L.3.a

include a statement by the general partner confirming that the new registered
officer is an individual who meets the requirements in section 8K(1)(a) to
(c), and

119.4.8L.3.b

be accompanied by a statement by the individual who is the new registered
officer confirming that the individual meets the requirements in section
8K(1)(a) to (c).

119.4.8L.4

A notice under subsection  (2)  must—

119.4.8L.4.a

include a statement by the general partner that the new named contact for the
corporate managing officer is a managing officer of the corporate managing
officer, and

119.4.8L.4.b

be accompanied by a statement by the individual who is the new named contact
confirming that the individual is an managing officer of the corporate
managing officer.

############# Duty to notify changes in general partner’s registered officer

119.4.8M

119.4.8M.1

A general partner that is a legal entity must give notice to the registrar of
any change in the required information about its registered officer (see Part
3  of the Schedule).

119.4.8M.2

A general partner that is a legal entity must give notice to the registrar of
any change in the required information about its proposed registered officer
that occurred—

119.4.8M.2.a

after the application for registration of the limited partnership in which the
entity is a general partner was delivered to the registrar under section 8A,
but

119.4.8M.2.b

before the limited partnership was registered.

119.4.8M.3

A notice under this section must specify the date on which the change to which
it relates occurred.

119.4.8M.4

A notice under subsection  (1)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the change occurs.

119.4.8M.5

A notice under subsection  (2)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the limited partnership was registered.

119.4.8M.6

In this section “ registered officer ” has the meaning given by section  8K
(4) .

############# Duty to notify named contact

119.4.8N

119.4.8N.1

A general partner that is a legal entity must give notice to the registrar if
a legal entity becomes a corporate managing officer of the general partner.

119.4.8N.2

A general partner that is a legal entity must give notice to the registrar if
a legal entity became a corporate managing officer of the general partner—

119.4.8N.2.a

after the application for registration of the limited partnership in which the
entity is a general partner was delivered to the registrar under section 8A,
but

119.4.8N.2.b

before the limited partnership was registered.

119.4.8N.3

A notice under this section must include a statement specifying the name of
the proposed named contact for the corporate managing officer.

119.4.8N.4

The proposed named contact for a corporate managing officer must be an
individual who is a managing officer of the corporate managing officer.

119.4.8N.5

The statement must—

119.4.8N.5.a

contain the required information about the proposed named contact specified in
the statement (see Part 4 of the Schedule), and

119.4.8N.5.b

be accompanied by a statement by the proposed named contact confirming that
the proposed named contact is a managing officer of the corporate managing
officer.

119.4.8N.6

A notice under subsection  (1)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the legal entity becomes a corporate managing
officer of the general partner.

119.4.8N.7

A notice under subsection  (2)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the limited partnership was registered.

############# Duty to notify changes in named contacts

119.4.8O

119.4.8O.1

This section applies where a general partner that is a legal entity has one or
more corporate managing officers.

119.4.8O.2

The general partner must give notice to the registrar of any change in the
required information about the named contact for any corporate managing
officer (see Part 4 of the Schedule).

119.4.8O.3

The general partner must give notice to the registrar of any change in the
required information about the proposed named contact for any corporate
managing officer that occurred—

119.4.8O.3.a

after the application for registration of the limited partnership in which the
entity is a general partner was delivered to the registrar under section 8A,
but

119.4.8O.3.b

before the limited partnership was registered.

119.4.8O.4

A notice under this section must specify the date on which the change to which
it relates occurred.

119.4.8O.5

A notice under subsection  (2)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the change occurs.

119.4.8O.6

A notice under subsection  (3)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the limited partnership was registered.

119.4.8O.7

In this section “ named contact ” has the meaning given by section  8K (5) .

############# Failure to comply with obligations relating to officers

119.4.8P

119.4.8P.1

If a general partner fails to comply with section  8K ,  8M ,  8N  or  8O  an
offence is committed by—

119.4.8P.1.a

the general partner, and

119.4.8P.1.b

if the general partner is a legal entity, any of its managing officers who is
in default.

119.4.8P.2

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

119.4.8P.2.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

119.4.8P.2.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

119.4.8P.3

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

119.4.8P.4

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

119.4.8P.5

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(4) ).

############# Regulations about change of registered officer’s address by registrar

119.4.8Q

119.4.8Q.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising or
requiring the registrar to change a registered service address of a registered
officer of a general partner if satisfied that the address does not meet the
requirements of section 1141(1) and (2) of the Companies Act 2006.

119.4.8Q.2

In this section—

“ registered officer ” has the meaning given by section 8K (4) ; “ registered
service address ”, in relation to a registered officer, means the address for
the time being shown in the register as the registered officer’s current
service address.

119.4.8Q.3

The regulations may authorise or require the address to be changed on the
registrar’s own motion or on an application by another person.

119.4.8Q.4

The regulations—

119.4.8Q.4.a

may include provision corresponding or similar to any provision that may be
included in regulations under section 1097B of the Companies Act 2006;

119.4.8Q.4.b

must include—

119.4.8Q.4.b.i

provision about appeals corresponding to the provision that must be included
in regulations under section 1097B by virtue of subsections (7) and (8) of
that section;

119.4.8Q.4.b.ii

provision corresponding to subsection (9) of that section.

119.4.8Q.5

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

###### Officers of general partners: transitional provision

120.1

This section applies in relation to a limited partnership that was registered
under the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 in pursuance of an application for
registration delivered to the registrar before section 119(3) came fully into
force.

120.2

Each general partner that is a legal entity and became a general partner in
the limited partnership on its registration must, within the transitional
period, deliver to the registrar—

120.2.a

a statement of the kind mentioned in section 8A (1C)  of the Limited

statement, mentioned in section 8A (1F)  of that Act (both inserted by section
119 (3)  of this Act), and

120.2.b

either—

120.2.b.i

a statement that the general partner does not have any corporate managing
officers, or

120.2.b.ii

if the general partner has one or more corporate managing officers, a
statement of the kind mentioned in section 8A (1D)(b)  of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 containing the information, and accompanied by the
statement, mentioned in section 8A (1G)  of that Act (both inserted by section
119 (3)  of this Act).

120.3

A general partner mentioned in subsection  (2)  is not required by the
provisions mentioned in subsection  (4)  to give notice to the registrar if a
legal entity becomes a corporate managing officer of the general partner
before whichever is earlier of—

120.3.a

the end of the transitional period, and

120.3.b

the delivery of the statement mentioned in subsection  (2)(b) .

120.4

The provisions are—

120.4.a

section  8N (1)  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 119
of this Act), and

120.4.b

so far as it relates to section  8N (1)  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
section  10D (2)(a)  of that Act (inserted by section 126 of this Act).

120.5

In this section—

“ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Limited Partnerships Act 1907
(see section 15 of that Act); “ transitional period ” means the period of 6
months beginning when section 119 (3)  came fully into force.
