##### Changes in partnerships

###### Notification of information about partners

122

After section 8Q of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 119
of this Act) insert—

########## Notification of information about partners

########### Duty to notify registrar of change in partners

122.8R

122.8R.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must give notice to the
registrar if a person—

122.8R.1.a

becomes a general partner or limited partner in the limited partnership, or

122.8R.1.b

ceases to be a general partner or limited partner in the limited partnership.

122.8R.2

A notice under subsection  (1)(a)  must contain the required information about
the general partner or limited partner (see Part 2 of the Schedule).

122.8R.3

A notice under subsection  (1)(a)  of a person becoming a general partner must
contain a statement that the new general partner is not disqualified under the
directors disqualification legislation (see section  8J (3)).

122.8R.4

A notice under subsection  (1)(a)  of a legal entity becoming a general
partner must be accompanied by a statement by the general partner specifying
the name of its proposed registered officer, who must be an individual who
meets the requirements in section  8K (1)(a) to (c).

122.8R.5

A notice under subsection  (1)(a)  of a legal entity becoming a general
partner must be accompanied by one of the following statements by the general
partner—

122.8R.5.a

a statement that the general partner does not have any corporate managing
officers, or

122.8R.5.b

if the general partner has one or more corporate managing officers, a
statement specifying, for each corporate managing officer, the name of the
proposed named contact for the corporate managing officer.

122.8R.6

The proposed named contact for a corporate managing officer must be an
individual who is a managing officer of the corporate managing officer.

122.8R.7

A statement under subsection  (4)  must—

122.8R.7.a

contain the required information about the proposed registered officer (see
Part 3 of the Schedule), and

122.8R.7.b

be accompanied by a statement by the individual who is the proposed registered
officer confirming that the individual meets the requirements in section  8K
(1)(a)  to  (1)(c) .

122.8R.8

A statement under subsection  (5)(b)  must—

122.8R.8.a

contain the required information about each proposed named contact specified
in the statement (see Part 4 of the Schedule), and

122.8R.8.b

be accompanied by a statement by each proposed named contact confirming that
the proposed named contact is a managing officer of the corporate managing
officer concerned.

122.8R.9

Subsection  (1)(a)  does not require the general partners, on registration of
the limited partnership, to give notice in relation to a person named as a
proposed general partner or a proposed limited partner in the application for
registration under section 8A.

122.8R.10

A notice under subsection  (1)  must specify the date on which the person
became or ceased to be a general partner or limited partner in the limited
partnership.

122.8R.11

A notice under subsection  (1)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the person becomes or ceases to be a general
partner or a limited partner.

########### Duty to notify registrar of changes of information about partners

122.8S

122.8S.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must give notice to the
registrar of any change in the required information about a partner (see Part
2 of the Schedule).

122.8S.2

The general partners in a limited partnership that is not a private fund
limited partnership must give notice to the registrar of any change to the sum
contributed by any limited partner.

122.8S.3

The general partners in a private fund limited partnership that was registered
as a limited partnership before 6th April 2017 must give notice to the
registrar of any withdrawal by a limited partner of the partner’s contribution
which has the effect that the amount of the partner’s contribution is less
than it was on the date on which the limited partnership was designated as a
private fund limited partnership.

122.8S.4

A notice under this section must specify the date on which the change to which
it relates occurred.

122.8S.5

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the change occurs.

########### Notification of changes occurring before registration

122.8T

122.8T.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must give notice to the
registrar if a person named as a proposed general partner or a proposed
limited partner in the application for registration under section 8A did not
become a general partner or limited partner on registration of the limited
partnership.

122.8T.2

The general partners in a limited partnership must give notice to the
registrar of any change in the required information about a proposed general
partner or a proposed limited partner (see Part 2 of the Schedule) that
occurred—

122.8T.2.a

after the application for the limited partnership’s registration under section
8A was delivered to the registrar, but

122.8T.2.b

before the limited partnership was registered.

122.8T.3

A notice under subsection  (2)  must specify the date on which the change
occurred.

122.8T.4

But the general partners are not required to give notice under subsection  (2)
in respect of a person if they give notice under subsection  (1)  in respect
of the person.

122.8T.5

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the limited partnership was registered.

########### Failure to notify information about partners

122.8U

122.8U.1

If the general partners fail to comply with section  8R ,  8S  or  8T  an
offence is committed by each general partner who is in default.

122.8U.2

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

122.8U.3

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity also commits the offence if—

122.8U.3.a

the managing officer is an individual who is in default, or

122.8U.3.b

the managing officer is a legal entity that is in default and one of its
managing officers is in default.

122.8U.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

122.8U.4.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

122.8U.4.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

122.8U.5

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

########### Prohibition on acting unless general partner notified

122.8V

122.8V.1

This section applies where—

122.8V.1.a

a person has become a general partner in a limited partnership otherwise than
on its registration, and

122.8V.1.b

notice under section  8R  of the person having done so has not been given
within the period mentioned in subsection  (11)  of that section.

122.8V.2

The general partner may not take part in the management of the partnership
business until notice is given under section  8R .

122.8V.3

If a general partner contravenes subsection  (2)  an offence is committed by—

122.8V.3.a

the general partner, and

122.8V.3.b

if the general partner is a legal entity, any of its managing officers who is
in default.

122.8V.4

But it is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that they reasonably believed that notice had been given under section
8R .

122.8V.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

122.8V.5.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

122.8V.5.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

122.8V.6

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

122.8V.7

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

122.8V.8

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(7) ).

122.8V.9

The only consequence of contravening subsection  (2)  is the offence provided
for by this section (so that, for example, a contravention does not in any way
affect the validity of the general partner’s actions).

122.8V.10

Nothing in this section shall affect the liability of the general partner for
all debts and obligations of the firm.

########### Regulations about change of general partner’s address by registrar

122.8W

122.8W.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision authorising or
requiring the registrar to—

122.8W.1.a

change a registered service address of a general partner in a limited
partnership if satisfied that the address does not meet the requirements of
section 1141(1) and (2) of the Companies Act 2006;

122.8W.1.b

change the address registered as the principal office of a general partner in
a limited partnership if satisfied that the address is not in fact their
principal office.

122.8W.2

In this section—

“ address registered as the principal office ”, in relation to a general
partner, means the address for the time being shown in the register as the
address of the general partner’s current principal office; “ registered
service address ”, in relation to a general partner, means the address for the
time being shown in the register as the general partner’s current service
address.

122.8W.3

The regulations may authorise or require the address to be changed on the
registrar’s own motion or on an application by another person.

122.8W.4

The regulations—

122.8W.4.a

may include provision corresponding or similar to any provision that may be
included in regulations under section 1097B of the Companies Act 2006;

122.8W.4.b

must include—

122.8W.4.b.i

provision about appeals corresponding to the provision that must be included
in regulations under section 1097B by virtue of subsections (7) and (8) of
that section;

122.8W.4.b.ii

provision corresponding to subsection (9) of that section.

122.8W.5

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

###### New partners: transitional provision about required information

123

123.1

This section applies in relation to a person who—

123.1.a

is a partner in a limited partnership, and

123.1.b

became a partner in the limited partnership before section 122 came fully into
force,

other than a person who became a partner in the limited partnership on its
registration.

123.2

The general partners in the limited partnership must, within the transitional
period, deliver a statement to the registrar specifying the required
information about the partner (within the meaning of the Schedule to the
Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by Schedule 4 to this Act)).

123.3

If a change in the required information about the partner occurs before
whichever is earlier of—

123.3.a

the end of the transitional period, and

123.3.b

the delivery of the statement mentioned in subsection  (2) ,

the general partners in the limited partnership are not required by the
provisions mentioned in subsection  (4)  to give notice to the registrar of
the change, unless it is a change to the partner’s name.

123.4

The provisions are—

123.4.a

section 8S(1) of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 122 of
this Act), and

123.4.b

so far as it relates to section 8S(1) of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
section  10D (2)(a)  of that Act (inserted by section 126 of this Act).

123.5

In this section—

“ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Limited Partnerships Act 1907
(see section 15 of that Act); “ transitional period ” means the period of 6
months beginning when section 122 came fully into force.

123.6

Failure by the general partners in a limited partnership to comply with
subsection  (2)  is, in the absence of any evidence to the contrary, to be
treated by the registrar as reasonable cause to believe that the limited
partnership has been dissolved for the purposes of section  19  of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 (registrar’s power to confirm dissolution of limited
partnership) (inserted by section 141 of this Act).

123.7

Where the registrar proposes to rely on a failure by the general partners in
the limited partnership to comply with subsection  (2)  as grounds for
exercising the power in section  19  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
subsections  (2)  to  (4)  of that section (publication of warning notice) do
not apply.

###### New general partners: transitional provision about officers

124

124.1

This section applies in relation to a general partner that—

124.1.a

is a legal entity, and

124.1.b

became a general partner before section 122 came fully into force,

other than a legal entity that became a general partner in a limited
partnership on its registration.

124.2

The general partner must, within the transitional period, deliver to the
registrar—

124.2.a

a statement of the kind mentioned in section 8R(4) of the Limited Partnerships
Act 1907 containing the information, and accompanied by the statement,
mentioned in section 8R(7) of that Act (both inserted by section 122 of this
Act), and

124.2.b

either a statement—

124.2.b.i

that the general partner does not have any corporate managing officers, or

124.2.b.ii

if the general partner has one or more corporate managing officers, a
statement of the kind mentioned in section 8R(5)(b) of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 containing the information, and accompanied by the
statement, mentioned in section 8R(8) of that Act (both inserted by section
122 of this Act).

124.3

The general partner is not required by the provisions mentioned in subsection
(4)  to give notice to the registrar if a legal entity becomes a corporate
managing officer of the general partner before whichever is earlier of—

124.3.a

the end of the transitional period, and

124.3.b

the delivery of the statement mentioned in subsection  (2)(b) .

124.4

The provisions are—

124.4.a

section  8N (1)  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 119
of this Act), and

124.4.b

so far as it relates to section  8N (1)  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907,
section  10D (2)(a)  of that Act (inserted by section 126 of this Act).

124.5

In this section—

“ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Limited Partnerships Act 1907
(see section 15 of that Act); “ transitional period ” means the period of 6
months beginning when section 122 came fully into force.

###### Notification of other changes

125

125.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

125.2

In section 8A (application for registration), in subsection (2), for paragraph
(a) substitute—

125.2.a

the intended general nature of the limited partnership’s business,

.

125.3

Omit section 9 (registration of changes in partnerships).

125.4

After section 10 insert—

############ Notification of other changes in partnerships

############# Duty to notify registrar of other changes in partnerships

125.4.10A

125.4.10A.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must give notice to the
registrar of any change mentioned in subsection  (2) .

125.4.10A.2

The changes are—

125.4.10A.2.a

in the case of any limited partnership, changes to—

125.4.10A.2.a.i

the firm name, or

125.4.10A.2.a.ii

the address of the principal place of business of the limited partnership;

125.4.10A.2.b

in the case of a limited partnership that is not a private fund limited
partnership, changes to—

125.4.10A.2.b.i

the general nature of the limited partnership’s business, or

125.4.10A.2.b.ii

the term or character of the limited partnership.

125.4.10A.3

The notice must specify the date on which the change occurred.

125.4.10A.4

A notice under subsection  (2)(b)(i)  may specify the change to the general
nature of the partnership business by reference to one or more categories of
any system of classifying business activities prescribed by regulations made
by the Secretary of State under section 8A (2A) .

125.4.10A.5

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the change occurs.

############# Notification of other changes occurring before registration

125.4.10B

125.4.10B.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must give notice to the
registrar if, on registration of the limited partnership, the address of the
principal place of business of the limited partnership is different to that
contained in the application for registration under section 8A.

125.4.10B.2

The general partners in a limited partnership that is not a private fund
limited partnership must give notice to the registrar if, on registration of
the limited partnership, any of the following details are different to those
contained in the application for registration under section 8A—

125.4.10B.2.a

the general nature of the limited partnership’s business,

125.4.10B.2.b

the term of the limited partnership,

125.4.10B.2.c

the amount of the capital contribution of a limited partner, or

125.4.10B.2.d

the form of the capital contribution of a limited partner.

125.4.10B.3

A notice under subsection  (1)  must specify the address of the principal
place of business of the limited partnership.

125.4.10B.4

A notice under subsection  (2)(a) —

125.4.10B.4.a

must specify the general nature of the limited partnership’s business, and

125.4.10B.4.b

may do so by reference to one or more categories of any system of classifying
business activities prescribed by regulations made by the Secretary of State
under section 8A (2A) .

125.4.10B.5

A notice under subsection  (2)(b) ,  (c)  or  (d)  must specify the details
mentioned in the paragraph under which the notice is given.

125.4.10B.6

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the limited partnership was registered.

############# Failure to notify other changes in partnerships

125.4.10C

125.4.10C.1

If the general partners fail to comply with section  10A  or  10B  an offence
is committed by each general partner who is in default.

125.4.10C.2

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

125.4.10C.3

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity who is in default also commits the offence if—

125.4.10C.3.a

the managing officer is an individual, or

125.4.10C.3.b

the managing officer is a legal entity and one of its managing officers is in
default.

125.4.10C.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

125.4.10C.4.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

125.4.10C.4.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

125.4.10C.5

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

###### Confirmation statements

126

After section 10C of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section
125 of this Act) insert—

########## Confirmation statements

########### Duty to deliver confirmation statements

126.10D

126.10D.1

The general partners in a limited partnership must, within the period of 14
days after each review period, deliver to the registrar a statement (a
“confirmation statement”) confirming that any information required by
subsection  (2)  is being delivered at the same time as the confirmation
statement.

126.10D.2

The information that must be delivered at the same time as the confirmation
statement is—

126.10D.2.a

a notice of any notifiable change in respect of which a notice under section
8N , 8R, 8S or  10A  has not been delivered,

126.10D.2.b

a notice under section  8F  if—

126.10D.2.b.i

the limited partnership’s registered office is not at an appropriate address
within the meaning given by section  8E (2)  when the confirmation statement
is made, and

126.10D.2.b.ii

the limited partnership has not given a notice under section  8F  that is
awaiting registration by the registrar,

126.10D.2.c

a notice under section  8I  if—

126.10D.2.c.i

the limited partnership’s registered email address is not at an appropriate
email address within the meaning given by section  8H (2)  when the
confirmation statement is made, and

126.10D.2.c.ii

the limited partnership has not given a notice under section  8I  that is
awaiting registration by the registrar,

126.10D.2.d

a notice under section  8L (1)  by each general partner that—

126.10D.2.d.i

is a legal entity,

126.10D.2.d.ii

has a registered officer who does not meet the requirements in section  8K
(1)(a)  to  (c) , and

126.10D.2.d.iii

has not given a notice under section  8L (1)  that is awaiting registration by
the registrar, and

126.10D.2.e

if any general partner that is a legal entity has one or more corporate
managing officers—

126.10D.2.e.i

for which the named contact is not an individual who is a managing officer of
the corporate managing officer, and

126.10D.2.e.ii

in respect of which the general partner has not given a notice under section
8L (2)  that is awaiting registration by the registrar,

a notice under section  8L (2)  by each such general partner in respect of
each such corporate managing officer.

126.10D.3

For the purposes of this section, each of the following is a review period—

126.10D.3.a

where the limited partnership was registered before this section comes fully
into force, the period—

126.10D.3.a.i

beginning with the date of the limited partnership’s registration, and

126.10D.3.a.ii

ending with the period of 6 months beginning when this section comes fully
into force;

126.10D.3.b

where the limited partnership was registered after this section comes fully
into force, the period of 12 months beginning with the date of the limited
partnership’s registration;

126.10D.3.c

each period of 12 months beginning with the day after the end of the previous
review period.

126.10D.4

But a review period may be shortened by the general partners—

126.10D.4.a

notifying the registrar of the shortened review period, and

126.10D.4.b

delivering the confirmation statement within the period of 14 days after that
shortened review period.

126.10D.5

For the purpose of making a confirmation statement, the general partners in a
limited partnership are entitled to assume that information that has been
delivered to the registrar has been properly delivered unless the registrar
has notified the limited partnership otherwise.

126.10D.6

In this section a “ notifiable change ” means a change mentioned in section
8N (1) , 8R(1), 8S(1) to (3) or  10A (2)  that occurred during the review
period.

########### Power to amend matters to be confirmed in confirmation statement

126.10E

126.10E.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
matters that must be confirmed in a confirmation statement delivered under
section  10D (1) .

126.10E.2

The regulations may—

126.10E.2.a

amend or repeal the provisions of section  10D , and

126.10E.2.b

provide for exceptions from the requirements of that section as it has effect
from time to time.

126.10E.3

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

########### Failure to deliver confirmation statement

126.10F

126.10F.1

If the general partners fail to comply with section  10D (1)  an offence is
committed by each general partner who is in default.

126.10F.2

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

126.10F.3

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity also commits the offence if—

126.10F.3.a

the managing officer is an individual who is in default, or

126.10F.3.b

the managing officer is a legal entity that is in default and one of its
managing officers is in default.

126.10F.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

126.10F.4.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

126.10F.4.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

126.10F.5

The contravention continues until such time as the general partners have
delivered the statement required by section  10D (1) .

126.10F.6

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

###### Confirmation statements: Scottish partnerships

127

In regulation 37 of the Scottish Partnerships (Register of People with
Significant Control) Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/694 ) (review period), for

127.4

For the purpose of making a confirmation statement, an eligible Scottish
partnership is entitled to assume that information that has been delivered to
the registrar has been properly delivered unless the registrar has notified
the eligible Scottish partnership otherwise.

##### Accounts

###### Power for HMRC to obtain accounts

128

After section 10F of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section
126 of this Act) insert—

########## Power for HMRC to obtain accounts

########### Power for HMRC to obtain accounts

128.10G

128.10G.1

HMRC may by notice in writing require the general partners in a limited
partnership to—

128.10G.1.a

prepare accounts in accordance with regulations made by the Secretary of State
for the purposes of this paragraph;

128.10G.1.b

deliver those accounts to HMRC, together with—

128.10G.1.b.i

an auditor’s report prepared in accordance with regulations made by the
Secretary of State for the purposes of this sub-paragraph;

128.10G.1.b.ii

such supporting evidence as may be required by regulations made by the
Secretary of the State for the purposes of this sub-paragraph.

128.10G.2

A requirement under this section may specify—

128.10G.2.a

the period to which the accounts must relate;

128.10G.2.b

the form and manner in which the documents are to be delivered;

128.10G.2.c

the period within which they are to be delivered.

128.10G.3

HMRC may by notice in writing extend a period specified in a requirement under
this section.

128.10G.4

If the general partners in a limited partnership fail to comply with a
requirement under this section an offence is committed by each general partner
who is in default.

128.10G.5

But where the general partner is a legal entity, it does not commit an offence
as a general partner in default unless one of its managing officers is in
default.

128.10G.6

Where any such offence is committed by a general partner that is a legal
entity, or any such offence is by virtue of this subsection committed by a
managing officer that is a legal entity, any managing officer of the legal
entity also commits the offence if—

128.10G.6.a

the managing officer is an individual who is in default, or

128.10G.6.b

the managing officer is a legal entity that is in default and one of its
managing officers is in default.

128.10G.7

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

128.10G.7.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

128.10G.7.b

on summary conviction—

128.10G.7.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

128.10G.7.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued contravention, a
daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory maximum;

128.10G.7.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both) and, for continued
contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-fifth of the statutory
maximum.

128.10G.8

A general partner or managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of
this section if they authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all
reasonable steps to prevent, the contravention.

128.10G.9

In this section “ HMRC ” means the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and
Customs.

128.10G.10

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

##### Dissolution, winding up and sequestration

###### Dissolution and winding up: modifications of general law

129

129.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

129.2

In section 4 (definition and constitution of limited partnership)—

129.2.a

in subsection (2), after “firm” insert  “(including debts and obligations
incurred in accordance with section 38 of the Partnership Act 1890)” ;

129.2.b

in subsections (2A) and (2B)(b), after “firm” insert  “(including debts or
obligations incurred in accordance with section 38 of the Partnership Act
1890)” ;

129.2.c

in subsection (3), after “firm” insert  “(including debts and obligations
incurred in accordance with section 38 of the Partnership Act 1890)” .

129.3

In section 6 (modifications of general law in case of limited partnerships)—

129.3.a

in subsection (1), after “firm”, in the third place it occurs, insert
“(including debts and obligations incurred in accordance with section 38 of
the Partnership Act 1890)” ;

129.3.b

for subsection (1A) substitute—

129.3.b.1A

Section 6A (actions by limited partners) makes provision supplementing
subsection (1).

;

129.3.c

in subsection (2) omit “or bankruptcy”;

129.3.d

after subsection (2) insert—

129.3.d.2A

A limited partnership shall not be dissolved under section 33(1) of the
Partnership Act 1890 by the bankruptcy of a partner.

129.3.d.2B

A limited partnership is dissolved if—

129.3.d.2B.a

it ceases to have any general partners,

129.3.d.2B.b

it ceases to have any limited partners, or

129.3.d.2B.c

each general partner is either insolvent or disqualified under the directors
disqualification legislation (see section 8J(3)), irrespective of whether they
became insolvent or disqualified before or after this subsection comes into
force.

;

129.3.e

omit subsection (3);

129.3.f

for subsections (3A) and (3B) substitute—

129.3.f.3A

If a limited partnership is dissolved at a time when the partnership has at
least one general partner who is—

129.3.f.3A.a

solvent, and

129.3.f.3A.b

not disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation,

the general partners at that time who are solvent and are not so disqualified
must either wind up the partnership’s affairs or take all reasonable steps to
ensure that its affairs are wound up by a person who is not a partner at that
time.

129.3.f.3B

If a limited partnership is dissolved at a time when the partnership does not
have a general partner who is—

129.3.f.3B.a

solvent, and

129.3.f.3B.b

not disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation,

the limited partners at that time who are solvent must take all reasonable
steps to ensure that the partnership’s affairs are wound up by a person who is
not a limited partner at that time.

129.3.f.3BA

For enforcement of the duties under subsections  (3A)  and  (3B)  see section
29.

;

129.3.g

omit subsection (3C).

129.4

In section 6A (private fund limited partnerships: actions by limited
partners)—

129.4.a

in the heading, omit “private fund limited partnerships:”;

129.4.b

before subsection (1) insert—

129.4.b.A1

A limited partner in a limited partnership is not to be regarded as taking
part in the management of the partnership business for the purposes of section
6(1) merely because the limited partner appoints a person to wind up the
limited partnership pursuant to section 6 (3B) .

;

129.4.c

omit subsection (2)(b);

129.4.d

in subsection (4)—

129.4.d.i

in paragraph (a), omit “private fund”;

129.4.d.ii

129.4.e.5

Nothing in subsections (1) to (3) affects the circumstances in which a limited
partner in a limited partnership that is not a private fund limited

###### Winding up limited partnerships on grounds of public interest

131

After section 27 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 144
of this Act) insert—

########## Winding up: applications and petitions to the court

########### Winding up limited partnerships on grounds of public interest

131.28

131.28.1

Where it appears to the Secretary of State that it is expedient in the public
interest for a limited partnership to be wound up, the Secretary of State may
present a petition to the court for it to be wound up.

131.28.2

Where it appears to the Scottish Ministers that it is expedient in the public
interest for a limited partnership registered in Scotland to be wound up, the
Scottish Ministers may present a petition to the court for it to be wound up.

131.28.3

Where it appears to the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland that it
is expedient in the public interest for a limited partnership registered in
Northern Ireland to be wound up, the Department may present a petition to the
court for it to be wound up.

131.28.4

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before presenting a
petition under subsection (1) in respect of a limited partnership registered
in Scotland.

131.28.5

The Secretary of State must consult the Department for the Economy in Northern
Ireland before presenting a petition under subsection (1) in respect of a
limited partnership registered in Northern Ireland.

131.28.6

If a petition is presented under this section, the court may wind up the
limited partnership if the court is of the opinion that it is just and
equitable for it to be wound up.

131.28.7

The power in subsection  (6)  does not limit any other power the court has in
the same circumstances.

###### Winding up dissolved limited partnerships

132

After section 28 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 131
of this Act) insert—

########## Winding up dissolved limited partnerships

132.29

132.29.1

Where a limited partnership is dissolved and it appears to the court that
there has been a failure to wind up the limited partnership under section
6(3A) or (3B) properly or at all, the court may make any order it considers
appropriate, including an order—

132.29.1.a

for the purposes of enforcing the duty in section 6 (3A)  or  (3B) ,

132.29.1.b

in connection with the performance of that duty, or

132.29.1.c

to wind up the limited partnership.

132.29.2

The court may make an order under subsection  (1)  on an application by any of
the following—

132.29.2.a

the Secretary of State;

132.29.2.b

the Scottish Ministers, but only if the limited partnership is registered in
Scotland or they appear to the court to have sufficient interest for any other
reason;

132.29.2.c

the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland, but only if the limited
partnership is registered in Northern Ireland or the Department appears to the
court to have sufficient interest for any other reason;

132.29.2.d

any other person appearing to the court to have sufficient interest.

132.29.3

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making an
application for an order under subsection (1) in respect of a limited
partnership registered in Scotland.

132.29.4

The Secretary of State must consult the Department for the Economy in Northern
Ireland before making an application for an order under subsection (1) in
respect of a limited partnership registered in Northern Ireland.

132.29.5

The power in subsection  (1)  does not limit any other power the court has in
the same circumstances.

###### Power to make provision about winding up

133

After section 29 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 132
of this Act) insert—

########## Power to make provision about winding up

133.30

133.30.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision in relation to the
winding up of a limited partnership under section 28 or 29 that corresponds or
is similar to any provision of the Insolvency Act 1986 or the Insolvency
(Northern Ireland) Order 1989 (including any provision of that Act or Order
that relates to the allocation of jurisdiction or distribution of business
between courts in any part of the United Kingdom).

133.30.2

Before making regulations under subsection  (1)  the Secretary of State must—

133.30.2.a

obtain the consent of the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland, so
far as the regulations relate to limited partnerships registered in Northern
Ireland;

133.30.2.b

obtain the consent of the Scottish Ministers, so far as the regulations relate
to limited partnerships registered in Scotland.

133.30.3

The provision that may be made by regulations under subsection  (1)  by virtue
of section 38(1) includes provision amending, repealing or revoking provision
made by or under either of the following, whenever passed or made—

133.30.3.a

an Act;

133.30.3.b

Northern Ireland legislation.

133.30.4

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

###### Winding up of limited partnerships: concurrent proceedings

134

134.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

134.2

In section 6 (modifications of general law in case of limited partnerships),
for subsection (3D) substitute—

134.2.3D

Subsections (3A) and (3B) have effect subject to any order of a court as to
the winding up of the affairs of the partnership and any award of
sequestration of the partnership’s estate under the Bankruptcy (Scotland) Act
2016.

134.3

After section  30  (inserted by section 133 of this Act) insert—

############ Winding up of limited partnerships: concurrent proceedings

134.3.31

134.3.31.1

Where a petition under section 28 in respect of a limited partnership is
pending, a general partner of the limited partnership who is or becomes aware
of any of the circumstances mentioned in subsection  (3)  must notify the
court to which the petition was presented.

134.3.31.2

Where an application under section 29 in respect of a limited partnership is
pending—

134.3.31.2.a

a general partner of the limited partnership who is or becomes aware any of
the circumstances mentioned in subsection  (3)  must notify the court to which
the application was made, and

134.3.31.2.b

if the application was made by a person other than the Secretary of State, the
applicant must notify the court to which the application was made if the
applicant is or becomes aware of any of the circumstances mentioned in
subsection  (3) .

134.3.31.3

The circumstances are that—

134.3.31.3.a

a petition for sequestration of the limited partnership’s estate under the
Bankruptcy (Scotland) Act 2016 is before a sheriff,

134.3.31.3.b

an application to the Accountant in Bankruptcy for sequestration of the
limited partnership’s estate under that Act is pending,

134.3.31.3.c

sequestration has been awarded by virtue of any such petition or application
and the limited partnership’s estate is being sequestrated,

134.3.31.3.d

a trust deed in respect of the limited partnership’s estate has been sent to
the Accountant in Bankruptcy for registration under that Act and the
registration has not been refused,

134.3.31.3.e

a protected trust deed (within the meaning of that Act) is in force in respect
of the limited partnership’s estate,

134.3.31.3.f

an application by the limited partnership for approval of a debt payment
programme under the Debt Arrangement and Attachment (Scotland) Act 2002 is
pending, or

134.3.31.3.g

such a programme has been approved under that Act and has not been completed.

134.3.31.4

A person is not required to notify the court of circumstances under subsection
(1)  or  (2)  if another person has notified the court of those circumstances.

134.3.31.5

If a person fails to comply with subsection  (1)  or  (2)  an offence is
committed by—

134.3.31.5.a

the person, and

134.3.31.5.b

if the person is a legal entity, any of its managing officers who is in
default.

134.3.31.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

134.3.31.6.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

134.3.31.6.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

134.3.31.7

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

134.3.31.8

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

134.3.31.9

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(8) ).

134.3.31.10

For the purposes of this section a petition or application is “pending” if it
has been presented or made and it has not fallen, been withdrawn or been
determined.

############ Power to amend circumstances for notification under section 

134.3.32

134.3.32.1

The Secretary of State or the Scottish Ministers may by regulations amend the
list in section  31 (3) .

134.3.32.2

Before making regulations under subsection  (1)  the Secretary of State must
obtain the consent of the Scottish Ministers.

134.3.32.3

Regulations made by the Secretary of State under subsection  (1)  are subject
to the affirmative resolution procedure.

134.3.32.4

Regulations made by the Scottish Ministers under subsection  (1)  are subject
to the affirmative procedure (see Part 2 of the Interpretation and Legislative
Reform (Scotland) Act  2010 (asp 10) ).
