##### The register of limited partnerships

###### The register of limited partnerships

136

136.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

136.2

In section 3 (interpretation of terms), in subsection (1) (created by section
110 of this Act), at the appropriate place insert—

“ the register of limited partnerships ” means the records kept by the
registrar under section 1080 of the Companies Act 2006 relating to limited
partnerships;

.

136.3

Omit sections 13 and 14.

136.4

For section 16 substitute—

############ The register of limited partnerships

############# Inspection and copies of the register of limited partnerships

136.4.16

136.4.16.1

Any person may—

136.4.16.1.a

inspect the register of limited partnerships;

136.4.16.1.b

require a copy of any material on the register of limited partnerships that is
available for inspection.

136.4.16.2

The right of inspection extends to the originals of documents delivered to the
registrar in hard copy form if, and only if, the record kept by the registrar
of the contents of the document is illegible or unavailable (see section
1083(1) of the Companies Act 2006 for provision about the retention of hard
copies by the registrar).

136.4.16.3

The registrar may specify the form and manner in which an application is to be
made for inspection or a copy.

136.4.16.4

The registrar may determine the form and manner in which the copies are to be
provided.

136.4.16.5

Section 1091 of the Companies Act 2006 (certification of copies), and any
regulations made under it, apply in relation to copies provided under this
section as they apply in relation to the copies provided as mentioned in that
section.

136.4.16.6

This section has effect subject to section  16A  and  16B .

###### Material not available for public inspection

137

137.1

After section 16 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 136
of this Act) insert—

############ Material not available for public inspection

137.1.16A

137.1.16A.1

The registrar must not make the following material available for public
inspection, so far as it forms part of the register of limited partnerships—

137.1.16A.1.a

any application or other document delivered to the registrar under section 8G,
8Q or 8W (changes of addresses by registrar) other than an order or direction
of the court;

137.1.16A.1.b

so much of any document delivered to the registrar as is required to contain—

137.1.16A.1.b.i

a limited partnership’s registered email address,

137.1.16A.1.b.ii

the email address of the named contact for a general partner’s managing
officer,

137.1.16A.1.b.iii

protected date of birth information, or

137.1.16A.1.b.iv

protected residential address information;

137.1.16A.1.c

so much of any statement delivered to the registrar under any of the following
provisions as is required to confirm that an individual is an individual whose
identity is verified (within the meaning of section 1110A of the Companies Act
2006)—

section 8A(1F)(b); section 8L(3)(a) or (b); section 8R(7)(b);

137.1.16A.1.d

any statement delivered to the registrar by virtue of section 33(3) (documents
to be delivered by authorised corporate service providers);

137.1.16A.1.e

any statement or other document delivered to the registrar by virtue of
section 1067A of the Companies Act 2006 (delivery of documents: identity
verification and authorised corporate service providers);

137.1.16A.1.f

any statement made in accordance with regulations made by virtue of section
1082(2)(c) of the Companies Act 2006 (statement of unique identifier);

137.1.16A.1.g

any document provided to the registrar under section  1092A  of the Companies
Act 2006 (power to require further information);

137.1.16A.1.h

any record of the information contained in a document or part of a document
that is unavailable because of any of the previous paragraphs of this
subsection;

137.1.16A.1.i

any e-mail address, identification code or password deriving from a document
delivered for the purpose of authorising or facilitating electronic filing
procedures or providing information by telephone;

137.1.16A.1.j

any other material excluded from public inspection by or under any other
enactment.

137.1.16A.2

The registrar need not retain material to which subsection  (1)  applies for
longer than appears to the registrar reasonably necessary for the purposes for
which the material was delivered to the registrar.

137.1.16A.3

In this section—

“ protected date of birth information ” means information as to the day of the
month (but not the month or year) on which— a partner was born, or a general
partner’s registered officer was born; “ protected residential address
information ” means information as to the usual residential address of— a
partner, a general partner’s registered officer, or the named contact for a
general partner’s managing officer.

137.1.16A.4

Information about a partner, registered officer or named contact does not
cease to be protected date of birth information or protected residential
address information when they cease to be a partner, registered officer or
named contact.

137.1.16A.5

The restrictions on making information available for public inspection imposed
by subsection  (1)(h)  and  (i)  do not affect the availability for public
inspection of the same information contained in material derived from another
description of document (or part of a document) in relation to which the
relevant restriction does not apply.

137.1.16A.6

In this section “registered officer” and “named contact” have the meanings
given by section  8K (4)  and  (5) .

137.2

In section 1083 of the Companies Act 2006 (preservation of original
documents), in subsection (1), for the second sentence substitute—

This is subject to—

137.2.a

section 1087(3) (extent of obligation to retain material not available for
public inspection);

137.2.b

section  16A (2)  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (extent of obligation
to retain material not available for public inspection);

137.2.c

section 22(5) of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
(extent of obligation to retain material not available for public inspection).

###### Records relating to dissolved or deregistered limited partnerships

138

After section  16A  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section
137 of this Act) insert—

########## Records relating to dissolved or deregistered limited partnerships

138.16B

138.16B.1

This section applies where a limited partnership is dissolved or deregistered
under section 26.

138.16B.2

The registrar need not make any information contained in records relating to
the limited partnership available for public inspection at any time after the
end of the period of 20 years beginning with the date on which the limited
partnership is dissolved or deregistered.

138.16B.3

The registrar of companies for England and Wales may, at any time after the
period of two years beginning with the date on which the limited partnership
is dissolved or deregistered, direct that any records relating to the limited
partnership that are held by the registrar are to be removed to the Public
Record Office.

138.16B.4

The registrar of companies for Northern Ireland may, at any time after the
period of two years beginning with the date on which the limited partnership
is dissolved or deregistered, direct that any records relating to the limited
partnership that are held by the registrar are to be removed to the Public
Record Office of Northern Ireland.

138.16B.5

Records in respect of which a direction is given under subsection  (3)  or
(4)  are to be disposed of under the enactments relating to the Public Record
Office or, as the case may be, the Public Record Office of Northern Ireland.

##### Disclosure of information

###### Disclosure of information about partners

139

139.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

139.2

After section  16B  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section
138 of this Act) insert—

############ Restriction on disclosure of information by registrar

############# Restriction on disclosure of information by registrar

139.2.16C

139.2.16C.1

The registrar must not disclose protected date of birth information or
protected residential address information except—

139.2.16C.1.a

in accordance with subsection  (2)  or  (3) ,

139.2.16C.1.b

in accordance with section  16E  (disclosure of protected residential address
information under court order), or

139.2.16C.1.c

as permitted by section  1110F  of the Companies Act 2006 (general powers of
disclosure by the registrar).

139.2.16C.2

The registrar may disclose protected date of birth information or protected
residential address information if the same information is required to be made
available for public inspection as a result of being contained in a document,
part of a document or record to which section  16A (1)  does not apply.

139.2.16C.3

The registrar may disclose protected date of birth information or protected
residential address information to a credit reference agency.

139.2.16C.4

The Secretary of State may make provision by regulations specifying conditions
for the disclosure of protected date of birth information or protected
residential address information in accordance with subsection  (3) .

139.2.16C.5

The Secretary of State may make provision by regulations requiring the
registrar, on application, to refrain from disclosing protected date of birth
information or protected residential address information to a credit reference
agency.

139.2.16C.6

Regulations under subsection  (5)  may make provision of the kind referred to
in section 243(5) to (6A) of the Companies Act 2006.

139.2.16C.7

In this section—

“ credit reference agency ” means a person carrying on a business comprising
the provision of information relevant to the financial standing of
individuals, being information collected by the agency for that purpose; “
protected date of birth information ” has the meaning given by section  16A
(3) ; “ protected residential address information ” has the meaning given by
section  16A (3) .

139.2.16C.8

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative resolution
procedure.

############ Restriction on use or disclosure of information by partners

############# Restriction on use or disclosure of information by partners

139.2.16D

139.2.16D.1

A limited partner must not—

139.2.16D.1.a

use or disclose protected residential address information, except for
communicating with the individual concerned, or

139.2.16D.1.b

use or disclose protected date of birth information.

139.2.16D.2

A general partner must not use or disclose protected residential address
information, except—

139.2.16D.2.a

for communicating with the individual concerned,

139.2.16D.2.b

in order to comply with any requirement of this Act as to information to be
sent to the registrar, or

139.2.16D.2.c

in accordance with section  16E  (disclosure of residential address
information under court order).

139.2.16D.3

A general partner must not use or disclose protected date of birth information
except in order to comply with any requirement of this Act as to information
to be sent to the registrar.

139.2.16D.4

Subsections  (1) ,  (2)  and  (3)  do not prohibit any use or disclosure of
protected date of birth information or protected residential address
information with the consent of the individual concerned.

139.2.16D.5

If a partner uses or discloses information in contravention of subsection  (1)
,  (2)  or  (3)  an offence is committed by—

139.2.16D.5.a

the partner, and

139.2.16D.5.b

if the partner is a legal entity, any of its managing officers who is in
default.

139.2.16D.6

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

139.2.16D.6.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

139.2.16D.6.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

139.2.16D.7

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

139.2.16D.8

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

139.2.16D.9

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(8) ).

139.2.16D.10

In this section—

“ protected date of birth information ” has the meaning given by section  16A
(3) ; “ protected residential address information ” has the meaning given by
section  16A (3) .

############ Disclosure of protected residential address information under court order

############# Disclosure of protected residential address information under court order

139.2.16E

139.2.16E.1

The court may make an order for the disclosure of protected residential
address information by the appropriate limited partnership or by the registrar
if—

139.2.16E.1.a

there is evidence that service of documents at a service address other than
the individual’s usual residential address is not effective to bring them to
the notice of the individual, or

139.2.16E.1.b

it is necessary or expedient for the information to be provided in connection
with the enforcement of an order or decree of the court,

and the court is otherwise satisfied that it is appropriate to make the order.

139.2.16E.2

An order for disclosure by the registrar may be made only if—

139.2.16E.2.a

the appropriate limited partnership does not have the protected residential
address information, or

139.2.16E.2.b

the appropriate limited partnership was dissolved.

139.2.16E.3

The order may be made on the application of a liquidator, creditor or partner
of the appropriate limited partnership, or any other person appearing to the
court to have a sufficient interest.

139.2.16E.4

The order must specify the persons to whom, and purposes for which, disclosure
is authorised.

139.2.16E.5

In this section—

“appropriate limited partnership” — in relation to protected residential
address information about a partner in a limited partnership means that
limited partnership; in relation to protected residential address information
about a registered officer of a general partner in a limited partnership means
that limited partnership; in relation to protected residential address
information about a named contact for the managing officer of a general
partner in a limited partnership means that limited partnership; “ named
contact ” has the meaning given by section  8K (5) ; “ protected residential
address information ” has the meaning given by section  16A (3) ; “ registered
officer ” has the meaning given by section  8K (4) .

139.3

In section 3 (interpretation of terms), in subsection (1) (created by section
110 of this Act), at the appropriate place insert—

“ the court ” has the same meaning as in the Companies Acts (see section 1156
of the Companies Act 2006);

.

##### The registrar's role relating to dissolution, revival and deregistration

###### Duty to notify registrar of dissolution

140

After section 17 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (power of board of trade
to make rules) insert—

########## Dissolution, revival and deregistration

########### Duty to notify registrar of dissolution

140.18

140.18.1

A person who is a general partner in a limited partnership at a time when it
is dissolved must notify the registrar of the dissolution within the period of
14 days beginning with the day on which the person becomes aware of its
dissolution.

140.18.2

A person who is a limited partner in a limited partnership at a time when it
is dissolved must, if there are no general partners at that time, notify the
registrar of the dissolution within the period of 14 days beginning with the
day on which the person becomes aware of its dissolution.

140.18.3

But no notice is required under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  if—

140.18.3.a

the limited partnership is dissolved under section 19(6) (dissolution on
publication of notice in Gazette),

140.18.3.b

another person has notified the registrar of the dissolution under subsection
(1)  or  (2) , or

140.18.3.c

a dissolution notice under section 19 is published before the end of the
period of 14 days mentioned in subsection  (1)  or  (2) .

140.18.4

If a person fails to comply with subsection  (1)  or  (2)  an offence is
committed by—

140.18.4.a

the person, and

140.18.4.b

if the person is a legal entity, any of its managing officers who is in
default.

140.18.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

140.18.5.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

140.18.5.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

140.18.6

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

140.18.7

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

140.18.8

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(7) ).

###### Registrar’s power to confirm dissolution of limited partnership

141

141.1

The Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is amended as follows.

141.2

After section 18 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 140
of this Act) insert—

############ Registrar’s power to confirm dissolution of limited partnership

141.2.19

141.2.19.1

If the registrar has reasonable cause to believe that a limited partnership
has been dissolved, the registrar may publish a notice in the Gazette (a
“dissolution notice”) stating that fact.

141.2.19.2

Where the registrar proposes to publish a dissolution notice, the registrar
must first publish in the Gazette a notice (a “warning notice”)—

141.2.19.2.a

explaining the registrar’s proposal and its effect (see subsection  (6) ), and

141.2.19.2.b

inviting any person to make representations about the registrar’s proposal.

141.2.19.3

The registrar must send a copy of the warning notice to—

141.2.19.3.a

the registered office of the limited partnership, and

141.2.19.3.b

at least one person who appears in the register of limited partnerships as a
general partner in the limited partnership (if there are any).

141.2.19.4

The registrar may not publish a dissolution notice until after the end of the
period of two months beginning with the first day on which the registrar has
complied with subsection  (2)  and subsection  (3) .

141.2.19.5

The dissolution notice must—

141.2.19.5.a

state the firm name of the limited partnership,

141.2.19.5.b

state the limited partnership’s registration number, and

141.2.19.5.c

explain the effect of the publication of the notice (see subsection  (6) ).

141.2.19.6

On the publication of a dissolution notice, the limited partnership to which
it relates is dissolved if it was not already dissolved.

141.2.19.7

For the purposes of subsection  (3) , a person “appears in the register of
limited partnerships as a general partner in the limited partnership” if—

141.2.19.7.a

either—

141.2.19.7.a.i

the person was named as a proposed general partner in the application for
registration of the limited partnership under section 8A, or

141.2.19.7.a.ii

the general partners have given the registrar notice under section 8R that the
person has become a general partner in the limited partnership, and

141.2.19.7.b

the general partners have not since—

141.2.19.7.b.i

given the registrar notice under section 8R that the person has ceased to be a
general partner in the limited partnership, or

141.2.19.7.b.ii

given the registrar notice under section 8T that the person did not become a
general partner on registration of the limited partnership.

############ Administrative revival

141.2.20

141.2.20.1

On an application under this section the registrar must revive a limited
partnership if the registrar is satisfied that the following conditions are
met.

141.2.20.2

Condition 1 is that the limited partnership was dissolved under section  19
(6)  (dissolution on publication of notice in Gazette).

141.2.20.3

Condition 2 is that the applicant has delivered to the registrar such
documents as are necessary to ensure that, if the limited partnership is
revived, the records kept by the registrar relating to the limited partnership
will be up to date.

141.2.20.4

Condition 3 is that each relevant person has paid any outstanding fines or
financial penalties imposed on them in respect of an offence—

141.2.20.4.a

under this Act, or

141.2.20.4.b

by virtue of regulations made under section  7A  of this Act,

relating to the limited partnership.

141.2.20.5

An application under this section may only be made by a person who was a
general partner in the limited partnership immediately before it was
dissolved.

141.2.20.6

The application must include a statement that—

141.2.20.6.a

the conditions in subsections  (2) ,  (3)  and  (4)  are met, and

141.2.20.6.b

the applicant is a person mentioned in subsection  (5) .

141.2.20.7

An application under this section may not be made after the end of the period
of six years beginning with the date on which the limited partnership was
dissolved.

141.2.20.8

For the purpose of subsection  (7)  an application is made when it is received
by the registrar.

141.2.20.9

In subsection  (4)  “ relevant person ” means—

141.2.20.9.a

the applicant,

141.2.20.9.b

any person who—

141.2.20.9.b.i

was a general partner in the limited partnership immediately before it was
dissolved, and

141.2.20.9.b.ii

if the limited partnership is revived, will be a general partner in the
limited partnership immediately after its revival, or

141.2.20.9.c

any person who is a managing officer of a legal entity where the legal entity
is—

141.2.20.9.c.i

a person mentioned in paragraph  (a)  or  (b) , or

141.2.20.9.c.ii

a person falling within this paragraph.

############ Registrar’s decision on application for administrative revival

141.2.21

141.2.21.1

The registrar must give notice to the applicant of the decision on an
application under section  20 .

141.2.21.2

If the limited partnership is revived, the revival takes effect on the date
that the notice is sent.

141.2.21.3

If the limited partnership is revived the registrar must—

141.2.21.3.a

enter on the register of limited partnerships a note of the date on which the
revival of the limited partnership takes effect, and

141.2.21.3.b

cause notice of the revival to be published in the Gazette.

141.2.21.4

Notes entered on the register of limited partnerships in accordance with
subsection (3)(a) are part of the register of limited partnerships.

141.2.21.5

The notice under subsection  (3)(b)  must state—

141.2.21.5.a

the limited partnership’s name (which must be the name that it had before it
was dissolved under section  19 (6) ),

141.2.21.5.b

the limited partnership’s registration number, and

141.2.21.5.c

the date on which the revival of the limited partnership takes effect.

############ Effect of administrative revival

141.2.22

141.2.22.1

The general effect of administrative revival is that the limited partnership
is to be treated as having continued in existence as if it had not been
dissolved under section  19 (6) .

141.2.22.2

The court may give such directions and make such provision as seems just for
placing the limited partnership and all other persons in the same position (as
nearly as may be) as if the limited partnership had not been dissolved under
section  19 (6) .

141.2.22.3

An application to the court for such directions or provision may be made at
any time within the period of three years beginning with the date on which the
revival of the limited partnership took effect.

############ Application to court for revival

141.2.23

141.2.23.1

An application may be made to the court to revive a limited partnership that
has been dissolved under section  19 (6)  (dissolution on publication of
notice in Gazette).

141.2.23.2

An application under this section may be made by—

141.2.23.2.a

the Secretary of State,

141.2.23.2.b

a person who was a partner in the limited partnership immediately before it
was dissolved, or

141.2.23.2.c

any other person appearing to the court to have an interest in the matter.

141.2.23.3

An application to the court for the revival of a limited partnership may only
be made—

141.2.23.3.a

within the period of six years beginning with the date on which the limited
partnership was dissolved, or

141.2.23.3.b

where the applicant made an application under section  20  that was refused,
within the period of 28 days beginning with the date on which notice of the
registrar’s decision was sent by the registrar to the applicant.

############ Decision on application for revival by the court

141.2.24

141.2.24.1

If, on an application under section  23 , the court orders revival of the
limited partnership, the revival takes effect on a copy of the court’s order
being delivered to the registrar.

141.2.24.2

The registrar must publish a notice in the Gazette of the revival of the
limited partnership.

141.2.24.3

The notice must state—

141.2.24.3.a

the limited partnership’s name (which must be the name that it had before it
was dissolved under section  19 (6) ),

141.2.24.3.b

the limited partnership’s registration number, and

141.2.24.3.c

the date on which the revival of the limited partnership takes effect.

############ Effect of court order for revival

141.2.25

141.2.25.1

The general effect of an order by the court for revival is that the limited
partnership is to be treated as having continued in existence as a limited
partnership as if it had not been dissolved under section  19 (6) .

141.2.25.2

The court may give such directions and make such provision as seems just for
placing the limited partnership and all other persons in the same position (as
nearly as may be) as if the limited partnership had not been dissolved under
section  19 (6) .

141.2.25.3

The court may also give directions as to—

141.2.25.3.a

the delivery to the registrar of such documents relating to the limited
partnership as are necessary to bring up to date the records kept by the
registrar, or

141.2.25.3.b

the payment of the costs (in Scotland, expenses) of the registrar in
connection with the proceedings for the revival of the limited partnership.

141.3

In section 3 (interpretation of terms), in subsection (1) (created by section
110 of this Act), at the appropriate place insert—

“ the Gazette ” means— as respects limited partnerships registered in England
and Wales, the London Gazette, as respects limited partnerships registered in
Scotland, the Edinburgh Gazette, and as respects limited partnerships
registered in Northern Ireland, the Belfast Gazette;

.

141.4

In section 10 (advertisement in Gazette), omit subsection (2).

###### Registrar’s power to confirm dissolution: transitional provision

142

If the registrar exercises the power in section  19 (1)  of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907 (power to confirm dissolution of limited partnership)
during the period of 6 months beginning when section 141 (2)  of this Act
comes fully into force, subsections  (2)  to  (4)  of section  19  of the
Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (publication of warning notice) do not apply.

###### Voluntary deregistration of limited partnership

143

After section 25 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 141
of this Act) insert—

########## Voluntary deregistration of limited partnership

143.26

143.26.1

The registrar must deregister a limited partnership if a statement is
delivered to the registrar which is authenticated by or on behalf of each
partner confirming that they want the limited partnership to be deregistered.

143.26.2

The registrar deregisters the limited partnership by publishing a notice in
the Gazette of the limited partnership’s deregistration (a “deregistration
notice”).

143.26.3

The deregistration notice must state—

143.26.3.a

the firm name of the limited partnership, and

143.26.3.b

the limited partnership’s registration number.

143.26.4

On the publication of the deregistration notice, the limited partnership
ceases to be registered as a limited partnership under this Act (but this does
not prevent any ongoing relationship from being a partnership).

###### Removal of limited partnership from index of names

144

After section 26 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 143
of this Act) insert—

########## Removal of limited partnership from index of names

144.27

144.27.1

The registrar must remove a limited partnership from the index of names as
soon as reasonably practicable if the registrar—

144.27.1.a

becomes aware that the limited partnership is dissolved (whether on the
receipt of a notice under section 18, the publication of a dissolution notice
under section 19(6) or otherwise), or

144.27.1.b

publishes a deregistration notice under section 26 in respect of the limited
partnership.

144.27.2

If the registrar removes a limited partnership from the index of names, the
registrar must include a note in the register of limited partnerships stating
either—

144.27.2.a

that the limited partnership has been removed from the index of names because
of its dissolution, or

144.27.2.b

that the limited partnership has been removed from the index of names because
of its deregistration under section 26.

144.27.3

The registrar must also publish a notice of the removal in the Gazette if the
limited partnership is removed from the index of names other than following
the publication of a dissolution notice under section 19 or a deregistration
notice under section 26.

144.27.4

Notes included in the register of limited partnerships in accordance with
subsection  (2)  are part of the register of limited partnerships.

144.27.5

A note may be removed if it no longer serves any useful purpose.

144.27.6

In this section “ the index of names ” means the index kept by the registrar
under section 1099 of the Companies Act 2006.

##### Delivery of documents

###### Delivery of documents relating to limited partnerships

145

After section 32 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 134
of this Act) insert—

########## Delivery of documents to the registrar

########### Documents to be delivered by authorised corporate service providers

145.33

145.33.1

An individual may not deliver a document under a provision listed in
subsection  (3)  to the registrar on their own behalf (and, accordingly, any
delivery of a document under such a provision must be made on the individual’s
behalf in accordance with subsection  (2) ).

145.33.2

An individual may not deliver a document under a provision listed in
subsection  (3)  to the registrar on behalf of another person unless—

145.33.2.a

the individual is an authorised corporate service provider, or

145.33.2.b

the individual is an officer or employee of an authorised corporate service
provider.

145.33.3

The provisions are—

145.33.3.a

section 8A (application for registration);

145.33.3.b

section 8F (change of address of registered office) or  8I  (change of
registered email address);

145.33.3.c

section  8L ,  8M ,  8N  or  8O  (changes relating to officers of general
partners);

145.33.3.d

section 8R, 8S or 8T (changes relating to partners);

145.33.3.e

section  10A  or  10B  (other changes in partnerships), other than a notice
under section  10A (2)(b)(i)  or  10B (2)(a) ;

145.33.3.f

section  10D  (confirmation statements);

145.33.3.g

section  20  (administrative revival).

145.33.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

145.33.4.a

amend this section for the purposes of changing who may deliver a document
under a provision listed in subsection  (3)  to the registrar on behalf of
another person;

145.33.4.b

amend the list in subsection  (3) .

145.33.5

Regulations under subsection  (4)  are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

###### General false statement offences

146

After section 33 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 145
of this Act) insert—

########## False statements: basic offence

146.34

146.34.1

It is an offence for a person, without reasonable excuse, to—

146.34.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for the purposes of this
Act, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular, or

146.34.1.b

make to the registrar, for the purposes of this Act, a statement that is
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

146.34.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, every managing officer of
the entity who is in default also commits the offence.

146.34.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

146.34.3.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

146.34.3.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

146.34.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

146.34.4

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

146.34.5

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

146.34.6

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(5) ).

########## False statements: aggravated offence

146.35

146.35.1

It is an offence for a person knowingly to—

146.35.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for the purposes of this
Act, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular, or

146.35.1.b

make to the registrar, for the purposes of this Act, a statement that is
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

146.35.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, every managing officer of
the entity who is in default also commits the offence.

146.35.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

146.35.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

146.35.3.b

on summary conviction—

146.35.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

146.35.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

146.35.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

146.35.4

A managing officer is “ in default ” for the purposes of this section if they
authorise or permit, participate in, or fail to take all reasonable steps to
prevent, the contravention.

146.35.5

But a corporate managing officer does not commit an offence as a managing
officer in default unless one of its managing officers is in default.

146.35.6

Where any such offence is committed by a corporate managing officer the
managing officer in question also commits the offence (subject to subsection
(5) ).

##### National security exemption from identity verification

###### National security exemption from identity verification

147

After section 35 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 146
of this Act) insert—

########## National security exemption from identity verification

########### National security exemption from identity verification

147.36

147.36.1

The Secretary of State may, by written notice given to a person, provide for
one or more of the effects listed in subsection  (2)  to apply in relation to
the person, if satisfied that to do so is necessary—

147.36.1.a

in the interests of national security, or

147.36.1.b

for the purposes of preventing or detecting serious crime.

147.36.2

The effects for which the notice may provide are that—

147.36.2.a

a statement under section 8A(1C) may name the person as a proposed general
partner’s proposed registered officer even if the person does not meet the
requirement in paragraph (c) of that subsection;

147.36.2.b

a statement by the person under section 8A(1F)(b) is not required to confirm
that the person meets the requirement in sub-paragraph (iii) of that
paragraph;

147.36.2.c

where the person is a general partner’s registered officer, section 8K(1)(c)
does not impose any obligation on the general partner;

147.36.2.d

a statement under section 8L(3)(a) or (b) made in relation to a notice naming
the person as a general partner’s new registered officer is not required to
confirm that the person meets the requirement in section 8K(1)(c);

147.36.2.e

a statement under section 8R(4) may name the person as a general partner’s
proposed registered officer even if the person does not meet the requirement
in section 8K(1)(c);

147.36.2.f

a statement by the person under section 8R(7)(b) is not required to confirm
that the person meets the requirement in section 8K(1)(c);

147.36.2.g

section 33 (documents to be delivered by authorised corporate service
providers) does not apply in relation to the delivery of documents to the
registrar by the person on their own behalf or on behalf of another.

147.36.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(b) —

147.36.3.a

“ crime ” means conduct which—

147.36.3.a.i

constitutes a criminal offence, or

147.36.3.a.ii

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute a criminal offence, and

147.36.3.b

crime is “serious” if—

147.36.3.b.i

the offence which is or would be constituted by the conduct is an offence for
which the maximum sentence (in any part of the United Kingdom) is imprisonment
for 3 years or more, or

147.36.3.b.ii

the conduct involves the use of violence, results in substantial financial
gain or is conduct by a large number of persons in pursuit of a common
purpose.

##### Service on a limited partnership

###### Service on a limited partnership

148

After section 36 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section 147
of this Act) insert—

########## Service of documents

########### Service of documents on limited partnership

148.37

A document may be served on a limited partnership by leaving it at, or sending
it by post to, the limited partnership’s registered office.

##### Application of other laws

###### Application of company law

149

After section 7 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 insert—

########## Application of company law

149.7A

149.7A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

149.7A.1.a

make provision in relation to limited partnerships that corresponds or is
similar to any provision relating to companies or other corporations made by
or under, or capable of being made under, any Act;

149.7A.1.b

provide for any such provision which would otherwise have effect in relation
to limited partnerships not to apply to them or to apply to them with such
modifications as appear appropriate.

149.7A.2

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may amend or repeal provision made by this
Act, the Partnership Act 1890 or the Companies Act 2006.

149.7A.3

The provision which may be made by regulations under subsection  (1)  by
virtue of section  38 (1)  includes provision amending, repealing or revoking
provision made by or under any Act, whenever passed or made.

149.7A.4

Regulations under subsection  (1)  are subject to the negative resolution
procedure if they only make provision that corresponds or is similar to
provision made or capable of being made by regulations subject to the negative
resolution procedure.

149.7A.5

Any other regulations under subsection  (1)  are subject to the affirmative
resolution procedure.

150.3

In relation to a limited partnership registered under the Limited Partnerships

##### Regulations

###### Limited partnerships: regulations

151

After section  37  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section
148 of this Act) insert—

########## Regulations

########### Regulations

151.38

151.38.1

A power to make regulations under any provision of this Act includes power to
make—

151.38.1.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;

151.38.1.b

different provision for different purposes.

151.38.2

Regulations made by the Secretary of State under this Act are to be made by
statutory instrument.

151.38.3

Where regulations under this Act are subject to “the affirmative resolution
procedure”, the regulations may not be made unless a draft of the statutory
instrument containing them has been laid before and approved by a resolution
of each House of Parliament.

151.38.4

Where regulations under this Act are subject to “the negative resolution
procedure”, the statutory instrument containing the regulations is subject to
annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

151.38.5

Any provision that may be made by regulations under this Act subject to the
negative resolution procedure may be made by regulations subject to the
affirmative resolution procedure.

##### Further amendments

###### Limited partnerships: further amendments

152

152.1

Section 17 of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 is omitted.

152.2

Schedule 5 contains consequential amendments relating to this Part.

#### Miscellaneous provision about partnerships

##### Registration of qualifying Scottish partnerships

153

153.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

153.1.a

make provision requiring the delivery to the registrar of information in
connection with a qualifying Scottish partnership;

153.1.b

make provision for the purpose of ensuring that a partner of a qualifying
Scottish partnership has at least one managing officer who is an individual
whose identity is verified (within the meaning of section 1110A of the
Companies Act 2006);

153.1.c

make provision in relation to qualifying Scottish partnerships that
corresponds or is similar to any provision relating to companies or limited
partnerships made by or under, or capable of being made under, any Act.

153.2

The regulations may create summary offences, punishable with a fine, in
connection with any provision made by virtue of subsection  (1)(a)  or  (b) .

153.3

Do not read subsection  (2)  as impliedly limiting the provision that can be
made by virtue of subsection  (1)(c) .

153.4

The provision that may be made by virtue of subsection  (1)(c)  includes
provision for the purpose mentioned in subsection  (1)(b) .

153.5

The provision which may be made by regulations under subsection  (1)  by
virtue of section 217(1)(a) includes provision amending, repealing or revoking
provision made by or under any Act, whenever passed or made.

153.6

In this section—

“ managing officer ” has the meaning given by section 3(1) of the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907; “ qualifying Scottish partnership ” means a
partnership, other than a limited partnership, that— is constituted under the
law of Scotland, and is a qualifying partnership with the meaning given by
regulation 3 of the Partnership (Accounts) Regulations 2008; “ the registrar ”
means registrar of companies for Scotland.

##### Power to amend disqualification legislation in relation to relevant entities: GB

154

After section 22H of the Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986 insert—

######### Power to amend application of Act in relation to relevant entities

154.22I

154.22I.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this Act for the purpose of
applying, or modifying the application of, any of its provisions in relation
to relevant entities.

154.22I.2

For that purpose, the regulations may in particular—

154.22I.2.a

extend the company disqualification conditions to include corresponding
conditions relating to a relevant entity;

154.22I.2.b

limit the company disqualification conditions to remove conditions relating to
a relevant entity;

154.22I.2.c

modify which company disqualification conditions can, in combination with each
other, result in a person being disqualified under this Act;

154.22I.2.d

provide for any of the company disqualification conditions to result in or
contribute to a person being disqualified from acting in a role or doing
something in relation to a relevant entity.

154.22I.3

In this section “ the company disqualification conditions ” means the
conditions that can result in or contribute to a person being disqualified
under this Act from acting in a role or doing something in relation to any
entity.

154.22I.4

In this section a “ relevant entity ” means—

154.22I.4.a

a limited partnership registered under the Limited Partnerships Act 1907;

154.22I.4.b

a limited liability partnership registered under the Limited Liability
Partnerships Act 2000;

154.22I.4.c

a partnership, other than a limited partnership, that is—

154.22I.4.c.i

constituted under the law of Scotland, and

154.22I.4.c.ii

a qualifying partnership within the meaning given by regulation 3 of the
Partnerships (Accounts) Regulations 2008.

154.22I.5

Regulations under this section may make—

154.22I.5.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;

154.22I.5.b

different provision for different purposes.

154.22I.6

The provision which may be made by virtue of subsection  (5)(a)  includes
provision amending provision made by or under either of the following,
whenever passed or made—

154.22I.6.a

an Act;

154.22I.6.b

Northern Ireland legislation.

154.22I.7

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

154.22I.8

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this section may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

155

155.1

.

155.3

After Article 25C insert—

########### Power to amend application of Order in relation to relevant entities

155.3.25D

155.3.25D.1

The Secretary of State or the Department may by regulations amend this Order
for the purpose of applying, or modifying the application of, any of its
provisions in relation to relevant entities.

155.3.25D.2

For that purpose, the regulations may in particular—

155.3.25D.2.a

extend the company disqualification conditions to include corresponding
conditions relating to a relevant entity;

155.3.25D.2.b

limit the company disqualification conditions to remove conditions relating to
a relevant entity;

155.3.25D.2.c

modify which company disqualification conditions can, in combination with each
other, result in a person being disqualified under this Order;

155.3.25D.2.d

provide for any of the company disqualification conditions to result in or
contribute to a person being disqualified from acting in a role or doing
something in relation to a relevant entity.

155.3.25D.3

The Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Department before making
regulations under this Article.

155.3.25D.4

In this Article “ the company disqualification conditions ” means the
conditions that can result in or contribute to a person being disqualified
under this Order from acting in a role or doing something in relation to any
entity.

155.3.25D.5

In this Article a “ relevant entity ” means—

155.3.25D.5.a

a limited partnership registered under the Limited Partnerships Act 1907;

155.3.25D.5.b

a limited liability partnership registered under the Limited Liability
Partnerships Act 2000;

155.3.25D.5.c

a partnership, other than a limited partnership, that is—

155.3.25D.5.c.i

constituted under the law of Scotland, and

155.3.25D.5.c.ii

a qualifying partnership within the meaning given by regulation 3 of the
Partnerships (Accounts) Regulations 2008.

155.3.25D.6

Regulations under this Article may make consequential, supplementary,
incidental, transitional or saving provision.

155.3.25D.7

The provision which may be made by regulations made by the Secretary of State
by virtue of paragraph  (6)  includes provision amending provision made by or
under either of the following, whenever passed or made—

155.3.25D.7.a

an Act;

155.3.25D.7.b

Northern Ireland legislation.

155.3.25D.8

The provision which may be made by regulations made by the Department by
virtue of paragraph (6) includes provision amending provision made by or under
Northern Ireland legislation, whenever passed or made.

155.3.25D.9

Regulations made by the Secretary of State under this Article are to be made
by statutory instrument.

155.3.25D.10

A statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Secretary of State
under this Article may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been
laid before and approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

155.3.25D.11

Regulations made by the Department under this Article are subject to negative
resolution.

############# Persons treated as beneficial owners where entity holds land as nominee

A person (“ X ”) is to be treated as a beneficial owner of an overseas entity

Y holds land in England or Wales as nominee for X Condition 1 is that Y— is
registered in the register of title kept under the Land Registration Act 2002
as the proprietor of a qualifying estate within the meaning of Schedule 4A to
that Act, became so registered in pursuance of an application made on or after
1 January 1999, and holds the qualifying estate as nominee for— X, or an
entity of which X is a beneficial owner by virtue of paragraph 6. Y holds land
in Scotland as nominee for X Condition 2 is that— Y— holds an interest in land
by virtue of being entered, on or after 8 December 2014, as proprietor in the
proprietorship section of the title sheet for a plot of land that is
registered in the Land Register of Scotland, is, in relation to a lease that
was recorded in the General Register of Sasines or registered in the Land
Register of Scotland before that date, by virtue of an assignation of the
lease registered in the Land Register of Scotland on or after that date, the
tenant under the lease, or is the tenant under a lease that was registered in
the Land Register of Scotland on or after that date, and Y holds the interest
in land referred to in paragraph (a)(i), (ii) or (iii) as nominee for— X, or
an entity of which X is a beneficial owner by virtue of paragraph 6. Y holds
land in Northern Ireland as nominee for X Condition 3 is that Y— is registered
in the register kept under the  and Registration Act (Northern Ireland) 1970
(c. 18 (N.I.))  as the owner of a qualifying estate within the meaning of
Schedule 8A to that Act, became so registered on or after the day on which
that Schedule came into force, and holds the qualifying estate as nominee for—
X, or an entity of which X is a beneficial owner by virtue of paragraph 6.

;

and 3(1)(c)” .

#### Inspection of the register and protection of information

##### Material unavailable for public inspection: verification information

166

In section 16 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
(verification of registrable beneficial owners and managing officers), in
subsection (2), after paragraph (c) insert—

166.d

requiring the registrar not to make available for public inspection certain

##### Material unavailable for public inspection

167

For sections 22 to 24 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act
2022 substitute—

######### Material unavailable for inspection

167.22

167.22.1

The following material must not, so far as it forms part of the register, be
made available by the registrar for public inspection—

167.22.1.a

so much of any application or other document delivered to the registrar under
section 4, 7 or 9 or Schedule 6 as is required to contain—

167.22.1.a.i

protected date of birth information;

167.22.1.a.ii

protected residential address information;

167.22.1.a.iii

protected trusts information;

167.22.1.a.iv

the name or contact details of an individual provided for the purposes of
section 4(1)(d), 7(1)(e) or 9(1)(f), paragraph 6(1)(g) or 7(1)(g) of Schedule
1 or paragraph 2(1)(d) of Schedule 6;

167.22.1.a.v

an overseas entity’s email address (see paragraph 2(1)(e) of Schedule 1);

167.22.1.a.vi

any title numbers or folio numbers in respect of land (see paragraph 2(1)(h),
(i) and (j) of Schedule 1);

167.22.1.b

any information that regulations under section 16 provide is not to be made
available for public inspection;

167.22.1.c

any application or other document delivered to the registrar under regulations
under section 23 (2)  (disclosure of protected trusts information);

167.22.1.d

the following—

167.22.1.d.i

any application or other document delivered to the registrar under regulations
under section 25 (regulations protecting material), other than information
provided by virtue of section 25(4);

167.22.1.d.ii

any information which regulations under section 25 require not to be made
available for public inspection;

167.22.1.e

any application or other document delivered to the registrar under section 28
(administrative removal of material from the register);

167.22.1.f

any court order under section 30 (rectification of the register under court
order) that the court has directed under section 31 is not to be made
available for public inspection;

167.22.1.g

any statement or other document delivered to the registrar by virtue of
section 1067A of the Companies Act 2006 (delivery of documents: identity
verification requirements etc);

167.22.1.h

any statement made in accordance with regulations made by virtue of section
1082(2)(c) of the Companies Act 2006 (statement of unique identifier);

167.22.1.i

any document provided to the registrar under section 1092A of the Companies
Act 2006 (power to require further information);

167.22.1.j

any email address, identification code or password deriving from a document
delivered for the purpose of authorising or facilitating electronic filing
procedures or providing information by telephone;

167.22.1.k

any record of the information contained in a document (or part of a document)
mentioned in any of the previous paragraphs of this subsection;

167.22.1.l

any other material excluded from public inspection by or under any other
enactment.

167.22.2

In this section—

“ protected date of birth information ” means information as to the day of the
month (but not the month or year) on which an individual who is a registrable
beneficial owner or managing officer of an overseas entity was born; “
protected residential address information ” means information as to the usual
residential address of an individual who is a registrable beneficial owner or
managing officer of an overseas entity; “ protected trusts information ”
means— the required information about a trust (see sections 4(3)(a), 7(3)(a)
and (4)(a) and 9(3)(a) and (4)(a) and paragraphs 3(2)(a), 4(2)(a) and 5(2)(a)
of Schedule 6), or any information required by virtue of section 7(3)(c) or
(4)(c) or 9(3)(c) or (4)(c) or paragraph 4(2)(c) of Schedule 6 (information
about beneficiaries).

167.22.3

Information about a registrable beneficial owner or managing officer does not
cease to be protected date of birth information or protected residential
address information when they cease to be a registrable beneficial owner or
managing officer.

167.22.4

Where subsection (1), or a provision referred to in subsection (1), imposes a
restriction by reference to material deriving from a particular description of
document (or part of a document), that does not affect the availability for
public inspection of the same information contained in material derived from
another description of document (or part of a document) in relation to which
no such restriction applies.

167.22.5

The registrar need not retain material to which subsection (1) applies for
longer than appears to the registrar reasonably necessary for the purposes for
which the material was delivered to the registrar.

######### Disclosure of protected information

167.23

167.23.1

The registrar must not disclose protected date of birth information, protected
residential address information or protected trusts information unless—

167.23.1.a

the disclosure is permitted by section 1110F of the Companies Act 2006
(general powers of disclosure by the registrar),

167.23.1.b

the information is required to be made available for public inspection (as a
result of being contained in a document, part of a document, or record to
which section  22 (1)  does not apply), or

167.23.1.c

the disclosure is permitted by regulations under subsection  (2) .

167.23.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring the
registrar, on application, to disclose relevant protected trusts information
to a person (unless required to refrain from doing so by regulations under
section 25).

167.23.3

In subsection  (2)  “ relevant protected trusts information ” means protected
trusts information other than information as to—

167.23.3.a

the day of the month (but not the month or year) on which an individual was
born, or

167.23.3.b

the usual residential address of an individual.

167.23.4

The regulations may make provision as to—

167.23.4.a

who may make an application;

167.23.4.b

the grounds on which an application may be made;

167.23.4.c

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application;

167.23.4.d

the notice to be given of an application and of its outcome;

167.23.4.e

how an application is to be determined.

167.23.5

Provision under subsection  (4)(e)  may in particular provide for a question
to be referred to a person other than the registrar for the purposes of
determining the application.

167.23.6

The regulations may include provision authorising or requiring the registrar
to impose conditions subject to which the information is disclosed (including
conditions restricting its use or further disclosure).

167.23.7

The regulations may create offences in relation to failures to comply with
conditions imposed by virtue of subsection  (6) .

167.23.8

The regulations must provide for any such offence to be punishable—

167.23.8.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, by a fine;

167.23.8.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, by a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

167.23.8.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, by a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

167.23.9

Regulations under this section may in particular confer a discretion on the
registrar.

167.23.10

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

167.23.11

In this section the following have the meaning given by section  22 (2) —

“protected date of birth information”; “protected residential address
information”; “protected trusts information”.

######### Consultation about regulations under section 23

167.24

167.24.1

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making
regulations under section 23 that contain provision that would be within the
legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if contained in an Act of
that Parliament.

167.24.2

The Secretary of State must consult the Department of Finance in Northern
Ireland before making regulations under section 23 that contain provision
that—

167.24.2.a

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly if
contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

167.24.2.b

would not, if contained in a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly,
result in the Bill requiring the consent of the Secretary of State under
section 8 of the Northern Ireland Act 1998.

##### Protection of information

168

For section 25 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
substitute—

######### Power to make regulations protecting material

168.25

168.25.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision requiring the
registrar, on application—

168.25.1.a

not to make available for public inspection any information on the register
relating to an individual;

168.25.1.b

to refrain from disclosing information on the register relating to an
individual except in specified circumstances;

168.25.1.c

not to make available for public inspection any address on the register that
is not information to which paragraph  (a)  applies;

168.25.1.d

to refrain from disclosing any such address except in specified circumstances.

168.25.2

The regulations may make provision as to—

168.25.2.a

who may make an application;

168.25.2.b

the grounds on which an application may be made;

168.25.2.c

the information to be included in and documents to accompany an application;

168.25.2.d

the notice to be given of an application and of its outcome;

168.25.2.e

how an application is to be determined;

168.25.2.f

the duration of, and procedures for revoking, any restrictions on the making
of information available for public inspection or its disclosure.

168.25.3

Provision under subsection  (2)(e)  or  (2)(f)  may in particular provide for
a question to be referred to a person other than the registrar for the
purposes of determining the application or revoking the restrictions.

168.25.4

Regulations under subsection  (1)(a)  or  (1)(c)  may provide that information
is not to be made unavailable for public inspection unless the person to whom
it relates provides such alternative information as may be specified.

168.25.5

The circumstances that may be specified under subsection  (1)(b)  or  (d)  by
way of an exception to a restriction on disclosure include circumstances where
the court has made an order, in accordance with the regulations, authorising
disclosure.

168.25.6

Regulations under subsection  (1)(b)  or  (d)  may not require the registrar
to refrain from disclosing information under section 1110F of the Companies
Act 2006 (general powers of disclosure by the registrar).

168.25.7

Regulations under this section may impose a duty on the registrar to publish,
in relation to such periods as may be specified—

168.25.7.a

details of how many applications have been made under the regulations and how
many of them have been allowed, and

168.25.7.b

such other details in connection with applications under the regulations as
may be specified in the regulations.

168.25.8

Regulations under this section may in particular confer a discretion on the
registrar.

168.25.9

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

Where it appears to the registrar that the information contained in a document
delivered to the registrar by an overseas entity in connection with the

the registrar under section 1080 of the Companies Act 2006, the registrar may

170

170.1

In the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022—

170.1.a

for section 28 substitute—

############# Administrative removal of material from the register

#### Offences

##### False statement offences in connection with information notices

171

For section 15 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
substitute—

######### Failure to comply with notice under section 12 or 13

171.15

171.15.1

A person who, without reasonable excuse, fails to comply with a notice under
section 12 or 13 commits an offence.

171.15.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, the offence is also
committed by every officer of the entity who is in default.

171.15.3

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under this section to
prove that the requirement to give information was frivolous or vexatious.

171.15.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

171.15.4.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

171.15.4.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

171.15.4.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

171.15.4.d

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both).

######### False statements under section 12 or 13: basic offence

171.15A

171.15A.1

A person who is given a notice under section 12 or 13 commits an offence if,
in purported compliance with the notice and without reasonable excuse, the
person makes a statement that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular.

171.15A.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, the offence is also
committed by every officer of the entity who is in default.

171.15A.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

171.15A.3.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

171.15A.3.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

171.15A.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

######### False statements under section 12 or 13: aggravated offence

171.15B

171.15B.1

A person who is given a notice under section 12 or 13 commits an offence if,
in purported compliance with the notice, the person makes a statement that the
person knows to be misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

171.15B.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, the offence is also
committed by every officer of the entity who is in default.

171.15B.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

171.15B.3.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

171.15B.3.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

171.15B.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

171.15B.3.d

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both).

##### General false statement offences

172

For section 32 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
substitute—

######### False statements: basic offence

172.32

172.32.1

It is an offence for a person, without reasonable excuse, to—

172.32.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for the purposes of this
Part, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular, or

172.32.1.b

make to the registrar, for the purposes of this Part, a statement that is
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

172.32.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, every officer of the entity
who is in default also commits the offence.

172.32.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

172.32.3.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

172.32.3.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

172.32.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

######### False statements: aggravated offence

172.32A

172.32A.1

It is an offence for a person knowingly to—

172.32A.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for the purposes of this
Part, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular, or

172.32A.1.b

make to the registrar, for the purposes of this Part, a statement that is
misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

172.32A.2

Where the offence is committed by a legal entity, every officer of the entity
who is in default also commits the offence.

172.32A.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

172.32A.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

172.32A.3.b

on summary conviction—

172.32A.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

172.32A.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

172.32A.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

##### Meaning of “registered overseas entity” in land registration legislation

177

177.1

In Schedule 4A to the Land Registration Act 2002 (overseas entities), for
paragraph 8 substitute—

177.1.8

177.1.8.1

For the purpose of this Schedule, an overseas entity that has failed to comply
with any of the following duties is not to be treated as being a “registered
overseas entity” until it remedies the failure.

177.1.8.2

The duties are—

177.1.8.2.a

the duty to deliver to the registrar of companies the documents required by
section 7 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
(updating duty);

177.1.8.2.b

the duty to provide information to the registrar of companies in accordance
with a notice under section  1092A  of the Companies Act 2006 (power of
registrar to require information).

177.1.8.3

For the purposes of this paragraph the failure is remedied when the documents
are delivered, or the information is provided, to the registrar of companies.

177.2

In section 21 of the Land Registration etc. (Scotland) Act  2012 (asp 5)
(application for registration of deed), the subsection (5) inserted by the
Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022 is renumbered
subsection (4A).

177.3

In schedule 1A to the Land Registration etc. (Scotland) Act 2012 (land
transactions: overseas entities), in paragraph 9, for sub-paragraphs (2) and
(3) substitute—

177.3.2

For the purpose of this schedule, an overseas entity that has failed to comply
with any of the following duties is not to be treated as being a “registered
overseas entity” until it remedies the failure.

177.3.3

The duties are—

177.3.3.a

the duty to deliver to the registrar of companies the documents required by
section 7 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
(updating duty);

177.3.3.b

the duty to provide information to the registrar of companies in accordance
with a notice under section  1092A  of the Companies Act 2006 (power of
registrar to require information).

177.3.4

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2)  the failure is remedied when the
documents are delivered, or the information is provided, to the registrar of
companies.

177.4

In Schedule 8A to the  Land Registration Act (Northern Ireland) 1970 (c. 18
(N.I.))  (overseas entities), for paragraph 7 substitute—

177.4.7

177.4.7.1

For the purpose of this Schedule, an overseas entity that fails to comply with
any of the following duties is not to be treated as being a “registered
overseas entity” until it remedies the failure.

177.4.7.2

The duties are—

177.4.7.2.a

the duty to deliver to the registrar of companies the documents required by
section 7 of the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022
(updating duty);

177.4.7.2.b

the duty to provide information to the registrar of companies in accordance
with a notice under section  1092A  of the Companies Act 2006 (power of

177.4.7.3

are delivered, or the information is provided, to the registrar of companies.

##### Power to apply Part 1 amendments to register of overseas entities

178

178.1

Where provision made by the Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act
2022 corresponds to provision made by the Companies Act 2006, the Secretary of
State may by regulations make amendments to the 2022 Act corresponding to any
amendments made by Part 1 of this Act to the provision in the 2006 Act.

178.2

The Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Scottish Ministers
before making regulations under this section that contain provision that would
be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if contained
in an Act of that Parliament.

178.3

The Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Department of Finance in
Northern Ireland before making regulations under this section that contain
provision that—

178.3.a

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly if
contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

178.3.b

would not, if contained in a Bill in the Northern Ireland Assembly, result in
the Bill requiring the consent of the Secretary of State under section 8 of
the Northern Ireland Act 1998.

### Cryptoassets

#### Cryptoassets: confiscation orders

179

Schedule 8 amends the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 to make provision in
connection with cryptoassets and confiscation orders under Parts 2, 3 and 4 of
that Act.

#### Cryptoassets: civil recovery

180

180.1

Schedule 9 amends the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 to make provision for a civil
recovery regime in relation to cryptoassets.

180.2

It also contains related amendments.

#### Cryptoassets: terrorism

181

181.1

Part 1 of Schedule 10 amends the Anti-terrorism, Crime and Security Act 2001
to make provision for a civil recovery regime in relation to cryptoassets
which—

181.1.a

are intended to be used for the purposes of terrorism,

181.1.b

consist of resources of an organisation which is a proscribed organisation, or

181.1.c

are, or represent, property obtained through terrorism.

181.2

Part 2 of Schedule 10 amends the Terrorism Act 2000 to make provision about
financial institutions and cryptoassets.

### Miscellaneous

#### Money laundering and terrorist financing

##### Money laundering: exiting and paying away exemptions

182

182.1

The Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 is amended as follows.

182.2

In section 327 (concealing etc), after subsection (2C) insert—

182.2.2D

A person (“ P ”) who does an act mentioned in paragraph (c) or (d) of
subsection (1) does not commit an offence under that subsection if—

182.2.2D.a

P is carrying on business in the regulated sector that is not excluded
business,

182.2.2D.b

P does the act, in the course of that business—

182.2.2D.b.i

in transferring or handing over to a customer or client money or other
property of, or owing to, the customer or client, and

182.2.2D.b.ii

for the purposes of the termination of P’s business relationship with the
customer or client,

182.2.2D.c

the total value of the criminal property so transferred or handed over to the
customer or client by P for those purposes is less than the threshold amount
determined under section 339A for the act, and

182.2.2D.d

before the act is done, P has complied with the customer due diligence duties.

182.2.2E

For the purposes of subsection  (2D) —

182.2.2E.a

business is “excluded” if it is of a description specified in regulations made
by the Secretary of State for the purposes of this paragraph;

182.2.2E.b

a reference to property being transferred or handed over to the customer or
client includes a reference to property being transferred or handed over to
another person at the direction of the customer or client;

182.2.2E.c

“ customer due diligence duties ” means all duties imposed on P in relation to
the customer or client by regulation 28(2), (3), (3A), (4), (8) or (10) of the
Money Laundering, Terrorist Financing and Transfer of Funds (Information on
the Payer) Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/692 ) (customer due diligence
measures).

182.3.6.b.i

in transferring or handing over to a customer or client money or other
property of, or owing to, the customer or client, and

182.3.6.b.ii

for the purposes of the termination of P’s business relationship with the
customer or client,

182.3.6.c

the total value of the criminal property so transferred or handed over to the

182.3.6.d
