##### Money laundering: exemptions for mixed-property transactions

183

183.1

The Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 is amended as follows.

183.2

In section 327 (concealing etc), after subsection (2E) (inserted by section
182) insert—

183.2.2F

A person (“ P ”) who does an act mentioned in paragraph (c), (d) or (e) of
subsection (1) does not commit an offence under that subsection if—

183.2.2F.a

P is carrying on business in the regulated sector,

183.2.2F.b

P does the act in the course of that business, on behalf of a customer or
client, in operating an account or accounts maintained with P or in connection
with holding any property for the customer or client,

183.2.2F.c

at the time of the act, P knows or suspects that part but not all of the funds
in the account or accounts, or of the property so held, is criminal property
(“the relevant criminal property”),

183.2.2F.d

it is not possible, at the time the act takes place, to identify the part of
the funds or property that is the relevant criminal property, and

183.2.2F.e

the value of the funds in the account or accounts, or of the property so held,
is not, as a direct or indirect result of the act, less than the value of the
relevant criminal property at the time of the act.

183.2.2G

Where subsection  (2F)  applies—

183.2.2G.a

if P does the act in operating an account or accounts, the funds in the
account or accounts immediately after the act are assumed to include the
relevant criminal property, and

183.2.2G.b

if P does the act in connection with holding any property for the customer or
client, such of that property as is held by P immediately after the act is
assumed to include the relevant criminal property.

183.3

In section 328 (arrangements), after subsection (7) (inserted by section 182)
insert—

183.3.8

A person (“ P ”) who does an act mentioned in subsection (1) does not commit
an offence under that subsection if—

183.3.8.a

P is carrying on business in the regulated sector,

183.3.8.b

P does the act in the course of that business, on behalf of a customer or
client, in operating an account or accounts maintained with P or in connection
with holding any property for the customer or client,

183.3.8.c

at the time of the act, P knows or suspects that part but not all of the funds
in the account or accounts, or of the property so held, is criminal property
(“the relevant criminal property”),

183.3.8.d

it is not possible, at the time the act takes place, to identify the part of
the funds or property that is the relevant criminal property, and

183.3.8.e

the value of the funds in the account or accounts, or of the property so held,
is not, as a direct or indirect result of the act, less than the value of the
relevant criminal property at the time of the act.

183.3.9

Where subsection  (8)  applies—

183.3.9.a

if P does the act in operating an account or accounts, the funds in the
account or accounts immediately after the act are assumed to include the
relevant criminal property, and

183.3.9.b

if P does the act in connection with holding any property for the customer or
client, such of that property as is held by P immediately after the act is
assumed to include the relevant criminal property.

183.4

In section 329 (acquisition, use and possession), after subsection (2E)
(inserted by section 182), insert—

183.4.2F

A person (“ P ”) who does an act mentioned in subsection (1) does not commit
an offence under that subsection if—

183.4.2F.a

P is carrying on business in the regulated sector,

183.4.2F.b

P does the act in the course of that business, on behalf of a customer or
client, in operating an account or accounts maintained with P or in connection
with holding any property for the customer or client,

183.4.2F.c

at the time of the act, P knows or suspects that part but not all of the funds
in the account or accounts, or of the property so held, is criminal property
(“the relevant criminal property”),

183.4.2F.d

it is not possible, at the time the act takes place, to identify the part of
the funds or property that is the relevant criminal property, and

183.4.2F.e

the value of the funds in the account or accounts, or of the property so held,
is not, as a direct or indirect result of the act, less than the value of the
relevant criminal property at the time of the act.

183.4.2G

Where subsection  (2F)  applies—

183.4.2G.a

if P does the act in operating an account or accounts, the funds in the
account or accounts immediately after the act are assumed to include the
relevant criminal property, and

183.4.2G.b

if P does the act in connection with holding any property for the customer or
client, such of that property as is held by P immediately after the act is
assumed to include the relevant criminal property.

########### Code of practice about certain information orders

185.12.339ZL

185.12.339ZL.1

The Secretary of State must make a code of practice in connection with the
exercise of the following functions by the Director General of the National
Crime Agency or an authorised NCA officer—

185.12.339ZL.1.a

the making of an application to the magistrates’ court for an information
order in reliance on Condition 3 or 4 in section 339ZH being met;

185.12.339ZL.1.b

the making of a request to a procurator fiscal for the procurator fiscal to
apply for an information order in reliance on Condition 3 or 4 in section
339ZH being met.

185.12.339ZL.2

Where the Secretary of State proposes to issue a code of practice the
Secretary of State must—

185.12.339ZL.2.a

publish a draft,

185.12.339ZL.2.b

consider any representations made about the draft, and

185.12.339ZL.2.c

if the Secretary of State thinks appropriate, modify the draft in the light of
any such representations.

185.12.339ZL.3

A requirement in paragraph (a), (b) or (c) of subsection (2) may be satisfied
by the carrying out of the action required by the paragraph in question before
this section comes into force.

185.12.339ZL.4

The Secretary of State must lay a draft of the code before Parliament.

185.12.339ZL.5

When the Secretary of State has laid a draft of the code before Parliament the
Secretary of State may bring it into operation by regulations.

185.12.339ZL.6

The Secretary of State may revise the whole or any part of the code and issue
the code as revised; and subsections (2) to  (5)  apply to a revised code as
they apply to the original code.

185.12.339ZL.7

A failure by a person to comply with a provision of the code does not of
itself make the person liable to criminal or civil proceedings.

185.12.339ZL.8

The code is admissible in evidence in criminal or civil proceedings and is to
be taken into account by a court or tribunal in any case in which it appears
to the court or tribunal to be relevant.

185.12.339ZL.9

A code of practice made under this section may be combined with a code of
practice under section 22F of the Terrorism Act 2000 (code of practice
relating to information orders under section 22B(1A) of that Act).

185.12.339ZL.10

In this section “ authorised NCA officer ” has the meaning given in section
339ZH(12).

#### Disclosures to prevent, detect or investigate economic crime etc

##### Direct disclosures of information: restrictions on civil liability

188

188.1

The protections set out in subsection (2) apply in relation to a disclosure
made by a person (“ A ”) to another person (“ B ”) if—

188.1.a

A is carrying on business in circumstances where subsection  (3)  applies,

188.1.b

B is also carrying on business in circumstances where that subsection applies,

188.1.c

the information relates to a person who is a customer or former customer of A
(“ the customer ”),

188.1.d

either the request condition or the warning condition is met,

188.1.e

A is satisfied that the disclosure of the information will or may assist B in
carrying out relevant actions of B, and

188.1.f

the disclosure is not a privileged disclosure.

188.2

The protections are that, subject to subsection (11), the disclosure does not—

188.2.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by A, or

188.2.b

give rise to any civil liability, on the part of A, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

188.3

This subsection applies—

188.3.a

where the business carried on is business in the regulated sector, and

188.3.b

in circumstances prescribed, in relation to the business or the person
carrying it on, by regulations made by the Secretary of State for the purposes
of this paragraph.

188.4

The request condition is that—

188.4.a

the disclosure is made in response to a request made by B, and

188.4.b

at the time the request is made, B has reason to believe that A holds
information relating to the customer the disclosure of which will or may
assist B in carrying out relevant actions of B.

188.5

The warning condition is that A, due to concerns about risks of economic
crime, has decided to take safeguarding action (or would have decided to take
such action but for the customer having ceased to be a customer of A).

188.6

For the purposes of subsection  (5) , “ safeguarding action ” means—

188.6.a

terminating a business relationship with the customer,

188.6.b

refusing the customer a product or service, or

188.6.c

restricting the customer’s access to elements of a product or service
available to other customers of A.

188.7

Where a disclosure is made to which subsection  (1)  applies, B’s use of the
disclosed information, for the purposes of any of B’s relevant actions, does
not breach any obligation of confidence owed by B.

188.8

The protections set out in subsection (9) apply in relation to a disclosure
made by a person (“ R ”) who is carrying on business in circumstances where
subsection  (3)  applies to another person for the purpose of making a
disclosure request if R has reason to believe that other person—

188.8.a

is carrying on business in circumstances where subsection  (3)  applies, and

188.8.b

has in their possession information about a customer or former customer of
theirs that will or may assist R to carry out any of R’s relevant actions.

188.9

The protections are that, subject to subsection (11), the disclosure does not—

188.9.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by R, or

188.9.b

give rise to any civil liability, on the part of R, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

188.10

Where a disclosure is made to which subsection  (8)  applies, the use by that
other person of the disclosed information, for the purposes of enabling a
disclosure to be made by them to which subsection  (1)  applies, does not—

188.10.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by them, or

188.10.b

give rise to any civil liability, on the part of R, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

This is subject to subsection (11).

188.11

Nothing in this section requires or authorises a disclosure of information
that would contravene, or prevents any civil liability arising under, the data
protection legislation.

##### Indirect disclosure of information: restrictions on civil liability

189

189.1

The protections set out in subsection (2) apply in relation to a disclosure
made by a person (“ A ”) to another person (“ B ”) if—

189.1.a

A is carrying on business in circumstances where subsection  (3)  applies,

189.1.b

the information relates to a person who is a customer or former customer of A
(“ the customer ”),

189.1.c

due to concerns about the risk of economic crime, A has decided to—

189.1.c.i

terminate a business relationship with the customer,

189.1.c.ii

refuse the customer a product or service, or

189.1.c.iii

restrict the customer’s access to elements of a product or service which are
available to other customers,

189.1.d

A is satisfied that the information disclosed to B, if it is disclosed by B to
one or more persons carrying on business in circumstances where subsection
(3)  applies, will or may assist those persons in carrying out their relevant
actions,

189.1.e

to the extent that the information is personal data, the UK GDPR applies to
the disclosure of the information by A,

189.1.f

A and B are parties to an agreement the terms of which provide that, to the
extent that the information is personal data, B will only disclose or
otherwise process it in circumstances where the UK GDPR applies to the
disclosure or other processing, and

189.1.g

the disclosure is not a privileged disclosure.

189.2

The protections are that, subject to subsection (10), the disclosure does not—

189.2.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by A, or

189.2.b

give rise to any civil liability, on the part of A, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

189.3

This subsection applies—

189.3.a

where the business carried on is business in the regulated sector as—

189.3.a.i

a deposit-taking body,

189.3.a.ii

an electronic money institution,

189.3.a.iii

a payment institution,

189.3.a.iv

a cryptoasset exchange provider, or

189.3.a.v

a custodian wallet provider,

189.3.b

where—

189.3.b.i

the business carried on is business in the regulated sector within paragraph
1(1)(j) to (n) of Schedule 9 to the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 (audit,
insolvency, accountancy, tax or legal services), and

189.3.b.ii

the UK revenue of the person carrying on the business is large or very large
for the relevant financial year (see subsection (11)), and

189.3.c

in circumstances prescribed, in relation to the business or the person
carrying it on, by regulations made by the Secretary of State for the purposes
of this paragraph.

189.4

Where subsection  (1)  applies to a disclosure of information made by A to B,
the protections set out in subsection (5) apply in relation to a further
disclosure of that information made by B to another person (“ C ”) if—

189.4.a

C is carrying on business in circumstances where subsection  (3)  applies, and

189.4.b

to the extent that the information is personal data, the UK GDPR applies to
all processing of the information by B, up to and including the disclosure of
the information to C.

189.5

The protections are that, subject to subsection (10), the disclosure does not—

189.5.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by B, or

189.5.b

give rise to any civil liability, on the part of B, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

189.6

Where a disclosure is made to which subsection  (4)  applies, C’s use of the
disclosed information, for the purposes of any of C’s relevant actions, does
not breach any obligation of confidence owed by C.

189.7

The protections set out in subsection (8) apply in relation to a disclosure
made by a person (“ R ”), who is carrying on business in circumstances where
subsection  (3)  applies, to another person, for the purposes of making a
request for a disclosure of information to be made to R by that other person
if, at the time the request is made, R has reason to believe that the
disclosure of information to which the request relates would be one to which
subsection  (4)  applies.

189.8

The protections are that, subject to subsection (10), the disclosure does not—

189.8.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by R, or

189.8.b

give rise to any civil liability, on the part of R, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

189.9

Where a disclosure is made to which subsection  (7)  applies, the use by that
other person, of the disclosed information, for the purposes of enabling a
disclosure to be made by them to which subsection  (4)  applies, does not—

189.9.a

give rise to a breach of any obligation of confidence owed by them, or

189.9.b

give rise to any civil liability, on their part, to the person to whom the
disclosed information relates.

This is subject to subsection (10).

189.10

Nothing in this section authorises a disclosure of information that would
contravene, or prevents any civil liability arising under, the data protection
legislation.

189.11

In subsection (3)(b) “relevant financial year”—

189.11.a

for the purposes of subsection (1)(a), means the financial year immediately
preceding that in which the disclosure by A is made;

189.11.b

for the purposes of subsection (4)(a), means the financial year immediately
preceding that in which the disclosure to C is made.

And, for the purposes of subsection (3)(b), the question of whether a person’s
UK revenue is large or very large for a particular financial year is to be
determined in accordance with sections 55 to 57 of the Finance Act 2022
(calculation of UK revenue for the economic crime (anti-money laundering)
levy).

##### Meaning of “privileged disclosure”

190

190.1

For the purposes of sections 188 and 189, “ privileged disclosure ” means a
disclosure of information made by a professional legal adviser or relevant
professional adviser in circumstances where the information disclosed came to
the adviser in privileged circumstances.

190.2

Information comes to a professional legal adviser or relevant professional
adviser in privileged circumstances if it is communicated or given to the
adviser—

190.2.a

by (or by a representative of) a client of the adviser in connection with the
giving by that person of legal advice to the client,

190.2.b

by (or by a representative of) a person seeking legal advice from the adviser,
or

190.2.c

by a person in connection with legal proceedings or contemplated legal
proceedings.

190.3

For the purposes of this section a “ relevant professional adviser ” means an
accountant, auditor or tax adviser who is a member of a professional body
which is established for accountants, auditors or tax advisers (as the case
may be) and which makes provision for—

190.3.a

testing the competence of those seeking admission to membership of such a body
as a condition for such admission, and

190.3.b

imposing and maintaining professional and ethical standards for its members,
as well as imposing sanctions for non-compliance with those standards.

##### Meaning of “relevant actions”

191

In sections 188 and 189, “relevant actions”, of a person, means the actions
of—

191.a

determining, for the purposes of preventing, detecting or investigating
economic crime—

191.a.i

whether it is appropriate to apply any customer due diligence measures, or any
similar measures, in respect of a customer or proposed customer of the person;

191.a.ii

the nature or extent of the measures;

191.b

carrying out, for such purposes—

191.b.i

effective measures for identifying or verifying the identity of, or

191.b.ii

any other customer due diligence measures in respect of,

a customer or proposed customer of the person;

191.c

determining, for such purposes, whether it is appropriate to—

191.c.i

terminate an existing business relationship with a customer or proposed
customer of the person;

191.c.ii

decline to establish a new business relationship with such a customer;

191.c.iii

decline to provide a product or service to such a customer;

191.c.iv

restrict the access of such a customer to an existing product or service which
is normally available to other customers;

191.c.v

decline to carry out a transaction for such a customer.

##### Meaning of “business relationship”

192

192.1

In sections 188 to 191, “ business relationship ” means a business,
professional or commercial relationship between a person carrying on relevant
business and a customer or client which—

192.1.a

arises out of the business of the person, and

192.1.b

has, or is expected by the person (at the time when contact is established) to
have, an element of duration.

192.2

In subsection (1) “ relevant business ” means—

192.2.a

in the case of section 188 (and section 191 as it applies for the purposes of
that section), business within section 188(3);

192.2.b

in the case of section 189 (and section 191 as it applies for the purposes of
that section), business within section 189(3).

##### Other defined terms in sections 188 to 191

193

193.1

In sections 188 to 191—

“ cryptoasset exchange provider ” has the meaning given by paragraph 1(12)(a)
of Schedule 9 to the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002; “ custodial wallet provider ”
has the meaning given by paragraph 1(12)(b) of Schedule 9 to the Proceeds of
Crime Act 2002; “ customer due diligence measures ” has the meaning given by
regulation 3(1) of the Money Laundering, Terrorist Financing and Transfer of
Funds (Information on the Payer) Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/692 ); “ the
data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data Protection
Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act); “ deposit-taking body ” means— a
business which engages in the activity of accepting deposits, or the National
Savings Bank; “ economic crime ” means an act which— constitutes an offence
listed in Schedule 11 (“a listed offence”), constitutes an attempt or
conspiracy to commit a listed offence, constitutes an offence— under Part 2 of
the Serious Crime Act 2007 (England and Wales and Northern Ireland:
encouraging or assisting crime) in relation to a listed offence, or under the
law of Scotland of inciting the commission of a listed offence, constitutes
aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring the commission of a listed offence,
or would constitute a listed offence or an offence specified in paragraph (b),
(c) or (d) if done in the United Kingdom; “ electronic money institution ” has
the same meaning as in the Electronic Money Regulations 2011 ( S.I. 2011/99 )
(see regulation 2 of those Regulations); “ enactment ” includes— an enactment
contained in subordinate legislation (as defined in section 21 of the
Interpretation Act 1978); an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made
under, a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru; an enactment contained in, or in an
instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish Parliament; an enactment
contained in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland legislation;
any retained direct EU legislation; “ financial year ” means a period of 12
months ending with 31 March; “ payment institution ” means an authorised
payment institution or small payment institution (each as defined in
regulation 2 of the Payment Services Regulations 2017 ( S.I. 2017/752 )); “
personal data ” and “ processing ” have the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act); “regulated sector”: see
subsection  (2) ; “ the UK GDPR ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

193.2

Part 1 of Schedule 9 to the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 has effect for the
purpose of determining what is a business in the regulated sector.

193.3

The Secretary of State may, by regulations, add an offence to or remove an
offence from the list in Schedule 11.

#### Power to strike out certain claims

##### Strategic litigation against public participation: requirement to make rules of court

194

194.1

The power to make Civil Procedure Rules must be exercised so as to secure that
Civil Procedure Rules include provision for ensuring that a claim may be
struck out before trial where the court determines—

194.1.a

that the claim is a SLAPP claim (see section 195), and

194.1.b

that the claimant has failed to show that it is more likely than not that the
claim would succeed at trial.

194.2

Rules made in compliance with subsection  (1)  may include rules about how a
determination under that subsection is to be made, including (in particular)—

194.2.a

rules for determining the nature and extent of the evidence that may or must
be considered;

194.2.b

rules about the extent to which evidence may or must be tested;

194.2.c

rules permitting or requiring the court to determine matters of fact by way of
presumptions.

194.3

Rules made in compliance with subsection  (1)  must include rules under which
the court may make a determination under that subsection of its own motion.

194.4

The power to make Civil Procedure Rules must be exercised so as to secure that
Civil Procedure Rules include provision for securing that, in respect of a
SLAPP claim, a court may not order a defendant to pay the claimant’s costs
except where, in the court’s view, misconduct of the defendant in relation to
the claim justifies such an order.

194.5

The Lord Chancellor may by regulations provide for subsections  (1)  to  (4)
to apply in relation to any rules of court that may be specified in the
regulations as those subsections apply in relation to Civil Procedure Rules.

194.6

In this section—

“ court ” includes a tribunal; “ rules of court ” means rules relating to the
practice and procedure of a court or tribunal.

##### Meaning of “SLAPP” claim

195

195.1

For the purposes of section 194 a claim is a “SLAPP claim” if—

195.1.a

the claimant’s behaviour in relation to the matters complained of in the claim
has, or is intended to have, the effect of restraining the defendant’s
exercise of the right to freedom of speech,

195.1.b

any of the information that is or would be disclosed by the exercise of that
right has to do with economic crime,

195.1.c

any part of that disclosure is or would be made for a purpose related to the
public interest in combating economic crime, and

195.1.d

any of the behaviour of the claimant in relation to the matters complained of
in the claim is intended to cause the defendant—

195.1.d.i

harassment, alarm or distress,

195.1.d.ii

expense, or

195.1.d.iii

any other harm or inconvenience,

beyond that ordinarily encountered in the course of properly conducted
litigation.

195.2

For the purposes of determining whether a claim meets the condition in
subsection  (1)(a)  or  (c) , any limitation prescribed by law on the exercise
of the right to freedom of speech (for example in relation to the making of
defamatory statements) is to be ignored.

195.3

For the purposes of this section, information mentioned in subsection  (1)(b)
“has to do with economic crime” if—

195.3.a

it relates to behaviour or circumstances which the defendant reasonably
believes (or, as the case requires, believed) to be evidence of the commission
of an economic crime, or

195.3.b

the defendant has (or, as the case requires, had) reason to suspect that an
economic crime may have occurred and believes (or, as the case requires,
believed) that the disclosure of the information would facilitate an
investigation into whether such a crime has (or had) occurred.

195.4

In determining whether any behaviour of the claimant falls within subsection
(1)(d) , the court may, in particular, take into account—

195.4.a

whether the behaviour is a disproportionate reaction to the matters complained
of in the claim, including whether the costs incurred by the claimant are out
of proportion to the remedy sought;

195.4.b

whether the defendant has access to fewer resources with which to defend the
claim than another person against whom the claimant could have brought (but
did not bring) proceedings in relation to the matters complained of in the
claim;

195.4.c

any relevant failure, or anticipated failure, by the claimant to comply with a
pre-action protocol, rule of court or practice direction, or to comply with or
follow a rule or recommendation of a professional regulatory body.

195.5

For the purposes of subsection  (4)(c)  a failure, or anticipated failure, is
“relevant” so far as it relates to—

195.5.a

the choice of jurisdiction,

195.5.b

the use of dilatory strategies,

195.5.c

the nature or amount of material sought on disclosure,

195.5.d

the way to respond to requests for comment or clarification,

195.5.e

the use of correspondence,

195.5.f

making or responding to offers to settle, or

195.5.g

the use of alternative dispute resolution procedures.

195.6

In this section—

“ court ” has the same meaning as in section 194; “ economic crime ” has the
meaning given by section 193 (1) ; “ the right to freedom of speech ” means
the right set out in Article 10 of the European Convention on Human Rights
(freedom of expression) so far as it consists of a right to impart ideas,
opinions or information by means of speech, writing or images (including in
electronic form).

195.7

In the definition of “the right to freedom of speech” in subsection  (6)  “
the European Convention on Human Rights ” means the Convention for the
Protection of Human Rights and Fundamental Freedoms agreed by the Council of
Europe at Rome on 4 November 1950 as it has effect for the time being in
relation to the United Kingdom.

#### Attributing criminal liability for economic crimes to certain bodies

##### Attributing criminal liability for economic crimes to certain bodies

196

196.1

If a senior manager of a body corporate or partnership (“the organisation”)
acting within the actual or apparent scope of their authority commits a
relevant offence after this section comes into force, the organisation is also
guilty of the offence.

This is subject to subsection  (3) .

196.2

“ Relevant offence ” means an act which constitutes—

196.2.a

an offence listed in Schedule 12 (“a listed offence”),

196.2.b

an attempt or conspiracy to commit a listed offence,

196.2.c

an offence—

196.2.c.i

under Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 (England and Wales and Northern
Ireland: encouraging or assisting crime) in relation to a listed offence, or

196.2.c.ii

under the law of Scotland of inciting the commission of a listed offence, or

196.2.d

aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring the commission of a listed offence.

196.3

Where no act or omission forming part of the relevant offence took place in
the United Kingdom, the organisation is not guilty of an offence under
subsection (1) unless it would be guilty of the relevant offence had it
carried out the acts that constituted that offence (in the location where the
acts took place).

196.4

In this section—

“ body corporate ” includes a body incorporated outside the United Kingdom,
but does not include— a corporation sole, or a partnership that, whether or
not a legal person, is not regarded as a body corporate under the law by which
it is governed; “ partnership ” means— a partnership within the meaning of the
Partnership Act 1890; a limited partnership registered under the Limited
Partnerships Act 1907; a firm or other entity of a similar character to one
within paragraph (a) or (b) formed under the law of a country or territory
outside the United Kingdom; “ senior manager ”, in relation to a body
corporate or partnership, means an individual who plays a significant role in—
the making of decisions about how the whole or a substantial part of the
activities of the body corporate or (as the case may be) partnership are to be
managed or organised, or the actual managing or organising of the whole or a
substantial part of those activities.

##### Power to amend list of economic crimes

197

197.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Schedule 12 by—

197.1.a

removing an offence from the list in the Schedule, or

197.1.b

adding an offence to that list.

197.2

The power in subsection  (1)  is exercisable by the Scottish Ministers (and
not by the Secretary of State) so far as it may be used to make provision that
would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if
contained in an Act of that Parliament.

197.3

The power in subsection  (1)  is exercisable by the Department of Justice in
Northern Ireland (and not by the Secretary of State) so far as it may be used
to make provision that—

197.3.a

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly if
contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

197.3.b

would not, if contained in a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly,
result in the Bill requiring the consent of the Secretary of State.

197.4

The Secretary of State may from time to time by regulations restate Schedule
12 as amended by virtue of subsections  (1)  to  (3)  (without changing the
effect of the Schedule).

##### Offences under section 196 committed by partnerships

198

198.1

Proceedings for an offence alleged to have been committed by a partnership by
virtue of section 196 must be brought in the name of the partnership (and not
in that of any of the partners).

198.2

For the purposes of such proceedings—

198.2.a

rules of court relating to the service of documents have effect as if the
partnership were a body corporate, and

198.2.b

the following provisions apply as they apply in relation to a body corporate—

198.2.b.i

section 33 of the Criminal Justice Act 1925 and Schedule 3 to the Magistrates’
Courts Act 1980;

198.2.b.ii

section 18 of the  Criminal Justice Act (Northern Ireland) 1945 (c. 15 (N.I.))
and Schedule 4 to the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 ( S.I.
1981/1675 (N.I. 26) );

198.2.b.iii

sections 34(2), 66(6AA) and 72D(2) of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act
1995.

198.3

A fine imposed on the partnership on its conviction for an offence committed
by virtue of section 196 is to be paid out of the partnership assets.

198.4

In this section “ partnership ” has the same meaning as in section 196.

#### Failure to prevent fraud

##### Failure to prevent fraud

199

199.1

A relevant body which is a large organisation (see sections 201 and 202) is
guilty of an offence if, in a financial year of the body (“the year of the
fraud offence”), a person who is associated with the body (“the associate”)
commits a fraud offence intending to benefit (whether directly or indirectly)—

199.1.a

the relevant body, or

199.1.b

any person to whom, or to whose subsidiary undertaking, the associate provides
services on behalf of the relevant body.

199.2

A relevant body is also guilty of an offence under subsection  (1)  if—

199.2.a

an employee of the relevant body commits a fraud offence intending to benefit
(whether directly or indirectly) the relevant body,

199.2.b

the fraud offence is committed in a financial year of a parent undertaking of
which the relevant body is a subsidiary undertaking (“the year of the fraud
offence”), and

199.2.c

the parent undertaking is a relevant body which is a large organisation.

199.3

But the relevant body is not guilty of an offence under subsection (1)(b) if
the body itself was, or was intended to be, a victim of the fraud offence.

199.4

It is a defence for the relevant body to prove that, at the time the fraud
offence was committed—

199.4.a

the body had in place such prevention procedures as it was reasonable in all
the circumstances to expect the body to have in place, or

199.4.b

it was not reasonable in all the circumstances to expect the body to have any
prevention procedures in place.

199.5

In subsection  (4)  “ prevention procedures ” means procedures designed to
prevent persons associated with the body from committing fraud offences.

199.6

A “fraud offence” is an act which constitutes—

199.6.a

an offence listed in Schedule 13 (a “listed offence”), or

199.6.b

aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring the commission of a listed offence.

199.7

For the purposes of this section a person is associated with a relevant body
if—

199.7.a

the person is an employee, agent or subsidiary undertaking of the relevant
body, or

199.7.b

the person otherwise performs services for or on behalf of the body.

199.8

For the purposes of this section a person is also associated with a relevant
body if the person is an employee of a subsidiary undertaking of the relevant
body; but for the purpose of determining whether an offence is committed by
virtue of this subsection, subsection  (1)  has effect with the omission of
paragraph  (b)  (and the “or” preceding it).

199.9

Whether or not a particular person performs services for or on behalf of a
relevant body is to be determined by reference to all the relevant
circumstances and not merely by reference to the nature of the relationship
between that person and the body.

199.10

Where a relevant body is liable to be proceeded against for an offence under
subsection  (1)  in a particular part of the United Kingdom, proceedings
against the body for the offence may be taken in any place in the United
Kingdom.

199.11

Where by virtue of subsection  (10)  proceedings against a relevant body for
an offence are to be taken in Scotland—

199.11.a

the body may be prosecuted, tried and punished in a sheriff court district
determined by the Lord Advocate, as if the offence had been committed in that
district, and

199.11.b

the offence is, for all purposes incidental to or consequential on the trial
or punishment, deemed to have been committed in that district.

199.12

A relevant body guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

199.12.a

on conviction on indictment, to a fine;

199.12.b

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

199.12.c

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
the statutory maximum.

199.13

In this section—

“ relevant body ” means a body corporate or a partnership (wherever
incorporated or formed); “ sheriff court district ” is to be read in
accordance with the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995 (see section 307(1)
of that Act).

199.14

In this section “financial year”—

199.14.a

in relation to a UK company, has the meaning given by the Companies Act 2006
(see section 390 of that Act);

199.14.b

in relation to a relevant body that is not a UK company means—

199.14.b.i

any period in respect of which a profit and loss account of the relevant body
is required to be made up (by its constitution or by the law under which it is
established), whether that period is a year or not, or

199.14.b.ii

if the body is not required by its constitution or the law under which it is
established to draw up a profit and loss account, a calendar year.

##### Fraud offences: supplementary

200

200.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Schedule 13 by—

200.1.a

removing an offence from the list in the Schedule, or

200.1.b

adding an offence to that list.

200.2

The power in subsection  (1)  is exercisable by the Scottish Ministers (and
not by the Secretary of State) so far as it may be used to make provision that
would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if
contained in an Act of that Parliament.

200.3

The power in subsection  (1)  is exercisable by the Department of Justice in
Northern Ireland (and not by the Secretary of State) so far as it may be used
to make provision that—

200.3.a

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly if
contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

200.3.b

would not, if contained in a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly,
result in the Bill requiring the consent of the Secretary of State.

200.4

An offence added under subsection  (1)(b)  must be—

200.4.a

an offence of dishonesty,

200.4.b

an offence that is otherwise of a similar character to those listed (on the
passing of this Act) in paragraphs 1 to 6 of Schedule 13, or

200.4.c

a relevant money laundering offence.

200.5

The Secretary of State may from time to time by regulations restate Schedule
13 as amended by virtue of subsections  (1)  to  (3)  (without changing the
effect of the Schedule).

200.6

For the purposes of section 199 (1) , where a fraud offence is found to have
been committed over a period of 2 or more days, or at some time during a
period of 2 or more days, and that period of days straddles the beginning of a
financial year of the relevant body in question, the fraud offence must be
taken to have been committed on the last of those days.

200.7

In this section “ relevant money laundering offence ” means an offence under
any of the following sections of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002—

200.7.a

section 327 (concealing etc);

200.7.b

section 328 (arrangements);

200.7.c

section 329 (acquisition, use and possession).

##### Section 199: large organisations

201

201.1

For the purposes of section 199 (1)  and  (2)  a relevant body is a “large
organisation” only if the body satisfied two or more of the following
conditions in the financial year of the body (“year P”) that precedes the year
of the fraud offence—

Turnover More than £36 million Balance sheet total More than £18 million
Number of employees More than 250.

201.2

The reference in subsection (1) to a relevant body does not include a relevant
body which is a parent undertaking (as to which see section 202).

201.3

For a period that is a relevant body’s financial year but not in fact a year,
the figure for turnover must be proportionately adjusted.

201.4

In subsection  (1)  the “ number of employees ” means the average number of
persons employed by the relevant body in year P, determined as follows—

201.4.a

find for each month in year P the number of persons employed under contracts
of service by the relevant body in that month (whether throughout the month or
not),

201.4.b

add together the monthly totals, and

201.4.c

divide by the number of months in year P.

201.5

In this section—

“ balance sheet total ”, in relation to a relevant body and a financial year—
means the aggregate of the amounts shown as assets in its balance sheet at the
end of the financial year, or where the body has no balance sheet for the
financial year, has a corresponding meaning; “turnover”— in relation to a UK
company, has the same meaning as in Part 15 of the Companies Act 2006 (see
section 474 of that Act); in relation to any other relevant body, has a
corresponding meaning; “year of the fraud offence” is to be interpreted in
accordance with section 199 (1) .

201.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations modify this section (other than this
subsection and subsections  (7)  and  (9) ) and section 202 for the purpose of
altering the meaning of “large organisation” in section 199 (1)  and  (2) .

201.7

The Secretary of State may (whether or not the power in subsection  (6)  has
been exercised) by regulations—

201.7.a

omit the words “which is a large organisation” in section 199 (1)  and  (2)(c)
, and

201.7.b

make any modifications of this section (other than this subsection) that the
Secretary of State thinks appropriate in consequence of provision made under
paragraph  (a) .

201.8

Before making regulations under subsection  (6)  or  (7)  the Secretary of
State must consult—

201.8.a

the Scottish Ministers, and

201.8.b

the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland.

201.9

Regulations under subsection  (6)  or  (7)  may make consequential amendments
of section 205.

##### Large organisations: parent undertakings

202

202.1

For the purposes of section 199 (1)  and  (2)  a relevant body which is a
parent undertaking is a “large organisation” only if the group headed by it
satisfied two or more of the following conditions in the financial year of the
body that precedes the year of the fraud offence—

Aggregate turnover More than £36 million net (or £43.2 million gross)
Aggregate balance sheet total More than £18 million net (or £21.6 million
gross) Aggregate number of employees More than 250.

202.2

The aggregate figures are ascertained by aggregating the relevant figures
determined in accordance with section 201 for each member of the group.

202.3

In relation to the aggregate figures for turnover and balance sheet total,
“net” and “gross”—

202.3.a

except where paragraph (b) applies, have the meaning given by subsection (6)
of section 466 of the Companies Act 2006;

202.3.b

in the case of accounts that are not of a kind specified in the definition of
“net” in that subsection, have a corresponding meaning.

202.4

In this section—

“ balance sheet total ” (in relation to a relevant body and a financial year)
has the same meaning as in section 201; “ group ” means a parent undertaking
and its subsidiary undertakings; “ turnover ” (in relation to a UK company or
other relevant body) has the same meaning as in section 201; “year of the
fraud offence” is to be interpreted in accordance with section 199 (1)  or
(2)  (as the case requires).

202.5

In this section “balance sheet total” and “ turnover ”, in relation to a
subsidiary undertaking which is not a relevant body, have a meaning
corresponding to the meaning given by subsection  (4) .

##### Offences under section 199 committed by partnerships

203

203.1

Proceedings for an offence under section 199 alleged to have been committed by
a partnership must be brought in the name of the partnership (and not in that
of any of the partners).

203.2

For the purposes of such proceedings—

203.2.a

rules of court relating to the service of documents have effect as if the
partnership were a body corporate, and

203.2.b

the following provisions apply as they apply in relation to a body corporate—

203.2.b.i

section 33 of the Criminal Justice Act 1925 and Schedule 3 to the Magistrates’
Courts Act 1980;

203.2.b.ii

section 18 of the  Criminal Justice Act (Northern Ireland) 1945 (c. 15 (N.I.))
and Schedule 4 to the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 ( S.I.
1981/1675 (N.I. 26) );

203.2.b.iii

sections 34(2), 66(6AA) and 72D(2) of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act
1995.

203.3

A fine imposed on the partnership on its conviction for an offence under
section 199 is to be paid out of the partnership assets.

##### Guidance about preventing fraud offences

204

204.1

The Secretary of State must issue guidance about procedures that relevant
bodies can put in place to prevent persons associated with them from
committing fraud offences as mentioned in section 199 (1) .

204.2

The Secretary of State may from time to time revise the whole or any part of
the guidance issued under this section.

204.3

The Secretary of State must publish—

204.3.a

any guidance issued under this section;

204.3.b

any revision of that guidance.

204.4

Before issuing or revising guidance under this section the Secretary of State
must consult—

204.4.a

the Scottish Ministers, and

204.4.b

the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland.

204.5

The requirement to consult those persons may be satisfied by consultation
carried out before this section comes into force.

##### Failure to prevent fraud: minor definitions

205

205.1

This section applies for the purposes of sections 199 to 204.

205.2

References to a person “associated with” a relevant body are to be interpreted
in accordance with section 199 (7) .

205.3

“ Financial year ” has the meaning given by section 199 (14) .

205.4

“ Fraud offence ” has the meaning given by section 199 (6) .

205.5

“ Modify ” includes amend or repeal (and references to modifications are to be
interpreted accordingly).

205.6

“ Parent undertaking ” has the same meaning as in the Companies Acts (see
section 1162 of the Companies Act 2006).

205.7

“ Partnership ” means—

205.7.a

a partnership within the meaning of the Partnership Act 1890;

205.7.b

a limited partnership registered under the Limited Partnerships Act 1907;

205.7.c

a firm or other entity of a similar character to one within paragraph (a) or
(b) formed under the law of a country or territory outside the United Kingdom.

205.8

“ Relevant body ” has the meaning given by section 199 (13) .

205.9

“ Subsidiary undertaking ” has the same meaning as in the Companies Acts (see
section 1162 of the Companies Act 2006).

205.10

“ UK company ” means a company formed and registered under the Companies Act
2006.

In a case where this subsection applies, subsection (2)(b) has effect as if

person may be directed to pay) were omitted.

207.1.2B

Subsection (2A) applies where the Society takes action against a person under
subsection (2)(b)—

207.1.2B.a

for failure to comply with a requirement or rule referred to in subsection
(1)(a), where—

207.1.2B.a.i

the requirement or rule applies only for purposes relating to the prevention
or detection of economic crime, or

207.1.2B.a.ii

the failure consisted of an act or omission which had the effect of inhibiting
the prevention or detection of economic crime, or

207.1.2B.b

for professional misconduct as referred to in subsection (1)(b), where the
misconduct consisted of an act or omission which had the effect of inhibiting
the prevention or detection of economic crime.

207.1.2C

In subsection (2B) “ economic crime ” has the meaning given by section 193(1)

207.2.2B

under sub-paragraph (2)(b) for failure to comply with a requirement or rule
referred to in sub-paragraph (1) where—

207.2.2B.a

the requirement or rule applies only for purposes relating to the prevention
or detection of economic crime, or

207.2.2B.b

the failure consisted of an act or omission which had the effect of inhibiting
the prevention or detection of economic crime.

207.2.2C

In sub-paragraph (2B) “ economic crime ” has the meaning given by section

207.3

##### Approved regulators: information powers relating to economic crime

210

210.1

The Legal Services Act 2007 is amended as follows.

210.2

After section 111 insert—

########### Approved regulators: information powers

############ The Law Society’s information powers relating to economic crime

############# The Law Society’s information powers relating to economic crime

210.2.111A

210.2.111A.1

The Law Society may, by notice, require a person falling within subsection
(3)  to—

210.2.111A.1.a

provide information, or information of a description, specified in the notice;

210.2.111A.1.b

produce documents, or documents of a description, specified in the notice.

210.2.111A.2

The Law Society may only exercise the power in subsection  (1)  in relation to
information or documents which the Law Society considers it necessary or
expedient to have for the purposes of, or in connection with, the performance
of its regulatory functions for purposes relating to the prevention or
detection of economic crime.

210.2.111A.3

The persons are—

210.2.111A.3.a

a solicitor;

210.2.111A.3.b

an employee of a solicitor;

210.2.111A.3.c

a body recognised under section 9 of the Administration of Justice Act 1985;

210.2.111A.3.d

an employee or manager of, or person with an interest in, such a body;

210.2.111A.3.e

a licensed body;

210.2.111A.3.f

a manager or employee of a licensed body;

210.2.111A.3.g

a non-authorised person who has an interest or an indirect interest, or holds
a material interest (within the meaning of Part 5 of this Act), in a licensed
body;

210.2.111A.3.h

a person who was, but is no longer, of a description mentioned within any of
paragraphs  (a)  to  (g) .

210.2.111A.4

A notice under subsection  (1) —

210.2.111A.4.a

may specify the manner and form in which the information is to be provided or
document produced;

210.2.111A.4.b

must specify the period within which the information is to be provided or
document produced;

210.2.111A.4.c

may require the information to be provided, or document to be produced, to the
Law Society or to a person specified in the notice.

210.2.111A.5

The Law Society may pay to any person such reasonable costs as may be incurred
by that person in connection with the provision of any information, or
production of any document, by that person pursuant to a notice under
subsection  (1) .

210.2.111A.6

The Law Society, or a person specified under subsection  (4)(c)  in a notice,
may take copies of or extracts from a document produced pursuant to a notice
under subsection  (1) .

210.2.111A.7

In this section “ economic crime ” has the meaning given by section 193(1) of
the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023.

############# Enforcement of information powers relating to economic crime

210.2.111B

210.2.111B.1

If a person refuses or otherwise fails to comply with a notice under section
111A (1) , the Law Society may apply to the High Court for an order requiring
the person to comply with the notice or with such directions for the like
purpose as may be contained in the order.

210.2.111B.2

On an application under subsection  (1) , the High Court may order a person
other than the person to whom the notice was given to provide information or
produce documents specified in the notice, if the High Court is satisfied that
there is reason to suspect that the information or documents have come into
the possession or custody or under the control of that other person.

210.2.111B.3

Section  111A (4)  applies in relation to an order under subsection  (2)  as
it applies in relation to a notice under section  111A (1) .

210.2.111B.4

An order under this section may direct the Law Society to pay such reasonable
costs as may be incurred by a person in connection with the provision of any
information, or production of any document, by that person pursuant to the
order.

210.2.111B.5

A person may take copies of or extracts from a document produced to them
pursuant to an order under this section.

############# Provision of information relating to economic crime by other persons

210.2.111C

210.2.111C.1

The Law Society may apply to the High Court for an order requiring a person
who does not fall within section  111A (3)  to—

210.2.111C.1.a

provide information, or information of a description, specified in the order,
or

210.2.111C.1.b

produce documents, or documents of a description, specified in the order.

210.2.111C.2

The High Court may make an order under this section only if it is satisfied—

210.2.111C.2.a

that it is likely that the information or document is in the possession or
custody of, or under the control of, the person, and

210.2.111C.2.b

that it is necessary or expedient for the Law Society to have the information
or document for the purposes of, or in connection with, the performance of its
regulatory functions for purposes relating to the prevention or detection of
economic crime.

210.2.111C.3

Section  111A (4)  applies in relation to an order under this section as it
applies in relation to a notice under section  111A (1) .

210.2.111C.4

An order under this section may direct the Law Society to pay such reasonable
costs as may be incurred by a person in connection with the provision of any
information, or production of any document, by that person pursuant to the
order.

210.2.111C.5

A person may take copies of or extracts from a document produced to them
pursuant to an order under this section.

210.2.111C.6

In this section “ economic crime ” has the meaning given by section 193(1) of
the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act 2023.

############ Other approved regulators: information powers relating to economic crime

############# Order to confer information powers on other approved regulators

210.2.111D

210.2.111D.1

The Lord Chancellor may by order amend this Part so as to—

210.2.111D.1.a

provide for sections  111A  to  111C  to apply in relation to an approved
regulator other than the Law Society as they apply in relation to the Law
Society, and

210.2.111D.1.b

specify the persons to whom notices under section  111A (1)  may be given by
that approved regulator.

210.2.111D.2

The Lord Chancellor may make an order under this section in relation to an
approved regulator only if—

210.2.111D.2.a

the Board has made a recommendation in accordance with section 111E in
relation to that approved regulator, and

210.2.111D.2.b

the persons specified in the order to whom notices under section 111A(1) may
be given by that approved regulator are the same as those persons specified in
the recommendation.

############# The Board’s power to recommend orders under section 111D

210.2.111E

210.2.111E.1

The Board may recommend to the Lord Chancellor that the Lord Chancellor make
an order under section  111D  in relation to an approved regulator.

210.2.111E.2

A recommendation must specify the persons to whom the approved regulator
should be able to give notices under section  111A (1) .

210.2.111E.3

A recommendation may only be made with the consent of the approved regulator.

210.2.111E.4

Before making a recommendation under this section, the Board must publish a
draft of the proposed recommendation.

210.2.111E.5

The draft must be accompanied by a notice which states that representations
about the proposed recommendation may be made to the Board within a specified
period.

210.2.111E.6

Before making the recommendation, the Board must have regard to any
representations duly made.

210.3

In section 206 (parliamentary control of orders and regulations), in
subsection (4), after paragraph (n) insert—

210.3.na

section 111D (order to confer information powers on other approved
regulators);

.

#### Reports on payments to governments

##### Reports on payments to governments regulations: false statement offences etc

212

For regulation 16 of the Reports on Payments to Governments Regulations 2014 (
S.I. 2014/3209 ) substitute—

######### False statements: basic offence

212.16

212.16.1

It is an offence for a person, without reasonable excuse, to—

212.16.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for the purposes of these
Regulations, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular, or

212.16.1.b

make to the registrar, for the purposes of these Regulations, a statement that
is misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

212.16.2

Where the offence is committed by a firm, every officer of the firm who is in
default also commits the offence.

212.16.3

In paragraph  (2)  “ firm ” has the meaning given by section 1173(1) of the
Act.

212.16.4

Sections 1121 to 1123 of the Act (liability of officers default:
interpretation etc) apply for the purposes of paragraph  (2)  as they apply
for the purposes of provisions of the Companies Acts.

212.16.5

A person guilty of an offence under this regulation is liable—

212.16.5.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

212.16.5.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale;

212.16.5.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on
the standard scale.

212.16.6

No proceedings are to be brought for an offence under this regulation—

212.16.6.a

in England and Wales except by or with the consent of the Secretary of State
or the Director of Public Prosecutions;

212.16.6.b

in Northern Ireland except by or with the consent of the Secretary of State or
the Director of Public Prosecutions for Northern Ireland.

######### False statements: aggravated offence

212.16BA

212.16BA.1

It is an offence for a person knowingly to—

212.16BA.1.a

deliver or cause to be delivered to the registrar, for the purposes of these
Regulations, a document that is misleading, false or deceptive in a material
particular, or

212.16BA.1.b

make to the registrar, for the purposes of these Regulations, a statement that
is misleading, false or deceptive in a material particular.

212.16BA.2

Where the offence is committed by a firm, every officer of the firm who is in
default also commits the offence.

212.16BA.3

In paragraph  (2)  “ firm ” has the meaning given by section 1173(1) of the
Act.

212.16BA.4

Sections 1121 to 1123 of the Act (liability of officers default:
interpretation etc) apply for the purposes of paragraph  (2)  as they apply
for the purposes of provisions of the Companies Acts.

212.16BA.5

A person guilty of an offence under this regulation is liable—

212.16BA.5.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

212.16BA.5.b

on summary conviction—

212.16BA.5.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

212.16BA.5.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

212.16BA.5.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

212.16BA.6

No proceedings are to be brought for an offence under this regulation—

212.16BA.6.a

in England and Wales except by or with the consent of the Secretary of State
or the Director of Public Prosecutions;

212.16BA.6.b

in Northern Ireland except by or with the consent of the Secretary of State or
the Director of Public Prosecutions for Northern Ireland.

213

#### Sanctions enforcement: monetary penalties

##### Sanctions enforcement: monetary penalties

214

214.1

In section 143 of the Policing and Crime Act 2017 (interpretation), in
subsection (4) (meaning of “ financial sanctions legislation ”), in paragraph
(f)—

214.1.a

the words from “contains” to the end become sub-paragraph (i);

214.1.b

at the end of that sub-paragraph insert—

;

214.1.b.ii

makes supplemental provision (within the meaning of section 1(6) of that Act)
in connection with any prohibition or requirement mentioned in sub-paragraph
(i).

214.2

The Sanctions and Anti-Money Laundering Act 2018 is amended as follows.

214.3

In section 17 (enforcement), in subsection (9), in paragraph (a), after “(2)”
insert  “or makes supplemental provision in connection with any such
prohibition or requirement” .

214.4

After section 17 insert—

########### Enforcement: monetary penalties

214.4.17A

214.4.17A.1

The provision that may be made by virtue of section 17(2) (enforcement of
prohibitions or requirements) includes provision authorising a prescribed
person to impose a monetary penalty on another person if satisfied, to the
prescribed standard of proof, that the other person has breached a
prohibition, or failed to comply with a requirement, that is imposed by or
under regulations.

214.4.17A.2

Regulations authorising the Treasury to impose a monetary penalty in respect
of a breach or failure for which the Treasury could impose a monetary penalty
under Part 8 of the Policing and Crime Act 2017 may not be made unless the
regulations also make provision of the kind mentioned in section 17(9) to
disapply Part 8 of that Act in respect of that breach or failure.

214.4.17A.3

Regulations authorising the imposition of a monetary penalty may make
provision that, in determining for the purposes of the regulations whether a
person has breached a prohibition, or failed to comply with a requirement, any
requirement relating to the person’s knowledge or intention is to be ignored.

214.4.17A.4

Regulations authorising the imposition of a monetary penalty must provide
that—

214.4.17A.4.a

a person is not liable to such a penalty in respect of conduct amounting to an
offence if—

214.4.17A.4.a.i

proceedings have been brought against the person for that offence in respect
of that conduct and the proceedings are ongoing, or

214.4.17A.4.a.ii

the person has been convicted of that offence in respect of that conduct, and

214.4.17A.4.b

no proceedings may be brought against a person in respect of conduct amounting
to an offence if the person has been given such a penalty under the
regulations in respect of that conduct.

214.4.17A.5

Where regulations authorising the imposition of a monetary penalty authorise a
prescribed person to determine the amount of the penalty, the regulations must
provide for a maximum penalty.

214.4.17A.6

The maximum penalty may be a prescribed sum of any amount or may be calculated
in accordance with the regulations.

214.4.17A.7

In this section—

“ conduct ” means an act or omission; “regulations” mean regulations under
section 1.

#### Report on costs orders for proceedings for civil recovery

##### Report on costs orders for proceedings for civil recovery

215

215.1

The Secretary of State must assess whether it would be appropriate to restrict
the court’s power to order that the costs of proceedings under Chapter 2 of
Part 5 of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 are payable by an enforcement
authority and, if so, how.

215.2

In carrying out the assessment, the Secretary of State must consult such
persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

215.3

The Secretary of State must publish and lay before Parliament a report on the
outcome of the assessment by the end of the period of 12 months beginning with
the day on which this Act is passed.

215.4

In this section “ the court ” means the High Court in England and Wales.

### General

#### Power to make consequential provision

216

216.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision that is consequential
on this Act.

216.2

Regulations under this section may amend, repeal or revoke provision made by
or under primary legislation passed—

216.2.a

before this Act, or

216.2.b

later in the same session of Parliament as this Act.

216.3

In this section “ primary legislation ” means—

216.3.a

an Act,

216.3.b

an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru,

216.3.c

an Act of the Scottish Parliament, or

216.3.d

Northern Ireland legislation.

#### Regulations

217

217.1

A power to make regulations under any provision of this Act includes power to
make—

217.1.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;

217.1.b

different provision for different purposes.

217.2

Regulations made by the Secretary of State or the Lord Chancellor under this
Act are to be made by statutory instrument.

217.3

For regulations made under this Act by the Scottish Ministers, see section 27
of the Interpretation and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act  2010 (asp 10)
(Scottish statutory instruments).

217.4

Any power of the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland to make regulations
under this Act is exercisable by statutory rule for the purposes of the
Statutory Rules (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12) ).

217.5

A statutory instrument containing any of the following (whether alone or with
other provision) may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been
laid before and approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament—

217.5.a

regulations under section 37;

217.5.b

regulations under section 39;

217.5.c

regulations under section 153, unless they are regulations under that section
that only make provision that corresponds or is similar to provision made or
capable of being made by a statutory instrument that is itself subject to
annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament;

217.5.d

regulations under section 178;

217.5.e

regulations under section 193;

217.5.f

regulations made by the Secretary of State under section 197 (1) ;

217.5.g

regulations made by the Secretary of State under section 200 (1) ;

217.5.h

regulations under section 201 (6)  or  (7) ;

217.5.i

regulations under section 216 that amend or repeal provision made by an Act.

217.6

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations under this Act is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

217.7

But subsection  (6)  does not apply to a statutory instrument that only
contains regulations appointing the appointed day for the purposes of section
50.

217.8

Regulations made by the Scottish Ministers under section 197 (1)  or 200 (1)
are subject to the affirmative procedure (see section 29 of the Interpretation
and Legislative Reform (Scotland) Act  2010 (asp 10) ).

217.9

Regulations made by the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland under
section 197 (1)  or 200 (1)  may not be made unless a draft of the regulations
has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, the Northern Ireland
Assembly.

217.10

This section does not apply to regulations under sections 219 and 220.

#### Extent

218

218.1

This Act extends to England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland, subject
to subsections  (2)  and  (3) .

218.2

Sections 194 and 195 extend to England and Wales only.

218.3

An amendment, repeal or revocation made by this Act has the same extent as the
provision amended, repealed or revoked.

#### Commencement

219

219.1

Except as provided by subsections  (2)  to  (5) , this Act comes into force on
such day as the Secretary of State or the Lord Chancellor may by regulations
made by statutory instrument appoint.

219.2

The following come into force on the day on which this Act is passed—

219.2.a

this Part;

219.2.b

any provision of, or amendment made by, Parts 1 to 5 so far as it confers a
power to make regulations or relates to the exercise of the power;

219.2.c

paragraph 1 of Schedule 9 so far as it inserts section 303Z25 into the
Proceeds of Crime Act 2002;

219.2.d

paragraph 17 of Schedule 9 so far as it relates to that section;

219.2.e

section 180 so far as it relates to the provisions mentioned in paragraphs
(c)  and  (d) ;

219.2.f

section 182;

219.2.g

section 184;

219.2.h

section 185(12) and (13);

219.2.i

section 186(13) and (14).

219.3

The following come into force at the end of the period of 2 months beginning
with the day on which this Act is passed—

219.3.a

section 196 and Schedule 12;

219.3.b

section 197;

219.3.c

section 198;

219.3.d

section 213.

219.4

The following come into force (so far as not brought into force by subsection
(2)(b) ) on such day as the Scottish Ministers may by regulations appoint
after consulting the Secretary of State—

219.4.a

Part 2 of Schedule 8, and

219.4.b

section 179 so far as it relates to that Part.

219.5

The following come into force (so far as not brought into force by subsection
(2)(b) ) on such day as the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland may by
order appoint after consulting the Secretary of State—

219.5.a

Part 3 of Schedule 8, and

219.5.b

section 179 so far as it relates to that Part.

219.6

No regulations may be made under subsection  (1)  bringing into force any of
the following provisions, so far as they extend to Scotland, unless the
Secretary of State has consulted the Scottish Ministers—

219.6.a

Schedule 9, and

219.6.b

section 180 so far as it relates to that Schedule.

219.7

No regulations may be made under subsection  (1)  bringing into force any of
the following provisions, so far as they extend to Northern Ireland, unless
the Secretary of State has consulted the Department of Justice in Northern
Ireland—

219.7.a

Schedule 9, other than paragraphs 6(7), 10 and 11, and

219.7.b

section 180 so far as it relates to that Schedule, other than paragraphs 6(7),
10 and 11.

219.8

No regulations may be made under subsection  (1)  bringing into force section
199 unless the Secretary of State has published guidance under section 204(3).

219.9

Regulations under subsection  (1)  or  (4) , and orders subsection  (5) , may
appoint different days for—

219.9.a

different purposes, and

219.9.b

where regulations under subsection  (1)  appoint a day for the coming into
force of any provision of Schedule 9 or 10, different areas.

219.10

A power of the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland to make an order
under subsection  (5)  is exercisable by statutory rule for the purposes of
the Statutory Rules (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12)
).

#### Transitional provision

220

220.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument make
transitional or saving provision in connection with the coming into force of
any provision of this Act, other than a provision mentioned in section 219 (4)
or  (5) .

220.2

The Scottish Ministers may by regulations make transitional or saving
provision in connection with the coming into force of a provision mentioned in
section 219 (4) .

220.3

The Department of Justice in Northern Ireland may by order make transitional
or saving provision in connection with the coming into force of a provision
mentioned in section 219 (5) .

220.4

The power to make regulations under subsection  (1)  or  (2) , and the power
to make orders under subsection  (3) , includes power to make different
provision for—

220.4.a

different purposes, and

220.4.b

where regulations under subsection  (1)  make provision in connection with the
coming into force of any provision of Schedule 9 or 10, different areas.

220.5

Transitional provision and savings made under subsections  (1)  to  (3)  are
additional, and without prejudice, to those made by or under any other
provision of this Act.

220.6

A power of the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland to make an order
under subsection  (3)  is exercisable by statutory rule for the purposes of
the Statutory Rules (Northern Ireland) Order 1979 ( S.I. 1979/1573 (N.I. 12)
).

#### Short title

221

This Act may be cited as the Economic Crime and Corporate Transparency Act
2023.

3.4.2

The central register is prima facie evidence of any matters about which a
company was required to deliver information to the registrar under Chapter 2A
by virtue of an election under section 128B at any time before the repeal of
that Chapter (including that section) by the Economic Crime and Corporate

3.4.3

Subsection  (2)  does not apply to information required to be included in a
