Abolition of certain local registers

Section 51

##### Register of directors

1

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

2

Omit—

2.a

sections 161A to 167F (register of directors etc);

2.b

the italic heading before section 161A.

3

3.1

Before section 168 (and before the italic heading before that section) insert—

########### Notification of information about directors

############ Duty to notify registrar of change in directors

3.1.167G

3.1.167G.1

A company must give notice to the registrar if a person—

3.1.167G.1.a

becomes a director of the company, or

3.1.167G.1.b

ceases to be a director of the company.

3.1.167G.2

The notice must specify the date on which the person became or ceased to be a
director of the company.

3.1.167G.3

A notice under subsection  (1)(a)  of a person having become a director must
contain—

3.1.167G.3.a

a statement of the required information about the new director (see sections
167J  and  167K );

3.1.167G.3.b

a statement by the company that the person has consented to act in that
capacity;

3.1.167G.3.c

if the person is an individual, a statement that their identity is verified
(see section 1110A);

3.1.167G.3.d

a statement that the person is not—

3.1.167G.3.d.i

disqualified under the directors disqualification legislation (see section
159A(2)), or

3.1.167G.3.d.ii

otherwise ineligible by virtue of any enactment for appointment as a director;

3.1.167G.3.e

if the person would be disqualified under the directors disqualification
legislation but for the permission of a court to act, a statement to that
effect specifying—

3.1.167G.3.e.i

the court by which permission was given, and

3.1.167G.3.e.ii

the date on which permission was given.

3.1.167G.3.f

if the person would be disqualified under the directors disqualification
legislation by virtue of section 11A of the Company Directors Disqualification
Act 1986 or Article 15A of the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern
Ireland) Order 2002 (designated persons under sanctions legislation) but for
the authority of a licence of the kind mentioned in that section or Article, a
statement to that effect specifying—

3.1.167G.3.f.i

the date on which the licence was issued, and

3.1.167G.3.f.ii

by whom it was issued.

3.1.167G.4

In subsection  (3)(e)  “ permission of a court to act ” means permission of a
court under a provision mentioned in column 2 of the table in section 159A(2).

3.1.167G.5

Subsection  (1)(a)  does not require a company, on its incorporation, to give
notice in relation to a person named as a proposed director in the statement
under section 12.

3.1.167G.6

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the person becomes or ceases to be a director.

############ Duty to notify registrar of changes of information

3.1.167H

3.1.167H.1

A company must give notice to the registrar of any change in the required
information about a director (see sections  167J  and  167K ).

3.1.167H.2

The notice must specify the date on which the change occurred.

3.1.167H.3

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the change occurs.

3.1.167H.4

Where a company gives notice of a change of a director’s service address but
not their residential address, the notice must contain a statement that the
residential address is unchanged.

############ Notification of changes occurring before company’s incorporation

3.1.167I

3.1.167I.1

A company must give notice to the registrar if a person named in the statement
under section 12 as a proposed director of the company did not become a
director on its incorporation.

3.1.167I.2

A company must give notice to the registrar of any change in the required
information about a proposed director that occurred—

3.1.167I.2.a

after the application for the company’s registration under section 9 was
delivered to the registrar, but

3.1.167I.2.b

before the company was incorporated.

3.1.167I.3

But a company is not required to give notice under subsection  (2)  in respect
of a person if it gives notice under subsection  (1)  in respect of the
person.

3.1.167I.4

A notice under subsection  (2)  must specify the date on which the change
occurred.

3.1.167I.5

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company was incorporated.

############ Required information about a director: individuals

3.1.167J

3.1.167J.1

The required information about a director (or proposed director) who is an
individual is—

3.1.167J.1.a

name, date of birth and nationality;

3.1.167J.1.b

any relevant former names;

3.1.167J.1.c

a service address (which may be stated as “The company’s registered office”);

3.1.167J.1.d

usual residential address;

3.1.167J.1.e

the part of the United Kingdom in which the individual is usually resident or,
if the individual is usually resident in a country or state outside the United
Kingdom, that country or state.

3.1.167J.2

In subsection  (1)(b)  “ relevant former name ” means any former name other
than—

3.1.167J.2.a

in the case of a peer, or an individual normally known by a British title, the
name by which the individual was known previous to the adoption of or
succession to the title, or

3.1.167J.2.b

in the case of any person—

3.1.167J.2.b.i

a former name which was changed or disused before the person attained the age
of 16 years,

3.1.167J.2.b.ii

a former name which has been changed or disused for 20 years or more, or

3.1.167J.2.b.iii

a former name which the registrar is required to refrain from making available
for public inspection or from disclosing (or both) by virtue of regulations
under section  1088 (1)(a)  or  (b) .

3.1.167J.3

In this section—

“ former name ” means a name by which the individual was formerly known for
business purposes; “ name ” means the individual’s forename and surname.

3.1.167J.4

Where a director (or proposed director) is a peer or an individual usually
known by a title, any requirement imposed by this Act to provide the
individual’s name because it forms part of the required information may be
satisfied by providing that title instead of the individual’s forename and
surname.

3.1.167J.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

3.1.167J.5.a

amend this section so as to change the required information about a director
(or proposed director) who is an individual;

3.1.167J.5.b

repeal subsection  (4) .

3.1.167J.6

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

############ Required information about a director: corporate directors and firms

3.1.167K

3.1.167K.1

The required information about a director (or proposed director) that is a
body corporate, or a firm that is a legal person under the law by which it is
governed, is—

3.1.167K.1.a

corporate or firm name;

3.1.167K.1.b

principal office;

3.1.167K.1.c

a service address (which may be stated as “The company’s registered office”);

3.1.167K.1.d

in the case of a limited company that is a UK-registered company, the
registered number;

3.1.167K.1.e

in any other case, particulars of—

3.1.167K.1.e.i

the legal form of the body corporate or firm and the law by which it is
governed, and

3.1.167K.1.e.ii

if applicable, the register in which it is entered (including details of the
state) and its registration number in that register.

3.1.167K.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section so as to change
the required information about a director (or proposed director) of a
description mentioned in subsection  (1) .

3.1.167K.3

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

############ Directors: offence of failure to notify of changes

3.1.167L

3.1.167L.1

If a company fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with section  167G ,
167H  or  167I , an offence is committed by—

3.1.167L.1.a

the company, and

3.1.167L.1.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

3.1.167L.2

For this purpose a shadow director is treated as an officer of the company.

3.1.167L.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

3.1.167L.3.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

3.1.167L.3.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

3.2

The provision that may be made under section 220 (1)  in connection with the
coming into force of this paragraph includes—

3.2.a

provision requiring a company to deliver to the registrar, at the same time as
a confirmation statement, a statement, in respect of any individual who became
a director of the company (otherwise than on its incorporation) before the
coming into force of this paragraph, confirming that the individual’s identity
is verified (within the meaning of section 1110A of the Companies Act 2006),
and

3.2.b

provision for section 853A(1)(b)(i) of the Companies Act 2006 (as substituted
by section 59 of this Act) to have effect as if it included a reference to the
duty imposed by virtue of paragraph  (a) .

3.3

In sub-paragraph  (2) —

“ confirmation statement ” has the meaning given by section 853A of the
Companies Act 2006; “ the registrar ” has the same meaning as in the Companies
Acts (see section 1060 of the Companies Act 2006).

##### Register of secretaries

4

The Companies Act 2006 is amended as follows.

5

Omit sections 274A to 279F (register of secretaries etc) (including the italic
heading before section 279A).

6

Before section 280 insert—

######### Notification of information about secretaries

########## Duty to notify registrar of change in secretary or joint secretary

6.279G

6.279G.1

A company must give notice to the registrar if a person—

6.279G.1.a

becomes the secretary or one of the joint secretaries of the company, or

6.279G.1.b

ceases to be the secretary or one of the joint secretaries of the company.

6.279G.2

The notice must specify the date on which the person became or ceased to be
the secretary or one of the joint secretaries of the company.

6.279G.3

A notice under subsection  (1)(a)  must contain—

6.279G.3.a

a statement of the required information about the secretary or joint secretary
(see sections  279J  and  279K ), and

6.279G.3.b

a statement by the company that the person has consented to act in that
capacity.

6.279G.4

Subsection  (1)(a)  does not require a company, on its incorporation, to give
notice in relation to a person named as the proposed secretary or one of the
proposed joint secretaries of the company in the statement under section 12.

6.279G.5

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the person becomes or ceases to be the
secretary or a joint secretary.

########## Duty to notify registrar of changes of information

6.279H

6.279H.1

A company must give notice to the registrar of any change in the required
information about the secretary or one of the joint secretaries of the company
(see sections  279J  and  279K ).

6.279H.2

The notice must specify the date on which the change occurred.

6.279H.3

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the change occurs.

########## Notification of changes occurring before company’s incorporation

6.279I

6.279I.1

A company must give notice to the registrar if—

6.279I.1.a

a person named in the statement under section 12 as the proposed secretary of
the company did not become the secretary on its incorporation, or

6.279I.1.b

a person named in the statement under section 12 as one of the proposed joint
secretaries of the company become did not become one of the joint secretaries
on its incorporation.

6.279I.2

A company must give notice to the registrar of any change in the required
information about a proposed secretary, or one of the proposed joint
secretaries, that occurred—

6.279I.2.a

after the application for the company’s registration under section 9 was
delivered to the registrar, but

6.279I.2.b

before the company was incorporated.

6.279I.3

But a company is not required to give notice under subsection  (2)  in respect
of a person if it gives notice under subsection  (1)  in respect of the
person.

6.279I.4

A notice under subsection  (2)  must specify the date on which the change
occurred.

6.279I.5

A notice under this section must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company was incorporated.

########## Required information about a secretary etc: individuals

6.279J

6.279J.1

The required information about a secretary or joint secretary (or proposed
secretary or joint secretary) who is an individual is—

6.279J.1.a

name;

6.279J.1.b

any relevant former names;

6.279J.1.c

a service address (which may be stated as “The company’s registered office”).

6.279J.2

In subsection  (1)(b)  “ relevant former name ” means any former name other
than—

6.279J.2.a

in the case of a peer, or an individual normally known by a British title, the
name by which the individual was known previous to the adoption of or
succession to the title, or

6.279J.2.b

in the case of any person—

6.279J.2.b.i

a former name which was changed or disused before the person attained the age
of 16 years,

6.279J.2.b.ii

a former name which has been changed or disused for 20 years or more, or

6.279J.2.b.iii

a former name which the registrar is required to refrain from making available
for public inspection or from disclosing (or both) by virtue of regulations
under section  1088 (1)(a)  or  (b) .

6.279J.3

In this section—

“ former name ” means a name by which the individual was formerly known for
business purposes; “ name ” means the individual’s forename and surname.

6.279J.4

Where a secretary or joint secretary (or proposed secretary or joint
secretary) is a peer or an individual usually known by a title, any
requirement of this Act to provide the individual’s name because it forms part
of the required information may be satisfied by providing that title instead
of the individual’s forename and surname.

6.279J.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

6.279J.5.a

amend this section so as to change the required information about a secretary
or joint secretary (or proposed secretary or joint secretary) who is an
individual;

6.279J.5.b

repeal subsection  (4) .

6.279J.6

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

########## Required information about a secretary etc: corporate secretaries and firms

6.279K

6.279K.1

The required information about a secretary or joint secretary (or proposed
secretary or joint secretary) that is a body corporate, or a firm that is a
legal person under the law by which it is governed, is—

6.279K.1.a

corporate or firm name;

6.279K.1.b

principal office;

6.279K.1.c

a service address (which may be stated as “The company’s registered office”);

6.279K.1.d

in the case of a limited company that is a UK-registered company, the
registered number;

6.279K.1.e

in any other case, particulars of—

6.279K.1.e.i

the legal form of the body corporate or firm and the law by which it is
governed, and

6.279K.1.e.ii

if applicable, the register in which it is entered (including details of the
state) and its registration number in that register.

6.279K.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section so as to change
the required information about a secretary or joint secretary (or proposed
secretary or joint secretary) of a description mentioned in subsection  (1) .

6.279K.3

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

########## Firms all of whose partners are joint secretaries

6.279L

6.279L.1

This section applies where—

6.279L.1.a

all the members in a firm are joint secretaries (or proposed joint
secretaries) of a company, and

6.279L.1.b

the firm is not a legal person under the law by which it is governed.

6.279L.2

Any requirement imposed by this Act to provide the required information about
the members as joint secretaries (or proposed joint secretaries) may instead
be satisfied by providing the information that would be required if the firm
were a legal person and the firm had been appointed as secretary.

########## Secretary or joint secretary: offence of failure to notify of changes

6.279M

6.279M.1

If a company fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with section  279G ,
279H  or  279I , an offence is committed by—

6.279M.1.a

the company, and

6.279M.1.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

6.279M.2

For this purpose a shadow director is treated as an officer of the company.

6.279M.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction—

6.279M.3.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

6.279M.3.b

in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the
standard scale and, for continued contravention, a daily default fine not
exceeding one-tenth of level 5 on the standard scale.

Person acting in dual capacity

.

Chapter 2A requires companies to notify the registrar of information relating

After section 790C insert—

######### References to “confirmation” etc of information

10.790CA

For the purposes of this Part a company has had confirmation of—

10.790CA.a

a person’s status as a registrable person or a registrable relevant legal
entity in relation to the company,

10.790CA.b

the required particulars of a person (see section 790K), or

10.790CA.c

any other information about a person,

if the person has supplied that information to the company whether or not in
pursuance of any duty imposed by this Part (and references to a company
obtaining confirmation of information are to be read accordingly).

11

For sections 790D and 790E substitute—

######### Duty to find out about persons with significant control

11.790CB

A company to which this Part applies must take reasonable steps to find out if
there is anyone who is a registrable person or a registrable relevant legal
entity in relation to the company and, if so, to identify them.

######### Company’s duty to give notices to persons with significant control

11.790D

11.790D.1

A company to which this Part applies must give a notice to a person under this
section if—

11.790D.1.a

the company knows or has cause to believe that the person is a registrable
person or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, but

11.790D.1.b

the company has not had confirmation of the person’s status as a registrable
person or registrable relevant legal entity or has not had confirmation of all
of the required particulars of the person (see section 790K).

11.790D.2

The notice must require the person—

11.790D.2.a

to inform the company whether the person is a registrable person or a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, and

11.790D.2.b

if they are, to give the company all of the required particulars of the person
(see section 790K).

11.790D.3

The notice must require the person to whom it is given to comply with the
notice by no later than the end of the period of one month beginning with the
day on which it is given.

11.790D.4

The company must give the notice—

11.790D.4.a

as soon as reasonably practicable after the company becomes subject to the
duty to give a notice under this section, and

11.790D.4.b

in any event before the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on
which the company becomes so subject.

11.790D.5

A company is not required to give a notice under this section to a person if—

11.790D.5.a

the application for the registration of the company contained a statement of
initial significant control naming the person as someone who would, on the
company’s incorporation, become a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to the company, and

11.790D.5.b

the company has no cause to believe that at any time since its incorporation
the person has ceased to be a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to the company.

11.790D.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
giving of notices under this section, including provision about their form and
content and the manner in which they must be given.

11.790D.7

Regulations under subsection  (6)  are subject to negative resolution
procedure.

######### Obtaining information from third parties

11.790DA

11.790DA.1

A company to which this Part applies may give a notice to a person under this
section if it knows or has cause to believe that the person—

11.790DA.1.a

knows the identity of someone who falls within subsection  (2) , or

11.790DA.1.b

knows the identity of someone likely to have that knowledge.

11.790DA.2

The persons who fall within this subsection are—

11.790DA.2.a

a registrable person in relation to the company;

11.790DA.2.b

a relevant legal entity in relation to the company;

11.790DA.2.c

an entity which would be a relevant legal entity in relation to the company
but for the fact that section 790C(6)(b) does not apply in respect of it.

11.790DA.3

A company must give a notice under subsection  (1)  to a person (“a third
party”) if the company—

11.790DA.3.a

knows or has cause to believe that a person is a registrable person or a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company (“a suspected
PSC”),

11.790DA.3.b

is under a duty to give the suspected PSC a notice under section  790D  but
does not have the information that it needs in order to contact them, and

11.790DA.3.c

knows or has cause to believe that the third party—

11.790DA.3.c.i

knows the identity of the suspected PSC, or

11.790DA.3.c.ii

knows the identity of someone likely to have that knowledge.

11.790DA.4

A notice under subsection  (1)  must require the person to whom it is given (“
the recipient ”)—

11.790DA.4.a

to inform the company whether the recipient knows the identity of any person
who—

11.790DA.4.a.i

falls within subsection  (2) , or

11.790DA.4.a.ii

is likely to know the identity of anyone who falls within subsection  (2) ,
and

11.790DA.4.b

if the recipient does, to give the company any information within the
recipient’s knowledge that would allow the company to contact each such
person.

11.790DA.5

The notice must require the person to whom it is given to comply with the
notice by no later than the end of the period of one month beginning with the
day on which it is given.

11.790DA.6

A person to whom a notice under subsection  (1)  is given is not required by
that notice to disclose any information in respect of which a claim to legal
professional privilege (in Scotland, to confidentiality of communications)
could be maintained in legal proceedings.

11.790DA.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
giving of notices under this section, including provision about their form and
content and the manner in which they must be given.

11.790DA.8

Regulations under subsection  (7)  are subject to negative resolution
procedure.

11.790DA.9

In this section a reference to knowing the identity of a person includes
knowing information from which that person can be identified.

######### Company’s duty to find out about changes in PSC information

11.790E

11.790E.1

This section applies if a company—

11.790E.1.a

knows or has cause to believe that there has been a change in the required
particulars of a registrable person or a registrable relevant legal entity in
relation to the company (see section 790K), but

11.790E.1.b

has not had confirmation that the change has occurred or has not had
confirmation of all of the information that the company would need to include
in a notice of the change under section  790LD (1) or  790LE (1).

11.790E.2

The company must give the person a notice requiring the person—

11.790E.2.a

to inform the company whether the change has occurred, and

11.790E.2.b

if it has, to give the company the information that the company would need to
include in a notice of the change under section  790LD (1) or  790LE (1).

11.790E.3

The notice must require the person to whom it is given to comply with the
notice by no later than the end of the period of one month beginning with the
day on which it is given.

11.790E.4

The company must give the notice—

11.790E.4.a

as soon as reasonably practicable after the company becomes subject to the
duty to give a notice under subsection (2), and

11.790E.4.b

in any event before the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on
which the company becomes so subject.

11.790E.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
giving of notices under this section, including provision about their form and
content and the manner in which they must be given.

11.790E.6

Regulations under subsection  (5)  are subject to negative resolution
procedure.

######### Company’s duty to find out about persons ceasing to be PSCs

11.790EA

11.790EA.1

This section applies if a company —

11.790EA.1.a

knows or has cause to believe that a person has ceased to be a registrable
person or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, but

11.790EA.1.b

has not had confirmation that the person has ceased to be a registrable person
or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company or has not
had confirmation of the date on which the person so ceased.

11.790EA.2

The company must give the person a notice requiring the person—

11.790EA.2.a

to inform the company whether the person has ceased to be a registrable person
or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, and

11.790EA.2.b

if the person has, to inform the company of the date on which the person so
ceased.

11.790EA.3

The notice must require the person to whom it is given to comply with the
notice by no later than the end of the period of one month beginning with the
day on which it is given.

11.790EA.4

The company must give the notice—

11.790EA.4.a

as soon as reasonably practicable after the company becomes subject to the
duty under subsection  (2) , and

11.790EA.4.b

in any event before the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on
which the company becomes so subject.

11.790EA.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about the
giving of notices under this section, including provision about their form and
content and the manner in which they must be given.

11.790EA.6

Regulations under subsection  (5)  are subject to negative resolution
procedure.

######### Company’s duty to notify failure to comply with notices

11.790EB

11.790EB.1

A company must notify the registrar if a person fails to comply with a notice
given by the company under section  790D ,  790DA ,  790E  or  790EA  within
the period specified in it.

11.790EB.2

The notice must be given within the period of 14 days beginning with the end
of the period specified in the notice under section  790D ,  790DA ,  790E  or
790EA .

######### Company’s duty to notify of late compliance with notices

11.790EC

11.790EC.1

A company must notify the registrar if a person who has failed to comply with
a notice given by the company under section  790D ,  790DA ,  790E  or  790EA
within the period specified in it subsequently complies.

11.790EC.2

The notice must be given within the period of 14 days beginning with the day
on which the person complied with the notice under section  790D ,  790DA ,
790E  or  790EA .

11

In section 790F (failure by company to comply with information duties), for
subsection (1) substitute—

11.1

If a company fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with a duty under
section  790CB , 790D,  790DA (3) , 790E,  790EA ,  790EB  or  790EC  to take
steps or give a notice, an offence is committed by—

11.1.a

the company, and

11.1.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

12

For sections 790G and 790H substitute—

######### Duty to notify company on becoming PSC

12.790G

12.790G.1

This section applies to a person if—

12.790G.1.a

the person knows that they are a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to a company,

12.790G.1.b

the material in the register that is available for public inspection does not
indicate the person’s status as a registrable person or registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to the company, and

12.790G.1.c

the person—

12.790G.1.c.i

has not informed the company of the person’s status as a registrable person or
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, or

12.790G.1.c.ii

has not given the company all of the required particulars of the person (see
section 790K).

12.790G.2

The person must—

12.790G.2.a

inform the company of the person’s status as a registrable person or
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, and

12.790G.2.b

give the company the required particulars (see section 790K).

12.790G.3

The person must comply with the duty in subsection  (2)  before the end of the
period of one month beginning with the day on which the conditions in
subsection (1) are met.

######### Duty to notify company of changes in PSC information

12.790H

12.790H.1

This section applies to a person if—

12.790H.1.a

the person knows that they are a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to a company,

12.790H.1.b

there has been a change in the required particulars of the person (see section
790K) and the person knows that to be the case, and

12.790H.1.c

the person has not informed the company of the change or has not given the
company all of the information that the company would need to include in a
notice of the change under section  790LD (1) or  790LE (1).

12.790H.2

The person must—

12.790H.2.a

inform the company of the change, and

12.790H.2.b

give the company the information that the company would need to include in a
notice of the change under section  790LD (1) or  790LE (1) .

12.790H.3

The person must comply with the duty in subsection (2) before the end of the
period of one month beginning with the day on which the conditions in
subsection (1) are met.

######### Duty to notify company of ceasing to be a PSC

12.790HA

12.790HA.1

This section applies to a person if—

12.790HA.1.a

the person knows that they have ceased to be a registrable person or a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company,

12.790HA.1.b

the material in the register that is available for public inspection does not
indicate the person as having ceased to be a registrable person or a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to a company, and

12.790HA.1.c

the person has not informed the company of having ceased to be a registrable
person or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company or
has not informed the company of the date on which the person so ceased.

12.790HA.2

The person must inform the company—

12.790HA.2.a

that the person has ceased to be a registrable person or a registrable
relevant legal entity in relation to the company, and

12.790HA.2.b

of the date on which the person so ceased.

12.790HA.3

The person must comply with the duty in subsection  (2)  before the end of the
period of one month beginning with the day on which the conditions in
subsection  (1)  are met.

######### Power to impose further duties

########## Power to impose further duties involving nominee shareholders

14.790IA

14.790IA.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision for the
purpose of enabling a company to which this Part applies to find out about
anyone who has become or ceased to be a person who is—

14.790IA.1.a

a registrable person in relation to the company by virtue of shares being held
by a nominee, or

14.790IA.1.b

a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company by virtue of
shares being held by a nominee.

14.790IA.2

The regulations may, in particular—

14.790IA.2.a

impose obligations on a company with a view to obtaining—

14.790IA.2.a.i

information about whether a person has become or ceased to be a nominee
shareholder;

14.790IA.2.a.ii

if they have, information about: (A) the shareholding; (B) the nominee; (C)
the person for whom the nominee holds or held the shares;

14.790IA.2.a.iii

any other information required by the regulations;

14.790IA.2.b

impose obligations on others (including nominees or former nominees) with a
view to providing the company with—

14.790IA.2.b.i

information of a kind described in paragraph (a)(i) or (ii);

14.790IA.2.b.ii

any other information required by the regulations.

14.790IA.3

The regulations may, in particular, make provision similar or corresponding to
any of the preceding provisions of this Chapter.

14.790IA.4

The provision that may be made by regulations under subsection (1) includes
provision amending this Chapter.

14.790IA.5

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

18

After section 790L insert—

######### Duty to notify registrar of persons with significant control and ID verification

########## Duty to notify registrar of persons with significant control

########### Duty to notify registrar of confirmed persons with significant control

18.790LA

18.790LA.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if it has had confirmation of—

18.790LA.1.a

a person’s status as a registrable person or a registrable relevant legal
entity in relation to the company, and

18.790LA.1.b

the required particulars of the person (see section 790K).

18.790LA.2

A notice under subsection (1) must contain a statement of the required
particulars.

18.790LA.3

A notice under subsection (1) must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company had confirmation as mentioned in
that subsection.

18.790LA.4

A company is not required to give a notice under this section in relation to a
person if—

18.790LA.4.a

the application for the registration of the company contained a statement of
initial significant control naming the person as someone who would, on the
company’s incorporation, become a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to the company, and

18.790LA.4.b

the company has no cause to believe that at any time since its incorporation
the person has ceased to be a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity in relation to the company.

18.790LA.5

Nothing in section 126 (notice of trusts not receivable by registrar) affects
the duty to give a notice under this section (or the receipt of that notice by
the registrar).

########### Option to provide ID verification information in notice of change

18.790LB

18.790LB.1

A notice under section  790LA (1)  that relates to a registrable person may
include a statement that the person’s identity is verified (see section
1110A).

18.790LB.2

A notice under section  790LA (1)  that relates to a registrable relevant
legal entity may include a statement that—

18.790LB.2.a

specifies the name of one of its relevant officers (within the meaning given
by section  790LO (6) ) who is an individual and whose identity is verified,
and

18.790LB.2.b

confirms that the individual’s identity is verified.

18.790LB.3

If the notice includes a statement under subsection  (2) , it must be
accompanied by a statement by the individual confirming that the individual is
a relevant officer of the registrable relevant legal entity.

18.790LB.4

To find out what happens if the option in subsection  (1)  or  (2)  is not
exercised, see sections  790LM  and  790LO .

18.790LB.5

In subsection  (1)  “ registrable person ” does not include a person mentioned
in section 790C(12)(a) to (d).

########### Duty to notify registrar of unconfirmed persons with significant control

18.790LC

18.790LC.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if—

18.790LC.1.a

it knows or has cause to believe that a person has become a registrable person
or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, but

18.790LC.1.b

it has not yet had confirmation as mentioned in section  790LA (1).

18.790LC.2

The notice must state that fact.

18.790LC.3

A notice under subsection (1) must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company first knows or has cause to
believe that the person has become a registrable person or a registrable
relevant legal entity in relation to the company.

18.790LC.4

Nothing in this section requires a company, on its incorporation, to give a
notice in relation to a person included in the statement of initial
significant control under section 12A.

########## Duty to notify registrar of changes in required particulars

########### Duties to notify of changes in required particulars

18.790LD

18.790LD.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if it—

18.790LD.1.a

has had confirmation that there has been a change in the required particulars
of a registrable person, or a registrable relevant legal entity, in relation
to the company (see section 790K), and

18.790LD.1.b

has had confirmation of how the required particulars have changed and the date
on which they changed.

18.790LD.2

The notice must state—

18.790LD.2.a

the change in the required particulars, and

18.790LD.2.b

the date on which the change occurred.

18.790LD.3

A notice under subsection (1) must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company had confirmation as mentioned in
that subsection.

18.790LD.4

Nothing in section 126 (notice of trusts not receivable by registrar) affects
the duty to give a notice under this section (or the receipt of that notice by
the registrar).

########### Duty to notify of pre-incorporation changes in required particulars

18.790LE

18.790LE.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if it—

18.790LE.1.a

has had confirmation that there was a pre-incorporation change in the required
particulars of a proposed PSC (see section 790K), and

18.790LE.1.b

has had confirmation of how the required particulars have changed and the date
on which they changed.

18.790LE.2

But a company is not required to give a notice under subsection (1) in respect
of a person if it has given a notice under section  790LG  in respect of the
person.

18.790LE.3

A notice under subsection (1) must state—

18.790LE.3.a

the change in the required particulars, and

18.790LE.3.b

the date on which the change occurred.

18.790LE.4

A notice under subsection (1) must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company had confirmation as mentioned in
that subsection.

18.790LE.5

In this section—

“ pre-incorporation change ” means a change that occurred— after the
application for the registration of the company was delivered to the
registrar, but before the company was incorporated; “ proposed PSC ”, in
relation to a company, means a person who was named in a statement under
section 12A(1)(a) as a person who would, on the company’s incorporation,
become a registrable person or registrable relevant legal entity in relation
to the company.

########## Duty to notify registrar of person ceasing to be person with significant control etc

########### Duty to notify registrar when person ceases to have significant control

18.790LF

18.790LF.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if it—

18.790LF.1.a

has had confirmation that a person has ceased to be a registrable person or a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to it, and

18.790LF.1.b

has had confirmation of the date on which the person so ceased.

18.790LF.2

A notice under subsection (1) must state—

18.790LF.2.a

the person’s name and service address, and

18.790LF.2.b

the date on which the person ceased to be a registrable person or a
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company.

18.790LF.3

A notice under subsection (1) must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company had confirmation as mentioned in
that subsection.

########### Notification of someone not becoming person with significant control on incorporation

18.790LG

18.790LG.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if it knows that a person named
in the statement under section 12A (1)(a)  as a person who would, on the
company’s incorporation, become a registrable person or a registrable relevant
legal entity did not so become.

18.790LG.2

A notice under subsection  (1)  must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company has the knowledge mentioned there.

########### Duty to notify registrar if company ceases to have persons with significant control

18.790LH

18.790LH.1

A company must give a notice to the registrar if it knows or has cause to
believe that—

18.790LH.1.a

there has at some time been a person who is a registrable person or
registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the company, and

18.790LH.1.b

there has ceased to be anyone who is a registrable person or registrable
relevant legal entity in relation to the company.

18.790LH.2

A notice under subsection (1) must —

18.790LH.2.a

state that the company has that knowledge or cause to believe, and

18.790LH.2.b

specify the date on which the company first had that knowledge or cause to
believe.

18.790LH.3

A notice under subsection (1) must be given within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the company first had the knowledge or cause
to believe mentioned in that subsection.

########### Power to create further duties to notify information

18.790LI

18.790LI.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations impose further duties on a company
to deliver information to the registrar about—

18.790LI.1.a

registrable persons, or registrable relevant legal entities, in relation to
the company (including information about whether it has any);

18.790LI.1.b

compliance with Chapter 2 by the company or any person to whom the company has
given a notice under that Chapter (including provision requiring a company to
provide the registrar with a copy of any such notice, whether on request or
otherwise).

18.790LI.2

The provision that may be made by regulations under subsection (1) includes
provision amending this Part.

18.790LI.3

The consequential provision that may be made by regulations under subsection
(1) by virtue of section 1292(1) also includes provision amending any other
provision of this Act.

18.790LI.4

Regulations under this section are subject to affirmative resolution
procedure.

########### Persons with significant control: offence of failure to notify

18.790LJ

18.790LJ.1

If a company fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with section  790LA ,
790LC ,  790LD ,  790LE ,  790LF ,  790LG  or  790LH , or regulations under
section  790LI , an offence is committed by—

18.790LJ.1.a

the company, and

18.790LJ.1.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

18.790LJ.2

For this purpose a shadow director is treated as an officer of the company.

18.790LJ.3

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale and, for
continued contravention, a daily default fine not exceeding one-tenth of level
3 on the standard scale.

########### Power of court to order company to remedy defaults or delay

18.790LK

18.790LK.1

Where a company makes default in complying with section  790LA ,  790LC ,
790LD ,  790LE ,  790LF ,  790LG  or  790LH , or regulations under section
790LI , an application may be made to the court for an order requiring the
company to deliver to the registrar the information (or statements) necessary
to rectify the position.

18.790LK.2

The application may be made by—

18.790LK.2.a

any person aggrieved by the default,

18.790LK.2.b

any member of the company, or

18.790LK.2.c

any person who is a registrable person or a registrable relevant legal entity
in relation to the company.

18.790LK.3

On an application under subsection  (1)  the court may either refuse the
application or may make the order and order the company to pay any damages
sustained by any party aggrieved.

18.790LK.4

On an application under subsection  (1)  the court may decide—

18.790LK.4.a

any question as to whether the name of any person who is a party to the
application should or should not be included in or omitted from information
delivered to the registrar under this Chapter about persons who are a
registrable person or a registrable relevant legal entity in relation to the
company, and

18.790LK.4.b

any question necessary or expedient to be decided for rectifying the position.

18.790LK.5

Nothing in this section affects a person’s rights under section 1094 or 1096
(rectification of register).

########### Information as to whether information has been delivered

18.790LL

18.790LL.1

A person may request a company to tell the person whether all of the
information that it is required to deliver to the registrar under this Chapter
has been delivered.

18.790LL.2

The company must comply with the request within the period of 14 days
beginning with the day on which the request is made.

18.790LL.3

If the company fails, without reasonable excuse, to do so, an offence is
committed by—

18.790LL.3.a

the company, and

18.790LL.3.b

every officer of the company who is in default.

18.790LL.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

18.790LL.5

Subsection  (1)  does not apply in relation to information if the company is
aware that, by virtue of regulations under section  1088 , the registrar is
required to refrain from making that information available for public
inspection.

19

Omit Chapters 3 and 4 of Part 21A (company registers of people with
significant control etc).

20

20.1

Schedule 1B (enforcement of disclosure requirements in relation to persons
with significant control) is amended as follows.

20.2

In each of the following provisions, for “or 790E” substitute  “,  790DA ,
790E or  790EA ” —

20.2.a

paragraph 1(1)(a) and (3)(a);

20.2.b

paragraph 8(3)(a);

20.2.c

paragraph 11(a) and (b);

20.2.d

paragraph 12(2)(b).

20.3

For paragraphs 13 and 14 substitute—

########### Offence of failing to comply with notices

20.3.13

20.3.13.1

A person to whom a notice under section  790D ,  790DA ,  790E  or  790EA  is
addressed commits an offence if the person fails, without reasonable excuse,
to comply with the notice.

20.3.13.2

Where the person is a legal entity, the offence is also committed by every
officer of the entity who is in default.

20.3.13.3

A person guilty of an offence under this paragraph is liable—

20.3.13.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

20.3.13.3.b

on summary conviction—

20.3.13.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

20.3.13.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

20.3.13.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

########### Offence of failing to provide information

20.3.14

20.3.14.1

A person commits an offence if the person fails, without reasonable excuse, to
comply with a duty under section  790G ,  790H  or  790HA .

20.3.14.2

Where the person is a legal entity, the offence is also committed by every
officer of the entity who is in default.

20.3.14.3

A person guilty of an offence under this paragraph is liable—

20.3.14.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

20.3.14.3.b

on summary conviction—

20.3.14.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or a fine (or both);

20.3.14.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or a fine not
exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

20.3.14.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

########### False statements: basic offence

20.3.14A

20.3.14A.1

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with a notice under
section  790D ,  790DA ,  790E  or  790EA  or in purported compliance with a
duty imposed by section  790G ,  790H  or  790HA , and without reasonable
excuse, the person makes a statement that is misleading, false or deceptive in
a material particular.

20.3.14A.2

Where the person is a legal entity, the offence is also committed by every
officer of the entity who is in default.

20.3.14A.3

A person guilty of an offence under this paragraph is liable on summary
conviction—

20.3.14A.3.a

in England and Wales, to a fine;

20.3.14A.3.b

in Scotland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale;

20.3.14A.3.c

in Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale.

########### False statements: aggravated offence

20.3.14B

20.3.14B.1

A person commits an offence if, in purported compliance with a notice under
section  790D ,  790DA ,  790E  or  790EA  or in purported compliance with a
duty imposed by section  790G ,  790H  or  790HA , the person makes a
statement that the person knows is misleading, false or deceptive in a
material particular.

20.3.14B.2

Where the person is a legal entity, the offence is also committed by every
officer of the entity who is in default.

20.3.14B.3

A person guilty of an offence under this paragraph is liable—

20.3.14B.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or a fine (or both);

20.3.14B.3.b

on summary conviction—

20.3.14B.3.b.i

in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding the general
limit in a magistrates’ court or to a fine (or both);

20.3.14B.3.b.ii

in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding twelve months or to a
fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

20.3.14B.3.b.iii

in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months or to
a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

Required information

Section 110

After section  38  of the Limited Partnerships Act 1907 (inserted by section
151 of this Act) insert the following as a Schedule to that Act— SCHEDULE
Required information PART 1 Introduction 1 In this Schedule— a Part  2  sets
out the required information about a partner (or proposed partner) for the
purposes of sections 8A,  8R ,  8S  and  8T , b Part  3  sets out the required
information about a registered officer (or proposed registered officer) for
the purposes of sections 8A,  8L ,  8M  and  8R , and c Part  4  sets out the
required information about a named contact (or proposed named contact) for the
purposes of sections 8A,  8L ,  8N ,  8O  and  8R . PART 2 Partners
Individuals 2 1 Where a partner (or proposed partner) is an individual, the
required information about the partner is— a name, date of birth and
nationality; b any relevant former names; c usual residential address; d the
part of the United Kingdom in which the individual is usually resident or, if
the individual is usually resident in a country or state outside the United
Kingdom, that country or state; e in the case of a general partner, a service
address (which may be stated as “The limited partnership’s registered
office”). 2 In sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  “ relevant former name ” means any
former name other than— a in the case of a peer, or an individual normally
known by a British title, the name by which the individual was known previous
to the adoption of or succession to the title, or b in the case of any person,
a former name which— i was changed or disused before the person attained the
age of 16 years, or ii has been changed or disused for 20 years or more. 3 In
this paragraph— “ former name ” means a name by which the individual was
formerly known for business purposes; “ name ” means the individual’s forename
and surname. 4 Where a partner (or proposed partner) who is an individual is a
peer or an individual usually known by a title, any requirement imposed by
this Act to provide the individual’s name because it forms part of the
required information may be satisfied by providing that title instead of the
individual’s forename and surname. Legal entities 3 Where a partner (or
proposed partner) is a legal entity, the required information about the
partner is— a name; b principal office; c a service address (which may be
stated as “The limited partnership’s registered office”); d the legal form of
the entity and the law by which it is governed; e in the case of a general
partner, any register in which the general partner is entered (including
details of the state) and, if applicable, its registration number in that
register. PART 3 Registered officers 4 1 The required information about a
registered officer (or proposed registered officer) is— a name, date of birth
and nationality; b any relevant former names; c usual residential address; d
the part of the United Kingdom in which the individual is usually resident or,
if the individual is usually resident in a country or state outside the United
Kingdom, that country or state; e a service address (which may be stated as
“The limited partnership’s registered office”). 2 In sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  “
relevant former name ” has the meaning given by paragraph  2(2) . 3 In this
paragraph “former name” and “name” have the meanings given by paragraph  2(3)
. 4 Where a registered officer (or proposed registered officer) who is an
individual is a peer or an individual usually known by a title, any
requirement imposed by this Act to provide the individual’s name because it
forms part of the required information may be satisfied by providing that
title instead of the individual’s forename and surname. PART 4 Named contacts
5 1 The required information about a named contact (or proposed named contact)
is— a name; b usual residential address; c email address. 2 In this paragraph
“ name ” has the meaning given by paragraph  2(3) .

######## Duty to take steps to obtain information

4.12

4.12.1

Before making an application for registration under section 4(1) an overseas
entity must take reasonable steps to obtain all of the information that it is
required to deliver to the registrar under that section if it is able to
obtain it.

4.12.2

Before complying with the updating duty under section 7 an overseas entity
must take reasonable steps to obtain all of the information that it is
required to deliver to the registrar under that section if it is able to
obtain it.

4.12.3

Before making an application for removal under section 9 an overseas entity
must take reasonable steps to obtain all of the information that it is
required to include in the application if it is able to obtain it.

4.12.4

The steps that an overseas entity must take by virtue of subsection  (1) ,
(2)  or  (3)  include giving a notice to any person that it knows, or has
reasonable cause to believe, is a registrable beneficial owner in relation to
the entity, requiring the person—

4.12.4.a

to state whether or not they are such a person, and

4.12.4.b

if they are, to provide or confirm information of the kind mentioned in
subsection  (1) ,  (2)  or  (3)  so far as relating to the person, or a trust
of which they are or were a trustee.

4.12.5

The steps that an overseas entity must take by virtue of subsection  (2)  or
(3)  also include giving a notice to any person that it knows, or has
reasonable cause to believe, has ceased to be a registrable beneficial owner
in relation to the entity during the update period (within the meaning of
section 7) or relevant period (within the meaning of section 9), requiring the
person—

4.12.5.a

to state whether or not they are such a person, and

4.12.5.b

if they are, to provide or confirm information of the kind mentioned in
subsection  (2)  or  (3)  so far as relating to the person, or a trust of
which they are or were a trustee.

4.12.6

A notice under subsection  (4)  or  (5)  must require the person to whom it is
given to comply with the notice within the period of one month beginning with
the day on which it is given.

4.12.7

A person given a notice under subsection  (4)  or  (5)  is not required by
that notice to disclose any information in respect of which a claim to legal
professional privilege or, in Scotland, confidentiality of communications,
could be maintained in legal proceedings.

5

In section 13, at the end insert—

5.6

A reference in this section to a person who is a registrable beneficial owner
in relation to an overseas entity includes, in connection with the obtaining
of information required by section 7(1)(b), 9(1)(c) or 42(1)(c)(i), a
reference to a person who has ceased to be a registrable beneficial owner.

6

After section 17 insert—

######## Exceptions to duty to provide change of beneficiary information

6.17A

6.17A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for exceptions to the
requirement to deliver information by virtue of section 7(3)(c) or (4)(c) or
9(3)(c) or (4)(c).

6.17A.2

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making
regulations under subsection (1) that contain provision that would be within
the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if contained in an Act
of that Parliament.

6.17A.3

The Secretary of State must consult the Department of Finance in Northern
Ireland before making regulations under subsection (1) that contain provision
that—

6.17A.3.a

would be within the legislative competence of the Northern Ireland Assembly if
contained in an Act of that Assembly, and

6.17A.3.b

would not, if contained in a Bill for an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly,
result in the Bill requiring the consent of the Secretary of State under
section 8 of the Northern Ireland Act 1998.

6.17A.4

Regulations under subsection (1) are subject to the negative resolution
procedure.

7

In section 43 (transitional information), after subsection (1) insert—

7.1A

In subsection (1) the reference to section 12 is to that section as it had
effect before the amendments made by Schedule 6 to the Economic Crime and
Corporate Transparency Act 2023 (duty to deliver information about changes in
beneficiaries).

In section 44 (interpretation), omit subsection (2).

Overseas entities: further information for transitional cases

Section 174

1

The Economic Crime (Transparency and Enforcement) Act 2022 is amended as
follows.

2

In section 16 (verification of registrable beneficial owners and managing
officers), in subsection (1), after paragraph (c) insert—

2.d

complies with the duty under Schedule 6 (duty to deliver further information
about transitional period).

3

After section 43 insert—

######## Duty to deliver further information for transitional cases

3.43A

Schedule 6 (duty to deliver further information for transitional cases)
imposes further duties on overseas entities to deliver information.

4

After Schedule 5 insert—

Duty to deliver further information for transitional cases

########## Application of this Schedule

4.1

4.1.1

This Schedule applies in relation to an overseas entity if—

4.1.1.a

the entity—

4.1.1.a.i

is registered as an overseas entity when this Schedule comes into force or has
been so registered at any earlier time, and

4.1.1.a.ii

was registered as the proprietor of a relevant interest in land in England and
Wales or Scotland at any time during the relevant period, or

4.1.1.b

the entity has committed an offence under paragraph 5 of Schedule 3 or
paragraph 10 of Schedule 4 (duty to register as overseas entity in certain
transitional cases).

4.1.2

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) —

4.1.2.a

an overseas entity is registered as the proprietor of a relevant interest in
land in England and Wales if the entity is registered in the register of title
kept under the Land Registration Act 2002 as the proprietor of a qualifying
estate within the meaning of Schedule 4A to that Act;

4.1.2.b

an overseas entity is registered as the proprietor of a relevant interest in
land in Scotland if the entity—

4.1.2.b.i

is entered, on or after 8 December 2014, as proprietor in the proprietorship
section of the title sheet for a plot of land that is registered in the Land
Register of Scotland,

4.1.2.b.ii

in relation to a lease that was recorded in the General Register of Sasines or
registered in the Land Register of Scotland before that date is, by virtue of
an assignation of the lease registered in the Land Register of Scotland on or
after that date, the tenant under the lease, or

4.1.2.b.iii

is the tenant under a lease that was registered in the Land Register of
Scotland on or after that date.

4.1.3

Expressions used in sub-paragraph  (2)(b)  are to be construed in accordance
with section 9(11) and (12).

4.1.4

In this Schedule “ the relevant period ” means the period—

4.1.4.a

beginning with 28 February 2022;

4.1.4.b

ending with 31 January 2023.

########## Duty to deliver statements and information

4.2

4.2.1

The overseas entity must deliver to the registrar—

4.2.1.a

any statements or information required by—

paragraph  3  (changes in beneficial ownership of overseas entity), paragraph
4  (information about trusts and changes in beneficiaries under trusts), and
paragraph  5  (information about changes in trusts in which beneficial owners
trustees),

4.2.1.b

a statement that the entity has complied with paragraph  8  of this Schedule
(duty to take steps to obtain information),

4.2.1.c

anything required by regulations under section 16 (verification of
information) to be delivered to the registrar, and

4.2.1.d

the name and contact details of an individual who may be contacted about the
statements and information.

4.2.2

If an overseas entity is registered as an overseas entity when this Schedule
comes into force it must deliver the statements and information required by
this Schedule—

4.2.2.a

at the same time as it delivers the statements and information required by
section 7 on the first occasion after the end of the period of 3 months
beginning with the day on which this Schedule comes into force, or

4.2.2.b

if it applies under section 9 for removal before then, at the same time as it
delivers the statements and information required by that section.

4.2.3

If an overseas entity is not registered as an overseas entity when this
Schedule comes into force it must deliver the statements and information
required by this Schedule within the period of 3 months beginning when it
comes into force.

########## Information about changes in beneficial ownership

4.3

4.3.1

The overseas entity must deliver to the registrar the statement in row 1 of
the following table or the statement and information listed in row 2.

Statement Information 1 A statement that the entity has noreasonable cause to
believe that anyone became or ceased to be a registrable beneficial owner
during the relevant period. 2 A statement that the entity has reasonable cause
to believe that at least one person became or ceased to be a registrable
beneficial owner during the relevant period. The required information about
each person who became or ceased to be a registrable beneficial owner during
the relevant period, or so much of that information as the entity has been
able to obtain. The date on which each of them became or ceased to be a
registrable beneficial owner, if the entity has been able to obtain that
information.

4.3.2

Where the information provided under sub-paragraph  (1)  includes information
that the person who became or ceased to be a registrable beneficial owner was
a registrable beneficial owner by virtue of being a trustee (see paragraphs
3(1)(f) and 5(1)(h) of Schedule 1), the overseas entity must also deliver to
the registrar—

4.3.2.a

the required information about the trust or so much of that information as the
overseas entity has been able to obtain, and

4.3.2.b

a statement as to whether the entity has any reasonable cause to believe that
there is required information about the trust that it has not been able to
obtain.

4.3.3

Statements required by this paragraph to be delivered to the registrar must
relate to the time when they are delivered.

4.3.4

Information required by this paragraph to be delivered to the registrar as a
result of a person having become or ceased to be a registrable beneficial
owner must relate to the state of affairs when the person became or ceased be
a registrable beneficial owner.

4.3.5

For the required information, see Schedule 1.

########## Information about trusts and changes in beneficiaries

4.4

4.4.1

The overseas entity must deliver to the registrar—

4.4.1.a

a statement that the entity has no reasonable cause to believe that there is
any person who, at the end of the relevant period, was a registrable
beneficial owner of the entity by virtue of being a trustee, or

4.4.1.b

a statement that the entity has reasonable cause to believe that there is at
least one such person.

4.4.2

Where a statement is delivered under sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  the overseas
entity must also deliver to the registrar —

4.4.2.a

the required information about each trust (a “relevant trust”) by virtue of
which a trustee was a registrable beneficial owner of the entity at the end of
the relevant period,

4.4.2.b

in relation to each relevant trust, a statement as to whether the entity has
any reasonable cause to believe that there is required information about the
trust that it has not been able to obtain, and

4.4.2.c

in relation to each relevant trust, the statement in row 1 of the table set
out in sub-paragraph  (3) , or the statement and information listed in row 2
of that table.

4.4.3

This is the table referred to in sub-paragraph  (2)(c) —

Statement Information 1 A statement that the entity has no reasonable cause to
believe that anyone became or ceased to be a beneficiary under the trust
during the relevant period. 2 A statement that the entity has reasonable cause
to believe that at least one person became or ceased to be a beneficiary under
the trust during the relevant period. The information specified in paragraph
8(1)(d) of Schedule 1 about each person who became or ceased to be a
beneficiary under the trust during the relevant period, or so much of that
information as the entity has been able to obtain. The date on which each of
them became or ceased to be a beneficiary under the trust, if the entity has
been able to obtain that information.

4.4.4

Statements required by this paragraph to be delivered to the registrar must
relate to the time when they are delivered.

4.4.5

Information required by sub-paragraph  (2)(a)  to be delivered to the
registrar must relate to the state of affairs at the end of the relevant
period.

4.4.6

Information required by sub-paragraph  (2)(c)  to be delivered to the
registrar as a result of a person having become or ceased to be a beneficiary
under a trust must relate to the state of affairs when the person became or
ceased be a beneficiary.

4.4.7

For the required information, see Schedule 1.

########## Information about changes in trusts of which registrable beneficial owners trustees

4.5

4.5.1

The overseas entity must deliver to the registrar—

4.5.1.a

a statement that the entity has no reasonable cause to believe that there is
any person who—

4.5.1.a.i

at the end of the relevant period, was a registrable beneficial owner of the
entity by virtue of being a trustee of a trust,

4.5.1.a.ii

at any time during the relevant period was a registrable beneficial owner by
virtue of being a trustee of a different trust, and

4.5.1.a.iii

at the end of the relevant period was not a registrable beneficial owner of
the entity by virtue of being a trustee of the trust mentioned in sub-
paragraph  (ii) , or

4.5.1.b

a statement that the entity has reasonable cause to believe that there is at
least one such person.

4.5.2

Where a statement is delivered under sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  the overseas
entity must deliver to the registrar—

4.5.2.a

the required information about each trust by virtue of which a trustee was a
registrable beneficial owner of the entity at any time during the relevant
period, or so much of that information as the overseas entity has been able to
obtain, and

4.5.2.b

in relation to each such trust, a statement as to whether the entity has any
reasonable cause to believe that there is required information about the trust
that it has not been able to obtain.

4.5.3

Statements required by this paragraph to be delivered to the registrar must
relate to the time when they are delivered.

4.5.4

Information required by sub-paragraph  (2)(a)  to be delivered to the
registrar must relate to the state of affairs—

4.5.4.a

at the beginning of the relevant period, if the registrable beneficial owner
was a trustee of the trust at that time, and

4.5.4.b

otherwise, at the time at which the registrable beneficial owner became a
trustee of the trust.

4.5.5

For the required information, see Schedule 1.

########## Compliance by confirmation of information previously provided

4.6

A requirement imposed by paragraphs  2  to  5  to provide information may be
met (in whole or in part) by confirming information previously provided.

########## Failure to comply with this Schedule

4.7

Section 8 (offence of failure to comply with updating duty) applies in
relation to a failure to comply with a duty imposed by paragraphs  2  to  5
of this Schedule as it applies in relation to a failure to comply with section
7.

########## Obtaining information

4.8

4.8.1

An overseas entity must comply with this paragraph before complying with the
requirements imposed by paragraphs  2  to  5 .

4.8.2

The entity must take reasonable steps—

4.8.2.a

to identify anyone who became or ceased to be a registrable beneficial owner
during the relevant period, and

4.8.2.b

if it identities any such person, to obtain—

4.8.2.b.i

the information mentioned in row 2 of column 2 of the table in paragraph 3(1),
and

4.8.2.b.ii

in the case of anyone mentioned in paragraph 3(2), the information mentioned
there.

4.8.3

The entity must take reasonable steps—

4.8.3.a

to identify any person who, at the end relevant period, was a registrable
beneficial owner by virtue of being a trustee, and

4.8.3.b

if it identities any such person, to obtain —

4.8.3.b.i

the information mentioned in paragraph 4(2)(a) about the relevant trust,

4.8.3.b.ii

information as to whether anyone became or ceased to be a beneficiary under
the relevant trust during the relevant period (a “relevant beneficiary”), and

4.8.3.b.iii

the information mentioned in row 2 of column 2 of the table in paragraph 4(3)
in relation to any relevant beneficiary.

4.8.4

The entity must take reasonable steps—

4.8.4.a

to identify any person who falls within paragraph 5(1)(a)(i) to (iii), and

4.8.4.b

if it identifies any such person, to obtain the information mentioned in
paragraph 5(2)(a).

4.8.5

The steps that an overseas entity must take by virtue of this paragraph
include giving an information notice under this paragraph to any person that
it knows, or has reasonable cause to believe, falls within sub-paragraph
(2)(a), (3)(a) or (4)(a).

4.8.6

An information notice under this paragraph is a notice requiring the recipient
to provide the information mentioned in sub-paragraph (2)(b), (3)(b) or
(4)(b).

4.8.7

Sections 15 to 15B (offences) apply in relation to information notices under
this paragraph as they apply in relation to information notices under section
12.

########## Power to exclude descriptions of registrable beneficial owner

4.9

4.9.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that, for the purposes of
any provision of this Schedule specified in the regulations, a person of a
description so specified is not to be treated as a registrable beneficial
owner of an overseas entity.

4.9.2

No regulations may be made under sub-paragraph (1) after the end of the period
of two years beginning with the day on which the Economic Crime and Corporate
Transparency Act 2023 is passed.

4.9.3

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making
regulations under sub-paragraph (1) that contain provision that would be
within the legislative competence of the Scottish Parliament if contained in
an Act of that Parliament.

4.9.4

Regulations under sub-paragraph (1) are subject to the negative resolution
procedure.

Cryptoassets: confiscation orders

Section 179

##### England and Wales

###### Introductory

1

Part 2 of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 (confiscation: England and Wales) is
amended as follows.

###### Seizure of property

2

In section 47B (conditions for exercise of seizure powers)—

2.a

in subsection (2), omit paragraph (b);

2.b

in subsection (3), omit paragraph (b).

3

3.1

Section 47C (power to seize property) is amended as follows.

3.2

In subsection (2), after “not” insert  “under subsection (1)” .

3.3

After subsection (5) insert—

3.3.5A

On being satisfied as mentioned in section 47B(1) an appropriate officer may
seize any free property if the officer has reasonable grounds for suspecting
that it is a cryptoasset-related item.

3.3.5B

A “cryptoasset-related item” is an item of property that is, or that contains
or gives access to information that is, likely to assist in the seizure under
subsection (1) of any cryptoasset.

3.3.5C

The circumstances in which a cryptoasset is “ seized ” for the purposes of
subsection (1) include circumstances in which it is transferred into a crypto
wallet controlled by the appropriate officer.

3.3.5D

If an appropriate officer is lawfully on any premises, the officer may, for
the purpose of—

3.3.5D.a

determining whether any property is a cryptoasset-related item, or

3.3.5D.b

enabling or facilitating the seizure under subsection (1) of any cryptoasset,

require any information which is stored in any electronic form and accessible
from the premises to be produced in a form in which it can be taken away and
in which it is visible and legible, or from which it can readily be produced
in a visible and legible form.

3.3.5E

But subsection (5D) does not authorise an appropriate officer to require a
person to produce information which the person would be entitled to refuse to
provide on grounds of legal professional privilege in proceedings in the High
Court.

3.3.5F

Where an appropriate officer has seized a cryptoasset-related item under
subsection (5A), they may use any information obtained from it for the purpose
of—

3.3.5F.a

identifying or gaining access to a crypto wallet, and

3.3.5F.b

by doing so, enabling or facilitating the seizure under subsection (1) of any
cryptoassets.

“or (5A)” .

property are to be treated as exercised by the appropriate officer who seized

A magistrates’ court may by order extend the period for which the property may

7.3.2B.a

“ exempt property ” has the meaning given in section 47C(4) (reading

8.6

If a cryptoasset-related item which has been released is not claimed within
the period of a year beginning with the date on which it was released, the
appropriate officer may—

8.6.a

retain the item and deal with it as they see fit,

8.6.b

###### Property held by persons subject to confiscation orders: destruction, realisation etc

9

10.1

Section 51 (powers of enforcement receiver) is amended as follows.

10.2

In subsection (2), at the end insert—

10.2.e

so far as the property consists of cryptoassets, power to destroy the
property.

10.3

In subsection (8)(a), for “or (c)” substitute  “, (c) or  (e) ” .

10.4

After subsection (9) insert—

10.4.9A

The court may confer the power mentioned in subsection (2) (e)  only where—

10.4.9A.a

it is not reasonably practicable to realise the cryptoassets in question, or

10.4.9A.b

there are reasonable grounds to believe that the realisation of the
cryptoassets would be contrary to the public interest, having regard in
particular to how likely it is that the entry of the cryptoassets into general
circulation would facilitate criminal conduct by any person.

10.4.9B

An order conferring that power—

10.4.9B.a

must set out the court’s assessment of the market value of the cryptoassets to
which it relates;

10.4.9B.b

may confer power to destroy the cryptoassets only to the extent that their
market value, as set out in the order, is less than or equal to the amount
remaining to be paid under the confiscation order.

10.4.9C

If the receiver destroys any cryptoassets in the exercise of that power, the
defendant is to be treated as having paid, towards satisfaction of the
confiscation order, an amount equal to the market value, as set out in the
order, of the cryptoassets which have been destroyed.

;

;

.
