12

After section 67 insert—

########## Cryptoassets

12.67ZA

12.67ZA.1

This section applies to cryptoassets which—

12.67ZA.1.a

are held by a person, and

12.67ZA.1.b

are held in a crypto wallet administered by a UK-connected cryptoasset service
provider,

but only so far as the cryptoassets are free property.

12.67ZA.2

Subsection (3) applies if—

12.67ZA.2.a

a confiscation order is made against a person holding cryptoassets to which
this section applies, and

12.67ZA.2.b

a receiver has not been appointed under section 50 in relation to the
cryptoassets.

12.67ZA.3

A magistrates’ court may order the UK-connected cryptoasset service provider
which administers the crypto wallet in which the cryptoassets are held—

12.67ZA.3.a

to realise the cryptoassets, or a portion of the cryptoassets having a
specified value,

12.67ZA.3.b

to pay the proceeds of that realisation to the designated officer for the
court on account of, and up to a maximum of, the amount payable under the
confiscation order, and

12.67ZA.3.c

to the extent that the proceeds of the realisation exceed the amount payable
under the confiscation order, to pay the excess to an appropriate officer
identified in the order.

“ Appropriate officer ” has the same meaning as in section 41A.

12.67ZA.4

A person applying for an order under subsection (3) must give notice of the
application to the UK-connected cryptoasset service provider.

12.67ZA.5

Where the crypto wallet in which the cryptoassets are held is administered on
behalf of someone other than the person against whom the confiscation order is
made, a magistrates’ court—

12.67ZA.5.a

may make an order under subsection (3) only if the extent of the person’s
interest in the money has been determined under section 10A, and

12.67ZA.5.b

must have regard to that determination in deciding what is the appropriate
order to make.

12.67ZA.6

If a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider fails to comply with an order
under subsection (3)—

12.67ZA.6.a

the magistrates’ court may order it to pay an amount not exceeding £5,000, and

12.67ZA.6.b

for the purposes of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980 the sum is to be treated
as adjudged to be paid by a conviction of the court.

12.67ZA.7

In order to take account of changes in the value of money the Secretary of
State may by order substitute another sum for the sum for the time being
specified in subsection (6)(a).

12.67ZA.8

Where a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider—

12.67ZA.8.a

is required by an order under subsection (3) to realise a portion of
cryptoassets having a specified value, but

12.67ZA.8.b

on realising cryptoassets under the order, obtains proceeds of an amount which
differs from that value,

it does not fail to comply with the order solely because of that difference in
value, provided that it took reasonable steps to obtain proceeds equal to the
value specified.

########## Meaning of “UK-connected cryptoasset service provider”

12.67ZB

12.67ZB.1

“UK-connected cryptoasset service provider” in section 67ZA means a
cryptoasset service provider which—

12.67ZB.1.a

is acting in the course of business carried on by it in the United Kingdom,

12.67ZB.1.b

has terms and conditions with the persons to whom it provides services which
provide for a legal dispute to be litigated in the courts of a part of the
United Kingdom,

12.67ZB.1.c

holds in the United Kingdom any data relating to the persons to whom it
provides services, or

12.67ZB.1.d

meets the condition in subsection (2).

12.67ZB.2

The condition in this subsection is that—

12.67ZB.2.a

the cryptoasset service provider has its registered office or, if it does not
have one, its head office in the United Kingdom, and

12.67ZB.2.b

the day-to-day management of the provider’s business is the responsibility of
that office or another establishment maintained by it in the United Kingdom.

12.67ZB.3

“Cryptoasset service provider” in subsections (1) and (2) includes a
cryptoasset exchange provider and a custodian wallet provider; and for this
purpose—

“ cryptoasset exchange provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way
of business provides one or more of the following services, including where
the firm or sole practitioner does so as creator or issuer of any of the
cryptoassets involved— exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a
view to the exchange of, cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets;
exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, one cryptoasset for another; operating a machine which utilises automated
processes to exchange cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets; “
custodian wallet provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way of
business provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer—
cryptoassets on behalf of its customers, or private cryptographic keys on
behalf of its customers in order to hold, store and transfer cryptoassets.

12.67ZB.4

In the definition of “cryptoasset exchange provider” in subsection (3), “
cryptoasset ” includes a right to, or interest in, a cryptoasset.

12.67ZB.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions in subsection
(3) (including by amending subsection (4)).

13

After section 67A insert—

########## Destruction of seized cryptoassets

13.67AA

13.67AA.1

This section applies to cryptoassets which are held by a person and which have
been seized by an appropriate officer under a relevant seizure power.

13.67AA.2

A magistrates’ court may by order authorise an appropriate officer to destroy
the cryptoassets if—

13.67AA.2.a

a confiscation order is made against the person by whom the cryptoassets are
held,

13.67AA.2.b

a receiver has not been appointed under section 50 in relation to the
cryptoassets, and

13.67AA.2.c

either—

13.67AA.2.c.i

it is not reasonably practicable to realise the cryptoassets, or

13.67AA.2.c.ii

there are reasonable grounds to believe that the realisation of the
cryptoassets would be contrary to the public interest, having regard in
particular to how likely it is that the entry of the cryptoassets into general
circulation would facilitate criminal conduct by any person.

13.67AA.3

An order under this section—

13.67AA.3.a

must set out the court’s assessment of the market value of the cryptoassets to
which it relates;

13.67AA.3.b

may authorise the destruction of cryptoassets only to the extent that their
market value, as set out in the order, is less than or equal to the amount
remaining to be paid under the confiscation order.

13.67AA.4

Before making an order under this section, the court must give persons who
hold interests in the cryptoassets a reasonable opportunity to make
representations to it.

13.67AA.5

If cryptoassets held by a person are destroyed following an order under this
section, the person is to be treated as having paid, towards satisfaction of
the confiscation order, an amount equal to the market value, as set out in the
order, of the cryptoassets which have been destroyed.

13.67AA.6

In this section “ appropriate officer ” and “ relevant seizure power ” have
the same meaning as in section 41A.

14.1

14.2

In subsection (1), for “67A” substitute  “67ZA(3), 67A(3) or 67AA(2)” .

14.3

In subsection (2), for “67A” substitute  “67ZA(3), 67A(3) or 67AA(2)” .

67AA(2)(a) (as applicable)” .

17.2A.c

###### Interpretation and miscellaneous provision

18

After section 84 insert—

########## Cryptoassets etc

18.84A

18.84A.1

“ Cryptoasset ” means a cryptographically secured digital representation of
value or contractual rights that uses a form of distributed ledger technology
and can be transferred, stored or traded electronically.

18.84A.2

“ Crypto wallet ” means—

18.84A.2.a

software,

18.84A.2.b

hardware,

18.84A.2.c

a physical item, or

18.84A.2.d

any combination of the things mentioned in paragraphs (a) to (c),

which is used to store the cryptographic private key that allows cryptoassets
to be accessed.

18.84A.3

“ Cryptoasset-related item ” has the meaning given in section 47C(5B).

18.84A.4

The circumstances in which a cryptoasset is taken to be “destroyed” include
circumstances where it is—

18.84A.4.a

disposed of,

18.84A.4.b

transferred, or

18.84A.4.c

otherwise dealt with,

in such a way as to ensure, or to make it virtually certain, that it will not
be the subject of any further transactions or be dealt with again in any other
way.

18.84A.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions of
“cryptoasset” and “crypto wallet” in this section.

21.1

Section 127C (power to seize property) is amended as follows.

21.2

In subsection (2), after “not” insert  “under subsection (1)” .

21.3

After subsection (5) insert—

21.3.5A

On being satisfied as mentioned in section 127B(1) an appropriate officer may
seize any free property if the officer has reasonable grounds for suspecting
that it is a cryptoasset-related item.

21.3.5B

A “cryptoasset-related item” is an item of property that is, or that contains
or gives access to information that is, likely to assist in the seizure under
subsection (1) of any cryptoasset.

21.3.5C

The circumstances in which a cryptoasset is “ seized ” for the purposes of
subsection (1) include circumstances in which it is transferred into a crypto
wallet controlled by the appropriate officer.

21.3.5D

If an appropriate officer is lawfully on any premises, the officer may, for
the purpose of—

21.3.5D.a

determining whether any property is a cryptoasset-related item, or

21.3.5D.b

enabling or facilitating the seizure under subsection (1) of any cryptoasset,

require any information which is stored in any electronic form and accessible
from the premises to be produced in a form in which it can be taken away and
in which it is visible and legible, or from which it can readily be produced
in a visible and legible form.

21.3.5E

But subsection (5D) does not authorise an appropriate officer to require a
person to produce any items subject to legal privilege (as defined in section
412).

21.3.5F

Where an appropriate officer has seized a cryptoasset-related item under
subsection (5A), they may use any information obtained from it for the purpose
of—

21.3.5F.a

identifying or gaining access to a crypto wallet, and

21.3.5F.b

by doing so, enabling or facilitating the seizure under subsection (1) of any
cryptoassets.

29

After section 131ZA insert—

########## Cryptoassets

29.131ZB

29.131ZB.1

This section applies to cryptoassets which—

29.131ZB.1.a

are held by a person, and

29.131ZB.1.b

are held in a crypto wallet administered by a UK-connected cryptoasset service
provider,

but only so far as the cryptoassets are free property.

29.131ZB.2

Subsection (3) applies if—

29.131ZB.2.a

a confiscation order is made against a person holding cryptoassets to which
this section applies, and

29.131ZB.2.b

an administrator has not been appointed under section 128 in relation to the
cryptoassets.

29.131ZB.3

The sheriff may order the UK-connected cryptoasset service provider which
administers the crypto wallet in which the cryptoassets are held—

29.131ZB.3.a

to realise the cryptoassets, or a portion of the cryptoassets having a
specified value,

29.131ZB.3.b

to pay the proceeds of that realisation to the appropriate clerk of court on
account of, and up to a maximum of, the amount payable under the confiscation
order, and

29.131ZB.3.c

to the extent that the proceeds of the realisation exceed the amount payable
under the confiscation order, to pay the excess to an appropriate officer
identified in the order.

29.131ZB.4

In subsection (3)—

“ appropriate clerk of court ” means the sheriff clerk of the sheriff court
responsible for enforcing the confiscation order under section 211 of the
Procedure Act as applied by section 118(1); “ appropriate officer ” has the
same meaning as in section 120A.

29.131ZB.5

An order under subsection (3) may be made—

29.131ZB.5.a

on the application of the prosecutor, or

29.131ZB.5.b

by the sheriff of the sheriff’s own accord.

29.131ZB.6

Where a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider—

29.131ZB.6.a

is required by an order under subsection (3) to realise a portion of
cryptoassets having a specified value, but

29.131ZB.6.b

on realising cryptoassets under the order, obtains proceeds of an amount which
differs from that value,

it does not fail to comply with the order solely because of that difference in
value, provided that it took reasonable steps to obtain proceeds equal to the
value specified.

########## Meaning of “UK-connected cryptoasset service provider”

29.131ZC

29.131ZC.1

“UK-connected cryptoasset service provider” in section 131ZB means a
cryptoasset service provider which—

29.131ZC.1.a

is acting in the course of business carried on by it in the United Kingdom,

29.131ZC.1.b

has terms and conditions with the persons to whom it provides services which
provide for a legal dispute to be litigated in the courts of a part of the
United Kingdom,

29.131ZC.1.c

holds in the United Kingdom any data relating to the persons to whom it
provides services, or

29.131ZC.1.d

meets the condition in subsection (2).

29.131ZC.2

The condition in this subsection is that—

29.131ZC.2.a

the cryptoasset service provider has its registered office or, if it does not
have one, its head office in the United Kingdom, and

29.131ZC.2.b

the day-to-day management of the provider’s business is the responsibility of
that office or another establishment maintained by it in the United Kingdom.

29.131ZC.3

“Cryptoasset service provider” in subsections (1) and (2) includes a
cryptoasset exchange provider and a custodian wallet provider; and for this
purpose—

“ cryptoasset exchange provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way
of business provides one or more of the following services, including where
the firm or sole practitioner does so as creator or issuer of any of the
cryptoassets involved— exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a
view to the exchange of, cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets;
exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, one cryptoasset for another; operating a machine which utilises automated
processes to exchange cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets; “
custodian wallet provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way of
business provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer—
cryptoassets on behalf of its customers, or private cryptographic keys on
behalf of its customers in order to hold, store and transfer cryptoassets.

29.131ZC.4

In the definition of “cryptoasset exchange provider” in subsection (3), “
cryptoasset ” includes a right to, or interest in, a cryptoasset.

29.131ZC.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions in subsection
(3) (including by amending subsection (4)).

29.131ZC.6

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making
regulations under subsection (5).

30

After section 131A insert—

########## Destruction of seized cryptoassets

30.131AA

30.131AA.1

This section applies to cryptoassets which are held by a person and which have
been seized by an appropriate officer under a relevant seizure power.

30.131AA.2

The sheriff may by order authorise an appropriate officer to destroy the
cryptoassets if—

30.131AA.2.a

a confiscation order is made against the person by whom the cryptoassets are
held,

30.131AA.2.b

an administrator has not been appointed under section 128 in relation to the
cryptoassets, and

30.131AA.2.c

either—

30.131AA.2.c.i

it is not reasonably practicable to realise the cryptoassets, or

30.131AA.2.c.ii

there are reasonable grounds to believe that the realisation of the
cryptoassets would be contrary to the public interest, having regard in
particular to how likely it is that the entry of the cryptoassets into general
circulation would facilitate criminal conduct by any person.

30.131AA.3

An order under this section may be made—

30.131AA.3.a

on the application of the prosecutor, or

30.131AA.3.b

by the sheriff of the sheriff’s own accord.

30.131AA.4

An order under this section—

30.131AA.4.a

must set out the sheriff’s assessment of the market value of the cryptoassets
to which it relates;

30.131AA.4.b

may authorise the destruction of cryptoassets only to the extent that their
market value, as set out in the order, is less than or equal to the amount
remaining to be paid under the confiscation order.

30.131AA.5

Before making an order under this section, the sheriff must give persons who
hold interests in the cryptoassets a reasonable opportunity to make
representations to it.

30.131AA.6

If cryptoassets held by a person are destroyed following an order under this
section, the person is to be treated as having paid, towards satisfaction of
the confiscation order, an amount equal to the market value, as set out in the
order, of the cryptoassets which have been destroyed.

30.131AA.7

In this section “ appropriate officer ” and “ relevant seizure power ” have
the same meaning as in section 120A.

43.3.2B.b

if it has already been determined to be such an item, to seize any related
cryptoassets under section 195C(1).

43.3.2C

An order under subsection (2A) may not extend the period for which the
property may be detained beyond the period of—

43.3.2C.a

six months beginning with the date of the order, or

43.3.2C.b

in the case of exempt property, 14 days beginning with that date.

This does not prevent the period from being further extended by another order
under this section.

43.3.2D

The period of 14 days referred to in subsection  (2C)(b)  is to be calculated
in accordance with section 195H(7) (reading the reference there to 48 hours as
a reference to 14 days).

43.4

In subsection (6), after “section” insert

—

“ exempt property ” has the meaning given in section 195C(4) (reading
references there to the defendant as references to the person by whom the
property is held);

.

44

In section 195R (release of property), after subsection (5) insert—

44.6

If a cryptoasset-related item which has been released is not claimed within
the period of a year beginning with the date on which it was released, the
appropriate officer may—

44.6.a

retain the item and deal with it as they see fit,

44.6.b

dispose of the item, or

44.6.c

destroy the item.

44.7

The powers in subsection  (6)  may be exercised only—

44.7.a

where the appropriate officer has taken reasonable steps to notify—

44.7.a.i

the person from whom the item was seized, and

44.7.a.ii

any other persons who the appropriate officer has reasonable grounds to
believe have an interest in the item,

that the item has been released, and

44.7.b

with the approval of a senior officer.

44.8

“Senior officer” in subsection (7) (b)  has the meaning given in section
195G(3).

44.9

Any proceeds of a disposal of the item are to be paid into the Consolidated
Fund.

###### Property held by persons subject to confiscation orders: destruction, realisation etc

45

In section 160A (determination of extent of defendant’s interest in property),
in subsection (3)(a), after “realisation” insert  “or destruction” .

46

46.1

Section 199 (powers of enforcement receiver) is amended as follows.

46.2

In subsection (2), at the end insert—

46.2.e

so far as the property consists of cryptoassets, power to destroy the
property.

46.3

In subsection (8)(a), for “or (c)” substitute  “, (c) or  (e) ” .

46.4

After subsection (9) insert—

46.4.9A

The court may confer the power mentioned in subsection (2) (e)  only where—

46.4.9A.a

it is not reasonably practicable to realise the cryptoassets in question, or

46.4.9A.b

there are reasonable grounds to believe that the realisation of the
cryptoassets would be contrary to the public interest, having regard in
particular to how likely it is that the entry of the cryptoassets into general
circulation would facilitate criminal conduct by any person.

46.4.9B

An order conferring that power—

46.4.9B.a

must set out the court’s assessment of the market value of the cryptoassets to
which it relates;

46.4.9B.b

may confer power to destroy the cryptoassets only to the extent that their
market value, as set out in the order, is less than or equal to the amount
remaining to be paid under the confiscation order.

46.4.9C

If the receiver destroys any cryptoassets in the exercise of that power, the
defendant is to be treated as having paid, towards satisfaction of the
confiscation order, an amount equal to the market value, as set out in the
order, of the cryptoassets which have been destroyed.

financial institution” .

In subsection (5A)—

47.3.a

for “a bank or building society” substitute  “a relevant financial

47.3.b

;

For the heading substitute  “Money” .

48

After section 215 insert—

########## Cryptoassets

48.215ZA

48.215ZA.1

This section applies to cryptoassets which—

48.215ZA.1.a

are held by a person, and

48.215ZA.1.b

are held in a crypto wallet administered by a UK-connected cryptoasset service
provider,

but only so far as the cryptoassets are free property.

48.215ZA.2

Subsection (3) applies if—

48.215ZA.2.a

a confiscation order is made against a person holding cryptoassets to which
this section applies, and

48.215ZA.2.b

a receiver has not been appointed under section 198 in relation to the
cryptoassets.

48.215ZA.3

A magistrates’ court may order the UK-connected cryptoasset service provider
which administers the crypto wallet in which the cryptoassets are held—

48.215ZA.3.a

to realise the cryptoassets, or a portion of the cryptoassets having a
specified value,

48.215ZA.3.b

to pay the proceeds of that realisation to the appropriate chief clerk on
account of, and up to a maximum of, the amount payable under the confiscation
order, and

48.215ZA.3.c

to the extent that the proceeds of the realisation exceed the amount payable
under the confiscation order, to pay the excess to an appropriate officer
identified in the order.

48.215ZA.4

In subsection (3)—

“ appropriate chief clerk ” has the same meaning as in section 202(7); “
appropriate officer ” has the same meaning as in section 195A.

48.215ZA.5

A person applying for an order under subsection (3) must give notice of the
application to the UK-connected cryptoasset service provider.

48.215ZA.6

Where the crypto wallet in which the cryptoassets are held is administered on
behalf of someone other than the person against whom the confiscation order is
made, a magistrates’ court—

48.215ZA.6.a

may make an order under subsection (3) only if the extent of the person’s
interest in the money has been determined under section 160A, and

48.215ZA.6.b

must have regard to that determination in deciding what is the appropriate
order to make.

48.215ZA.7

If a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider fails to comply with an order
under subsection (3)—

48.215ZA.7.a

the magistrates’ court may order it to pay an amount not exceeding £5,000, and

48.215ZA.7.b

for the purposes of the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 (
S.I. 1981/1675 (N.I. 26) ) the sum is to be treated as adjudged to be paid by
a conviction of the court.

48.215ZA.8

In order to take account of changes in the value of money the Department of
Justice in Northern Ireland may by order substitute another sum for the sum
for the time being specified in subsection (7)(a).

48.215ZA.9

Where a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider—

48.215ZA.9.a

is required by an order under subsection (3) to realise a portion of
cryptoassets having a specified value, but

48.215ZA.9.b

on realising cryptoassets under the order, obtains proceeds of an amount which
differs from that value,

it does not fail to comply with the order solely because of that difference in
value, provided that it took reasonable steps to obtain proceeds equal to the
value specified.

########## Meaning of “UK-connected cryptoasset service provider”

48.215ZB

48.215ZB.1

“UK-connected cryptoasset service provider” in section 215ZA means a
cryptoasset service provider which—

48.215ZB.1.a

is acting in the course of business carried on by it in the United Kingdom,

48.215ZB.1.b

has terms and conditions with the persons to whom it provides services which
provide for a legal dispute to be litigated in the courts of a part of the
United Kingdom,

48.215ZB.1.c

holds in the United Kingdom any data relating to the persons to whom it
provides services, or

48.215ZB.1.d

meets the condition in subsection (2).

48.215ZB.2

The condition in this subsection is that—

48.215ZB.2.a

the cryptoasset service provider has its registered office or, if it does not
have one, its head office in the United Kingdom, and

48.215ZB.2.b

the day-to-day management of the provider’s business is the responsibility of
that office or another establishment maintained by it in the United Kingdom.

48.215ZB.3

“Cryptoasset service provider” in subsections (1) and (2) includes a
cryptoasset exchange provider and a custodian wallet provider; and for this
purpose—

“ cryptoasset exchange provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way
of business provides one or more of the following services, including where
the firm or sole practitioner does so as creator or issuer of any of the
cryptoassets involved— exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a
view to the exchange of, cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets;
exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, one cryptoasset for another; operating a machine which utilises automated
processes to exchange cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets; “
custodian wallet provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way of
business provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer—
cryptoassets on behalf of its customers, or private cryptographic keys on
behalf of its customers in order to hold, store and transfer cryptoassets.

48.215ZB.4

In the definition of “cryptoasset exchange provider” in subsection (3), “
cryptoasset ” includes a right to, or interest in, a cryptoasset.

48.215ZB.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions in subsection
(3) (including by amending subsection (4)).

48.215ZB.6

The Secretary of State must consult the Department of Justice in Northern
Ireland before making regulations under subsection (5).

49

After section 215A insert—

########## Destruction of seized cryptoassets

49.215AA

49.215AA.1

This section applies to cryptoassets which are held by a person and which have
been seized by an appropriate officer under a relevant seizure power.

49.215AA.2

A magistrates’ court may by order authorise an appropriate officer to destroy
the cryptoassets if—

49.215AA.2.a

a confiscation order is made against the person by whom the cryptoassets are
held,

49.215AA.2.b

a receiver has not been appointed under section 198 in relation to the
cryptoassets, and

49.215AA.2.c

either—

49.215AA.2.c.i

it is not reasonably practicable to realise the cryptoassets, or

49.215AA.2.c.ii

there are reasonable grounds to believe that the realisation of the
cryptoassets would be contrary to the public interest, having regard in
particular to how likely it is that the entry of the cryptoassets into general
circulation would facilitate criminal conduct by any person.

49.215AA.3

An order under this section—

49.215AA.3.a

must set out the court’s assessment of the market value of the cryptoassets to
which it relates;

49.215AA.3.b

may authorise the destruction of cryptoassets only to the extent that their
market value, as set out in the order, is less than or equal to the amount
remaining to be paid under the confiscation order.

49.215AA.4

Before making an order under this section, the court must give persons who
hold interests in the cryptoassets a reasonable opportunity to make
representations to it.

49.215AA.5

If cryptoassets held by a person are destroyed following an order under this
section, the person is to be treated as having paid, towards satisfaction of
the confiscation order, an amount equal to the market value, as set out in the
order, of the cryptoassets which have been destroyed.

49.215AA.6

In this section “ appropriate officer ” and “ relevant seizure power ” have
the same meaning as in section 190A.

215AA(2)(a) (as applicable)” .

insert—

enables the court to give a receiver the power to destroy cryptoassets),

the power conferred on a magistrates’ court by section 215AA (power to order
destruction of cryptoassets).

###### Interpretation and miscellaneous provision

54

After section 232 insert—

########## Cryptoassets etc

54.232A

54.232A.1

“ Cryptoasset ” means a cryptographically secured digital representation of
value or contractual rights that uses a form of distributed ledger technology
and can be transferred, stored or traded electronically.

54.232A.2

“ Crypto wallet ” means—

54.232A.2.a

software,

54.232A.2.b

hardware,

54.232A.2.c

a physical item, or

54.232A.2.d

any combination of the things mentioned in paragraphs (a) to (c),

which is used to store the cryptographic private key that allows cryptoassets
to be accessed.

54.232A.3

“ Cryptoasset-related item ” has the meaning given in section 195C(5B).

54.232A.4

The circumstances in which a cryptoasset is taken to be “destroyed” include
circumstances where it is—

54.232A.4.a

disposed of,

54.232A.4.b

transferred, or

54.232A.4.c

otherwise dealt with,

in such a way as to ensure, or to make it virtually certain, that it will not
be the subject of any further transactions or be dealt with again in any other
way.

54.232A.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions of
“cryptoasset” and “crypto wallet” in this section.

54.232A.6

The Secretary of State must consult the Department of Justice in Northern
Ireland before making regulations under subsection (5).

Cryptoassets: civil recovery

Section 180

##### Amendments of Part 5 of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002

1

In Part 5 of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 (civil recovery of the proceeds
etc of unlawful conduct), after section 303Z19 insert—

######### Recovery of cryptoassets: searches, seizure and detention

########## Definitions

########### Definitions

1.303Z20

1.303Z20.1

In this Part—

1.303Z20.1.a

“ cryptoasset ” means a cryptographically secured digital representation of
value or contractual rights that uses a form of distributed ledger technology
and can be transferred, stored or traded electronically;

1.303Z20.1.b

“ crypto wallet ” means—

1.303Z20.1.b.i

software,

1.303Z20.1.b.ii

hardware,

1.303Z20.1.b.iii

a physical item, or

1.303Z20.1.b.iv

any combination of the things mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to  (iii) ,

which is used to store the cryptographic private key that allows cryptoassets
to be accessed.

1.303Z20.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions of
“cryptoasset” and “crypto wallet” in this section.

1.303Z20.3

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers and the Department
of Justice before making regulations under subsection  (2) .

1.303Z20.4

In this Chapter—

1.303Z20.4.a

“ enforcement officer ” means—

1.303Z20.4.a.i

an officer of Revenue and Customs,

1.303Z20.4.a.ii

a constable,

1.303Z20.4.a.iii

an SFO officer, or

1.303Z20.4.a.iv

an accredited financial investigator who falls within a description specified
in an order made for the purposes of this Chapter by the Secretary of State or
the Welsh Ministers under section 453;

1.303Z20.4.b

“ senior officer ” means—

1.303Z20.4.b.i

an officer of Revenue and Customs of a rank designated by the Commissioners
for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs as equivalent to that of a senior police
officer of at least the rank of inspector,

1.303Z20.4.b.ii

a senior police officer of at least the rank of inspector,

1.303Z20.4.b.iii

the Director of the Serious Fraud Office,

1.303Z20.4.b.iv

the Director General of the National Crime Agency or any other National Crime
Agency officer authorised by the Director General (whether generally or
specifically) for this purpose, or

1.303Z20.4.b.v

an accredited financial investigator who falls within a description specified
in an order made for the purposes of this Chapter by the Secretary of State or
the Welsh Ministers under section 453.

########## Searches

########### Searches

1.303Z21

1.303Z21.1

If an enforcement officer—

1.303Z21.1.a

is lawfully on any premises, and

1.303Z21.1.b

has reasonable grounds for suspecting that there is on the premises a
cryptoasset-related item,

the enforcement officer may search for the cryptoasset-related item there.

1.303Z21.2

For the purposes of this Chapter, a “cryptoasset-related item” is an item of
property that is, or that contains or gives access to information that is,
likely to assist in the seizure under this Part of cryptoassets that—

1.303Z21.2.a

are recoverable property, or

1.303Z21.2.b

are intended by any person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z21.3

The powers conferred by subsection  (6)  are exercisable by an enforcement
officer if—

1.303Z21.3.a

the enforcement officer has reasonable grounds for suspecting that there is a
cryptoasset-related item in a vehicle,

1.303Z21.3.b

it appears to the officer that the vehicle is under the control of a person
(the suspect) who is in or in the vicinity of the vehicle, and

1.303Z21.3.c

the vehicle is in a place falling within subsection  (4) .

1.303Z21.4

The places referred to in subsection  (3)(c)  are—

1.303Z21.4.a

a place to which, at the time of the proposed exercise of the powers, the
public or any section of the public has access, on payment or otherwise, as of
right or by virtue of express or implied permission, and

1.303Z21.4.b

any other place to which at that time people have ready access but which is
not a dwelling.

1.303Z21.5

But if the vehicle is in a garden or yard or other land occupied with and used
for the purposes of a dwelling, the enforcement officer may exercise the
powers conferred by subsection  (6)  only if the enforcement officer has
reasonable grounds for believing—

1.303Z21.5.a

that the suspect does not reside in the dwelling, and

1.303Z21.5.b

that the vehicle is not in the place in question with the express or implied
permission of a person who resides in the dwelling.

1.303Z21.6

The powers conferred by this subsection are—

1.303Z21.6.a

power to require the suspect to permit entry to the vehicle;

1.303Z21.6.b

power to require the suspect to permit a search of the vehicle.

1.303Z21.7

If an enforcement officer has reasonable grounds for suspecting that a person
(the suspect) is carrying a cryptoasset-related item, the enforcement officer
may require the suspect—

1.303Z21.7.a

to permit a search of any article the suspect has with them;

1.303Z21.7.b

to permit a search of the suspect’s person.

1.303Z21.8

The powers conferred by subsections  (6)  and  (7)  are exercisable only so
far as the enforcement officer thinks it necessary or expedient.

1.303Z21.9

An enforcement officer may—

1.303Z21.9.a

in exercising powers conferred by subsection  (6) , detain the vehicle for so
long as is necessary for their exercise;

1.303Z21.9.b

in exercising powers conferred by subsection  (7)(b) , detain the suspect for
so long as is necessary for their exercise.

1.303Z21.10

The powers conferred by this section are exercisable by an SFO officer or an
accredited financial investigator only in relation to the following—

1.303Z21.10.a

premises in England, Wales or Northern Ireland (in the case of subsection  (1)
);

1.303Z21.10.b

vehicles and suspects in England, Wales or Northern Ireland (in the case of
subsection  (6) );

1.303Z21.10.c

suspects in England, Wales or Northern Ireland (in the case of subsection  (7)
).

########### Searches: supplemental provision

1.303Z22

1.303Z22.1

The powers conferred by section  303Z21  are exercisable only so far as
reasonably required for the purpose of finding a cryptoasset-related item.

1.303Z22.2

Section  303Z21  does not require a person to submit to an intimate search or
strip search (within the meaning of section 164 of the Customs and Excise
Management Act 1979).

########### Prior approval

1.303Z23

1.303Z23.1

The powers conferred by section  303Z21  may be exercised only with the
appropriate approval unless, in the circumstances, it is not practicable to
obtain that approval before exercising the power.

1.303Z23.2

The appropriate approval means the approval of a judicial officer or (if that
is not practicable in any case) the approval of a senior officer.

1.303Z23.3

A judicial officer means—

1.303Z23.3.a

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, a justice of the peace;

1.303Z23.3.b

in relation to Scotland, the sheriff.

1.303Z23.4

If the powers are exercised without the approval of a judicial officer in a
case where—

1.303Z23.4.a

no property is seized by virtue of section  303Z26 , or

1.303Z23.4.b

any property so seized is not detained for more than 48 hours (calculated in
accordance with section  303Z27 ),

the relevant officer who exercised the power must give a written report to the
appointed person.

1.303Z23.5

But the duty in subsection  (4)  does not apply if, during the course of
exercising the powers conferred by section  303Z21 , the enforcement officer
seizes cash by virtue of section 294 or property by virtue of section 303J and
the cash or property so seized is detained for more than 48 hours (calculated
in accordance with section 295(1B) or 303K(5)).

1.303Z23.6

A report under subsection  (4)  must give particulars of the circumstances
which led the relevant officer to believe that—

1.303Z23.6.a

the powers were exercisable, and

1.303Z23.6.b

it was not practicable to obtain the approval of a judicial officer.

1.303Z23.7

In this section and in section  303Z24  the appointed person means—

1.303Z23.7.a

in relation to England and Wales, a person appointed by the Secretary of
State;

1.303Z23.7.b

in relation to Scotland, a person appointed by the Scottish Ministers;

1.303Z23.7.c

in relation to Northern Ireland, a person appointed by the Department of
Justice.

1.303Z23.8

The appointed person must not be a person employed under or for the purposes
of a government department or of the Scottish Administration; and the terms
and conditions of the person’s appointment, including any remuneration or
expenses to be paid to the person, are to be determined by the person making
the appointment.

########### Report on exercise of powers

1.303Z24

1.303Z24.1

As soon as possible after the end of each financial year, the appointed person
must prepare a report for that year.

1.303Z24.2

“ Financial year ” means—

1.303Z24.2.a

the period beginning with the day on which this section came into force and
ending with the next 31 March (which is the first financial year), and

1.303Z24.2.b

each subsequent period of 12 months beginning with 1 April.

1.303Z24.3

The report must give the appointed person’s opinion as to the circumstances
and manner in which the powers conferred by section  303Z21  are being
exercised in cases where the enforcement officer who exercised them is
required to give a report under section  303Z23 (4) .

1.303Z24.4

In the report, the appointed person may make any recommendations they consider
appropriate.

1.303Z24.5

The appointed person must send a copy of the report to whichever of the
Secretary of State, the Scottish Ministers or the Department of Justice
appointed the person.

1.303Z24.6

The Secretary of State must lay a copy of any report the Secretary of State
receives under this section before Parliament and arrange for it to be
published.

1.303Z24.7

The Scottish Ministers must lay a copy of any report they receive under this
section before the Scottish Parliament and arrange for it to be published.

1.303Z24.8

The Department of Justice must lay a copy of any report it receives under this
section before the Northern Ireland Assembly and arrange for it to be
published.

1.303Z24.9

Section 41(3) of the Interpretation Act (Northern Ireland) 1954 applies for
the purposes of subsection  (8)  in relation to the laying of a copy of a
report as it applies in relation to the laying of a statutory document under
an enactment.

########### Codes of practice

1.303Z25

1.303Z25.1

The requirements to make codes of practice set out in sections 303G, 303H and
303I apply in relation to the powers conferred by section  303Z21  as they
apply in relation to the powers conferred by section 303C.

1.303Z25.2

A requirement in section 303G(2), 303H(2) or 303I(2), as applied by subsection
(1), to carry out a relevant action may be satisfied by the carrying out of
that action before this section comes into force.

1.303Z25.3

In subsection  (2)  “ relevant action ” means any of the following—

1.303Z25.3.a

publishing a draft code of practice;

1.303Z25.3.b

considering any representations made about the draft;

1.303Z25.3.c

modifying the draft in light of any such representations.

1.303Z25.4

The requirement in section 303G(3), as applied by subsection (1), to consult
the Attorney General may be satisfied by consultation carried out before this
section comes into force.

########## Seizure and detention of cryptoasset-related items

########### Seizure of cryptoasset-related items

1.303Z26

1.303Z26.1

An enforcement officer may seize any item of property if the enforcement
officer has reasonable grounds for suspecting that the item is a cryptoasset-
related item.

1.303Z26.2

If an enforcement officer is lawfully on any premises, the officer may, for
the purpose of—

1.303Z26.2.a

determining whether any property is a cryptoasset-related item, or

1.303Z26.2.b

enabling or facilitating the seizure under this Chapter of any cryptoasset,

require any information which is stored in any electronic form and accessible
from the premises to be produced in a form in which it can be taken away and
in which it is visible and legible, or from which it can readily be produced
in a visible and legible form.

1.303Z26.3

But subsection  (2)  does not authorise an enforcement officer to require a
person to produce privileged information.

1.303Z26.4

In this section “ privileged information ” means information which a person
would be entitled to refuse to provide—

1.303Z26.4.a

in England and Wales and Northern Ireland, on grounds of legal professional
privilege in proceedings in the High Court;

1.303Z26.4.b

in Scotland, on grounds of legal privilege as defined by section 412.

1.303Z26.5

Where an enforcement officer has seized a cryptoasset-related item under
subsection  (1) , the officer may use any information obtained from the item
for the purpose of—

1.303Z26.5.a

identifying or gaining access to a crypto wallet, and

1.303Z26.5.b

by doing so, enabling or facilitating the seizure under this Chapter of any
cryptoassets.

1.303Z26.6

This section does not authorise the seizure by an SFO officer or an accredited
financial investigator of an item found in Scotland.

########### Initial detention of seized cryptoasset-related items

1.303Z27

1.303Z27.1

Property seized under section  303Z26  may be detained for an initial period
of 48 hours.

1.303Z27.2

Subsection  (1)  authorises the detention of property only for so long as an
enforcement officer continues to have reasonable grounds for suspicion in
relation to that property as described in section  303Z26 (1) .

1.303Z27.3

In calculating a period of 48 hours for the purposes of this section, no
account is to be taken of—

1.303Z27.3.a

any Saturday or Sunday,

1.303Z27.3.b

Christmas Day,

1.303Z27.3.c

Good Friday,

1.303Z27.3.d

any day that is a bank holiday under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act
1971 in the part of the United Kingdom within which the property is seized, or

1.303Z27.3.e

any day prescribed by virtue of section 8(2) of the Criminal Procedure
(Scotland) Act 1995 as a court holiday in a sheriff court in the sheriff court
district within which the property is seized.

########### Further detention of seized cryptoasset-related items

1.303Z28

1.303Z28.1

The period for which property seized under section  303Z26  may be detained
may be extended by an order made—

1.303Z28.1.a

in England and Wales or Northern Ireland, by a magistrates’ court;

1.303Z28.1.b

in Scotland, by the sheriff.

1.303Z28.2

An order under subsection  (1)  may not authorise the detention of any
property—

1.303Z28.2.a

beyond the end of the period of 6 months beginning with the date of the order,
and

1.303Z28.2.b

in the case of any further order under this section, beyond the end of the
period of 2 years beginning with the date of the first order; but this is
subject to subsection  (4) .

1.303Z28.3

A justice of the peace may also exercise the power of a magistrates’ court to
make the first order under subsection  (1) .

1.303Z28.4

The court or sheriff may make an order for the period of 2 years in subsection
(2)(b)  to be extended to a period of up to 3 years beginning with the date of
the first order.

1.303Z28.5

An application for an order under subsection  (1)  or  (4)  may be made—

1.303Z28.5.a

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, by—

1.303Z28.5.a.i

the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs,

1.303Z28.5.a.ii

a constable,

1.303Z28.5.a.iii

an SFO officer, or

1.303Z28.5.a.iv

an accredited financial investigator who falls within a description specified
in an order made for the purposes of this Chapter by the Secretary of State or
the Welsh Ministers under section 453;

1.303Z28.5.b

in relation to Scotland, by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their
functions under section  303Z41  or by a procurator fiscal.

1.303Z28.6

The court, sheriff or justice may make an order under subsection  (1)  if
satisfied, in relation to the item of property to be further detained, that—

1.303Z28.6.a

there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that it is a cryptoasset-related
item, and

1.303Z28.6.b

its continued detention is justified.

1.303Z28.7

The court or sheriff may make an order under subsection  (4)  if satisfied
that a request for assistance is outstanding in relation to the item of
property to be further detained.

1.303Z28.8

A “request for assistance” in subsection  (7)  means a request for assistance
in obtaining evidence (including information in any form or article) in
connection with the property to be further detained, made—

1.303Z28.8.a

by a judicial authority in the United Kingdom under section 7 of the Crime
(International Co-operation) Act 2003,

1.303Z28.8.b

by an enforcement officer, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in
a foreign country,

1.303Z28.8.c

by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their functions under this Part,
to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a foreign country, or

1.303Z28.8.d

by a person under section 375A or 408A (evidence overseas).

1.303Z28.9

An order under subsection  (1)  must provide for notice to be given to persons
affected by the order.

########### Seizure of cryptoassets

1.303Z29

1.303Z29.1

An enforcement officer may seize cryptoassets if the enforcement officer has
reasonable grounds for suspecting that the cryptoassets are recoverable
property or intended by any person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z29.2

The circumstances in which a cryptoasset is “ seized ” for the purposes of
subsection  (1)  include circumstances in which it is transferred into a
crypto wallet controlled by the enforcement officer.

1.303Z29.3

This section does not authorise the seizure by an SFO officer or an accredited
financial investigator of cryptoassets as a result of information obtained
from a cryptoasset-related item found in Scotland.

########### Prior authorisation for detention of cryptoassets

1.303Z30

1.303Z30.1

Where an order is made under section  303Z28  in respect of a cryptoasset-
related item, the court, sheriff or justice making the order may, at the same
time, make an order to authorise the detention of any cryptoassets that may be
seized as a result of information obtained from that item.

1.303Z30.2

An application for an order under this section may be made, by a person
mentioned in section  303Z28 (5) , at the same time as an application for an
order under section  303Z28  is made by that person.

1.303Z30.3

The court, sheriff or justice may make an order under this section if
satisfied that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that the
cryptoassets that may be seized are recoverable property or intended by any
person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z30.4

An order under this section authorises detention of the cryptoassets for the
same period of time as the order under section  303Z28  authorises detention
in respect of the cryptoasset-related item to which those cryptoassets relate.

########### Initial detention of seized cryptoassets

1.303Z31

1.303Z31.1

Cryptoassets seized under section  303Z29  may be detained for an initial
period of 48 hours.

1.303Z31.2

Subsection  (1)  authorises the detention of property only for so long as an
enforcement officer continues to have reasonable grounds for suspicion in
relation to those cryptoassets as described in section  303Z29 (1) .

1.303Z31.3

In calculating a period of 48 hours for the purposes of this section, no
account is to be taken of—

1.303Z31.3.a

any Saturday or Sunday,

1.303Z31.3.b

Christmas Day,

1.303Z31.3.c

Good Friday,

1.303Z31.3.d

any day that is a bank holiday under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act
1971 in the part of the United Kingdom within which the property is seized, or

1.303Z31.3.e

any day prescribed by virtue of section 8(2) of the Criminal Procedure
(Scotland) Act 1995 as a court holiday in a sheriff court in the sheriff court
district within which the property is seized.

1.303Z31.4

This section is subject to section  303Z30 .

########### Further detention of seized cryptoassets

1.303Z32

1.303Z32.1

The period for which cryptoassets seized under section  303Z29  may be
detained may be extended by an order made—

1.303Z32.1.a

in England and Wales or Northern Ireland, by a magistrates’ court;

1.303Z32.1.b

in Scotland, by the sheriff.

1.303Z32.2

An order under subsection  (1)  may not authorise the detention of any
cryptoassets—

1.303Z32.2.a

beyond the end of the period of 6 months beginning with the date of the order,
and

1.303Z32.2.b

in the case of any further order under this section, beyond the end of the
period of 2 years beginning with the date of the first order; but this is
subject to subsection  (4) .

1.303Z32.3

A justice of the peace may also exercise the power of a magistrates’ court to
make the first order under subsection  (1) .

1.303Z32.4

The court or sheriff may make an order for the period of 2 years in subsection
(2)(b)  to be extended to a period of up to 3 years beginning with the date of
the first order.

1.303Z32.5

An application for an order under subsection  (1)  or  (4)  may be made—

1.303Z32.5.a

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, by—

1.303Z32.5.a.i

the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs,

1.303Z32.5.a.ii

a constable,

1.303Z32.5.a.iii

an SFO officer, or

1.303Z32.5.a.iv

an accredited financial investigator who falls within a description specified
in an order made for the purposes of this Chapter by the Secretary of State or
the Welsh Ministers under section 453,

1.303Z32.5.b

in relation to Scotland, by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their
functions under section  303Z41  or by a procurator fiscal.

1.303Z32.6

The court, sheriff or justice may make an order under subsection  (1)  if
satisfied, in relation to the cryptoassets to be further detained, that there
are reasonable grounds for suspecting that the cryptoassets are recoverable
property or intended by any person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z32.7

The court or sheriff may make an order under subsection  (4)  if satisfied
that a request for assistance is outstanding in relation to the cryptoassets
to be further detained.

1.303Z32.8

A “request for assistance” in subsection  (7)  means a request for assistance
in obtaining evidence (including information in any form or article) in
connection with the cryptoassets to be further detained, made—

1.303Z32.8.a

by a judicial authority in the United Kingdom under section 7 of the Crime
(International Co-operation) Act 2003,

1.303Z32.8.b

by an enforcement officer, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in
a foreign country,

1.303Z32.8.c

by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their functions under this Part,
to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a foreign country, or

1.303Z32.8.d

by a person under section 375A or 408A (evidence overseas).

1.303Z32.9

An order under subsection  (1)  must provide for notice to be given to persons
affected by the order.

########### Safekeeping of cryptoassets and cryptoasset-related items

1.303Z33

1.303Z33.1

An enforcement officer must arrange for any item of property seized under
section  303Z26  to be safely stored throughout the period during which it is
detained under this Chapter.

1.303Z33.2

An enforcement officer must arrange for any cryptoassets seized under section
303Z29  to be safely stored throughout the period during which they are
detained under this Chapter.

########### Release of cryptoassets and cryptoasset-related items

1.303Z34

1.303Z34.1

This section applies while any cryptoasset or other item of property is
detained under this Chapter.

1.303Z34.2

A magistrates’ court or (in Scotland) the sheriff may direct the release of
the whole or any part of the property if the following condition is met.

1.303Z34.3

The condition is that the court or sheriff is satisfied, on an application by
the person from whom the property was seized, that the conditions for the
detention of the property in this Chapter are no longer met in relation to the
property to be released.

1.303Z34.4

A person within subsection  (5)  may, after notifying the magistrates’ court,
sheriff or justice under whose order property is being detained, release the
whole or any part of the property if satisfied that the detention of the
property to be released is no longer justified.

1.303Z34.5

The following persons are within this subsection—

1.303Z34.5.a

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, an enforcement officer;

1.303Z34.5.b

in relation to Scotland—

1.303Z34.5.b.i

the Scottish Ministers,

1.303Z34.5.b.ii

an officer of Revenue and Customs,

1.303Z34.5.b.iii

a constable, and

1.303Z34.5.b.iv

a procurator fiscal.

1.303Z34.6

If any cryptoasset-related item which has been released is not claimed within
the period of a year beginning with the date on which it was released, an
enforcement officer may—

1.303Z34.6.a

retain the item and deal with it as they see fit,

1.303Z34.6.b

dispose of the item, or

1.303Z34.6.c

destroy the item.

1.303Z34.7

The powers in subsection  (6)  may be exercised only—

1.303Z34.7.a

where the enforcement officer has taken reasonable steps to notify—

1.303Z34.7.a.i

the person from whom the item was seized, and

1.303Z34.7.a.ii

any other persons who the enforcement officer has reasonable grounds to
believe have an interest in the item,

that the item has been released, and

1.303Z34.7.b

with the approval of a senior officer.

1.303Z34.8

Any proceeds of a disposal of the item are to be paid—

1.303Z34.8.a

into the Consolidated Fund if—

1.303Z34.8.a.i

the item was directed to be released by a magistrates’ court, or

1.303Z34.8.a.ii

a magistrates’ court or justice was notified under subsection  (4)  of the
release;

1.303Z34.8.b

into the Scottish Consolidated Fund if—

1.303Z34.8.b.i

the item was directed to be released by the sheriff, or

1.303Z34.8.b.ii

the sheriff was notified under subsection  (4)  of the release.

######### Recovery of cryptoassets: freezing orders

########## Definitions

########### Definitions

1.303Z35

1.303Z35.1

In this Chapter—

1.303Z35.1.a

“ cryptoasset exchange provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way
of business provides one or more of the following services, including where
the firm or sole practitioner does so as creator or issuer of any of the
cryptoassets involved—

1.303Z35.1.a.i

exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets,

1.303Z35.1.a.ii

exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, one cryptoasset for another, or

1.303Z35.1.a.iii

operating a machine which utilises automated processes to exchange
cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets;

1.303Z35.1.b

“ custodian wallet provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way of
business provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer—

1.303Z35.1.b.i

cryptoassets on behalf of its customers, or

1.303Z35.1.b.ii

private cryptographic keys on behalf of its customers in order to hold, store
and transfer cryptoassets;

1.303Z35.1.c

“ cryptoasset service provider ” includes cryptoasset exchange provider and
custodian wallet provider.

1.303Z35.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(a) , “ money ” means—

1.303Z35.2.a

money in sterling,

1.303Z35.2.b

money in any other currency, or

1.303Z35.2.c

money in any other medium of exchange,

but does not include a cryptoasset.

1.303Z35.3

In the definition of “cryptoasset exchange provider” in subsection  (1) , “
cryptoasset ” includes a right to, or interest in, a cryptoasset.

1.303Z35.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions in this
section.

1.303Z35.5

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers and the Department
of Justice before making regulations under subsection  (4) .

########## Freezing of crypto wallets

########### Application for crypto wallet freezing order

1.303Z36

1.303Z36.1

This section applies if an enforcement officer has reasonable grounds for
suspecting that cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet administered by a UK-
connected cryptoasset service provider—

1.303Z36.1.a

are recoverable property, or

1.303Z36.1.b

are intended by any person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z36.2

Where this section applies (but subject to subsection  (3) ) the enforcement
officer may apply to the relevant court for a crypto wallet freezing order in
relation to the crypto wallet in which the cryptoassets are held.

1.303Z36.3

An enforcement officer may not apply for a crypto wallet freezing order unless
the officer is a senior officer or is authorised to do so by a senior officer.

1.303Z36.4

For the purposes of this Chapter—

1.303Z36.4.a

a crypto wallet freezing order is an order that, subject to any exclusions
(see section  303Z39 ), prohibits each person by or for whom the crypto wallet
to which the order applies is administered from—

1.303Z36.4.a.i

making withdrawals or payments from the crypto wallet, or

1.303Z36.4.a.ii

using the crypto wallet in any other way;

1.303Z36.4.b

a crypto wallet is administered by or for a person if the person is the person
to whom services are being provided by a cryptoasset service provider in
relation to that crypto wallet.

1.303Z36.5

An application for a crypto wallet freezing order may be made without notice
if the circumstances of the case are such that notice of the application would
prejudice the taking of any steps under this Part to forfeit cryptoassets that
are recoverable property or intended by any person for use in unlawful
conduct.

1.303Z36.6

An application for a crypto wallet freezing order under this section may be
combined with an application for an account freezing order under section 303Z1
where a single entity—

1.303Z36.6.a

is both a relevant financial institution for the purposes of section 303Z1 and
a cryptoasset service provider for the purposes of this section, and

1.303Z36.6.b

operates or administers, for the same person, both an account holding money
(above the minimum amount specified in section 303Z8) and a crypto wallet.

1.303Z36.7

An application for a crypto wallet freezing order may not be made by an SFO
officer, or an accredited financial investigator, in relation to a UK-
connected cryptoasset service provider where—

1.303Z36.7.a

the provider has its registered office, or if it does not have one, its head
office in Scotland, and

1.303Z36.7.b

the day-to-day management of the provider’s business is the responsibility of
that office or another establishment maintained by it in Scotland.

1.303Z36.8

In this Chapter—

“ enforcement officer ” has the meaning given by section  303Z20 ; “ relevant
court ” means— in England and Wales and Northern Ireland, a magistrates’
court, and in Scotland, the sheriff; “ senior officer ” has the meaning given
by section  303Z20 ; “ UK-connected cryptoasset service provider ” means a
cryptoasset service provider which— is acting in the course of business
carried on by it in the United Kingdom, has terms and conditions with the
persons to whom it provides services which provide for a legal dispute to be
litigated in the courts of a part of the United Kingdom, holds, in the United
Kingdom, any data relating to the persons to whom it provides services, or
meets the condition in subsection  (9) .

1.303Z36.9

The condition in this subsection is that—

1.303Z36.9.a

the cryptoasset service provider has its registered office, or if it does not
have one, its head office in the United Kingdom, and

1.303Z36.9.b

the day-to-day management of the provider’s business is the responsibility of
that office or another establishment maintained by it in the United Kingdom.

########### Making of a crypto wallet freezing order

1.303Z37

1.303Z37.1

This section applies where an application for a crypto wallet freezing order
is made under section  303Z36  in relation to a crypto wallet.

1.303Z37.2

The relevant court may make the order if satisfied that there are reasonable
grounds for suspecting that some or all of the cryptoassets held in the crypto
wallet—

1.303Z37.2.a

are recoverable property, or

1.303Z37.2.b

are intended by any person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z37.3

A crypto wallet freezing order ceases to have effect at the end of the period
specified in the order (which may be varied under section  303Z38 ) unless it
ceases to have effect at an earlier or later time in accordance with this
Chapter or Chapter 3E or 3F.

1.303Z37.4

The period specified by the relevant court for the purposes of subsection  (3)
(whether when the order is first made or on a variation under section  303Z38
) may not exceed the period of 2 years, beginning with the day on which the
crypto wallet freezing order is (or was) made; but this is subject to
subsection  (5) .

1.303Z37.5

The relevant court may make an order for the period of 2 years in subsection
(4)  to be extended to a period of up to 3 years beginning with the day on
which the crypto wallet freezing order is (or was) made.

1.303Z37.6

The relevant court may make an order under subsection  (5)  if satisfied that
a request for assistance is outstanding in relation to some or all of the
cryptoassets held in the crypto wallet.

1.303Z37.7

A “request for assistance” in subsection  (6)  means a request for assistance
in obtaining evidence (including information in any form or article) in
connection with some or all of the cryptoassets held in the crypto wallet,
made—

1.303Z37.7.a

by a judicial authority in the United Kingdom under section 7 of the Crime
(International Co-operation) Act 2003,

1.303Z37.7.b

by an enforcement officer, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in
a foreign country,

1.303Z37.7.c

by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their functions under this Part,
to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a foreign country, or

1.303Z37.7.d

by a person under section 375A or 408A (evidence overseas).

1.303Z37.8

A crypto wallet freezing order must provide for notice to be given to persons
affected by the order.

########### Variation and setting aside of crypto wallet freezing order

1.303Z38

1.303Z38.1

The relevant court may at any time vary or set aside a crypto wallet freezing
order on an application made by—

1.303Z38.1.a

an enforcement officer, or

1.303Z38.1.b

any person affected by the order.

1.303Z38.2

But an enforcement officer may not make an application under subsection  (1)
unless the officer is a senior officer or is authorised to do so by a senior
officer.

1.303Z38.3

Before varying or setting aside a crypto wallet freezing order the court must
(as well as giving the parties to the proceedings an opportunity to be heard)
give such an opportunity to any person who may be affected by its decision.

1.303Z38.4

In relation to Scotland, the references in this section to setting aside an
order are to be read as references to recalling it.

########### Exclusions

1.303Z39

1.303Z39.1

The power to vary a crypto wallet freezing order includes (amongst other
things) power to make exclusions from the prohibition on making withdrawals or
payments from the crypto wallet to which the order applies.

1.303Z39.2

Exclusions from the prohibition may also be made when the order is made.

1.303Z39.3

An exclusion may (amongst other things) make provision for the purpose of
enabling a person by or for whom the crypto wallet is administered—

1.303Z39.3.a

to meet the person’s reasonable living expenses, or

1.303Z39.3.b

to carry on any trade, business, profession or occupation.

1.303Z39.4

An exclusion may be made subject to conditions.

1.303Z39.5

Where a magistrates’ court exercises the power to make an exclusion for the
purpose of enabling a person to meet legal expenses that the person has
incurred, or may incur, in respect of proceedings under this Part, it must
ensure that the exclusion—

1.303Z39.5.a

is limited to reasonable legal expenses that the person has reasonably
incurred or that the person reasonably incurs,

1.303Z39.5.b

specifies the total amount that may be released for legal expenses in
pursuance of the exclusion, and

1.303Z39.5.c

is made subject to the same conditions as would be the required conditions
(see section 286A) if the order had been made under section 245A (in addition
to any conditions imposed under subsection  (4) ).

1.303Z39.6

A magistrates’ court, in deciding whether to make an exclusion for the purpose
of enabling a person to meet legal expenses in respect of proceedings under
this Part—

1.303Z39.6.a

must have regard to the desirability of the person being represented in any
proceedings under this Part in which the person is a participant, and

1.303Z39.6.b

must disregard the possibility that legal representation of the person in any
such proceedings might, were an exclusion not made—

1.303Z39.6.b.i

be made available under arrangements made for the purposes of Part 1 of the
Legal Aid, Sentencing and Punishment of Offenders Act 2012, or

1.303Z39.6.b.ii

be funded by the Department of Justice.

1.303Z39.7

The sheriff’s power to make exclusions may not be exercised for the purpose of
enabling any person to meet any legal expenses in respect of proceedings under
this Part.

1.303Z39.8

The power to make exclusions must, subject to subsection  (6) , be exercised
with a view to ensuring, so far as practicable, that there is not undue
prejudice to the taking of any steps under this Part to forfeit cryptoassets
that are recoverable property or intended by any person for use in unlawful
conduct.

########### Restrictions on proceedings and remedies

1.303Z40

1.303Z40.1

If a court in which proceedings are pending in respect of a crypto wallet
administered by a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider is satisfied that
a crypto wallet freezing order has been applied for or made in respect of the
crypto wallet, it may either stay the proceedings or allow them to continue on
any terms it thinks fit.

1.303Z40.2

Before exercising the power conferred by subsection  (1) , the court must (as
well as giving the parties to any of the proceedings concerned an opportunity
to be heard) give such an opportunity to any person who may be affected by the
court’s decision.

1.303Z40.3

In relation to Scotland, the reference in subsection  (1)  to staying the
proceedings is to be read as a reference to sisting the proceedings.

######### Forfeiture of cryptoassets following detention or freezing order

########## Forfeiture orders

########### Forfeiture order

1.303Z41

1.303Z41.1

This section applies—

1.303Z41.1.a

while any cryptoassets are detained under Chapter 3C, or

1.303Z41.1.b

while a crypto wallet freezing order made under section  303Z37  has effect.

1.303Z41.2

An application for the forfeiture of some or all of the cryptoassets that are
detained or held in the crypto wallet that is subject to the crypto wallet
freezing order may be made—

1.303Z41.2.a

to a magistrates’ court by a person within subsection  (3) , or

1.303Z41.2.b

to the sheriff by the Scottish Ministers.

1.303Z41.3

The following persons are within this subsection—

1.303Z41.3.a

the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs,

1.303Z41.3.b

a constable,

1.303Z41.3.c

an SFO officer, and

1.303Z41.3.d

an accredited financial investigator who falls within a description specified
in an order made for the purposes of this Chapter by the Secretary of State or
the Welsh Ministers under section 453.

1.303Z41.4

The court or sheriff may order the forfeiture of some or all of the
cryptoassets if satisfied that the cryptoassets—

1.303Z41.4.a

are recoverable property, or

1.303Z41.4.b

are intended by any person for use in unlawful conduct.

1.303Z41.5

An order under subsection  (4)  made by a magistrates’ court may provide for
payment under section  303Z49  of reasonable legal expenses that a person has
reasonably incurred, or may reasonably incur, in respect of—

1.303Z41.5.a

the proceedings in which the order is made, or

1.303Z41.5.b

any related proceedings under this Chapter.

1.303Z41.6

A sum in respect of a relevant item of expenditure is not payable under
section  303Z49  in pursuance of provision under subsection  (5)  unless—

1.303Z41.6.a

the person who applied for the order under subsection  (4)  agrees to its
payment, or

1.303Z41.6.b

the court has assessed the amount allowed in respect of that item and the sum
is paid in respect of the assessed amount.

1.303Z41.7

For the purposes of subsection  (6) —

1.303Z41.7.a

a “relevant item of expenditure” is an item of expenditure to which
regulations under section 286B would apply if the order under subsection  (4)
had instead been a recovery order;

1.303Z41.7.b

an amount is “allowed” in respect of a relevant item of expenditure if it
would have been allowed by those regulations;

1.303Z41.7.c

if the person who applied for the order under subsection  (4)  was a
constable, an SFO officer or an accredited financial investigator, that person
may not agree to the payment of a sum unless the person is a senior officer or
is authorised to do so by a senior officer.

1.303Z41.8

Subsection  (4)  ceases to apply on the transfer of an application made under
this section in accordance with section  303Z45 (1) .

1.303Z41.9

In this Chapter—

“ crypto wallet freezing order ” has the same meaning as in Chapter 3D (see
section  303Z36 ); “ enforcement officer ” has the meaning given by section
303Z20 ; “ senior officer ” has the meaning given by section  303Z20 .

1.303Z41.10

Section  303Z36 (4)(b)  applies in relation to this Chapter as it applies in
relation to Chapter 3D.

########### Forfeiture order: supplementary

1.303Z42

1.303Z42.1

Subsection  (2)  applies where an application is made under section  303Z41
for the forfeiture of any cryptoassets detained under Chapter 3C.

1.303Z42.2

The cryptoassets are to continue to be detained under Chapter 3C (and may not
be released under any power conferred by this Part) until any proceedings in
pursuance of the application (including any proceedings on appeal) are
concluded.

This subsection is subject to Chapter 3F (conversion to money).

1.303Z42.3

Where an application is made under section 303Z41 in relation to cryptoassets
held in a crypto wallet that is subject to a crypto wallet freezing order—

1.303Z42.3.a

subsections (4) and (5) apply, and

1.303Z42.3.b

the crypto wallet freezing order is to continue to have effect until the time
referred to in subsection (4)(b) or (5).

1.303Z42.4

Where the cryptoassets are ordered to be forfeited under section  303Z41 (4)
or  303Z45 (3) —

1.303Z42.4.a

the cryptoasset service provider that administers the crypto wallet must
transfer the cryptoassets into a crypto wallet nominated by an enforcement
officer, and

1.303Z42.4.b

immediately after the transfer has been made, the freezing order ceases to
have effect.

1.303Z42.5

Where the application is determined or otherwise disposed of other than by the
making of an order under section  303Z41 (4)  or  303Z45 (3) , the crypto
wallet freezing order ceases to have effect immediately after that
determination or other disposal.

1.303Z42.6

Subsections  (4) (b) and  (5)  are subject to section  303Z46  and Chapter 3F.

1.303Z42.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section to make provision
about the forfeiture of cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet that is subject
to a crypto wallet freezing order.

1.303Z42.8

Regulations under subsection  (7)  may in particular make provision about—

1.303Z42.8.a

the process for the forfeiture of cryptoassets;

1.303Z42.8.b

the realisation of forfeited cryptoassets;

1.303Z42.8.c

the application of the proceeds of such realisation.

1.303Z42.9

Regulations under subsection  (7)  may make consequential amendments of this
Chapter.

1.303Z42.10

The Secretary of State may not make regulations under subsection  (7)  unless
the Secretary of State has—

1.303Z42.10.a

consulted the Scottish Ministers and the Department of Justice, and

1.303Z42.10.b

given a notice containing the relevant information to the Scottish Ministers
and the Department of Justice.

1.303Z42.11

Consultation under subsection  (10)(a)  must include consultation about any
effects that the Secretary of State considers the regulations may have on—

1.303Z42.11.a

a person in Scotland or Northern Ireland (as the case may be) applying for the
forfeiture of cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet that is subject to a crypto
wallet freezing order, and

1.303Z42.11.b

a sheriff or court in Scotland or a court in Northern Ireland (as the case may
be) considering such an application or making an order for such forfeiture.

1.303Z42.12

In subsection  (10)(b)  “ relevant information ” means—

1.303Z42.12.a

a description of—

1.303Z42.12.a.i

the process undertaken in order to comply with subsection  (10)(a)  in
relation to the Scottish Ministers or the Department of Justice (as the case
may be), and

1.303Z42.12.a.ii

any agreement, objection or other views expressed as part of that process by
the Scottish Ministers or the Department of Justice (as the case may be), and

1.303Z42.12.b

an explanation of whether and how such views have been taken into account in
the regulations (including, in a case where the Secretary of State proposes to
make the regulations despite an objection, an explanation of the reasons for
doing so).

########### Associated and joint property

1.303Z43

1.303Z43.1

Sections  303Z44  and  303Z45  apply if—

1.303Z43.1.a

an application is made under section  303Z41  in respect of cryptoassets,

1.303Z43.1.b

the court or sheriff is satisfied that some or all of the cryptoassets are
recoverable property or are intended by any person for use in unlawful
conduct, and

1.303Z43.1.c

there exists property that is associated with the cryptoassets in relation to
which the court or sheriff is satisfied as mentioned in paragraph (b).

1.303Z43.2

Sections  303Z44  and  303Z45  also apply in England and Wales and Northern
Ireland if—

1.303Z43.2.a

an application is made under section  303Z41  in respect of cryptoassets,

1.303Z43.2.b

the court is satisfied that some or all of the cryptoassets are recoverable
property, and

1.303Z43.2.c

the cryptoassets in relation to which the court is satisfied as mentioned in
paragraph  (b)  belong to joint tenants and one of the tenants is an excepted
joint owner.

1.303Z43.3

In this section and sections  303Z44  and  303Z45  “ associated property ”
means property of any of the following descriptions that is not itself the
forfeitable property—

1.303Z43.3.a

any interest in the forfeitable property;

1.303Z43.3.b

any other interest in the property in which the forfeitable property subsists;

1.303Z43.3.c

if the forfeitable property is part of a larger property, but not a separate
part, the remainder of that property.

References to property being associated with forfeitable property are to be
read accordingly.

1.303Z43.4

In this section and sections  303Z44  and  303Z45 , the “ forfeitable property
” means the cryptoassets in relation to which the court or sheriff is
satisfied as mentioned in subsection  (1)(b)  or  (2)(b)  (as the case may
be).

########### Agreements about associated and joint property

1.303Z44

1.303Z44.1

Where—

1.303Z44.1.a

this section applies, and

1.303Z44.1.b

the person who applied for the order under section  303Z41  (on the one hand)
and the person who holds the associated property or who is the excepted joint
owner (on the other hand) agree,

the magistrates’ court or sheriff may, instead of making an order under
section  303Z41 (4) , make an order requiring the person who holds the
associated property or who is the excepted joint owner to make a payment to a
person identified in the order.

1.303Z44.2

The amount of the payment is (subject to subsection  (3) ) to be the amount
which the persons referred to in subsection  (1)(b)  agree represents—

1.303Z44.2.a

in a case where this section applies by virtue of section  303Z43 (1) , the
value of the forfeitable property;

1.303Z44.2.b

in a case where this section applies by virtue of section  303Z43 (2) , the
value of the forfeitable property less the value of the excepted joint owner’s
share.

1.303Z44.3

The amount of the payment may be reduced if the person who applied for the
order under section  303Z41  agrees that the other party to the agreement has
suffered loss as a result of—

1.303Z44.3.a

the seizure of the forfeitable property under section  303Z29  and its
subsequent detention, or

1.303Z44.3.b

the making of a crypto wallet freezing order under section  303Z37 .

1.303Z44.4

The reduction that is permissible by virtue of subsection  (3)  is such amount
as the parties to the agreement agree is reasonable, having regard to the loss
suffered and any other relevant circumstances.

1.303Z44.5

An order under subsection  (1)  may, so far as required for giving effect to
the agreement, include provision for vesting, creating or extinguishing any
interest in property.

1.303Z44.6

An order under subsection  (1)  made by a magistrates’ court may provide for
payment under subsection  (12)  of reasonable legal expenses that a person has
reasonably incurred, or may reasonably incur, in respect of—

1.303Z44.6.a

the proceedings in which the order is made, or

1.303Z44.6.b

any related proceedings under this Chapter.

1.303Z44.7

A sum in respect of a relevant item of expenditure is not payable under
subsection  (12)  in pursuance of provision under subsection  (6)  unless—

1.303Z44.7.a
