any other persons who the authorised officer has reasonable grounds to believe
have an interest in the item,

that the item has been released, and

2.10Z7AI.7.b

with the approval of a senior officer.

2.10Z7AI.8

Any proceeds of a disposal of the item are to be paid—

2.10Z7AI.8.a

into the Consolidated Fund if—

2.10Z7AI.8.a.i

the item was directed to be released by a magistrates’ court, or

2.10Z7AI.8.a.ii

a magistrates’ court or justice was notified under sub-paragraph  (4)  of the
release;

2.10Z7AI.8.b

into the Scottish Consolidated Fund if—

2.10Z7AI.8.b.i

the item was directed to be released by the sheriff, or

2.10Z7AI.8.b.ii

the sheriff was notified under sub-paragraph  (4)  of the release.

2.10Z7AI.9

If (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the property is connected, the property is
not to be released under this paragraph (and so is to continue to be detained)
until the proceedings are concluded.

######### Terrorist cryptoassets: crypto wallet freezing orders

########## Interpretation

2.10Z7B

2.10Z7B.1

In this Part—

2.10Z7B.1.a

“ cryptoasset exchange provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way
of business provides one or more of the following services, including where
the firm or sole practitioner does so as creator or issuer of any of the
cryptoassets involved—

2.10Z7B.1.a.i

exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets,

2.10Z7B.1.a.ii

exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, one cryptoasset for another, or

2.10Z7B.1.a.iii

operating a machine which utilises automated processes to exchange
cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets;

2.10Z7B.1.b

“ custodian wallet provider ” means a firm or sole practitioner who by way of
business provides services to safeguard, or to safeguard and administer—

2.10Z7B.1.b.i

cryptoassets on behalf of its customers, or

2.10Z7B.1.b.ii

private cryptographic keys on behalf of its customers in order to hold, store
and transfer cryptoassets;

2.10Z7B.1.c

“ cryptoasset service provider ” includes cryptoasset exchange provider and
custodian wallet provider.

2.10Z7B.2

In the definition of “cryptoasset exchange provider” in sub-paragraph  (1) —

2.10Z7B.2.a

“ cryptoasset ” includes a right to, or interest in, a cryptoasset;

2.10Z7B.2.b

“ money ” means—

2.10Z7B.2.b.i

money in sterling,

2.10Z7B.2.b.ii

money in any other currency, or

2.10Z7B.2.b.iii

money in any other medium of exchange,

but does not include a cryptoasset.

2.10Z7B.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend
the definitions in sub-paragraphs  (1)  and  (2) .

2.10Z7B.4

Regulations under sub-paragraph  (3) —

2.10Z7B.4.a

may make different provision for different purposes;

2.10Z7B.4.b

may make consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

2.10Z7B.5

A statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph  (3)  may
not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved
by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

2.10Z7B.6

For the purposes of this Part—

2.10Z7B.6.a

a crypto wallet freezing order is an order that, subject to any exclusions
(see paragraph  10Z7BD ), prohibits each person by or for whom the crypto
wallet to which the order applies is administered from—

2.10Z7B.6.a.i

making withdrawals or payments from the crypto wallet, or

2.10Z7B.6.a.ii

using the crypto wallet in any other way;

2.10Z7B.6.b

a crypto wallet is administered by or for a person if the person is the person
to whom services are being provided by a cryptoasset service provider in
relation to that crypto wallet.

2.10Z7B.7

In this Part—

“ enforcement officer ” means— a constable, or a counter-terrorism financial
investigator; “ relevant court ” means— in England and Wales and Northern
Ireland, a magistrates’ court, and in Scotland, the sheriff; “ senior officer
” means a police officer of at least the rank of superintendent; “ UK-
connected cryptoasset service provider ” means a cryptoasset service provider
which— is acting in the course of business carried on by it in the United
Kingdom, has terms and conditions with the persons to whom it provides
services which provide for a legal dispute to be litigated in the courts of a
part of the United Kingdom, holds, in the United Kingdom, any data relating to
the persons to whom it provides services, or meets the condition in sub-
paragraph  (8) .

2.10Z7B.8

The condition in this sub-paragraph is that—

2.10Z7B.8.a

the cryptoasset service provider has its registered office, or if it does not
have one, its head office in the United Kingdom, and

2.10Z7B.8.b

the day-to-day management of the provider’s business is the responsibility of
that office or another establishment maintained by it in the United Kingdom.

########## Application for crypto wallet freezing order

2.10Z7BA

2.10Z7BA.1

This paragraph applies if an enforcement officer has reasonable grounds for
suspecting that cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet administered by a UK-
connected cryptoasset service provider are terrorist cryptoassets.

2.10Z7BA.2

Where this paragraph applies the enforcement officer may apply to the relevant
court for a crypto wallet freezing order in relation to the crypto wallet in
which the cryptoassets are held.

2.10Z7BA.3

But—

2.10Z7BA.3.a

an enforcement officer may not apply for a crypto wallet freezing order unless
the officer is a senior officer or is authorised to do so by a senior officer,
and

2.10Z7BA.3.b

the senior officer must consult the Treasury before making the application for
the order or (as the case may be) authorising the application to be made,
unless in the circumstances it is not reasonably practicable to do so.

2.10Z7BA.4

An application for a crypto wallet freezing order may be made without notice
if the circumstances of the case are such that notice of the application would
prejudice the taking of any steps under this Schedule to forfeit cryptoassets
that are terrorist cryptoassets.

2.10Z7BA.5

An application for a crypto wallet freezing order under this paragraph may be
combined with an application for an account freezing order under paragraph 10Q
where a single entity—

2.10Z7BA.5.a

is both a relevant financial institution for the purposes of paragraph 10Q and
a cryptoasset service provider for the purposes of this Part, and

2.10Z7BA.5.b

operates or administers, for the same person, both an account holding money
and a crypto wallet.

########## Making of crypto wallet freezing order

2.10Z7BB

2.10Z7BB.1

This paragraph applies where an application for a crypto wallet freezing order
is made under paragraph  10Z7BA  in relation to a crypto wallet.

2.10Z7BB.2

The relevant court may make the order if satisfied that there are reasonable
grounds for suspecting that some or all of the cryptoassets held in the crypto
wallet are terrorist cryptoassets.

2.10Z7BB.3

A crypto wallet freezing order ceases to have effect at the end of the period
specified in the order (which may be varied under paragraph  10Z7BC ) unless
it ceases to have effect at an earlier or later time in accordance with this
Part or Part 4BC or 4BD.

2.10Z7BB.4

The period specified by the relevant court for the purposes of sub-paragraph
(3)  (whether when the order is first made or on a variation under paragraph
10Z7BC ) may not exceed the period of 2 years, beginning with the day on which
the crypto wallet freezing order is (or was) made; but this is subject to sub-
paragraph  (5) .

2.10Z7BB.5

The relevant court may make an order for the period of 2 years in sub-
paragraph  (4)  to be extended to a period of up to 3 years beginning with the
day on which the crypto wallet freezing order is (or was) made.

2.10Z7BB.6

The relevant court may make an order under sub-paragraph  (5)  if satisfied
that a request for assistance is outstanding in relation to some or all of the
cryptoassets held in the crypto wallet.

2.10Z7BB.7

A “request for assistance” in sub-paragraph  (6)  means a request for
assistance in obtaining evidence (including information in any form or
article) in connection with some or all of the cryptoassets held in the crypto
wallet, made—

2.10Z7BB.7.a

by a judicial authority in the United Kingdom under section 7 of the Crime
(International Co-operation) Act 2003,

2.10Z7BB.7.b

by an enforcement officer, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in
a foreign country,

2.10Z7BB.7.c

by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their functions under this
Schedule, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a foreign
country, or

2.10Z7BB.7.d

by a person under section 375A or 408A of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002
(evidence overseas).

2.10Z7BB.8

A crypto wallet freezing order must provide for notice to be given to persons
affected by the order.

########## Variation and setting aside of crypto wallet freezing order

2.10Z7BC

2.10Z7BC.1

The relevant court may at any time vary or set aside a crypto wallet freezing
order on an application made by—

2.10Z7BC.1.a

an enforcement officer, or

2.10Z7BC.1.b

any person affected by the order.

2.10Z7BC.2

But an enforcement officer may not make an application under sub-paragraph
(1)  unless the officer is a senior officer or is authorised to do so by a
senior officer.

2.10Z7BC.3

Before varying or setting aside a crypto wallet freezing order the court must
(as well as giving the parties to the proceedings an opportunity to be heard)
give such an opportunity to any person who may be affected by its decision.

2.10Z7BC.4

In relation to Scotland, the references in this paragraph to setting aside an
order are to be read as references to recalling it.

########## Exclusions

2.10Z7BD

2.10Z7BD.1

The power to vary a crypto wallet freezing order includes (amongst other
things) power to make exclusions from the prohibition on making withdrawals or
payments from the crypto wallet to which the order applies.

2.10Z7BD.2

Exclusions from the prohibition may also be made when the order is made.

2.10Z7BD.3

An exclusion may (amongst other things) make provision for the purpose of
enabling a person by or for whom the crypto wallet is administered—

2.10Z7BD.3.a

to meet the person’s reasonable living expenses, or

2.10Z7BD.3.b

to carry on any trade, business, profession or occupation.

2.10Z7BD.4

An exclusion may be made subject to conditions.

2.10Z7BD.5

Where a magistrates’ court exercises the power to make an exclusion for the
purpose of enabling a person to meet legal expenses that the person has
incurred, or may incur, in respect of proceedings under this Schedule, it must
ensure that the exclusion—

2.10Z7BD.5.a

is limited to reasonable legal expenses that the person has reasonably
incurred or that the person reasonably incurs,

2.10Z7BD.5.b

specifies the total amount that may be released for legal expenses in
pursuance of the exclusion, and

2.10Z7BD.5.c

is made subject to the same conditions as would be the required conditions
(see section 286A of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002) if the order had been
made under section 245A of that Act (in addition to any conditions imposed
under sub-paragraph  (4) ).

2.10Z7BD.6

A magistrates’ court, in deciding whether to make an exclusion for the purpose
of enabling a person to meet legal expenses in respect of proceedings under
this Schedule—

2.10Z7BD.6.a

must have regard to the desirability of the person being represented in any
proceedings under this Schedule in which the person is a participant, and

2.10Z7BD.6.b

must disregard the possibility that legal representation of the person in any
such proceedings might, were an exclusion not made—

2.10Z7BD.6.b.i

be made available under arrangements made for the purposes of Part 1 of the
Legal Aid, Sentencing and Punishment of Offenders Act 2012, or

2.10Z7BD.6.b.ii

be funded by the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland.

2.10Z7BD.7

The sheriff’s power to make exclusions may not be exercised for the purpose of
enabling any person to meet any legal expenses in respect of proceedings under
this Schedule.

2.10Z7BD.8

The power to make exclusions must, subject to sub-paragraph  (6) , be
exercised with a view to ensuring, so far as practicable, that there is not
undue prejudice to the taking of any steps under this Schedule to forfeit
cryptoassets that are terrorist cryptoassets.

########## Restriction on proceedings and remedies

2.10Z7BE

2.10Z7BE.1

If a court in which proceedings are pending in respect of a crypto wallet
administered by a UK-connected cryptoasset service provider is satisfied that
a crypto wallet freezing order has been applied for or made in respect of the
crypto wallet, it may either stay the proceedings or allow them to continue on
any terms it thinks fit.

2.10Z7BE.2

Before exercising the power conferred by sub-paragraph  (1) , the court must
(as well as giving the parties to any of the proceedings concerned an
opportunity to be heard) give such an opportunity to any person who may be
affected by the court’s decision.

2.10Z7BE.3

In relation to Scotland, the reference in sub-paragraph  (1)  to staying the
proceedings is to be read as a reference to sisting the proceedings.

######### Forfeiture of terrorist cryptoassets

########## Interpretation

2.10Z7C

2.10Z7C.1

In this Part—

“ cryptoasset service provider ” has the same meaning as in Part 4BB (see
paragraph  10Z7B (1) ); “ crypto wallet freezing order ” has the same meaning
as in Part 4BB (see paragraph  10Z7B (6) ); “ senior officer ” means— a senior
police officer; an officer of Revenue and Customs of a rank designated by the
Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs as equivalent to that of a
senior police officer; an immigration officer of a rank designated by the
Secretary of State as equivalent to that of a senior police officer; “ senior
police officer ” means a police officer of at least the rank of
superintendent.

2.10Z7C.2

Paragraph  10Z7B (6)(b)  (administration of crypto wallets) applies in
relation to this Part as it applies in relation to Part  4BB .

########## Forfeiture

2.10Z7CA

2.10Z7CA.1

This paragraph applies—

2.10Z7CA.1.a

while any cryptoassets are detained under Part 4BA, or

2.10Z7CA.1.b

while a crypto wallet freezing order made under paragraph  10Z7BB  has effect.

2.10Z7CA.2

An application for the forfeiture of some or all of the cryptoassets that are
detained or held in the crypto wallet that is subject to the crypto wallet
freezing order may be made—

2.10Z7CA.2.a

to a magistrates’ court by the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and
Customs or an authorised officer, or

2.10Z7CA.2.b

to the sheriff by the Scottish Ministers.

2.10Z7CA.3

The court or sheriff may order the forfeiture of some or all of the
cryptoassets if satisfied that the cryptoassets are terrorist cryptoassets.

2.10Z7CA.4

An order under sub-paragraph  (3)  made by a magistrates’ court may provide
for payment under paragraph  10Z7CJ  of reasonable legal expenses that a
person has reasonably incurred, or may reasonably incur, in respect of—

2.10Z7CA.4.a

the proceedings in which the order is made, or

2.10Z7CA.4.b

any related proceedings under this Part.

2.10Z7CA.5

A sum in respect of a relevant item of expenditure is not payable under
paragraph  10Z7CJ  in pursuance of provision under sub-paragraph  (4)  unless—

2.10Z7CA.5.a

the person who applied for the order under sub-paragraph  (3)  agrees to its
payment, or

2.10Z7CA.5.b

the court has assessed the amount allowed in respect of that item and the sum
is paid in respect of the assessed amount.

2.10Z7CA.6

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (5) —

2.10Z7CA.6.a

a “relevant item of expenditure” is an item of expenditure to which
regulations under section 286B of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 would apply
if the order under sub-paragraph  (3)  had instead been a recovery order made
under section 266 of that Act;

2.10Z7CA.6.b

an amount is “allowed” in respect of a relevant item of expenditure if it
would have been allowed by those regulations;

2.10Z7CA.6.c

if the person who applied for the order under sub-paragraph  (3)  was an
authorised officer, that person may not agree to the payment of a sum unless
the person is a senior officer or is authorised to do so by a senior officer.

2.10Z7CA.7

Sub-paragraph  (3)  ceases to apply on the transfer of an application made
under this paragraph in accordance with paragraph  10Z7CE .

########## Forfeiture: supplementary

2.10Z7CB

2.10Z7CB.1

Sub-paragraph  (2)  applies where an application is made under paragraph
10Z7CA  for the forfeiture of any cryptoassets detained under Part 4BA.

2.10Z7CB.2

The cryptoassets are to continue to be detained under Part 4BA (and may not be
released under any power conferred by this Schedule) until any proceedings in
pursuance of the application (including any proceedings on appeal) are
concluded.

This is subject to Part  4BD  (conversion to money).

2.10Z7CB.3

Where an application is made under paragraph  10Z7CA  in relation to
cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet that is subject to a crypto wallet
freezing order—

2.10Z7CB.3.a

sub-paragraphs  (4)  and  (5)  apply, and

2.10Z7CB.3.b

the crypto wallet freezing order is to continue to have effect until the time
referred to in sub-paragraph  (4) (b)  or  (5) .

2.10Z7CB.4

Where the cryptoassets are ordered to be forfeited under paragraph  10Z7CA (3)
or  10Z7CE (3) —

2.10Z7CB.4.a

the cryptoasset service provider that administers the crypto wallet must
transfer the cryptoassets into a crypto wallet nominated by an authorised
officer, and

2.10Z7CB.4.b

immediately after the transfer has been made, the freezing order ceases to
have effect.

2.10Z7CB.5

Where the application is determined or otherwise disposed of other than by the
making of an order under paragraph  10Z7CA (3)  or  10Z7CE (3) , the crypto
wallet freezing order ceases to have effect immediately after that
determination or other disposal.

2.10Z7CB.6

Sub-paragraphs  (4) (b)  and  (5)  are subject to paragraph  10Z7CF  and Part
4BD .

2.10Z7CB.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend
this paragraph to make provision about the forfeiture of cryptoassets held in
a crypto wallet that is subject to a crypto wallet freezing order.

2.10Z7CB.8

Regulations under sub-paragraph  (7)  may in particular make provision about—

2.10Z7CB.8.a

the process for the forfeiture of cryptoassets;

2.10Z7CB.8.b

the realisation of forfeited cryptoassets;

2.10Z7CB.8.c

the application of the proceeds of such realisation.

2.10Z7CB.9

Regulations under sub-paragraph  (7)  may—

2.10Z7CB.9.a

make different provision for different purposes;

2.10Z7CB.9.b

make consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or
saving provision, including provision which makes consequential amendments to
this Part.

2.10Z7CB.10

A statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph  (7)  may
not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved
by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

########## Associated and joint property

2.10Z7CC

2.10Z7CC.1

Paragraphs  10Z7CD  and  10Z7CE  apply if—

2.10Z7CC.1.a

an application is made under paragraph  10Z7CA  in respect of cryptoassets,

2.10Z7CC.1.b

the court or sheriff is satisfied that some or all of the cryptoassets are
terrorist cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7CC.1.c

there exists property that is associated with the cryptoassets in relation to
which the court or sheriff is satisfied as mentioned in paragraph  (b) .

2.10Z7CC.2

Paragraphs  10Z7CD  and  10Z7CE  also apply in England and Wales and Northern
Ireland if—

2.10Z7CC.2.a

an application is made under paragraph  10Z7CA  in respect of cryptoassets,

2.10Z7CC.2.b

the court is satisfied that some or all of the cryptoassets are earmarked as
terrorist property, and

2.10Z7CC.2.c

the cryptoassets in relation to which the court is satisfied as mentioned in
paragraph  (b)  belong to joint tenants and one of the tenants is an excepted
joint owner.

2.10Z7CC.3

In this paragraph and paragraphs  10Z7CD  and  10Z7CE , “ associated property
” means property of any of the following descriptions that is not itself the
forfeitable property—

2.10Z7CC.3.a

any interest in the forfeitable property;

2.10Z7CC.3.b

any other interest in the property in which the forfeitable property subsists;

2.10Z7CC.3.c

if the forfeitable property is part of a larger property, but not a separate
part, the remainder of that property.

References to property being associated with forfeitable property are to be
read accordingly.

2.10Z7CC.4

In this paragraph and paragraphs  10Z7CD  and  10Z7CE , the “ forfeitable
property ” means the cryptoassets in relation to which the court or sheriff is
satisfied as mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  or  (2)(b)  (as the case may
be).

2.10Z7CC.5

For the purposes of this paragraph and paragraphs  10Z7CD  and  10Z7CE —

2.10Z7CC.5.a

an excepted joint owner is a joint tenant who obtained the property in
circumstances in which it would not (as against them) be earmarked, and

2.10Z7CC.5.b

references to the excepted joint owner’s share of property are to so much of
the property as would have been theirs if the joint tenancy had been severed.

########## Agreements about associated and joint property

2.10Z7CD

2.10Z7CD.1

Where—

2.10Z7CD.1.a

this paragraph applies, and

2.10Z7CD.1.b

the person who applied for the order under paragraph  10Z7CA  (on the one
hand) and the person who holds the associated property or who is the excepted
joint owner (on the other hand) agree,

the magistrates’ court or sheriff may, instead of making an order under
paragraph  10Z7CA (3) , make an order requiring the person who holds the
associated property or who is the excepted joint owner to make a payment to a
person identified in the order.

2.10Z7CD.2

The amount of the payment is (subject to sub-paragraph  (3) ) to be the amount
which the persons referred to in sub-paragraph  (1)(b)  agree represents—

2.10Z7CD.2.a

in a case where this paragraph applies by virtue of paragraph  10Z7CC (1) ,
the value of the forfeitable property;

2.10Z7CD.2.b

in a case where this paragraph applies by virtue of paragraph  10Z7CC (2) ,
the value of the forfeitable property less the value of the excepted joint
owner’s share.

2.10Z7CD.3

The amount of the payment may be reduced if the person who applied for the
order under paragraph  10Z7CA  agrees that the other party to the agreement
has suffered loss as a result of—

2.10Z7CD.3.a

the seizure of the forfeitable property under paragraph  10Z7AD  and its
subsequent detention, or

2.10Z7CD.3.b

the making of a crypto wallet freezing order under paragraph  10Z7BB .

2.10Z7CD.4

The reduction that is permissible by virtue of sub-paragraph  (3)  is such
amount as the parties to the agreement agree is reasonable, having regard to
the loss suffered and any other relevant circumstances.

2.10Z7CD.5

An order under sub-paragraph  (1)  may, so far as required for giving effect
to the agreement, include provision for vesting, creating or extinguishing any
interest in property.

2.10Z7CD.6

An order under sub-paragraph  (1)  made by a magistrates’ court may provide
for payment under sub-paragraph  (11)  of reasonable legal expenses that a
person has reasonably incurred, or may reasonably incur, in respect of—

2.10Z7CD.6.a

the proceedings in which the order is made, or

2.10Z7CD.6.b

any related proceedings under this Part.

2.10Z7CD.7

A sum in respect of a relevant item of expenditure is not payable under sub-
paragraph  (11)  in pursuance of provision under sub-paragraph  (6)  unless—

2.10Z7CD.7.a

the person who applied for the order under paragraph  10Z7CA  agrees to its
payment, or

2.10Z7CD.7.b

the court has assessed the amount allowed in respect of that item and the sum
is paid in respect of the assessed amount.

2.10Z7CD.8

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (7) —

2.10Z7CD.8.a

a “relevant item of expenditure” is an item of expenditure to which
regulations under section 286B of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002 would apply
if the order under sub-paragraph  (1)  had instead been a recovery order made
under section 266 of that Act;

2.10Z7CD.8.b

an amount is “allowed” in respect of a relevant item of expenditure if it
would have been allowed by those regulations.

2.10Z7CD.9

If there is more than one item of associated property or more than one
excepted joint owner, the total amount to be paid under sub-paragraph  (1) ,
and the part of that amount which is to be provided by each person who holds
any such associated property or who is an excepted joint owner, is to be
agreed between both (or all) of them and the person who applied for the order
under paragraph  10Z7CA .

2.10Z7CD.10

If the person who applied for the order under paragraph  10Z7CA  was an
authorised officer, that person may enter into an agreement for the purposes
of any provision of this paragraph only if the person is a senior officer or
is authorised to do so by a senior officer.

2.10Z7CD.11

An amount received under an order under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be applied as
follows—

2.10Z7CD.11.a

first, it must be applied in making any payment of legal expenses which, after
giving effect to sub-paragraph  (7) , are payable under this sub-paragraph in
pursuance of provision under sub-paragraph  (6) ;

2.10Z7CD.11.b

second, it must be applied in payment or reimbursement of any reasonable costs
incurred in storing or insuring the forfeitable property and any associated
property whilst detained under this Schedule;

2.10Z7CD.11.c

third, it must be paid—

2.10Z7CD.11.c.i

if the order was made by a magistrates’ court, into the Consolidated Fund;

2.10Z7CD.11.c.ii

if the order was made by the sheriff, into the Scottish Consolidated Fund.

########## Associated and joint property: default of agreement

2.10Z7CE

2.10Z7CE.1

Where this paragraph applies and there is no agreement under paragraph  10Z7CD
, the magistrates’ court or sheriff may transfer the application made under
paragraph  10Z7CA  to the appropriate court.

2.10Z7CE.2

The “appropriate court” is—

2.10Z7CE.2.a

the High Court, where the application under paragraph  10Z7CA  was made to a
magistrates’ court;

2.10Z7CE.2.b

the Court of Session, where the application under paragraph  10Z7CA  was made
to the sheriff.

2.10Z7CE.3

Where (under sub-paragraph  (1) ) an application made under paragraph  10Z7CA
is transferred to the appropriate court, the appropriate court may order the
forfeiture of the property to which the application relates, or any part of
that property, if satisfied that what is to be forfeited—

2.10Z7CE.3.a

is within subsection (1)(a) or (b) of section 1, or

2.10Z7CE.3.b

is property earmarked as terrorist property.

2.10Z7CE.4

An order under sub-paragraph  (3)  made by the High Court may include
provision of the type that may be included in an order under paragraph  10Z7CA
(3)  made by a magistrates’ court by virtue of paragraph  10Z7CA (4) .

2.10Z7CE.5

If provision is included in an order of the High Court by virtue of sub-
paragraph  (4)  of this paragraph, paragraph  10Z7CA (5)  and  (6)  apply with
the necessary modifications.

2.10Z7CE.6

The appropriate court may, as well as making an order under sub-paragraph  (3)
, make an order—

2.10Z7CE.6.a

providing for the forfeiture of the associated property or (as the case may
be) for the excepted joint owner‘s interest to be extinguished, or

2.10Z7CE.6.b

providing for the excepted joint owner‘s interest to be severed.

2.10Z7CE.7

Where (under sub-paragraph  (1) ) the magistrates’ court or sheriff decides
not to transfer an application made under paragraph  10Z7CA  to the
appropriate court, the magistrates’ court or sheriff may, as well as making an
order under paragraph  10Z7CA (3) , make an order—

2.10Z7CE.7.a

providing for the forfeiture of the associated property or (as the case may
be) for the excepted joint owner‘s interest to be extinguished, or

2.10Z7CE.7.b

providing for the excepted joint owner‘s interest to be severed.

2.10Z7CE.8

An order under sub-paragraph  (6)  or  (7)  may be made only if the
appropriate court, the magistrates’ court or the sheriff (as the case may be)
thinks it just and equitable to do so.

2.10Z7CE.9

An order under sub-paragraph  (6)  or  (7)  must provide for the payment of an
amount to the person who holds the associated property or who is an excepted
joint owner.

2.10Z7CE.10

In making an order under sub-paragraph  (6)  or  (7) , and including provision
in it by virtue of sub-paragraph  (9) , the appropriate court, the
magistrates’ court or the sheriff (as the case may be) must have regard to—

2.10Z7CE.10.a

the rights of any person who holds the associated property or who is an
excepted joint owner and the value to that person of that property or (as the
case may be) of that person’s share (including any value that cannot be
assessed in terms of money), and

2.10Z7CE.10.b

the interest of the person who applied for the order under paragraph  10Z7CA
in realising the value of the forfeitable property.

2.10Z7CE.11

If the appropriate court, the magistrates’ court or the sheriff (as the case
may be) is satisfied that—

2.10Z7CE.11.a

the person who holds the associated property or who is an excepted joint owner
has suffered loss as a result of—

2.10Z7CE.11.a.i

the seizure of the forfeitable property under paragraph  10Z7AD  and its
subsequent detention, or

2.10Z7CE.11.a.ii

the making of the crypto wallet freezing order under paragraph  10Z7BB , and

2.10Z7CE.11.b

the circumstances are exceptional,

an order under sub-paragraph  (6)  or  (7)  may require the payment of
compensation to that person.

2.10Z7CE.12

The amount of compensation to be paid by virtue of sub-paragraph  (11)  is the
amount the appropriate court, the magistrates’ court or the sheriff (as the
case may be) thinks reasonable, having regard to the loss suffered and any
other relevant circumstances.

2.10Z7CE.13

Compensation to be paid by virtue of sub-paragraph  (11)  is to be paid in the
same way that compensation is to be paid under paragraph  10Z7CM .

########## Continuation of crypto wallet freezing order pending appeal

2.10Z7CF

2.10Z7CF.1

This paragraph applies where, on an application under paragraph  10Z7CA  in
relation to a crypto wallet to which a crypto wallet freezing order applies—

2.10Z7CF.1.a

the magistrates’ court or sheriff decides—

2.10Z7CF.1.a.i

to make an order under paragraph  10Z7CA (3)  in relation to some but not all
of the cryptoassets to which the application related, or

2.10Z7CF.1.a.ii

not to make an order under paragraph  10Z7CA (3) , or

2.10Z7CF.1.b

if the application is transferred in accordance with paragraph  10Z7CE (1) ,
the High Court or Court of Session decides—

2.10Z7CF.1.b.i

to make an order under paragraph  10Z7CE (3)  in relation to some but not all
of the cryptoassets to which the application related, or

2.10Z7CF.1.b.ii

not to make an order under paragraph  10Z7CE (3) .

2.10Z7CF.2

The person who made the application under paragraph  10Z7CA  may apply without
notice to the court or sheriff that made the decision referred to in sub-
paragraph  (1)  for an order that the crypto wallet freezing order is to
continue to have effect.

2.10Z7CF.3

Where the court or sheriff makes an order under sub-paragraph  (2)  the crypto
wallet freezing order is to continue to have effect until—

2.10Z7CF.3.a

the end of the period of 48 hours starting with the making of the order under
sub-paragraph  (2) , or

2.10Z7CF.3.b

if within that period of 48 hours an appeal is brought (whether under
paragraph  10Z7CG  or otherwise) against the decision referred to in sub-
paragraph  (1) , the time when the appeal is determined or otherwise disposed
of.

2.10Z7CF.4

Sub-paragraph  (3)  of paragraph  10Z7AF  applies for the purposes of sub-
paragraph  (3)  as it applies for the purposes of that paragraph.

########## Paragraphs 

2.10Z7CG

2.10Z7CG.1

Any party to proceedings for an order for the forfeiture of cryptoassets under
paragraph  10Z7CA  may appeal against—

2.10Z7CG.1.a

the making of an order under paragraph  10Z7CA ;

2.10Z7CG.1.b

the making of an order under paragraph  10Z7CE (7) ;

2.10Z7CG.1.c

a decision not to make an order under paragraph  10Z7CA  unless the reason
that no order was made is that an order was instead made under paragraph
10Z7CD ;

2.10Z7CG.1.d

a decision not to make an order under paragraph  10Z7CE (7) .

Paragraphs  (c)  and  (d)  do not apply if the application for the order under
paragraph  10Z7CA  was transferred in accordance with paragraph  10Z7CE (1) .

2.10Z7CG.2

Where an order under paragraph  10Z7CD  is made by a magistrates’ court, any
party to the proceedings for the order (including any party to the proceedings
under paragraph  10Z7CA  that preceded the making of the order) may appeal
against a decision to include, or not to include, provision in the order under
paragraph  10Z7CD (6) .

2.10Z7CG.3

An appeal under this paragraph lies—

2.10Z7CG.3.a

in relation to England and Wales, to the Crown Court;

2.10Z7CG.3.b

in relation to Scotland, to the Sheriff Appeal Court;

2.10Z7CG.3.c

in relation to Northern Ireland, to a county court.

2.10Z7CG.4

An appeal under this paragraph must be made before the end of the period of 30
days starting with the day on which the court or sheriff makes the order or
decision.

2.10Z7CG.5

Sub-paragraph  (4)  is subject to paragraph  10Z7CH .

2.10Z7CG.6

The court hearing the appeal may make any order it thinks appropriate.

2.10Z7CG.7

If the court upholds an appeal against an order forfeiting any cryptoasset or
other item of property, it may, subject to sub-paragraph  (8) , order the
release of the whole or any part of the property.

2.10Z7CG.8

If (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the property is connected, the property is
not to be released under this paragraph (and so is to continue to be detained)
until the proceedings are concluded.

########## Extended time for appealing in certain cases where deproscription order made

2.10Z7CH

2.10Z7CH.1

This paragraph applies where—

2.10Z7CH.1.a

a successful application for an order under paragraph  10Z7CA  relies (wholly
or partly) on the fact that an organisation is proscribed,

2.10Z7CH.1.b

an application under section 4 of the Terrorism Act 2000 for a deproscription
order in respect of the organisation is refused by the Secretary of State,

2.10Z7CH.1.c

the property forfeited by the order under paragraph  10Z7CA  was seized under
this Schedule on or after the date of the refusal of that application,

2.10Z7CH.1.d

an appeal against that refusal is allowed under section 5 of the Terrorism Act
2000,

2.10Z7CH.1.e

a deproscription order is made accordingly, and

2.10Z7CH.1.f

if the order is made in reliance on section 123(5) of the Terrorism Act 2000,
a resolution is passed by each House of Parliament under section 123(5)(b) of
that Act.

2.10Z7CH.2

Where this paragraph applies, an appeal under paragraph  10Z7CG  against the
making of an order under paragraph  10Z7CA , and against the making (in
addition) of any order under paragraph  10Z7CE (7) , may be brought at any
time before the end of the period of 30 days beginning with the date on which
the deproscription order comes into force.

2.10Z7CH.3

In this paragraph a “ deproscription order ” means an order under section
3(3)(b) or (8) of the Terrorism Act 2000.

########## Realisation or destruction of forfeited cryptoassets etc

2.10Z7CI

2.10Z7CI.1

This paragraph applies where any cryptoasset or other item of property is
forfeited under this Part.

2.10Z7CI.2

An authorised officer must—

2.10Z7CI.2.a

realise the property, or

2.10Z7CI.2.b

make arrangements for its realisation.

This is subject to sub-paragraphs  (3)  to  (5) .

2.10Z7CI.3

The property is not to be realised—

2.10Z7CI.3.a

before the end of the period within which an appeal may be made (whether under
paragraph  10Z7CG  or otherwise), or

2.10Z7CI.3.b

if an appeal is made within that period, before the appeal is determined or
otherwise disposed of.

2.10Z7CI.4

The realisation of property under sub-paragraph  (2)  must be carried out, so
far as practicable, in the manner best calculated to maximise the amount
obtained for the property.

2.10Z7CI.5

Where an authorised officer is satisfied that—

2.10Z7CI.5.a

it is not reasonably practicable to realise any cryptoasset, or

2.10Z7CI.5.b

there are reasonable grounds to believe that the realisation of any
cryptoasset would be contrary to the public interest,

the authorised officer may destroy the cryptoasset.

2.10Z7CI.6

But—

2.10Z7CI.6.a

the authorised officer may destroy the cryptoasset only if the officer is a
senior officer or is authorised to do so by a senior officer, and

2.10Z7CI.6.b

the cryptoasset is not to be destroyed—

2.10Z7CI.6.b.i

before the end of the period within which an appeal may be made (whether under
paragraph  10Z7CG  or otherwise), or

2.10Z7CI.6.b.ii

if an appeal is made within that period, before the appeal is determined or
otherwise disposed of.

2.10Z7CI.7

The question of whether the realisation of the cryptoasset would be contrary
to the public interest is to be determined with particular reference to how
likely it is that the entry of the cryptoasset into general circulation would
facilitate criminal conduct by any person.

########## Proceeds of realisation

2.10Z7CJ

2.10Z7CJ.1

This paragraph applies where any cryptoasset or other item of property is
realised under paragraph  10Z7CI .

2.10Z7CJ.2

The proceeds of the realisation must be applied as follows—

2.10Z7CJ.2.a

first, they must be applied in making any payment required to be made by
virtue of paragraph  10Z7CE (9) ;

2.10Z7CJ.2.b

second, they must be applied in making any payment of legal expenses which,
after giving effect to paragraph  10Z7CA (5)  (including as applied by
paragraph  10Z7CE (5) ), are payable under this sub-paragraph in pursuance of
provision under paragraph  10Z7CA (4)  or, as the case may be,  10Z7CE (4) ;

2.10Z7CJ.2.c

third, they must be applied in payment or reimbursement of any reasonable
costs incurred in storing or insuring the property whilst detained under this
Schedule and in realising the property;

2.10Z7CJ.2.d

fourth, they must be paid—

2.10Z7CJ.2.d.i

if the property was forfeited by a magistrates’ court or the High Court, into
the Consolidated Fund;

2.10Z7CJ.2.d.ii

if the property was forfeited by the sheriff or the Court of Session, into the
Scottish Consolidated Fund.

2.10Z7CJ.3

If what is realised under paragraph  10Z7CI  represents part only of an item
of property, the reference in sub-paragraph  (2)(c)  to costs incurred in
storing or insuring the property is to be read as a reference to costs
incurred in storing or insuring the whole of the property.

########## Victims etc: detained cryptoassets

2.10Z7CK

2.10Z7CK.1

A person who claims that any cryptoassets detained under this Schedule belong
to the person may apply for some or all of the cryptoassets to be released.

2.10Z7CK.2

An application under sub-paragraph  (1)  is to be made—

2.10Z7CK.2.a

in England and Wales or Northern Ireland, to a magistrates’ court;

2.10Z7CK.2.b

in Scotland, to the sheriff.

2.10Z7CK.3

The application may be made in the course of proceedings under paragraph
10Z7AG  or  10Z7CA  or at any other time.

2.10Z7CK.4

The court or sheriff may, subject to sub-paragraph  (8) , order the
cryptoassets to which the application relates to be released to the applicant
if it appears to the court or sheriff that—

2.10Z7CK.4.a

the applicant was deprived of the cryptoassets to which the application
relates, or of property which they represent, by criminal conduct,

2.10Z7CK.4.b

the cryptoassets the applicant was deprived of were not, immediately before
the applicant was deprived of them, property obtained by or in return for
criminal conduct and nor did they then represent such property, and

2.10Z7CK.4.c

the cryptoassets belong to the applicant.

2.10Z7CK.5

If sub-paragraph  (6)  applies, the court or sheriff may, subject to sub-
paragraph  (8) , order the cryptoassets to which the application relates to be
released to the applicant or to the person from whom they were seized.

2.10Z7CK.6

This sub-paragraph applies where—

2.10Z7CK.6.a

the applicant is not the person from whom the cryptoassets to which the
application relates were seized,

2.10Z7CK.6.b

it appears to the court or sheriff that those cryptoassets belong to the
applicant,

2.10Z7CK.6.c

the court or sheriff is satisfied that the release condition is met in
relation to those cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7CK.6.d

no objection to the making of an order under sub-paragraph  (5)  has been made
by the person from whom those cryptoassets were seized.

2.10Z7CK.7

The release condition is met—

2.10Z7CK.7.a

if the conditions in Part  4BA  for the detention of the cryptoassets are no
longer met, or

2.10Z7CK.7.b

in relation to cryptoassets which are subject to an application for forfeiture
under paragraph  10Z7CA , if the court or sheriff decides not to make an order
under that paragraph in relation to the cryptoassets.

2.10Z7CK.8

If (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the cryptoassets are connected, the
cryptoassets are not to be released under this paragraph (and so are to
continue to be detained) until the proceedings are concluded.

########## Victims etc: crypto wallet freezing orders

2.10Z7CL

2.10Z7CL.1

A person who claims that any cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet in respect
of which a crypto wallet freezing order has effect belong to the person may
apply for some or all of the cryptoassets to be released.

2.10Z7CL.2

An application under sub-paragraph  (1)  is to be made—

2.10Z7CL.2.a

in England and Wales or Northern Ireland, to a magistrates’ court;

2.10Z7CL.2.b

in Scotland, to the sheriff.

2.10Z7CL.3

The application may be made in the course of proceedings under paragraph
10Z7BB  or  10Z7CA  or at any other time.

2.10Z7CL.4

The court or sheriff may, subject to sub-paragraph  (8) , order the
cryptoassets to which the application relates to be released to the applicant
if it appears to the court or sheriff that—

2.10Z7CL.4.a

the applicant was deprived of the cryptoassets to which the application
relates, or of property which they represent, by criminal conduct,

2.10Z7CL.4.b

the cryptoassets the applicant was deprived of were not, immediately before
the applicant was deprived of them, property obtained by or in return for
criminal conduct and nor did they then represent such property, and

2.10Z7CL.4.c

the cryptoassets belong to the applicant.

2.10Z7CL.5

If sub-paragraph  (6)  applies, the court or sheriff may, subject to sub-
paragraph  (8) , order the cryptoassets to which the application relates to be
released to the applicant.

2.10Z7CL.6

This sub-paragraph applies where—

2.10Z7CL.6.a

the applicant is not the person from whom the cryptoassets to which the
application relates were seized,

2.10Z7CL.6.b

it appears to the court or sheriff that those cryptoassets belong to the
applicant,

2.10Z7CL.6.c

the court or sheriff is satisfied that the release condition is met in
relation to those cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7CL.6.d

no objection to the making of an order under sub-paragraph  (5)  has been made
by the person from whom those cryptoassets were seized.

2.10Z7CL.7

The release condition is met—

2.10Z7CL.7.a

if the conditions for the making of the crypto wallet freezing order are no
longer met in relation to the cryptoassets to which the application relates,
or

2.10Z7CL.7.b

in relation to cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet subject to a crypto wallet
freezing order which are subject to an application for forfeiture under
paragraph  10Z7CA , if the court or sheriff decides not to make an order under
that paragraph in relation to the cryptoassets.

2.10Z7CL.8

Cryptoassets are not to be released under this paragraph—

2.10Z7CL.8.a

if an application for their forfeiture under paragraph  10Z7CA  is made, until
any proceedings in pursuance of the application (including any proceedings on
appeal) are concluded;

2.10Z7CL.8.b

if (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the cryptoassets are connected, until the
proceedings are concluded.

2.10Z7CL.9

In relation to cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet that is subject to a
crypto wallet freezing order, references in this paragraph to a person from
whom cryptoassets were seized include a reference to a person by or for whom
the crypto wallet was administered immediately before the crypto wallet
freezing order was made.

########## Compensation

2.10Z7CM

2.10Z7CM.1

This paragraph applies if no order is made under paragraph  10Z7CA ,  10Z7CD
or  10Z7CE  in respect of cryptoassets detained under this Schedule or held in
a crypto wallet that is subject to a crypto wallet freezing order under
paragraph  10Z7BB .

2.10Z7CM.2

Where this paragraph applies, the following may make an application to the
relevant court for compensation—

2.10Z7CM.2.a

a person to whom the cryptoassets belong or from whom they were seized;

2.10Z7CM.2.b

a person by or for whom a crypto wallet to which the crypto wallet freezing
order applies is administered.

2.10Z7CM.3

If the relevant court is satisfied that the applicant has suffered loss as a
result of the detention of the cryptoassets or the making of the crypto wallet
freezing order and that the circumstances are exceptional, the relevant court
may order compensation to be paid to the applicant.

2.10Z7CM.4

The amount of compensation to be paid is the amount the relevant court thinks
reasonable, having regard to the loss suffered and any other relevant
circumstances.

2.10Z7CM.5

If the cryptoassets were seized, or the crypto wallet freezing order was
applied for, by an officer of Revenue and Customs, the compensation is to be
paid by the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs.

2.10Z7CM.6

If the cryptoassets were seized, or the crypto wallet freezing order was
applied for, by a constable, the compensation is to be paid as follows—

2.10Z7CM.6.a

in the case of a constable of a police force in England and Wales, it is to be
paid out of the police fund from which the expenses of the police force are
met;

2.10Z7CM.6.b

in the case of a constable of the Police Service of Scotland, it is to be paid
by the Scottish Police Authority;

2.10Z7CM.6.c

in the case of a police officer within the meaning of the Police (Northern
Ireland) Act 2000, it is to be paid out of money provided by the Chief
Constable of the Police Service of Northern Ireland.

2.10Z7CM.7

If the cryptoassets were seized, or the crypto wallet freezing order was
applied for, by a counter-terrorism financial investigator, the compensation
is to be paid as follows—

2.10Z7CM.7.a

in the case of a counter-terrorism financial investigator who was—

2.10Z7CM.7.a.i

a member of the civilian staff of a police force (including the metropolitan
police force), within the meaning of Part 1 of the Police Reform and Social
Responsibility Act 2011, or

2.10Z7CM.7.a.ii

a member of staff of the City of London police force,

it is to be paid out of the police fund from which the expenses of the police
force are met;

2.10Z7CM.7.b

in the case of a counter-terrorism financial investigator who was a member of
staff of the Police Service of Northern Ireland, it is to be paid out of money
provided by the Chief Constable of the Police Service of Northern Ireland.

2.10Z7CM.8

If the cryptoassets were seized, or the crypto wallet freezing order was
applied for, by an immigration officer, the compensation is to be paid by the
Secretary of State.

2.10Z7CM.9

If an order under paragraph  10Z7BB ,  10Z7CA ,  10Z7CD  or  10Z7CE  is made
in respect of some of the cryptoassets detained or held, this paragraph has
effect in relation to the remainder.

2.10Z7CM.10

This paragraph does not apply if the relevant court makes an order under
paragraph  10Z7CK  or  10Z7CL .

2.10Z7CM.11

In this paragraph “ relevant court ” means—

2.10Z7CM.11.a

in England and Wales and Northern Ireland, a magistrates’ court;

2.10Z7CM.11.b

in Scotland, the sheriff.

######### Conversion of cryptoassets

########## Interpretation

2.10Z7D

2.10Z7D.1

In this Part—

“ converted cryptoassets ” is to be read in accordance with paragraphs  10Z7DD
and 10Z7DE; “ crypto wallet freezing order ” has the same meaning as in Part
4BB  (see paragraph  10Z7B (6) ); “ relevant court ” means— in England and
Wales and Northern Ireland, a magistrates’ court; in Scotland, the sheriff; “
relevant financial institution ” has the same meaning as in Part 4B (see
paragraph 10Q); “ UK-connected cryptoasset service provider ” has the same
meaning as in Part  4BB  (see paragraph  10Z7B (7) ).

2.10Z7D.2

Paragraph  10Z7B (6)(b)  (administration of crypto wallets) applies in
relation to this Part as it applies in relation to Part  4BB .

2.10Z7D.3

In this Part references to the conversion of cryptoassets into money are
references to the conversion of cryptoassets into—

2.10Z7D.3.a

cash, or

2.10Z7D.3.b

money held in an account maintained with a relevant financial institution.

2.10Z7D.4

For the purposes of Parts 2 to 4, converted cryptoassets detained under this
Part are not to be treated as cash detained under this Schedule.

########## Detained cryptoassets: conversion

2.10Z7DA

2.10Z7DA.1

Sub-paragraph  (2)  applies while any cryptoassets are detained in pursuance
of an order under paragraph  10Z7AE  or  10Z7AG  (including where cryptoassets
are subject to forfeiture proceedings).

2.10Z7DA.2

A person within sub-paragraph  (3)  may apply to the relevant court for an
order requiring all of the cryptoassets detained pursuant to the order to be
converted into money.

2.10Z7DA.3

The following persons are within this sub-paragraph—

2.10Z7DA.3.a

an authorised officer;

2.10Z7DA.3.b

a person from whom the cryptoassets were seized.

2.10Z7DA.4

In deciding whether to make an order under this paragraph, the court must have
regard to whether the cryptoassets (as a whole) are likely to suffer a
significant loss in value during the period before they are released or
forfeited (including the period during which an appeal against an order for
forfeiture may be made).

2.10Z7DA.5

Before making an order under this paragraph the court must give an opportunity
to be heard to—

2.10Z7DA.5.a

the parties to the proceedings, and

2.10Z7DA.5.b

any other person who may be affected by its decision.

2.10Z7DA.6

As soon as practicable after an order is made under this paragraph, an
authorised officer must convert the cryptoassets, or arrange for the
cryptoassets to be converted, into money.

2.10Z7DA.7

The conversion of cryptoassets under sub-paragraph  (6)  must be carried out,
so far as practicable, in the manner best calculated to maximise the amount of
money obtained for the cryptoassets.

2.10Z7DA.8

At the first opportunity after the cryptoassets are converted, the authorised
officer must arrange for the amount of money obtained for the cryptoassets to
be paid into an interest-bearing account and held there.

2.10Z7DA.9

Interest accruing on the amount is to be added to it on its forfeiture or
release.

2.10Z7DA.10

Where cryptoassets are converted into money in accordance with an order made
under this paragraph—

2.10Z7DA.10.a

the cryptoassets are no longer to be treated as being detained in pursuance of
an order under paragraph  10Z7AE  or  10Z7AG , and

2.10Z7DA.10.b

any application made under paragraph  10Z7CA (2)  in relation to the
cryptoassets which has not yet been determined or otherwise disposed of
(including under paragraph  10Z7CD  or  10Z7CE ) is to be treated as if it
were an application made under paragraph  10Z7DG (2)  in relation to the
converted cryptoassets.

2.10Z7DA.11

An order made under this paragraph must provide for notice to be given to
persons affected by the order.

2.10Z7DA.12

No appeal may be made against an order made under this paragraph.

########## Frozen crypto wallet: conversion

2.10Z7DB

2.10Z7DB.1

This paragraph applies while a crypto wallet freezing order under paragraph
10Z7BB  has effect (including where cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet that
is subject to a crypto wallet freezing order are subject to forfeiture
proceedings).

2.10Z7DB.2

A person within sub-paragraph  (3)  may apply to the relevant court for an
order requiring all of the cryptoassets held in the crypto wallet to be
converted into money.

2.10Z7DB.3

The following persons are within this sub-paragraph—

2.10Z7DB.3.a

an authorised officer;

2.10Z7DB.3.b

a person by or for whom the crypto wallet is administered.

2.10Z7DB.4

In deciding whether to make an order under this paragraph, the court must have
regard to whether the cryptoassets (as a whole) are likely to suffer a
significant loss in value during the period before—

2.10Z7DB.4.a

the crypto wallet freezing order ceases to have effect, or

2.10Z7DB.4.b

the cryptoassets are forfeited (including the period during which an appeal
against an order for forfeiture may be made).

2.10Z7DB.5

Before making an order under this paragraph the court must give an opportunity
to be heard to—

2.10Z7DB.5.a

the parties to the proceedings, and

2.10Z7DB.5.b

any other person who may be affected by its decision.

2.10Z7DB.6

As soon as practicable after an order is made under this paragraph, the UK-
connected cryptoasset service provider that administers the crypto wallet must
convert the cryptoassets, or arrange for the cryptoassets to be converted,
into money.

2.10Z7DB.7

The conversion of cryptoassets under sub-paragraph  (6)  must be carried out,
so far as practicable, in the manner best calculated to maximise the amount of
money obtained for the cryptoassets.

2.10Z7DB.8

At the first opportunity after the cryptoassets are converted, the UK-
connected cryptoasset service provider must arrange for the amount of money
obtained for the cryptoassets to be paid into an interest-bearing account
nominated by an authorised officer and held there.

2.10Z7DB.9

But—

2.10Z7DB.9.a

the UK-connected cryptoasset service provider may deduct any reasonable
expenses incurred by the provider in connection with the conversion of the
cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7DB.9.b

the amount to be treated as the proceeds of the conversion of the cryptoassets
is to be reduced accordingly.

2.10Z7DB.10

Interest accruing on the amount obtained for the cryptoassets is to be added
to it on its forfeiture or release.

2.10Z7DB.11

Where cryptoassets are converted in accordance with an order made under this
paragraph—

2.10Z7DB.11.a

the crypto wallet freezing order ceases to have effect,

2.10Z7DB.11.b

any application made under paragraph  10Z7CA (2)  in relation to the
cryptoassets which has not yet been determined or otherwise disposed of
(including under paragraph  10Z7CD  or  10Z7CE ) is to be treated as if it
were an application made under paragraph  10Z7DG (2)  in relation to the
converted cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7DB.11.c

any application made under paragraph  10Z7CF (2)  in relation to the crypto
wallet which has not yet been determined or otherwise disposed of may not be
proceeded with.

2.10Z7DB.12

An order made under this paragraph must provide for notice to be given to
persons affected by the order.

2.10Z7DB.13

No appeal may be made against an order made under this paragraph.

########## Conversion: existing forfeiture proceedings

2.10Z7DC

2.10Z7DC.1

Where—

2.10Z7DC.1.a

cryptoassets are forfeited under paragraph  10Z7CA  or  10Z7CE , and

2.10Z7DC.1.b

before the cryptoassets are realised or destroyed in accordance with paragraph
10Z7CI , an order is made under paragraph  10Z7DA  requiring the cryptoassets
to be converted into money,

paragraph  10Z7DJ (1)  applies in relation to the converted cryptoassets as if
they had been detained under paragraph  10Z7DD  and forfeited under paragraph
10Z7DG  (and accordingly paragraph  10Z7CI  ceases to apply).

2.10Z7DC.2

Where—

2.10Z7DC.2.a

cryptoassets are forfeited under paragraph  10Z7CA  or  10Z7CE , and

2.10Z7DC.2.b

before the cryptoassets are realised or destroyed in accordance with paragraph
10Z7CI , an order is made under paragraph  10Z7DB  requiring the cryptoassets
to be converted into money,

paragraph  10Z7DJ (2)  applies in relation to the converted cryptoassets as if
they had been detained under paragraph  10Z7DE  and forfeited under paragraph
10Z7DG  (and accordingly paragraph  10Z7CI  ceases to apply).

2.10Z7DC.3

Where—

2.10Z7DC.3.a

an appeal may be made under paragraph  10Z7CG (1)  or  (2)  in relation to the
determination of an application under paragraph  10Z7CA (2)  for the
forfeiture of cryptoassets (including where paragraph  10Z7CD  or  10Z7CE
applies), and

2.10Z7DC.3.b

an order is made under paragraph  10Z7DA  or  10Z7DB  requiring the
cryptoassets to be converted into money,

the appeal may instead be made under paragraph  10Z7DH  (within the time
allowed by paragraph  10Z7CG (4) ) as if it were an appeal against the
determination of an application under paragraph  10Z7DG .

2.10Z7DC.4

Where—

2.10Z7DC.4.a

an appeal is made under paragraph  10Z7CG (1)  or  (2)  in relation to the
determination of an application under paragraph  10Z7CA (2)  for the
forfeiture of cryptoassets (including where paragraph  10Z7CD  or  10Z7CE
applies), and

2.10Z7DC.4.b

before the appeal is determined or otherwise disposed of, an order is made
under paragraph  10Z7DA  or  10Z7DB  requiring the cryptoassets to be
converted into money,

the appeal is to be treated as if it had been made under paragraph  10Z7DH (1)
in relation to the determination of an application under paragraph  10Z7DG
for the forfeiture of the converted cryptoassets.

########## Detained cryptoassets: detention of proceeds of conversion

2.10Z7DD

2.10Z7DD.1

This paragraph applies where cryptoassets are converted into money in
accordance with an order under paragraph  10Z7DA .

2.10Z7DD.2

The proceeds of the conversion (the “converted cryptoassets”) may be detained
initially until the end of the period that the cryptoassets could, immediately
before the conversion, have been detained under Part  4BA  (ignoring the
possibility of any extension of that period).

2.10Z7DD.3

The period for which the converted cryptoassets may be detained may be
extended by an order made by the relevant court.

2.10Z7DD.4

An order under sub-paragraph  (3)  may not authorise the detention of the
converted cryptoassets beyond the end of the period of 2 years beginning with
the relevant date; but this is subject to sub-paragraph  (5) .

2.10Z7DD.5

The relevant court may make an order for the period of 2 years in sub-
paragraph  (4)  to be extended to a period of up to 3 years beginning with the
relevant date.

2.10Z7DD.6

In sub-paragraphs  (4)  and  (5)  “ the relevant date ” means the date on
which the first order under paragraph  10Z7AE  or  10Z7AG  (as the case may
be) was made in relation to the cryptoassets.

2.10Z7DD.7

An application for an order under sub-paragraph  (3)  or  (5)  may be made—

2.10Z7DD.7.a

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, by the Commissioners
for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs or an authorised officer;

2.10Z7DD.7.b

in relation to Scotland, by a procurator fiscal.

2.10Z7DD.8

The relevant court may make an order under sub-paragraph  (3)  only if
satisfied that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that the converted
cryptoassets to be further detained—

2.10Z7DD.8.a

are within subsection (1)(a) or (b) of section 1, or

2.10Z7DD.8.b

are property earmarked as terrorist property.

2.10Z7DD.9

The relevant court may make an order under sub-paragraph  (5)  only if
satisfied that a request for assistance is outstanding in relation to the
cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) .

2.10Z7DD.10

A “request for assistance” in sub-paragraph  (9)  means a request for
assistance in obtaining evidence (including information in any form or
article) in connection with the cryptoassets, made—

2.10Z7DD.10.a

by a judicial authority in the United Kingdom under section 7 of the Crime
(International Co-operation) Act 2003,

2.10Z7DD.10.b

by an authorised officer, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a
foreign country,

2.10Z7DD.10.c

by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their functions under this
Schedule, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a foreign
country, or

2.10Z7DD.10.d

by a person under section 375A or 408A of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002
(evidence overseas).

########## Frozen crypto wallets: detention of proceeds of conversion

2.10Z7DE

2.10Z7DE.1

This paragraph applies where cryptoassets held in a crypto wallet subject to a
crypto wallet freezing order are converted into money in accordance with an
order under paragraph  10Z7DB .

2.10Z7DE.2

The proceeds of the conversion (the “converted cryptoassets”) may be detained
initially until the end of the period that the crypto wallet freezing order
was, immediately before the conversion, due to have effect under Part  4BB
(ignoring the possibility of any extension of that period).

2.10Z7DE.3

The period for which the converted cryptoassets may be detained may be
extended by an order made by the relevant court.

2.10Z7DE.4

An order under sub-paragraph  (3)  may not authorise the detention of the
converted cryptoassets beyond the end of the period of 2 years beginning with
the day on which the crypto wallet freezing order was made; but this is
subject to sub-paragraph  (5) .

2.10Z7DE.5

The relevant court may make an order for the period of 2 years in sub-
paragraph  (4)  to be extended to a period of up to 3 years beginning with the
day on which the crypto wallet freezing order was made.

2.10Z7DE.6

An application for an order under sub-paragraph  (3)  or  (5)  may be made—

2.10Z7DE.6.a

in relation to England and Wales and Northern Ireland, by the Commissioners
for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs or an authorised officer;

2.10Z7DE.6.b

in relation to Scotland, by a procurator fiscal.

2.10Z7DE.7

The relevant court may make an order under sub-paragraph  (3)  only if
satisfied that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that the converted
cryptoassets to be further detained—

2.10Z7DE.7.a

are within subsection (1)(a) or (b) of section 1, or

2.10Z7DE.7.b

are property earmarked as terrorist property.

2.10Z7DE.8

The relevant court may make an order under sub-paragraph  (5)  only if
satisfied that a request for assistance is outstanding in relation to the
cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) .

2.10Z7DE.9

A “request for assistance” in sub-paragraph  (8)  means a request for
assistance in obtaining evidence (including information in any form or
article) in connection with the cryptoassets, made—

2.10Z7DE.9.a

by a judicial authority in the United Kingdom under section 7 of the Crime
(International Co-operation) Act 2003,

2.10Z7DE.9.b

by an authorised officer, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a
foreign country,

2.10Z7DE.9.c

by the Scottish Ministers in connection with their functions under this
Schedule, to an authority exercising equivalent functions in a foreign
country, or

2.10Z7DE.9.d

by a person under section 375A or 408A of the Proceeds of Crime Act 2002
(evidence overseas).

########## Release of detained converted cryptoassets

2.10Z7DF

2.10Z7DF.1

This paragraph applies while any converted cryptoassets are detained under
paragraph  10Z7DD  or  10Z7DE .

2.10Z7DF.2

The relevant court may, subject to sub-paragraph  (7) , direct the release of
the whole or any part of the converted cryptoassets if the following condition
is met.

2.10Z7DF.3

The condition is that, on an application by the relevant person, the court is
not satisfied that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that the
converted cryptoassets to be released—

2.10Z7DF.3.a

are within subsection (1)(a) or (b) of section 1, or

2.10Z7DF.3.b

are property earmarked as terrorist property.

2.10Z7DF.4

In sub-paragraph  (3)  “ the relevant person ” means—

2.10Z7DF.4.a

in the case of converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DD , the
person from whom the cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)  of that
paragraph were seized, and

2.10Z7DF.4.b

in the case of converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DE , any
person affected by the crypto wallet freezing order mentioned in sub-paragraph
(1)  of that paragraph.

2.10Z7DF.5

A person within sub-paragraph  (6)  may, subject to sub-paragraph  (7)  and
after notifying the magistrates’ court or sheriff under whose order converted
cryptoassets are being detained, release the whole or any part of the
converted cryptoassets if satisfied that the detention is no longer justified.

2.10Z7DF.6

The following persons are within this sub-paragraph—

2.10Z7DF.6.a

in relation to England and Wales or Northern Ireland, an authorised officer;

2.10Z7DF.6.b

in relation to Scotland, a procurator fiscal.

2.10Z7DF.7

Converted cryptoassets are not to be released under this paragraph (and so are
to continue to be detained)—

2.10Z7DF.7.a

if an application for their forfeiture under paragraph  10Z7DG  is made, until
any proceedings in pursuance of the application (including any proceedings on
appeal) are concluded;

2.10Z7DF.7.b

if (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the converted cryptoassets are connected,
until the proceedings are concluded.

########## Forfeiture

2.10Z7DG

2.10Z7DG.1

This paragraph applies while any converted cryptoassets are detained under
paragraph  10Z7DD  or  10Z7DE .

2.10Z7DG.2

An application for the forfeiture of some or all of the converted cryptoassets
may be made—

2.10Z7DG.2.a

to a magistrates’ court, by the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and
Customs or an authorised officer;

2.10Z7DG.2.b

to the sheriff, by the Scottish Ministers.

2.10Z7DG.3

The court or sheriff may order the forfeiture of some or all of the converted
cryptoassets if satisfied that the converted cryptoassets to be forfeited—

2.10Z7DG.3.a

are within subsection (1)(a) or (b) of section 1, or

2.10Z7DG.3.b

are property earmarked as terrorist property.

2.10Z7DG.4

But in the case of property which belongs to joint tenants, one of whom is an
excepted joint owner, the order may not apply to so much of it as the court
thinks is attributable to the excepted joint owner’s share.

2.10Z7DG.5

Where an application for forfeiture is made under this paragraph, the
converted cryptoassets are to continue to be detained under paragraph  10Z7DD
or  10Z7DE  (and may not be released under any power conferred by this Part)
until any proceedings in pursuance of the application (including any
proceedings on appeal) are concluded.

2.10Z7DG.6

For the purposes of this paragraph—

2.10Z7DG.6.a

an excepted joint owner is a joint tenant who obtained the property in
circumstances in which it would not (as against them) be earmarked, and

2.10Z7DG.6.b

references to the excepted joint owner’s share of property are to so much of
the property as would have been theirs if the joint tenancy had been severed.

########## Forfeiture: appeals

2.10Z7DH

2.10Z7DH.1

Any party to proceedings for an order for the forfeiture of converted
cryptoassets under paragraph  10Z7DG  who is aggrieved by an order under that
paragraph or by the decision of the court not to make such an order may
appeal—

2.10Z7DH.1.a

from an order or decision of a magistrates’ court in England and Wales, to the
Crown Court;

2.10Z7DH.1.b

from an order or decision of the sheriff, to the Sheriff Appeal Court;

2.10Z7DH.1.c

from an order or decision of a magistrates’ court in Northern Ireland, to a
county court.

2.10Z7DH.2

An appeal under sub-paragraph  (1)  must be made before the end of the period
of 30 days starting with the day on which the court makes the order or
decision.

2.10Z7DH.3

The court hearing the appeal may make any order it thinks appropriate.

2.10Z7DH.4

If the court upholds an appeal against an order forfeiting the converted
cryptoassets, it may, subject to sub-paragraph  (5) , order the release of
some or all of the converted cryptoassets.

2.10Z7DH.5

If (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the converted cryptoassets are connected, the
converted cryptoassets are not to be released under this paragraph (and so are
to continue to be detained) until the proceedings are concluded.

########## Extended time for appealing in certain cases where deproscription order made

2.10Z7DI

2.10Z7DI.1

This paragraph applies where—

2.10Z7DI.1.a

a successful application for an order under paragraph  10Z7DG  relies (wholly
or partly) on the fact that an organisation is proscribed,

2.10Z7DI.1.b

an application under section 4 of the Terrorism Act 2000 for a deproscription
order in respect of the organisation is refused by the Secretary of State,

2.10Z7DI.1.c

the converted cryptoassets forfeited by the order under paragraph  10Z7DG
were converted from cryptoassets which were seized under this Schedule on or
after the date of the refusal of that application,

2.10Z7DI.1.d

an appeal against that refusal is allowed under section 5 of the Terrorism Act
2000,

2.10Z7DI.1.e

a deproscription order is made accordingly, and

2.10Z7DI.1.f

if the order is made in reliance on section 123(5) of the Terrorism Act 2000,
a resolution is passed by each House of Parliament under section 123(5)(b) of
that Act.

2.10Z7DI.2

Where this paragraph applies, an appeal under paragraph  10Z7DH  against the
making of an order under paragraph  10Z7DG  may be brought at any time before
the end of the period of 30 days beginning with the date on which the
deproscription order comes into force.

2.10Z7DI.3

In this paragraph a “ deproscription order ” means an order under section
3(3)(b) or (8) of the Terrorism Act 2000.

########## Application of forfeited converted cryptoassets

2.10Z7DJ

2.10Z7DJ.1

Converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DD  and forfeited under
paragraph  10Z7DG , and any accrued interest on them, must be applied as
follows—

2.10Z7DJ.1.a

first, they must be applied in making any payment of reasonable expenses
incurred by an authorised officer in connection with the safe storage of the
cryptoassets mentioned in paragraph  10Z7DD (1)  during the period the
cryptoassets were detained under Part  4BA ;

2.10Z7DJ.1.b

second, they must be applied in making any payment of reasonable expenses
incurred by an authorised officer in connection with the conversion of those
cryptoassets under paragraph  10Z7DA (6) ;

2.10Z7DJ.1.c

third, they must be applied in making any payment of reasonable expenses
incurred by an authorised officer in connection with the detention of the
converted cryptoassets under this Part;

2.10Z7DJ.1.d

fourth, they must be paid—

2.10Z7DJ.1.d.i

if forfeited by a magistrates’ court in England and Wales or Northern Ireland,
into the Consolidated Fund, and

2.10Z7DJ.1.d.ii

if forfeited by the sheriff, into the Scottish Consolidated Fund.

2.10Z7DJ.2

Converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DE  and forfeited under
paragraph  10Z7DG , and any accrued interest on them, must be applied as
follows—

2.10Z7DJ.2.a

first, they must be applied in making any payment of reasonable expenses
incurred by an authorised officer in connection with the detention of the
converted cryptoassets under this Part;

2.10Z7DJ.2.b

second, they must be paid—

2.10Z7DJ.2.b.i

if forfeited by a magistrates’ court in England and Wales or Northern Ireland,
into the Consolidated Fund, and

2.10Z7DJ.2.b.ii

if forfeited by the sheriff, into the Scottish Consolidated Fund.

2.10Z7DJ.3

But converted cryptoassets are not to be applied or paid under sub-paragraph
(1)  or  (2) —

2.10Z7DJ.3.a

before the end of the period within which an appeal under paragraph  10Z7DH
may be made, or

2.10Z7DJ.3.b

if a person appeals under that paragraph, before the appeal is determined or
otherwise disposed of.

########## Victims etc

2.10Z7DK

2.10Z7DK.1

This paragraph applies where converted cryptoassets are detained under this
Part.

2.10Z7DK.2

Where this paragraph applies, a person (“ P ”) who claims that the relevant
cryptoassets belonged to P immediately before—

2.10Z7DK.2.a

the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or

2.10Z7DK.2.b

the crypto wallet freezing order was made in relation to the crypto wallet in
which the relevant cryptoassets were held,

may apply to the relevant court for some or all of the converted cryptoassets
to be released to P.

2.10Z7DK.3

The application may be made in the course of proceedings under paragraph
10Z7DD ,  10Z7DE  or  10Z7DG  or at any other time.

2.10Z7DK.4

The relevant court may, subject to sub-paragraph  (9) , order the converted
cryptoassets to which the application relates to be released to the applicant
if it appears to the relevant court that the condition in sub-paragraph  (5)
is met.

2.10Z7DK.5

The condition in this sub-paragraph is that—

2.10Z7DK.5.a

the applicant was deprived of the relevant cryptoassets, or of property which
they represent, by criminal conduct,

2.10Z7DK.5.b

the relevant cryptoassets the applicant was deprived of were not, immediately
before the applicant was deprived of them, property obtained by or in return
for criminal conduct and nor did they then represent such property, and

2.10Z7DK.5.c

the relevant cryptoassets belonged to the applicant immediately before—

2.10Z7DK.5.c.i

the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or

2.10Z7DK.5.c.ii

the crypto wallet freezing order was made in relation to the crypto wallet in
which the relevant cryptoassets were held.

2.10Z7DK.6

If sub-paragraph  (7)  applies, the relevant court may, subject to sub-
paragraph  (9) , order the converted cryptoassets to which the application
relates to be released to the applicant or to the person from whom the
relevant cryptoassets were seized.

2.10Z7DK.7

This sub-paragraph applies where—

2.10Z7DK.7.a

the applicant is not the person from whom the relevant cryptoassets were
seized,

2.10Z7DK.7.b

it appears to the relevant court that the relevant cryptoassets belonged to
the applicant immediately before—

2.10Z7DK.7.b.i

the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or

2.10Z7DK.7.b.ii

the crypto wallet freezing order was made in relation to the crypto wallet in
which the relevant cryptoassets were held,

2.10Z7DK.7.c

the relevant court is satisfied that the release condition is met in relation
to the converted cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7DK.7.d

no objection to the making of an order under sub-paragraph  (6)  has been made
by the person from whom the relevant cryptoassets were seized.

2.10Z7DK.8

The release condition is met—

2.10Z7DK.8.a

if the conditions in this Part for the detention of the converted cryptoassets
are no longer met, or

2.10Z7DK.8.b

in relation to converted cryptoassets which are subject to an application for
forfeiture under paragraph  10Z7DG , if the court or sheriff decides not to
make an order under that paragraph in relation to the converted cryptoassets.

2.10Z7DK.9

If (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the converted cryptoassets are connected, the
converted cryptoassets are not to be released under this paragraph (and so are
to continue to be detained) until the proceedings are concluded

2.10Z7DK.10

Where sub-paragraph  (2)(b)  applies, references in this paragraph to a person
from whom relevant cryptoassets were seized include a reference to a person by
or for whom the crypto wallet mentioned in that provision was administered
immediately before the crypto wallet freezing order was made in relation to
the crypto wallet.

2.10Z7DK.11

In this paragraph “ the relevant cryptoassets ” means—

2.10Z7DK.11.a

in relation to converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DD , some
or all of the cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)  of that paragraph,
and

2.10Z7DK.11.b

in relation to converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DE , some
or all of the cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)  of that paragraph.

########## Compensation

2.10Z7DL

2.10Z7DL.1

This paragraph applies if no order is made under paragraph  10Z7DG  in respect
of converted cryptoassets detained under this Part.

2.10Z7DL.2

Where this paragraph applies, the following may make an application to the
relevant court for compensation—

2.10Z7DL.2.a

a person to whom the relevant cryptoassets belonged immediately before they
were seized;

2.10Z7DL.2.b

a person from whom the relevant cryptoassets were seized;

2.10Z7DL.2.c

a person by or for whom the crypto wallet mentioned in paragraph  10Z7DE (1)
was administered immediately before the crypto wallet freezing order was made
in relation to the crypto wallet.

2.10Z7DL.3

If the relevant court is satisfied that—

2.10Z7DL.3.a

the applicant has suffered loss as a result of—

2.10Z7DL.3.a.i

the conversion of the relevant cryptoassets into money, or

2.10Z7DL.3.a.ii

the detention of the converted cryptoassets, and

2.10Z7DL.3.b

the circumstances are exceptional,

the relevant court may order compensation to be paid to the applicant.

2.10Z7DL.4

The amount of compensation to be paid is the amount the relevant court thinks
reasonable, having regard to the loss suffered and any other relevant
circumstances.

2.10Z7DL.5

If the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or the relevant crypto wallet
freezing order was applied for, by an officer of Revenue and Customs, the
compensation is to be paid by the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and
Customs.

2.10Z7DL.6

If the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or the relevant crypto wallet
freezing order was applied for, by a constable, the compensation is to be paid
as follows—

2.10Z7DL.6.a

in the case of a constable of a police force in England and Wales, it is to be
paid out of the police fund from which the expenses of the police force are
met;

2.10Z7DL.6.b

in the case of a constable of the Police Service of Scotland, it is to be paid
by the Scottish Police Authority;

2.10Z7DL.6.c

in the case of a police officer within the meaning of the Police (Northern
Ireland) Act 2000, it is to be paid out of money provided by the Chief
Constable of the Police Service of Northern Ireland.

2.10Z7DL.7

If the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or the relevant crypto wallet
freezing order was applied for, by a counter-terrorism financial investigator,
the compensation is to be paid as follows—

2.10Z7DL.7.a

in the case of a counter-terrorism financial investigator who was—

2.10Z7DL.7.a.i

a member of the civilian staff of a police force (including the metropolitan
police force), within the meaning of Part 1 of the Police Reform and Social
Responsibility Act 2011, or

2.10Z7DL.7.a.ii

a member of staff of the City of London police force,

it is to be paid out of the police fund from which the expenses of the police
force are met;

2.10Z7DL.7.b

in the case of a counter-terrorism financial investigator who was a member of
staff of the Police Service of Northern Ireland, it is to be paid out of money
