provided by the Chief Constable of the Police Service of Northern Ireland.

2.10Z7DL.8

If the relevant cryptoassets were seized, or the relevant crypto wallet
freezing order was applied for, by an immigration officer, the compensation is
to be paid by the Secretary of State.

2.10Z7DL.9

This paragraph does not apply if the relevant court makes an order under
paragraph  10Z7DK .

2.10Z7DL.10

In this paragraph—

“ the relevant cryptoassets ” means— in relation to converted cryptoassets
detained under paragraph  10Z7DD , the cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph
(1)  of that paragraph; in relation to converted cryptoassets detained under
paragraph  10Z7DE , the cryptoassets mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)  of that
paragraph; “ the relevant crypto wallet freezing order ”, in relation to
converted cryptoassets detained under paragraph  10Z7DE , means the crypto
wallet freezing order mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1)  of that paragraph.

3

In Part 1, in paragraph 1(1) (terrorist cash), for “and 4B” substitute  “to
4BD ” .

4

In Part 4B (forfeiture of terrorist money held in bank and building society
accounts), after paragraph 10Z6 insert—

######### Victims etc

4.10Z6A

4.10Z6A.1

A person who claims that money in respect of which an account freezing order
has effect belongs to them may apply to the relevant court for the money to be
released.

4.10Z6A.2

The application may be made in the course of proceedings under paragraph 10S
or 10Z2 or at any other time.

4.10Z6A.3

The court may, subject to sub-paragraph  (7) , order the money to which the
application relates to be released to the applicant if it appears to the court
that—

4.10Z6A.3.a

the applicant was deprived of the money to which the application relates, or
of property which it represents, by criminal conduct,

4.10Z6A.3.b

the money the applicant was deprived of was not, immediately before the
applicant was deprived of it, property obtained by or in return for criminal
conduct and nor did it then represent such property, and

4.10Z6A.3.c

the money belongs to the applicant.

4.10Z6A.4

If sub-paragraph  (5)  applies, the court may, subject to sub-paragraph  (7) ,
order the money to which the application relates to be released to the
applicant.

4.10Z6A.5

This sub-paragraph applies where—

4.10Z6A.5.a

the applicant is not the person from whom the money to which the application
relates was seized,

4.10Z6A.5.b

it appears to the court that the money belongs to the applicant,

4.10Z6A.5.c

the court is satisfied that the release condition is met in relation to the
money, and

4.10Z6A.5.d

no objection to the making of an order under sub-paragraph  (4)  has been made
by the person from whom the money was seized.

4.10Z6A.6

The release condition is met—

4.10Z6A.6.a

in relation to money held in a frozen account, if the conditions for making an
order under paragraph 10S in relation to the money are no longer met, or

4.10Z6A.6.b

in relation to money held in a frozen account which is subject to an
application for forfeiture under paragraph 10Z2, if the court or sheriff
decides not to make an order under that paragraph in relation to the money.

4.10Z6A.7

Money is not to be released under this paragraph—

4.10Z6A.7.a

if an account forfeiture notice under paragraph 10W is given in respect of the
money, until any proceedings in pursuance of the notice (including any
proceedings on appeal) are concluded;

4.10Z6A.7.b

if an application for its forfeiture under paragraph 10Z2, is made, until any
proceedings in pursuance of the application (including any proceedings on
appeal) are concluded;

4.10Z6A.7.c

if (in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) proceedings are started against any
person for an offence with which the cash is connected, until the proceedings
are concluded.

4.10Z6A.8

In relation to money held in an account that is subject to an account freezing
order, references in this paragraph to a person from whom money was seized
include a reference to a person by or for whom the account was operated
immediately before the account freezing order was made.

5

In Part 6, in paragraph 19(1), at the appropriate places insert—

“ cryptoasset ” has the meaning given by paragraph  10Z7A (1) ;

;

“ crypto wallet ” has the meaning given by paragraph  10Z7A (1) ;

;

“ justice of the peace ”, in relation to Northern Ireland, means lay
magistrate;

;

“ terrorist cryptoasset ” has the meaning given by paragraph  10Z7A (1) ;

.

##### Amendments to the Terrorism Act 2000

6

The Terrorism Act 2000 is amended as follows.

7

In Schedule 6 (financial information)—

7.a

in paragraph 6(1) (meaning of financial institution)—

7.a.i

omit the “and” after paragraph (ha), and

7.a.ii

after paragraph (i) insert—

7.a.ii.j

a cryptoasset exchange provider, and

7.a.ii.k

a custodian wallet provider.

;

7.b

after paragraph 6(1AA) insert—

7.b.1AB

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (1)(j), “ cryptoasset exchange provider ”
means a firm or sole practitioner who by way of business provides one or more
of the following services, including where the firm or sole practitioner does
so as creator or issuer of any of the cryptoassets involved—

7.b.1AB.a

exchanging or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange of,
cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets,

7.b.1AB.b

exchanging, or arranging or making arrangements with a view to the exchange
of, one cryptoasset for another, or

7.b.1AB.c

operating a machine which utilises automated processes to exchange
cryptoassets for money or money for cryptoassets.

7.b.1AC

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (1)(k), “ custodian wallet provider ” means
a firm or sole practitioner who by way of business provides services to
safeguard, or to safeguard and administer—

7.b.1AC.a

cryptoassets on behalf of its customers, or

7.b.1AC.b

private cryptographic keys on behalf of its customers in order to hold, store
and transfer cryptoassets.

7.b.1AD

For the purposes of sub-paragraphs (1AB) and (1AC), “ cryptoasset ” means a
cryptographically secured digital representation of value or contractual
rights that uses a form of distributed ledger technology and can be
transferred, stored or traded electronically.

7.b.1AE

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (1AB)—

7.b.1AE.a

“ cryptoasset ” includes a right to, or interest in, the cryptoasset;

7.b.1AE.b

“ money ” means—

7.b.1AE.b.i

money in sterling,

7.b.1AE.b.ii

money in any other currency, or

7.b.1AE.b.iii

money in any other medium of exchange,

but does not include a cryptoasset.

7.b.1AF

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definitions in sub-
paragraphs (1AB) to (1AE).”

8

In section 123 (orders and regulations), after subsection (6ZE) insert—

8.6ZF

Regulations under paragraph 6(1AF) of Schedule 6 may not be made unless a
draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a resolution of
each House of Parliament.

Economic crime offences

Section 193

##### Common law offences

1

Cheating the public revenue.

2

Conspiracy to defraud.

3

In Scotland, the following offences at common law—

3.a

fraud;

3.b

uttering;

3.c

embezzlement;

3.d

theft.

##### Statutory offences

4

An offence under any of the following provisions of the Theft Act 1968—

4.a

section 1 (theft);

4.b

section 17 (false accounting);

4.c

section 19 (false statements by company directors etc);

4.d

section 20 (suppression etc of documents);

4.e

section 24A (dishonestly retaining a wrongful credit).

5

An offence under any of the following provisions of the Theft Act (Northern
Ireland) 1969—

5.a

section 1 (theft);

5.b

section 17 (false accounting);

5.c

section 18 (false statements by company directors etc);

5.d

section 19 (suppression etc of documents);

5.e

section 23A (dishonestly retaining a wrongful credit).

6

An offence under any of the following provisions of the Customs and Excise
Management Act 1979—

6.a

section 68 (offences in relation to exportation of prohibited or restricted
goods);

6.b

section 167 (untrue declarations etc);

6.c

section 170 (fraudulent evasion of duty).

7

An offence under the Forgery and Counterfeiting Act 1981 (forgery,
counterfeiting and kindred offences).

8

An offence under section 72 of the Value Added Tax Act 1994 (fraudulent
evasion of VAT).

9

An offence under section 46A of the Criminal Law (Consolidation) (Scotland)
Act 1995 (false monetary instruments).

10

An offence under any of the following sections of the Financial Services and
Markets Act 2000—

10.a

section 23 (contravention of prohibition on carrying on regulated activity
unless authorised or exempt);

10.b

section 25 (contravention of restrictions on financial promotion);

10.c

section 85 (prohibition of dealing etc in transferable securities without
approved prospectus);

10.d

section 398 (misleading the FCA or PRA).

11

An offence under any of the following sections of the Terrorism Act 2000—

11.a

section 15 (fund-raising);

11.b

section 16 (use and possession);

11.c

section 17 (funding arrangements);

11.d

section 18 (money laundering);

11.e

section 63 (terrorist finance: jurisdiction).

12

An offence under any of the following sections of the Proceeds of Crime Act
2002—

12.a

section 327 (concealing etc criminal property);

12.b

section 328 (arrangements facilitating acquisition etc of criminal property);

12.c

section 329 (acquisition, use and possession of criminal property);

12.d

section 330 (failing to disclose knowledge or suspicion of money laundering);

12.e

section 333A (tipping off).

13

An offence under any of the following sections of the Companies Act 2006—

13.a

section 658 (general rule against limited company acquiring its own shares);

13.b

section 680 (prohibited financial assistance);

13.c

section 993 (fraudulent trading).

14

An offence under any of the following sections of the Fraud Act 2006—

14.a

section 1 (fraud);

14.b

section 6 (possession etc of articles for use in frauds);

14.c

section 7 (making or supplying articles for use in frauds);

14.d

section 9 (participating in fraudulent business carried on by sole trader);

14.e

section 11 (obtaining services dishonestly).

15

An offence under any of the following sections of the Bribery Act 2010—

15.a

section 1 (bribing another person);

15.b

section 2 (being bribed);

15.c

section 6 (bribery of foreign public officials);

15.d

section 7 (failure of commercial organisations to prevent bribery).

16

An offence under section 49 of the Criminal Justice and Licensing (Scotland)
Act 2010 (possession, making or supplying articles for use in frauds).

17

An offence under any of the following sections of the Financial Services Act
2012—

17.a

section 89 (misleading statements);

17.b

section 90 (misleading impressions);

17.c

section 91 (misleading statements etc in relation to benchmarks).

18

An offence under section 45 or 46 of the Criminal Finances Act 2017 (failure
to prevent the facilitation of UK tax evasion offences or foreign tax evasion
offences).

19

An offence under regulation 86 of the Money Laundering, Terrorist Financing
and Transfer of Funds (Information on the Payer) Regulations 2017.

20

An offence under regulations made under section 49 of the Sanctions and Anti-
Money Laundering Act 2018 (money laundering and terrorist financing etc).

21

An offence under section 199 of this Act (failure to prevent fraud).

22

22.1

An offence under an instrument made under section 2(2) of the European
Communities Act 1972 for the purpose of implementing, or otherwise in relation
to, EU obligations created or arising by or under an EU financial sanctions
Regulation.

22.2

An offence under an Act or under subordinate legislation where the offence was
created for the purpose of implementing a UN financial sanctions Resolution.

22.3

An offence under paragraph 7 of Schedule 3 to the Anti-terrorism, Crime and
Security Act 2001 (freezing orders).

22.4

An offence under paragraph 30 or 30A of Schedule 7 to the Counter-Terrorism
Act 2008 where the offence relates to a requirement of the kind mentioned in
paragraph 13 of that Schedule.

22.5

An offence under paragraph 31 of Schedule 7 to the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008.

22.6

An offence under regulations made under section 1 of the Sanctions and Anti-
Money Laundering Act 2018 (sanctions regulations).

22.7

In this paragraph—

“ EU financial sanctions Regulation ” and “ UN financial sanctions Resolution
” have the same meanings as in Part 8 of the Policing and Crime Act 2017 (see
section 143 of that Act); “ subordinate legislation ” has the same meaning as
in the Interpretation Act 1978.
